
"Arcturus" is his other name&mdash; I'd rather call him "Star."

It's very mean of Science

To go and interfere!

I slew a worm the other day&mdash; A "Savant" passing by

Murmured "Resurgam"&mdash;"Centipede"!

"Oh Lord&mdash;how frail are we"!

I pull a flower from the woods&mdash; A monster with a glass

Computes the stamens in a breath&mdash; And has her in a "class"!

Whereas I took the Butterfly

Aforetime in my hat&mdash;

He sits erect in "Cabinets"&mdash; The Clover bells forgot.

What once was "Heaven"

Is "Zenith" now&mdash;

Where I proposed to go

When Time's brief masquerade was done

Is mapped and charted too.

What if the poles should frisk about

And stand upon their heads!

I hope I'm ready for "the worst"&mdash; Whatever prank betides!

Perhaps the "Kingdom of Heaven's" changed&mdash; I hope the "Children" there Won't be "new fashioned" when I come&mdash; And laugh at me&mdash;and stare&mdash; I hope the Father in the skies

Will lift his little girl&mdash;

Old fashioned&mdash;naught&mdash;everything&mdash; Over the stile of "Pearl."

Emily Dickinson





"Faith" is a fine invention


"Faith" is a fine invention

When Gentlemen can see&mdash;

But Microscopes are prudent

In an Emergency.

Emily Dickinson






"Heaven" has different Signs&mdash;to me&mdash; Sometimes, I think that Noon

Is but a symbol of the Place&mdash; And when again, at Dawn,

A mighty look runs round the World

And settles in the Hills&mdash;

An Awe if it should be like that

Upon the Ignorance steals&mdash;

The Orchard, when the Sun is on&mdash; The Triumph of the Birds

When they together Victory make&mdash; Some Carnivals of Clouds&mdash;

The Rapture of a finished Day&mdash; Returning to the West&mdash;

All these&mdash;remind us of the place That Men call "paradise"&mdash; Itself be fairer&mdash;we suppose&mdash; But how Ourself, shall be

Adorned, for a Superior Grace&mdash; Not yet, our eyes can see&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





"Heaven"&mdash;is what I cannot reach!


"Heaven"&mdash;is what I cannot reach!

The Apple on the Tree&mdash;

Provided it do hopeless&mdash;hang&mdash; That&mdash;"Heaven" is&mdash;to Me!

The Color, on the Cruising Cloud&mdash; The interdicted Land&mdash;

Behind the Hill&mdash;the House behind&mdash; There&mdash;Paradise&mdash;is found!

Her teasing Purples&mdash;Afternoons&mdash; The credulous&mdash;decoy&mdash; Enamored&mdash;of the Conjuror&mdash; That spurned us&mdash;Yesterday!

Emily Dickinson






"Hope" is the thing with feathers&mdash; That perches in the soul&mdash;

And sings the tune without the words&mdash; And never stops&mdash;at all&mdash; And sweetest&mdash;in the Gale&mdash;is heard&mdash; And sore must be the storm&mdash;

That could abash the little Bird

That kept so many warm&mdash;

I've heard it in the chillest land&mdash; And on the strangest Sea&mdash;

Yet, never, in Extremity,

It asked a crumb&mdash;of Me.

Emily Dickinson






"Houses"&mdash;so the Wise Men tell me&mdash;

"Mansions"! Mansions must be warm!

Mansions cannot let the tears in,

Mansions must exclude the storm!

"Many Mansions," by "his Father,"

I don't know him; snugly built!

Could the Children find the way there&mdash; Some, would even trudge tonight!

Emily Dickinson






"I want"&mdash;it pleaded&mdash;All its life&mdash; I want&mdash;was chief it said

When Skill entreated it&mdash;the last&mdash; And when so newly dead&mdash;

I could not deem it late&mdash;to hear That single&mdash;steadfast sigh&mdash; The lips had placed as with a "Please"

Toward Eternity&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






"Morning"&mdash;means "Milking"&mdash;to the Farmer&mdash; Dawn&mdash;to the Teneriffe&mdash; Dice&mdash;to the Maid&mdash;

Morning means just Risk&mdash;to the Lover&mdash; Just revelation&mdash;to the Beloved&mdash; Epicures&mdash;date a Breakfast&mdash;by it&mdash; Brides&mdash;an Apocalypse&mdash; Worlds&mdash;a Flood&mdash;

Faint-going Lives&mdash;Their Lapse from Sighing&mdash; Faith&mdash;The Experiment of Our Lord Emily Dickinson





"Nature" is what we see


"Nature" is what we see&mdash; The Hill&mdash;the Afternoon&mdash; Squirrel&mdash;Eclipse&mdash;the Bumble bee&mdash; Nay&mdash;Nature is Heaven&mdash; Nature is what we hear&mdash;

The Bobolink&mdash;the Sea&mdash; Thunder&mdash;the Cricket&mdash; Nay&mdash;Nature is Harmony&mdash; Nature is what we know&mdash;

Yet have no art to say&mdash;

So impotent Our Wisdom is

To her Simplicity.

Emily Dickinson






"Speech"&mdash;is a prank of Parliament&mdash;

"Tears"&mdash;is a trick of the nerve&mdash; But the Heart with the heaviest freight on&mdash; Doesn't&mdash;always&mdash;move&mdash; Emily Dickinson






"They have not chosen me," he said,

"But I have chosen them!"

Brave&mdash;Broken hearted statement&mdash; Uttered in Bethlehem!

I could not have told it,

But since Jesus dared&mdash;

Sovereign! Know a Daisy

They dishonor shared!

Emily Dickinson






"Unto Me?" I do not know you&mdash; Where may be your House?

"I am Jesus&mdash;Late of Judea&mdash; Now&mdash;of Paradise"&mdash; Wagons&mdash;have you&mdash;to convey me?

This is far from Thence&mdash;

"Arms of Mine&mdash;sufficient Phaeton&mdash; Trust Omnipotence"&mdash;

I am spotted&mdash;"I am Pardon"&mdash; I am small&mdash;"The Least

Is esteemed in Heaven the Chiefest&mdash; Occupy my House"&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





"Why do I love" You, Sir?


"Why do I love" You, Sir?

Because&mdash;

The Wind does not require the Grass

To answer&mdash;Wherefore when He pass She cannot keep Her place.

Because He knows&mdash;and

Do not You&mdash;

And We know not&mdash;

Enough for Us

The Wisdom it be so&mdash;

The Lightning&mdash;never asked an Eye Wherefore it shut&mdash;when He was by&mdash; Because He knows it cannot speak&mdash; And reasons not contained&mdash;

&mdash;Of Talk&mdash;

There be&mdash;preferred by Daintier Folk&mdash; The Sunrise&mdash;Sire&mdash;compelleth Me&mdash; Because He's Sunrise&mdash;and I see&mdash; Therefore&mdash;Then&mdash;

I love Thee&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





A Bird Came Down

A bird came down the walk:

He did not know I saw;

He bit an angle-worm in halves

And ate the fellow, raw.

And then he drank a dew

From a convenient grass,

And then hopped sidewise to the wall

To let a beetle pass.

He glanced with rapid eyes

That hurried all abroad,--

They looked like frightened beads, I thought; He stirred his velvet head

Like one in danger; cautious,

I offered him a crumb,

And he unrolled his feathers

And rowed him softer home

Than oars divide the ocean,

Too silver for a seam,

Or butterflies, off banks of noon,

Leap, splashless, as they swim.

Emily Dickinson





A Bird came down the Walk


A Bird came down the Walk&mdash;

He did not know I saw&mdash;

He bit an angle-worm in halves

And ate the fellow, raw,

And then he drank a Dew

From a convenient Grass,

And then hopped sidewise to the Wall

To let a Beetle pass&mdash;

He glanced with rapid eyes

That hurried all abroa&mdash;

They looked like frightened Beads, I thought&mdash; He stirred his velvet head

Like one in danger, Cautious,

I offered him a Crumb,

And he unrolled his feathers

And rowed him softer home&mdash;

Than Oars divide the Ocean,

Too silver for a seam&mdash;

Or Butterflies, off Banks of Noon,

Leap, plashless as they swim.

Emily Dickinson





A Book

There is no frigate like a book

To take us lands away,

Nor any coursers like a page

Of prancing poetry.

This traverse may the poorest take

Without oppress of toll;

How frugal is the chariot

That bears a human soul!

Emily Dickinson





A Burdock&mdash;clawed my Gown


A Burdock&mdash;clawed my Gown&mdash; Not Burdock's&mdash;blame&mdash; But mine&mdash;

Who went too near

The Burdock's Den&mdash;

A Bog&mdash;affronts my shoe&mdash; What else have Bogs&mdash;to do&mdash; The only Trade they know&mdash;

The splashing Men!

Ah, pity&mdash;then!

'Tis Minnows can despise!

The Elephant's&mdash;calm eyes

Look further on!

Emily Dickinson





A Burdock—clawed my Gown


A Burdock—clawed my Gown—

Not Burdock's—blame—

But mine—

Who went too near

The Burdock's Den—

A Bog—affronts my shoe—

What else have Bogs—to do—

The only Trade they know—

The splashing Men!

Ah, pity—then!

'Tis Minnows can despise!

Look further on!

A Charm invests a face


A Charm invests a face

Imperfectly beheld&mdash;

The Lady date not lift her Veil

For fear it be dispelled&mdash;

But peers beyond her mesh&mdash;

And wishes&mdash;and denies&mdash; Lest Interview&mdash;annul a want

That Image&mdash;satisfies&mdash; Emily Dickinson





A Clock stopped


A Clock stopped&mdash;

Not the Mantel's&mdash;

Geneva's farthest skill

Can't put the puppet bowing&mdash; That just now dangled still&mdash; An awe came on the Trinket!

The Figures hunched, with pain&mdash; Then quivered out of Decimals&mdash; Into Degreeless Noon&mdash;

It will not stir for Doctors&mdash; This Pendulum of snow&mdash;

This Shopman importunes it&mdash;

While cool&mdash;concernless No&mdash; Nods from the Gilded pointers&mdash; Nods from the Seconds slim&mdash;

Decades of Arrogance between

The Dial life&mdash;

And Him&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





A Clock Stopped -- Not The Mantel's

A clock stopped -- not the mantel's

Geneva's farthest skill

Can't put the puppet bowing

That just now dangled still.

An awe came on the trinket!

The figures hunched with pain,

Then quivered out of decimals

Into degreeless noon.

It will not stir for doctors,

This pendulum of snow;

The shopman importunes it,

While cool, concernless No

Nods from the gilded pointers,

Nods from seconds slim,

Decades of arrogance between

The dial life and him.

Emily Dickinson





A Cloud withdrew from the Sky


A Cloud withdrew from the Sky

Superior Glory be

But that Cloud and its Auxiliaries

Are forever lost to me

Had I but further scanned

Had I secured the Glow

In an Hermetic Memory

It had availed me now.

Never to pass the Angel

With a glance and a Bow

Till I am firm in Heaven

Is my intention now.

Emily Dickinson





A Coffin&mdash;is a small Domain


A Coffin&mdash;is a small Domain,

Yet able to contain

A Citizen of Paradise

In it diminished Plane.

A Grave&mdash;is a restricted Breadth&mdash; Yet ampler than the Sun&mdash;

And all the Seas He populates

And Lands He looks upon

To Him who on its small Repose

Bestows a single Friend&mdash;

Circumference without Relief&mdash; Or Estimate&mdash;or End&mdash; Emily Dickinson

A Day! Help! Help! Another Day!


A Day! Help! Help! Another Day!

Your prayers, oh Passer by!

From such a common ball as this

Might date a Victory!

From marshallings as simple

The flags of nations swang.

Steady&mdash;my soul: What issues

Upon thine arrow hang!

Emily Dickinson





A Death blow is a Life blow to Some


A Death blow is a Life blow to Some

Who till they died, did not alive become&mdash; Who had they lived, had died but when

They died, Vitality begun.

Emily Dickinson





A door just opened on a street

A door just opened on a street--

I, lost, was passing by--

An instant's width of warmth disclosed And wealth, and company.

The door as sudden shut, and I,

I, lost, was passing by,--

Lost doubly, but by contrast most,

Enlightening misery.

Emily Dickinson





A doubt if it be Us


A doubt if it be Us

Assists the staggering Mind

In an extremer Anguish

Until it footing find.

An Unreality is lent,

A merciful Mirage

That makes the living possible

While it suspends the lives.

Emily Dickinson





A drop fell on the apple tree

A drop fell on the apple tree

Another on the roof;

A half a dozen kissed the eaves,

And made the gables laugh.

A few went out to help the brook,

That went to help the sea.

Myself conjectured, Were they pearls,

What necklaces could be!

The dust replaced in hoisted roa

The birds jocoser sung;

The sunshine threw his hat away,

The orchards spangles hung.

The breezes brought dejected

And bathed them in the glee;

The East put out a single flag,

And signed the fete away.

Emily Dickinson






A Dying Tiger&mdash;moaned for Drink&mdash; I hunted all the Sand&mdash;

I caught the Dripping of a Rock

And bore it in my Hand&mdash;

His Mighty Balls&mdash;in death were thick&mdash; But searching&mdash;I could see

A Vision on the Retina

Of Water&mdash;and of me&mdash;

'Twas not my blame&mdash;who sped too slow&mdash;

'Twas not his blame&mdash;who died While I was reaching him&mdash;

But 'twas&mdash;the fact that He was dead&mdash; Emily Dickinson





A Dying Tiger—moaned for Drink


A Dying Tiger—moaned for Drink—

I hunted all the Sand—

I caught the Dripping of a Rock

And bore it in my Hand—

His Mighty Balls—in death were thick—

But searching—I could see

A Vision on the Retina

Of Water—and of me—

'Twas not my blame—who sped too slow—

'Twas not his blame—who died

While I was reaching him—

But 'twas—the fact that He was dead—

Emily Dickinson





A feather from the Whippoorwill


A feather from the Whippoorwill

That everlasting&mdash;sings!

Whose galleries&mdash;are Sunrise&mdash; Whose Opera&mdash;the Springs&mdash; Whose Emerald Nest the Ages spin

Of mellow&mdash;murmuring thread&mdash; Whose Beryl Egg, what Schoolboys hunt

In "Recess"&mdash;Overhead!

Emily Dickinson





A first Mute Coming


A first Mute Coming&mdash;

In the Stranger's House&mdash;

A first fair Going&mdash;

When the Bells rejoice&mdash;

A first Exchange&mdash;of

What hath mingled&mdash;been&mdash; For Lot&mdash;exhibited to

Faith&mdash;alone&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





A fuzzy fellow, without feet


A fuzzy fellow, without feet,

Yet doth exceeding run!

Of velvet, is his Countenance,

And his Complexion, dun!

Sometime, he dwelleth in the grass!

Sometime, upon a bough,

From which he doth descend in plush

Upon the Passer-by!

All this in summer.

But when winds alarm the Forest Folk,

He taketh Damask Residence&mdash;

And struts in sewing silk!

Then, finer than a Lady,

Emerges in the spring!

A Feather on each shoulder!

You'd scarce recognize him!

By Men, yclept Caterpillar!

By me! But who am I,

To tell the pretty secret

Of the Butterfly!

Emily Dickinson





A happy lip&mdash;breaks sudden


A happy lip&mdash;breaks sudden&mdash; It doesn't state you how

It contemplated&mdash;smiling&mdash; Just consummated&mdash;now&mdash; But this one, wears its merriment

So patient&mdash;like a pain&mdash; Fresh gilded&mdash;to elude the eyes Unqualified, to scan&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





A happy lip—breaks sudden


A happy lip—breaks sudden—

It doesn't state you how

It contemplated—smiling—

Just consummated—now—

But this one, wears its merriment

So patient—like a pain—

Fresh gilded—to elude the eyes

Unqualified, to scan—

Emily Dickinson





A House upon the Height


A House upon the Height&mdash;

That Wagon never reached&mdash;

No Dead, were ever carried down&mdash; No Peddler's Cart&mdash;approached&mdash; Whose Chimney never smoked&mdash;

Whose Windows&mdash;Night and Morn&mdash; Caught Sunrise first&mdash;and Sunset&mdash;last&mdash; Then&mdash;held an Empty Pane&mdash; Whose fate&mdash;Conjecture knew&mdash; No other neighbor&mdash;did&mdash; And what it was&mdash;we never lisped&mdash; Because He&mdash;never told&mdash; Emily Dickinson





A Lady red&mdash;amid the Hill


A Lady red&mdash;amid the Hill

Her annual secret keeps!

A Lady white, within the Field

In placid Lily sleeps!

The tidy Breezes, with their Brooms&mdash; Sweep vale&mdash;and hill&mdash;and tree!

Prithee, My pretty Housewives!

Who may expected be?

The Neighbors do not yet suspect!

The Woods exchange a smile!

Orchard, and Buttercup, and Bird&mdash; In such a little while!

And yet, how still the Landscape stands!

How nonchalant the Hedge!

As if the "Resurrection"

Were nothing very strange!

Emily Dickinson

A light exists in spring

A light exists in spring

Not present on the year

At any other period.

When March is scarcely here

A color stands abroad

On solitary hills

That science cannot overtake,

But human naturefeels.

It waits upon the lawn;

It shows the furthest tree

Upon the furthest slope we know;

It almost speaks to me.

Then, as horizons step,

Or noons report away,

Without the formula of sound,

It passes, and we stay:

A quality of loss

Affecting our content,

As trade had suddenly encroached

Upon a sacrament.

Emily Dickinson






A little bread&mdash;a crust&mdash;a crumb&mdash; A little trust&mdash;a demijohn&mdash; Can keep the soul alive&mdash;

Not portly, mind! but breathing&mdash;warm&mdash; Conscious&mdash;as old Napoleon,

The night before the Crown!

A modest lot&mdash;A fame petite&mdash; A brief Campaign of sting and sweet

Is plenty! Is enough!

A Sailor's business is the shore!

A Soldier's&mdash;balls! Who asketh more, Must seek the neighboring life!

Emily Dickinson





A little bread—a crust—a crumb


A little bread—a crust—a crumb—

A little trust—a demijohn—

Can keep the soul alive—

Not portly, mind! but breathing—warm—

Conscious—as old Napoleon,

The night before the Crown!

A modest lot—A fame petite—

A brief Campaign of sting and sweet

Is plenty! Is enough!

A Sailor's business is the shore!

A Soldier's—balls! Who asketh more,

Must seek the neighboring life!

Emily Dickinson





A little East of Jordan


A little East of Jordan,

Evangelists record,

A Gymnast and an Angel

Did wrestle long and hard&mdash;

Till morning touching mountain&mdash; And Jacob, waxing strong,

The Angel begged permission

To Breakfast&mdash;to return&mdash; Not so, said cunning Jacob!

"I will not let thee go

Except thou bless me"&mdash;Stranger!

The which acceded to&mdash;

Light swung the silver fleeces

"Peniel" Hills beyond,

And the bewildered Gymnast

Found he had worsted God!

Emily Dickinson





A little road not made man

A little road not made of man,

Enabled of the eye,

Accessible to thill of bee,

Or cart of butterfly.

If town it have, beyond itself,

'T is that I cannot say;

I only sigh,--no vehicle

Bears me along that way.

Emily Dickinson

A long&mdash;long Sleep&mdash;A famous&mdash;Sleep&mdash; That makes no show for Morn&mdash; By Stretch of Limb&mdash;or stir of Lid&mdash; An independent One&mdash;

Was ever idleness like This?

Upon a Bank of Stone

To bask the Centuries away&mdash;

Nor once look up&mdash;for Noon?

Emily Dickinson





A long, long sleep, a famous sleep

A long, long sleep, a famous sleep

That makes no show for dawn

By strech of limb or stir of lid, --

An independent one.

Was ever idleness like this?

Within a hut of stone

To bask the centuries away

Nor once look up for noon?

Emily Dickinson





A loss of something ever felt I


A loss of something ever felt I&mdash; The first that I could recollect

Bereft I was&mdash;of what I knew not Too young that any should suspect

A Mourner walked among the children

I notwithstanding went about

As one bemoaning a Dominion

Itself the only Prince cast out&mdash; Elder, Today, a session wiser

And fainter, too, as Wiseness is&mdash; I find myself still softly searching

For my Delinguent Palaces&mdash;

And a Suspicion, like a Finger

Touches my Forehead now and then

That I am looking oppositely

For the site of the Kingdom of Heaven&mdash; Emily Dickinson





A Man may make a Remark


A Man may make a Remark&mdash;

In itself&mdash;a quiet thing

That may furnish the Fuse unto a Spark In dormant nature&mdash;lain&mdash; Let us deport&mdash;with skill&mdash; Let us discourse&mdash;with care&mdash; Powder exists in Charcoal&mdash;

Before it exists in Fire.

Emily Dickinson





A Mien to move a Queen


A Mien to move a Queen&mdash;

Half Child&mdash;Half Heroine&mdash; An Orleans in the Eye

That puts its manner by

For humbler Company

When none are near

Even a Tear&mdash;

Its frequent Visitor&mdash;

A Bonnet like a Duke&mdash;

And yet a Wren's Peruke

Were not so shy

Of Goer by&mdash;

And Hands&mdash;so slight&mdash; They would elate a Sprite

With Merriment&mdash;

A Voice that Alters&mdash;Low

And on the Ear can go

Like Let of Snow&mdash;

Or shift supreme&mdash;

As tone of Realm

On Subjects Diadem&mdash;

Too small&mdash;to fear&mdash; Too distant&mdash;to endear&mdash; And so Men Compromise

And just&mdash;revere&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





A Moth the hue of this


A Moth the hue of this

Haunts Candles in Brazil.

Nature's Experience would make

Our Reddest Second pale.

Nature is fond, I sometimes think,

Of Trinkets, as a Girl.

Emily Dickinson






A Murmur in the Trees&mdash;to note&mdash; Not loud enough&mdash;for Wind&mdash; A Star&mdash;not far enough to seek&mdash; Nor near enough&mdash;to find&mdash; A long&mdash;long Yellow&mdash;on the Lawn&mdash; A Hubbub&mdash;as of feet&mdash; Not audible&mdash;as Ours&mdash;to Us&mdash; But dapperer&mdash;More Sweet&mdash; A Hurrying Home of little Men

To Houses unperceived&mdash;

All this&mdash;and more&mdash;if I should tell&mdash; Would never be believed&mdash;

Of Robins in the Trundle bed

How many I espy

Whose Nightgowns could not hide the Wings&mdash; Although I heard them try&mdash;

But then I promised ne'er to tell&mdash; How could I break My Word?

So go your Way&mdash;and I'll go Mine&mdash; No fear you'll miss the Road.

Emily Dickinson





A Murmur in the Trees—to note


A Murmur in the Trees—to note—

Not loud enough—for Wind—

A Star—not far enough to seek—

Nor near enough—to find—

A long—long Yellow—on the Lawn—

A Hubbub—as of feet—

Not audible—as Ours—to Us—

But dapperer—More Sweet—

A Hurrying Home of little Men

To Houses unperceived—

All this—and more—if I should tell—

Would never be believed—

Of Robins in the Trundle bed

How many I espy

Whose Nightgowns could not hide the Wings—

Although I heard them try—

But then I promised ne'er to tell—

How could I break My Word?

So go your Way—and I'll go Mine—

No fear you'll miss the Road.

Emily Dickinson





A narrow fellow in the grass

A narrow fellow in the grass

Occasionally rides;

You may have met him,--did you not,

His notice sudden is.

The grass divides as with a comb,

A spotted shaft is seen;

And then it closes at your feet

And opens further on.

He likes a boggy acre,

A floor too cool for corn.

Yet when a child, and barefoot,

I more than once, at morn,

Have passed, I thought, a whip-lash

Unbraiding in the sun,--

When, stooping to secure it,

It wrinkled, and was gone.

Several of nature's people

I know, and they know me;

I feel for them a transport

Of cordiality;

But never met this fellow,

Attended or alone,

Without a tighter breathing,

And zero at the bone.

Emily Dickinson





A nearness to Tremendousness


A nearness to Tremendousness&mdash; An Agony procures&mdash;

Affliction ranges Boundlessness&mdash; Vicinity to Laws

Contentment's quiet Suburb&mdash;

Affliction cannot stay

In Acres&mdash;Its Location

Is Illocality&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






A Night&mdash;there lay the Days between&mdash; The Day that was Before&mdash;

And Day that was Behind&mdash;were one&mdash; And now&mdash;'twas Night&mdash;was here&mdash; Slow&mdash;Night&mdash;that must be watched away&mdash; As Grains upon a shore&mdash;

Too imperceptible to note&mdash;

Till it be night&mdash;no more&mdash; Emily Dickinson





A Night—there lay the Days between


A Night—there lay the Days between—

The Day that was Before—

And Day that was Behind—were one—

And now—'twas Night—was here—

Slow—Night—that must be watched away—

As Grains upon a shore—

Too imperceptible to note—

Till it be night—no more—

Emily Dickinson





A Planted Life&mdash;diversified


A Planted Life&mdash;diversified

With Gold and Silver Pain

To prove the presence of the Ore

In Particles&mdash;'tis when

A Value struggle&mdash;it exist&mdash; A Power&mdash;will proclaim

Although Annihilation pile

Whole Chaoses on Him&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

A poor&mdash;torn heart&mdash;a tattered heart&mdash; That sat it down to rest&mdash;

Nor noticed that the Ebbing Day

Flowed silver to the West&mdash;

Nor noticed Night did soft descend&mdash; Nor Constellation burn&mdash;

Intent upon the vision

Of latitudes unknown.

The angels&mdash;happening that way This dusty heart espied&mdash;

Tenderly took it up from toil

And carried it to God&mdash;

There&mdash;sandals for the Barefoot&mdash; There&mdash;gathered from the gales&mdash; Do the blue havens by the hand

Lead the wandering Sails.

Emily Dickinson





A poor—torn heart—a tattered heart

A poor—torn heart—a tattered heart—

That sat it down to rest—

Nor noticed that the Ebbing Day

Flowed silver to the West—

Nor noticed Night did soft descend—

Nor Constellation burn—

Intent upon the vision

Of latitudes unknown.

The angels—happening that way

This dusty heart espied—

Tenderly took it up from toil

And carried it to God—

There—sandals for the Barefoot—

There—gathered from the gales—

Do the blue havens by the hand

Lead the wandering Sails.

Emily Dickinson






A precious&mdash;mouldering pleasure&mdash;'tis&mdash; To meet an Antique Book&mdash;

In just the Dress his Century wore&mdash; A privilege&mdash;I think&mdash; His venerable Hand to take&mdash;

And warming in our own&mdash;

A passage back&mdash;or two&mdash;to make&mdash; To Times when he&mdash;was young&mdash; His quaint opinions&mdash;to inspect&mdash; His thought to ascertain

On Themes concern our mutual mind&mdash; The Literature of Man&mdash;

What interested Scholars&mdash;most&mdash; What Competitions ran&mdash;

When Plato&mdash;was a Certainty&mdash; And Sophocles&mdash;a Man&mdash; When Sappho&mdash;was a living Girl&mdash; And Beatrice wore

The Gown that Dante&mdash;deified&mdash; Facts Centuries before

He traverses&mdash;familiar&mdash; As One should come to Town&mdash;

And tell you all your Dreams&mdash;were true&mdash; He lived&mdash;where Dreams were born&mdash; His presence is Enchantment&mdash; You beg him not to go&mdash;

Old Volume shake their Vellum Heads

And tantalize&mdash;just so&mdash; Emily Dickinson





A precious—mouldering pleasure


A precious—mouldering pleasure—'tis—

To meet an Antique Book—

In just the Dress his Century wore—

A privilege—I think—

His venerable Hand to take—

And warming in our own—

A passage back—or two—to make—

To Times when he—was young—

His quaint opinions—to inspect—

His thought to ascertain

On Themes concern our mutual mind—

The Literature of Man—

What interested Scholars—most—

What Competitions ran—

When Plato—was a Certainty—

And Sophocles—a Man—

When Sappho—was a living Girl—

And Beatrice wore

The Gown that Dante—deified—

Facts Centuries before

He traverses—familiar—

As One should come to Town—

And tell you all your Dreams—were true—

He lived—where Dreams were born—

His presence is Enchantment—

You beg him not to go—

Old Volume shake their Vellum Heads

And tantalize—just so—

Emily Dickinson





A Prison gets to be a friend


A Prison gets to be a friend&mdash; Between its Ponderous face

And Ours&mdash;a Kinsmanship express&mdash; And in its narrow Eyes&mdash;

We come to look with gratitude

For the appointed Beam

It deal us&mdash;stated as our food&mdash; And hungered for&mdash;the same&mdash; We learn to know the Planks&mdash; That answer to Our feet&mdash;

So miserable a sound&mdash;at first&mdash; Nor ever now&mdash;so sweet&mdash; As plashing in the Pools&mdash;

When Memory was a Boy&mdash;

But a Demurer Circuit&mdash;

A Geometric Joy&mdash;

The Posture of the Key

That interrupt the Day

To Our Endeavor&mdash;Not so real

The Check of Liberty&mdash;

As this Phantasm Steel&mdash;

Whose features&mdash;Day and Night&mdash; Are present to us&mdash;as Our Own&mdash; And as escapeless&mdash;quite&mdash; The narrow Round&mdash;the Stint&mdash; The slow exchange of Hope&mdash;

For something passiver&mdash;Content Too steep for lookinp up&mdash;

The Liberty we knew

Avoided&mdash;like a Dream&mdash; Too wide for any Night but Heaven&mdash; If That&mdash;indeed&mdash;redeem&mdash; Emily Dickinson





A Route of Evanescence

A Route of Evanescence

With a revolving Wheel--

A Resonance of Emerald--

A Rush of Cochineal--

And every Blossom on the Bush

Adjusts its tumbled Head--

The mail from Tunis, probably,

An easy Morning's Ride--

Emily Dickinson






A science&mdash;so the Savants say,

"Comparative Anatomy"&mdash; By which a single bone&mdash;

Is made a secret to unfold

Of some rare tenant of the mold,

Else perished in the stone&mdash;

So to the eye prospective led,

This meekest flower of the mead

Upon a winter's day,

Stands representative in gold

Of Rose and Lily, manifold,

And countless Butterfly!

Emily Dickinson

A Secret told


A Secret told&mdash;

Ceases to be a Secret&mdash;then&mdash; A Secret&mdash;kept&mdash;

That&mdash;can appal but One&mdash; Better of it&mdash;continual be afraid&mdash; Than it&mdash;

A sepal, petal, and a thorn


A sepal, petal, and a thorn

Upon a common summer's morn&mdash; A flask of Dew&mdash;A Bee or two&mdash; A Breeze&mdash;a caper in the trees&mdash; And I'm a Rose!

A Shade upon the mind there passes


A Shade upon the mind there passes

As when on Noon

A Cloud the mighty Sun encloses

Remembering

That some there be too numb to notice

Oh God

Why give if Thou must take away

The Loved?

Emily Dickinson





A shady friend for torrid days

A shady friend for torrid days

Is easier to find

Than one of higher temperature

For frigid hour of mind.

The vane a little to the east

Scares muslin souls away;

If broadcloth breasts are firmer

Than those of organdy,

Who is to blame? The weaver?

Ah! the bewildering thread!

The tapestries of paradise!

So notelessly are made!

Emily Dickinson

A single Screw of Flesh


Is all that pins the Soul

That stands for Deity, to Mine,

Upon my side the Veil&mdash;

Once witnessed of the Gauze&mdash; Its name is put away

As far from mine, as if no plight

Had printed yesterday,

In tender&mdash;solemn Alphabet,

My eyes just turned to see,

When it was smuggled by my sight

Into Eternity&mdash;

More Hands&mdash;to hold&mdash;These are but Two&mdash; One more new-mailed Nerve

Just granted, for the Peril's sake&mdash; Some striding&mdash;Giant&mdash;Love&mdash; So greater than the Gods can show,

They slink before the Clay,

That not for all their Heaven can boast Will let its Keepsake&mdash;go

Emily Dickinson





A slash of Blue


A slash of Blue&mdash;

A sweep of Gray&mdash;

Some scarlet patches on the way,

Compose an Evening Sky&mdash;

A little purple&mdash;slipped between&mdash; Some Ruby Trousers hurried on&mdash; A Wave of Gold&mdash;

A Bank of Day&mdash;

This just makes out the Morning Sky.

Emily Dickinson





A Solemn thing within the Soul


A Solemn thing within the Soul

To feel itself get ripe&mdash;

And golden hang&mdash;while farther up&mdash; The Maker's Ladders stop&mdash;

And in the Orchard far below&mdash; You hear a Being&mdash;drop&mdash; A Wonderful&mdash;to feel the Sun

Still toiling at the Cheek

You thought was finished&mdash;

Cool of eye, and critical of Work&mdash; He shifts the stem&mdash;a little&mdash; To give your Core&mdash;a look&mdash; But solemnest&mdash;to know

Your chance in Harvest moves

A little nearer&mdash;Every Sun

The Single&mdash;to some lives.

Emily Dickinson






A solemn thing&mdash;it was&mdash;I said&mdash; A woman&mdash;white&mdash;to be&mdash; And wear&mdash;if God should count me fit&mdash; Her blameless mystery&mdash;

A hallowed thing&mdash;to drop a life Into the purple well&mdash;

Too plummetless&mdash;that it return&mdash; Eternity&mdash;until&mdash;

I pondered how the bliss would look&mdash; And would it feel as big&mdash;

When I could take it in my hand&mdash; As hovering&mdash;seen&mdash;through fog&mdash; And then&mdash;the size of this "small" life&mdash; The Sages&mdash;call it small&mdash; Swelled&mdash;like Horizons&mdash;in my vest&mdash; And I sneered&mdash;softly&mdash;"small"!

Emily Dickinson





A solemn thing—it was—I said


A solemn thing—it was—I said—

A woman—white—to be—

And wear—if God should count me fit—

Her blameless mystery—

A hallowed thing—to drop a life

Into the purple well—

Too plummetless—that it return—

Eternity—until—

I pondered how the bliss would look—

And would it feel as big—

When I could take it in my hand—

As hovering—seen—through fog—

And then—the size of this "small" life—

The Sages—call it small—

Swelled—like Horizons—in my vest—

And I sneered—softly—"small"!

Emily Dickinson





A something in a summer's Day


A something in a summer's Day

As slow her flambeaux burn away

Which solemnizes me.

A something in a summer's noon&mdash; A depth&mdash;an Azure&mdash;a perfume&mdash; Transcending ecstasy.

And still within a summer's night

A something so transporting bright

I clap my hands to see&mdash;

Then veil my too inspecting face

Lets such a subtle&mdash;shimmering grace Flutter too far for me&mdash;

The wizard fingers never rest&mdash; The purple brook within the breast

Still chafes it narrow bed&mdash;

Still rears the East her amber Flag&mdash; Guides still the sun along the Crag

His Caravan of Red&mdash;

So looking on&mdash;the night&mdash;the morn Conclude the wonder gay&mdash;

And I meet, coming thro' the dews

Another summer's Day!

Emily Dickinson

A still—Volcano—Life


A still—Volcano—Life—

That flickered in the night—

When it was dark enough to do

Without erasing sight—

A quiet—Earthquake Style—

Too subtle to suspect

By natures this side Naples—

The North cannot detect

The Solemn—Torrid—Symbol—

The lips that never lie—

Whose hissing Corals part—and shut—

And Cities—ooze away—

Emily Dickinson





A Thought went up my mind today


A Thought went up my mind today&mdash; That I have had before&mdash;

But did not finish&mdash;some way back&mdash; I could not fix the Year&mdash;

Nor where it went&mdash;nor why it came The second time to me&mdash;

Nor definitely, what it was&mdash; Have I the Art to say&mdash;

But somewhere&mdash;in my Soul&mdash;I know&mdash; I've met the Thing before&mdash;

It just reminded me&mdash;'twas all&mdash; And came my way no more&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





A thought went up my mind to-day

A thought went up my mind to-day

That I have had before,

But did not finish,--some way back,

I could not fix the year,

Nor where it went, nor why it came

The second time to me,

Nor definitely what it was,

Have I the art to say.

But somewhere in my soul, I know

I've met the thing before;

It just reminded me--'t was all--

And came my way no more.

Emily Dickinson





A throe upon the features


A throe upon the features&mdash;

A hurry in the breath&mdash;

An ecstasy of parting

Denominated "Death"&mdash; An anguish at the mention

Which when to patience grown,

I've known permission given

To rejoin its own.

Emily Dickinson





A toad can die of light!

A toad can die of light!

Death is the common right

Of toads and men,--

Of earl and midge

The privilege.

Why swagger then?

The gnat's supremacy

Is large as thine.

Emily Dickinson

Of Earl and Midge

Naked of Flask&mdash;Naked of Cask&mdash; Bare Rhine&mdash;

Which Ruby's mine?

A Tongue&mdash;to tell Him I am true!


A Tongue&mdash;to tell Him I am true!

Its fee&mdash;to be of Gold&mdash; Had Nature&mdash;in Her monstrous House A single Ragged Child&mdash;

To earn a Mine&mdash;would run

That Interdicted Way,

And tell Him&mdash;Charge thee speak it plain&mdash; That so far&mdash;Truth is True?

And answer What I do&mdash;

Beginning with the Day

That Night&mdash;begun&mdash;

Nay&mdash;Midnight&mdash;'twas&mdash; Since Midnight&mdash;happened&mdash;say&mdash; If once more&mdash;Pardon&mdash;Boy&mdash; The Magnitude thou may

Enlarge my Message&mdash;If too vast Another Lad&mdash;help thee&mdash; Thy Pay&mdash;in Diamonds&mdash;be&mdash; And His&mdash;in solid Gold&mdash; Say Rubies&mdash;if He hesitate&mdash; My Message&mdash;must be told&mdash; Say&mdash;last I said&mdash;was This&mdash; That when the Hills&mdash;come down&mdash; And hold no higher than the Plain&mdash; My Bond&mdash;have just begun&mdash; And when the Heavens&mdash;disband&mdash; And Deity conclude&mdash;

A Tongue—to tell Him I am true!


A Tongue—to tell Him I am true!

Its fee—to be of Gold—

Had Nature—in Her monstrous House

A single Ragged Child—

To earn a Mine—would run

That Interdicted Way,

And tell Him—Charge thee speak it plain—

That so far—Truth is True?

And answer What I do—

Beginning with the Day

That Night—begun—

Nay—Midnight—'twas—

Since Midnight—happened—say—

If once more—Pardon—Boy—

The Magnitude thou may

Enlarge my Message—If too vast

Another Lad—help thee—

Thy Pay—in Diamonds—be—

And His—in solid Gold—

Say Rubies—if He hesitate—

My Message—must be told—

Say—last I said—was This—

That when the Hills—come down—

And hold no higher than the Plain—

My Bond—have just begun—

And when the Heavens—disband—

And Deity conclude—

Then—look for me. Be sure you say—

Least Figure—on the Road—

Emily Dickinson





A Tooth upon Our Peace


A Tooth upon Our Peace

The Peace cannot deface&mdash;

Then Wherefore be the Tooth?

To vitalize the Grace&mdash;

The Heaven hath a Hell&mdash;

Itself to signalize&mdash;

And every sign before the Place

Is Gilt with Sacrifice&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





A transport one cannot contain


A transport one cannot contain

May yet a transport be&mdash;

Though God forbid it lift the lid&mdash; Unto its Ecstasy!

A Diagram&mdash;of Rapture!

A sixpence at a Show&mdash;

With Holy Ghosts in Cages!

The Universe would go!

Emily Dickinson





A Visitor in Marl


A Visitor in Marl&mdash;

Who influences Flowers&mdash;

Till they are orderly as Busts&mdash; And Elegant&mdash;as Glass&mdash; Who visits in the Night&mdash;

And just before the Sun&mdash;

Concludes his glistening interview&mdash; Caresses&mdash;and is gone&mdash; But whom his fingers touched&mdash; And where his feet have run&mdash; And whatsoever Mouth be kissed&mdash; Is as it had not been&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





A Weight with Needles on the pounds


A Weight with Needles on the pounds&mdash; To push, and pierce, besides&mdash; That if the Flesh resist the Heft&mdash; The puncture&mdash;coolly tries&mdash; That not a pore be overlooked

Of all this Compound Frame&mdash;

As manifold for Anguish&mdash;

As Species&mdash;be&mdash;for name&mdash; Emily Dickinson






A Wife&mdash;at daybreak I shall be&mdash; Sunrise&mdash;Hast thou a Flag for me?

At Midnight, I am but a Maid,

How short it takes to make a Bride&mdash; Then&mdash;Midnight, I have passed from thee Unto the East, and Victory&mdash;

Midnight&mdash;Good Night! I hear them call, The Angels bustle in the Hall&mdash; Softly my Future climbs the Stair,

I fumble at my Childhood's prayer

So soon to be a Child no more&mdash; Eternity, I'm coming&mdash;Sire,

Savior&mdash;I've seen the face&mdash;before!

A Wounded Deer&mdash;leaps highest&mdash; I've heard the Hunter tell&mdash;

'Tis but the Ecstasy of death&mdash; And then the Brake is still!

The Smitten Rock that gushes!

The trampled Steel that springs!

A Cheek is always redder

Just where the Hectic stings!

Mirth is the Mail of Anguish

In which it Cautious Arm,

Lest anybody spy the blood

And "you're hurt" exclaim!

Emily Dickinson

Abraham to Kill Him

Abraham to kill him

Was distinctly told—

Isaac was an Urchin—

Abraham was old—

Not a hesitation—

Abraham complied—

Flattered by Obeisance

Tyranny demurred—

Isaac—to his children

Lived to tell the tale—

Moral—with a mastiff

Manners may prevail.

Emily Dickinson

Deeper than without&mdash;

Adrift! A little boat adrift!


Adrift! A little boat adrift!

And night is coming down!

Will no one guide a little boat

Unto the nearest town?

So Sailors say&mdash;on yesterday&mdash; Just as the dusk was brown

One little boat gave up its strife

And gurgled down and down.

So angels say&mdash;on yesterday&mdash; Just as the dawn was red

One little boat&mdash;o'erspent with gales&mdash; Retrimmed its masts&mdash;redecked its sails&mdash; And shot&mdash;exultant on!

Emily Dickinson





Afraid! Of whom am I afraid?


Afraid! Of whom am I afraid?

Not Death&mdash;for who is He?

The Porter of my Father's Lodge

As much abasheth me!

Of Life? 'Twere odd I fear [a] thing

That comprehendeth me

In one or two existences&mdash;

As Deity decree&mdash;

Of Resurrection? Is the East

Afraid to trust the Morn

With her fastidious forehead?

As soon impeach my Crown!

Emily Dickinson





After a hundred years

After a hundred years

Nobody knows the place,--

Agony, that enacted there,

Motionless as peace.

Weeds triumphant ranged,

Strangers strolled and spelled

At the lone orthography

Of the elder dead.

Winds of summer fields

Recollect the way,--

Instinct picking up the key

Dropped by memory.

Emily Dickinson





After Great Pain, A Formal Feeling Comes After great pain, a formal feeling comes--

The Nerves sit ceremonious, like Toombs--

The stiff Heart questions was it He, that bore, And Yesterday, or Centuries before?

The Feet, mechanical, go round--

Of Ground, or Air, or Ought--

A Wooden way

Regardless grown,

A Quartz contentment, like a stone--

This is the Hour of Lead--

Remembered, if outlived,

As Freezing persons recollect the Snow--

First--Chill--then Stupor--then the letting go--

Emily Dickinson

Again&mdash;his voice is at the door&mdash; I feel the old Degree&mdash;

I hear him ask the servant

For such an one&mdash;as me&mdash; I take a flower&mdash;as I go&mdash; My face to justify&mdash;

He never saw me&mdash;in this life&mdash; I might surprise his eye!

I cross the Hall with mingled steps&mdash; I&mdash;silent&mdash;pass the door&mdash; I look on all this world contains&mdash; Just his face&mdash;nothing more!

We talk in careless&mdash;and it toss&mdash; A kind of plummet strain&mdash;

Each&mdash;sounding&mdash;shyly&mdash; Just&mdash;how&mdash;deep&mdash; The other's one&mdash;had been&mdash; We walk&mdash;I leave my Dog&mdash;at home&mdash; A tender&mdash;thoughtful Moon&mdash; Goes with us&mdash;just a little way&mdash; And&mdash;then&mdash;we are alone&mdash; Alone&mdash;if Angels are "alone"&mdash; First time they try the sky!

Alone&mdash;if those "veiled faces"&mdash;be&mdash; We cannot count&mdash;on High!

I'd give&mdash;to live that hour&mdash;again&mdash; The purple&mdash;in my Vein&mdash; But He must count the drops&mdash;himself&mdash; My price for every stain!

Emily Dickinson





Again—his voice is at the door


Again—his voice is at the door—

I feel the old Degree—

I hear him ask the servant

For such an one—as me—

I take a flower—as I go—

My face to justify—

He never saw me—in this life—

I might surprise his eye!

I cross the Hall with mingled steps—

I—silent—pass the door—

I look on all this world contains—

Just his face—nothing more!

We talk in careless—and it toss—

A kind of plummet strain—

Each—sounding—shyly—

Just—how—deep—

The other's one—had been—

We walk—I leave my Dog—at home—

A tender—thoughtful Moon—

Goes with us—just a little way—

And—then—we are alone—

Alone—if Angels are "alone"—

First time they try the sky!

Alone—if those "veiled faces"—be—

We cannot count—on High!

I'd give—to live that hour—again—

The purple—in my Vein—

But He must count the drops—himself—

My price for every stain!

Emily Dickinson





Ah, Moon&mdash;and Star!


Ah, Moon&mdash;and Star!

You are very far&mdash;

But were no one

Farther than you&mdash;

Do you think I'd stop

For a Firmament&mdash;

Or a Cubit&mdash;or so?

I could borrow a Bonnet

Of the Lark&mdash;

And a Chamois' Silver Boot&mdash;

And a stirrup of an Antelope&mdash; And be with you&mdash;Tonight!

But, Moon, and Star,

Though you're very far&mdash;

There is one&mdash;farther than you&mdash; He&mdash;is more than a firmament&mdash;from Me&mdash; So I can never go!

Emily Dickinson

Ah, Necromancy Sweet!


Ah, Necromancy Sweet!

Ah, Wizard erudite!

Teach me the skill,

That I instil the pain

Surgeons assuage in vain,

Nor Herb of all the plain

Can Heal!

Ah, Teneriffe!


Ah, Teneriffe!

Retreating Mountain!

Purples of Ages&mdash;pause for you&mdash; Sunset&mdash;reviews her Sapphire Regiment&mdash; Day&mdash;drops you her Red Adieu!

Still&mdash;Clad in your Mail of ices&mdash; Thigh of Granite&mdash;and thew&mdash;of Steel&mdash; Heedless&mdash;alike&mdash;of pomp&mdash;or parting Ah, Teneriffe!

I'm kneeling&mdash;still&mdash; Emily Dickinson





All but Death, can be Adjusted


All but Death, can be Adjusted&mdash; Dynasties repaired&mdash;

Systems&mdash;settled in their Sockets&mdash; Citadels&mdash;dissolved&mdash; Wastes of Lives&mdash;resown with Colors By Succeeding Springs&mdash;

Death&mdash;unto itself&mdash;Exception&mdash; Is exempt from Change&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





All Circumstances are the Frame


All Circumstances are the Frame

In which His Face is set&mdash;

All Latitudes exist for His

Sufficient Continent&mdash;

The Light His Action, and the Dark

The Leisure of His Will&mdash;

In Him Existence serve or set

A Force illegible.

Emily Dickinson





All forgot for recollecting


All forgot for recollecting

Just a paltry One&mdash;

All forsook, for just a Stranger's

New Accompanying&mdash;

Grace of Wealth, and Grace of Station

Less accounted than

An unknown Esteem possessing&mdash; Estimate&mdash;Who can&mdash;

Home effaced&mdash;Her faces dwindled&mdash; Nature&mdash;altered small&mdash; Sun&mdash;if shone&mdash;or Storm&mdash;if shattered&mdash; Overlooked I all&mdash;

Dropped&mdash;my fate&mdash;a timid Pebble&mdash; In thy bolder Sea&mdash;

Prove&mdash;me&mdash;Sweet&mdash;if I regret it&mdash; Prove Myself&mdash;of Thee&mdash; Emily Dickinson





All I may, if small


All I may, if small,

Do it not display

Larger for the Totalness&mdash;

'Tis Economy

To bestow a World

And withhold a Star&mdash;

Utmost, is Munificence&mdash;

Less, tho' larger, poor.

Emily Dickinson





All overgrown by cunning moss


All overgrown by cunning moss,

All interspersed with weed,

The little cage of "Currer Bell"

In quiet "Haworth" laid.

Gathered from many wanderings&mdash; Gethsemane can tell

Thro' what transporting anguish

She reached the Asphodel!

Soft falls the sounds of Eden

Upon her puzzled ear&mdash;

Oh what an afternoon for Heaven,

When "Bronte" entered there!

Emily Dickinson





All the letters I can write


All the letters I can write

Are not fair as this&mdash;

Syllables of Velvet&mdash;

Sentences of Plush,

Depths of Ruby, undrained,

Hid, Lip, for Thee&mdash;

Play it were a Humming Bird&mdash; And just sipped&mdash;me&mdash; Emily Dickinson





All these my banners be


All these my banners be.

I sow my pageantry

In May&mdash;

It rises train by train&mdash;

Then sleeps in state again&mdash;

My chancel&mdash;all the plain

Today.

To lose&mdash;if one can find again&mdash; To miss&mdash;if one shall meet&mdash; The Burglar cannot rob&mdash;then&mdash; The Broker cannot cheat.

So build the hillocks gaily

Thou little spade of mine

Leaving nooks for Daisy

And for Columbine&mdash;

You and I the secret

Of the Crocus know&mdash;

Let us chant it softly&mdash;

"There is no more snow!"

To him who keeps an Orchis' heart&mdash; The swamps are pink with June.

Emily Dickinson





Alone, I cannot be


Alone, I cannot be&mdash;

For Hosts&mdash;do visit me&mdash; Recordless Company&mdash;

Who baffle Key&mdash;

They have no Robes, nor Names&mdash; No Almanacs&mdash;nor Climes&mdash; But general Homes

Like Gnomes&mdash;

Their Coming, may be known

By Couriers within&mdash;

Their going&mdash;is not&mdash; For they've never gone&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Alter! When the Hills do


Alter! When the Hills do&mdash;

Falter! When the Sun

Question if His Glory

Be the Perfect One&mdash;

Surfeit! When the Daffodil

Doth of the Dew&mdash;

Even as Herself&mdash;Sir&mdash; I will&mdash;of You&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Although I put away his life


Although I put away his life&mdash; An Ornament too grand

For Forehead low as mine, to wear,

This might have been the Hand

That sowed the flower, he preferred&mdash; Or smoothed a homely pain,

Or pushed the pebble from his path&mdash; Or played his chosen tune&mdash;

On Lute the least&mdash;the latest&mdash; But just his Ear could know

That whatsoe'er delighted it,

I never would let go&mdash;

The foot to bear his errand&mdash; A little Boot I know&mdash;

Would leap abroad like Antelope&mdash; With just the grant to do&mdash;

His weariest Commandment&mdash;

A sweeter to obey,

Than "Hide and Seek"&mdash; Or skip to Flutes&mdash;

Or all Day, chase the Bee&mdash;

Your Servant, Sir, will weary&mdash; The Surgeon, will not come&mdash;

The World, will have its own&mdash;to do&mdash; The Dust, will vex your Fame&mdash; The Cold will force your tightest door Some February Day,

But say my apron bring the sticks

To make your Cottage gay&mdash;

That I may take that promise

To Paradise, with me&mdash;

To teach the Angels, avarice,

You, Sir, taught first&mdash;to me.

Emily Dickinson





Always Mine!


Always Mine!

No more Vacation!

Term of Light this Day begun!

Failless as the fair rotation

Of the Seasons and the Sun.

Old the Grace, but new the Subjects&mdash; Old, indeed, the East,

Yet upon His Purple Programme

Every Dawn, is first.

Emily Dickinson





Ambition cannot find him


Ambition cannot find him.

Affection doesn't know

How many leagues of nowhere

Lie between them now.

Yesterday, undistinguished!

Eminent Today

For our mutual hone, Immortality!

Emily Dickinson





Ample make this Bed


Ample make this Bed&mdash;

Excellent and Fair.

Be its Mattress straight&mdash;

Be its Pillow round&mdash;

Let no Sunrise' yellow noise

Interrupt this Ground&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

An altered look about the hills


An altered look about the hills&mdash; A Tyrian light the village fills&mdash; A wider sunrise in the morn&mdash; A deeper twilight on the lawn&mdash; A print of a vermillion foot&mdash; A purple finger on the slope&mdash; A flippant fly upon the pane&mdash; A spider at his trade again&mdash; An added strut in Chanticleer&mdash; A flower expected everywhere&mdash; An axe shrill singing in the woods&mdash; Fern odors on untravelled roads&mdash; All this and more I cannot tell&mdash; A furtive look you know as well&mdash; And Nicodemus' Mystery

Receives its annual reply!

Emily Dickinson





An awful Tempest mashed the air


An awful Tempest mashed the air&mdash; The clouds were gaunt, and few&mdash; A Black&mdash;as of a Spectre's Cloak Hid Heaven and Earth from view.

The creatures chuckled on the Roofs&mdash; And whistled in the air&mdash;

And shook their fists&mdash;

And gnashed their teeth&mdash;

And swung their frenzied hair.

The morning lit&mdash;the Birds arose&mdash; The Monster's faded eyes

Turned slowly to his native coast&mdash; And peace&mdash;was Paradise!

Emily Dickinson





An English Breeze

UP with the sun, the breeze arose,

Across the talking corn she goes,

And smooth she rustles far and wide

Through all the voiceful countryside.

Through all the land her tale she tells; She spins, she tosses, she compels

The kites, the clouds, the windmill sails And all the trees in all the dales.

God calls us, and the day prepares

With nimble, gay and gracious airs:

And from Penzance to Maidenhead

The roads last night He watered.

God calls us from inglorious ease,

Forth and to travel with the breeze

While, swift and singing, smooth and strong She gallops by the fields along.

Emily Dickinson

An ignorance a Sunset


An ignorance a Sunset

Exhilirate&mdash;Debase&mdash; Omnipotence' inspection

Of Our inferior face&mdash;

And when the solemn features

Confirm&mdash;in Victory&mdash; We start&mdash;as if detected

In Immortality&mdash;

Angels, in the early morning


Angels, in the early morning

May be seen the Dews among,

Stooping&mdash;plucking&mdash;smiling&mdash;flying&mdash; Do the Buds to them belong?

Angels, when the sun is hottest

May be seen the sands among,

Stooping&mdash;plucking&mdash;sighing&mdash;flying&mdash; Parched the flowers they bear along.

Answer July


Answer July&mdash;

Where is the Bee&mdash;

Where is the Blush&mdash;

Where is the Hay?

Ah, said July&mdash;

Where is the Seed&mdash;

Where is the Bud&mdash;

Where is the May&mdash;

Answer Thee&mdash;Me&mdash;

Nay&mdash;said the May&mdash;

Show me the Snow&mdash;

Show me the Bells&mdash;

Show me the Jay!

Quibbled the Jay&mdash;

Where be the Maize&mdash;

Where be the Haze&mdash;

Where be the Bur?

Here&mdash;said the Year&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Apology for Her

Be rendered by the Bee&mdash;

Herself, without a Parliament

Apology for Me.

Apparently with no Surprise

Apparently with no surprise,

To any happy flower,

The frost beheads it at its play,

In accidental power.

The blond assassin passes on.

The sun proceeds unmoved,

To measure off another day,

For an approving God.

Emily Dickinson





Arcturus

"Arcturus" is his other name—

I'd rather call him "Star."

It's very mean of Science

To go and interfere!

I slew a worm the other day—

A "Savant" passing by

Murmured "Resurgam"—"Centipede"!

"Oh Lord—how frail are we"!

I pull a flower from the woods—

A monster with a glass

Computes the stamens in a breath—

And has her in a "class"!

Whereas I took the Butterfly

Aforetime in my hat—

He sits erect in "Cabinets"—

The Clover bells forgot.

What once was "Heaven"

Is "Zenith" now—

Where I proposed to go

When Time's brief masquerade was done

Is mapped and charted too.

What if the poles should frisk about

And stand upon their heads!

I hope I'm ready for "the worst"—

Whatever prank betides!

Perhaps the "Kingdom of Heaven's" changed—

I hope the "Children" there Won't be "new fashioned" when I come—

And laugh at me—and stare—

I hope the Father in the skies

Will lift his little girl—

Old fashioned—naught—everything—

Over the stile of "Pearl."

Emily Dickinson





Artists wrestled here!


Artists wrestled here!

Lo, a tint Cashmere!

Lo, a Rose!

Student of the Year!

For the easel here

Say Repose!

Emily Dickinson





As by the dead we love to sit


As by the dead we love to sit,

Become so wondrous dear&mdash;

As for the lost we grapple

Tho' all the rest are here&mdash;

In broken mathematics

We estimate our prize

Vast&mdash;in its fading ration

To our penurious eyes!

Emily Dickinson





As Children bid the Guest


As Children bid the Guest "Good Night"

And then reluctant turn—

My flowers raise their pretty lips—

Then put their nightgowns on.

As children caper when they wake

Merry that it is Morn—

My flowers from a hundred cribs

Will peep, and prance again.

Emily Dickinson

As far from pity, as complaint


As far from pity, as complaint&mdash; As cool to speech&mdash;as stone&mdash; As numb to Revelation

As if my Trade were Bone&mdash;

As far from time&mdash;as History&mdash; As near yourself&mdash;Today&mdash; As Children, to the Rainbow's scarf&mdash; Or Sunset's Yellow play

To eyelids in the Sepulchre&mdash; How dumb the Dancer lies&mdash;

While Color's Revelations break&mdash; And blaze&mdash;the Butterflies!

As Frost is best conceived


As Frost is best conceived

By force of its Result&mdash;

Affliction is inferred

By subsequent effect&mdash;

If when the sun reveal,

The Garden keep the Gash&mdash;

If as the Days resume

The wilted countenance

Cannot correct the crease

Or counteract the stain&mdash;

Presumption is Vitality

Was somewhere put in twain.

Emily Dickinson





As if I asked a common Alms


As if I asked a common Alms,

And in my wondering hand

A Stranger pressed a Kingdom,

And I, bewildered, stand&mdash;

As if I asked the Orient

Had it for me a Morn&mdash;

And it should lift its purple Dikes,

And shatter me with Dawn!

Emily Dickinson





As if some little Arctic flower


As if some little Arctic flower

Upon the polar hem&mdash;

Went wandering down the Latitudes

Until it puzzled came

To continents of summer&mdash;

To firmaments of sun&mdash;

To strange, bright crowds of flowers&mdash; And birds, of foreign tongue!

I say, As if this little flower

To Eden, wandered in&mdash;

What then? Why nothing,

Only, your inference therefrom!

Emily Dickinson





As if the Sea should part


As if the Sea should part

And show a further Sea&mdash;

And that&mdash;a further&mdash;and the Three But a presumption be&mdash;

Of Periods of Seas&mdash;

Unvisited of Shores&mdash;

Themselves the Verge of Seas to be&mdash; Eternity&mdash;is Those&mdash; Emily Dickinson





As imperceptibly as Grief


As imperceptibly as Grief

The Summer lapsed away&mdash;

Too imperceptible at last

To seem like Perfidy&mdash;

A Quietness distilled

As Twilight long begun,

Or Nature spending with herself

Sequestered Afternoon&mdash;

The Dusk drew earlier in&mdash;

The Morning foreign shone&mdash;

A courteous, yet harrowing Grace,

As Guest, that would be gone&mdash; And thus, without a Wing

Or service of a Keel

Our Summer made her light escape

Into the Beautiful.

Emily Dickinson





As One does Sickness over


As One does Sickness over

In convalescent Mind,

His scrutiny of Chances

By blessed Health obscured&mdash;

As One rewalks a Precipice

And whittles at the Twig

That held Him from Perdition

Sown sidewise in the Crag

A Custom of the Soul

Far after suffering

Identity to question

For evidence't has been&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





As plan for Noon and plan for Night


As plan for Noon and plan for Night

So differ Life and Death

In positive Prospective&mdash;

The Foot upon the Earth

At Distance, and Achievement, strains, The Foot upon the Grave

Makes effort at conclusion

Assisted faint of Love.

Emily Dickinson





As Sleigh Bells seem in summer


As Sleigh Bells seem in summer

Or Bees, at Christmas show&mdash;

So fairy&mdash;so fictitious

The individuals do

Repealed from observation&mdash;

A Party that we knew&mdash;

More distant in an instant

Than Dawn in Timbuctoo.

Emily Dickinson






As the Starved Maelstrom laps the Navies As the Vulture teased

Forces the Broods in lonely Valleys

As the Tiger eased

By but a Crumb of Blood, fasts Scarlet Till he meet a Man

Dainty adorned with Veins and Tissues

And partakes&mdash;his Tongue

Cooled by the Morsel for a moment

Grows a fiercer thing

Till he esteem his Dates and Cocoa

A Nutrition mean

I, of a finer Famine

Deem my Supper dry

For but a Berry of Domingo

And a Torrid Eye.

Emily Dickinson





As Watchers hang upon the East


As Watchers hang upon the East,

As Beggars revel at a feast

By savory Fancy spread&mdash;

As brooks in deserts babble sweet

On ear too far for the delight,

Heaven beguiles the tired.

As that same watcher, when the East

Opens the lid of Amethyst

And lets the morning go&mdash;

That Beggar, when an honored Guest,

Those thirsty lips to flagons pressed, Heaven to us, if true.

Emily Dickinson

Between our feet, and Day!

Awake ye muses nine, sing me a strain divine, Unwind the solemn twine, and tie my Valentine!

Oh the Earth was made for lovers, for damsel, and hopeless swain, For sighing, and gentle whispering, and unity made of twain.

All things do go a courting, in earth, or sea, or air, God hath made nothing single but thee in His world so fair!

The bride, and then the bridegroom, the two, and then the one, Adam, and Eve, his consort, the moon, and then the sun; The life doth prove the precept, who obey shall happy be, Who will not serve the sovereign, be hanged on fatal tree.

The high do seek the lowly, the great do seek the small, None cannot find who seeketh, on this terrestrial ball; The bee doth court the flower, the flower his suit receives, And they make merry wedding, whose guests are hundred leaves; The wind doth woo the branches, the branches they are won, And the father fond demandeth the maiden for his son.

The storm doth walk the seashore humming a mournful tune, The wave with eye so pensive, looketh to see the moon, Their spirits meet together, they make their solemn vows, No more he singeth mournful, her sadness she doth lose.

The worm doth woo the mortal, death claims a living bride, Night unto day is married, morn unto eventide; Earth is a merry damsel, and heaven a knight so true, And Earth is quite coquettish, and beseemeth in vain to sue.

Now to the application, to the reading of the roll, To bringing thee to justice, and marshalling thy soul: Thou art a human solo, a being cold, and lone, Wilt have no kind companion, thou reap'st what thou hast sown.

Hast never silent hours, and minutes all too long, And a deal of sad reflection, and wailing instead of song?

There's Sarah, and Eliza, and Emeline so fair, And Harriet, and Susan, and she with curling hair!

Thine eyes are sadly blinded, but yet thou mayest see Six true, and comely maidens sitting upon the tree; Approach that tree with caution, then up it boldly climb, And seize the one thou lovest, nor care for space, or time!

Then bear her to the greenwood, and build for her a bower, And give her what she asketh, jewel, or bird, or flower&mdash; And bring the fife, and trumpet, and beat upon the drum&mdash; And bid the world Goodmorrow, and go to glory home!

Emily Dickinson





Away from Home are some and I—


Away from Home are some and I—

An Emigrant to be

In a Metropolis of Homes

Is easy, possibly—

The Habit of a Foreign Sky

We—difficult—acquire

As Children, who remain in Face

The more their Feet retire.

Emily Dickinson

Banish Air from Air—


Banish Air from Air—

Divide Light if you dare—

They'll meet

While Cubes in a Drop

Or Pellets of Shape

Fit

Films cannot annul

Odors return whole

Force Flame

And with a Blonde push

Over your impotence

Flits Steam.

Emily Dickinson

And with a Blonde push

Over your impotence

Flits Steam.

Emily Dickinson

Because I could not stop for Death

Because I could not stop for Death,

He kindly stopped for me;

The carriage held but just ourselves

And Immortality.

We slowly drove, he knew no haste,

And I had put away

My labor, and my leisure too,

For his civility.

We passed the school where children played, Their lessons scarcely done;

We passed the fields of grazing grain, We passed the setting sun.

We paused before a house that seemed

A swelling of the ground;

The roof was scarcely visible,

The cornice but a mound.

Since then 't is centuries; but each

Feels shorter than the day

I first surmised the horses' heads

Were toward eternity.

Emily Dickinson






He kindly stopped for me--

The Carriage held but just Ourselves--

And Immortality.

We slowly drove--He knew no haste

And I had put away

My labor and my leisure too,

For His Civility--

We passed the School, where Children strove At Recess--in the Ring--

We passed the Fields of Gazing Grain--

We passed the Setting Sun--

Or rather--He passed us--

The Dews drew quivering and chill--

For only Gossamer, my Gown--

My Tippet--only Tulle--

We paused before a House that seemed

A Swelling of the Ground--

The Roof was scarcely visible--

The Cornice--in the Ground--

Since then--'tis Centuries--and yet

Feels shorter than the Day

I first surmised the Horses' Heads

Were toward Eternity--

Emily Dickinson

Because the Bee may blameless hum


Because the Bee may blameless hum

For Thee a Bee do I become

List even unto Me.

Because the Flowers unafraid

May lift a look on thine, a Maid

Alway a Flower would be.

Nor Robins, Robins need not hide

When Thou upon their Crypts intrude

So Wings bestow on Me

Or Petals, or a Dower of Buzz

That Bee to ride, or Flower of Furze

I that way worship Thee.

Emily Dickinson





Beclouded

The sky is low, the clouds are mean,

A travelling flake of snow

Across a barn or through a rut

Debates if it will go.

A narrow wind complains all day

How some one treated him;

Nature, like us, is sometimes caught

Without her diadem.

Emily Dickinson





Bee! I'm expecting you!


Bee! I'm expecting you!

Was saying Yesterday

To Somebody you know

That you were due&mdash;

The Frogs got Home last Week&mdash; Are settled, and at work&mdash;

Birds, mostly back&mdash;

The Clover warm and thick&mdash;

You'll get my Letter by

The seventeenth; Reply

Or better, be with me&mdash;

Yours, Fly.

Before I got my eye put out


Before I got my eye put out

I liked as well to see&mdash;

As other Creatures, that have Eyes

And know no other way&mdash;

But were it told to me&mdash;Today&mdash; That I might have the sky

For mine&mdash;I tell you that my Heart Would split, for size of me&mdash; The Meadows&mdash;mine&mdash;

The Mountains&mdash;mine&mdash; All Forests&mdash;Stintless Stars&mdash; As much of Noon as I could take

Between my finite eyes&mdash;

The Motions of the Dipping Birds&mdash; The Morning's Amber Road&mdash;

For mine&mdash;to look at when I liked&mdash; The News would strike me dead&mdash; So safer&mdash;guess&mdash;with just my soul Upon the Window pane&mdash;

Where other Creatures put their eyes&mdash; Incautious&mdash;of the Sun&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Before the ice is in the pools


Before the ice is in the pools&mdash; Before the skaters go,

Or any check at nightfall

Is tarnished by the snow&mdash;

Before the fields have finished,

Before the Christmas tree,

Wonder upon wonder

Will arrive to me!

What we touch the hems of

On a summer's day&mdash;

What is only walking

Just a bridge away&mdash;

That which sings so&mdash;speaks so&mdash; When there's no one here&mdash;

Will the frock I wept in

Answer me to wear?

Emily Dickinson





Before you thought of spring,

Before you thought of spring,

Except as a surmise,

You see, God bless his suddenness,

A fellow in the skies

Of independent hues,

A little weather-worn,

Inspiriting habiliments

Of indigo and brown.

With specimens of song,

As if for you to choose,

Discretion in the interval,

With gay delays he goes

To some superior tree

Without a single leaf,

And shouts for joy to nobody

But his seraphic self!

Emily Dickinson





Behind Me&mdash;dips Eternity


Behind Me&mdash;dips Eternity&mdash; Before Me&mdash;Immortality&mdash; Myself&mdash;the Term between&mdash; Death but the Drift of Eastern Gray,

Dissolving into Dawn away,

Before the West begin&mdash;

'Tis Kingdoms&mdash;afterward&mdash;they say&mdash; In perfect&mdash;pauseless Monarchy&mdash; Whose Prince&mdash;is Son of None&mdash; Himself&mdash;His Dateless Dynasty&mdash; Himself&mdash;Himself diversify&mdash; In Duplicate divine&mdash;

Behind Me—dips Eternity


Behind Me—dips Eternity—

Before Me—Immortality—

Myself—the Term between—

Death but the Drift of Eastern Gray,

Dissolving into Dawn away,

Before the West begin—

'Tis Kingdoms—afterward—they say—

In perfect—pauseless Monarchy—

Whose Prince—is Son of None—

Himself—His Dateless Dynasty—

Himself—Himself diversify—

In Duplicate divine—

'Tis Miracle before Me—then—

'Tis Miracle behind—between—

A Crescent in the Sea—

With Midnight to the North of Her—

And Midnight to the South of Her—

And Maelstrom—in the Sky—

Emily Dickinson





Bereaved of all, I went abroad


Bereaved of all, I went abroad&mdash; No less bereaved was I

Upon a New Peninsula&mdash;

The Grave preceded me&mdash;

Obtained my Lodgings, ere myself&mdash; And when I sought my Bed&mdash;

The Grave it was reposed upon

The Pillow for my Head&mdash;

I waked to find it first awake&mdash; I rose&mdash;It followed me&mdash; I tried to drop it in the Crowd&mdash; To lose it in the Sea&mdash;

In Cups of artificial Drowse

To steep its shape away&mdash;

The Grave&mdash;was finished&mdash;but the Spade Remained in Memory&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

Bereavement in their death to feel

Besides the Autumn poets sing


Besides the Autumn poets sing

A few prosaic days

A little this side of the snow

And that side of the Haze&mdash;

A few incisive Mornings&mdash;

A few Ascetic Eves&mdash;

Gone&mdash;Mr. Bryant's "Golden Rod"&mdash; And Mr. Thomson's "sheaves."

Still, is the bustle in the Brook&mdash; Sealed are the spicy valves&mdash; Mesmeric fingers softly touch

The Eyes of many Elves&mdash;

Perhaps a squirrel may remain&mdash; My sentiments to share&mdash;

Grant me, Oh Lord, a sunny mind&mdash; Thy windy will to bear!

Better&mdash;than Music! For I&mdash;who heard it&mdash; I was used&mdash;to the Birds&mdash;before&mdash; This&mdash;was different&mdash;'Twas Translation&mdash; Of all tunes I knew&mdash;and more&mdash;

So&mdash;Children&mdash;told how Brooks in Eden&mdash; Bubbled a better&mdash;Melody&mdash; Quaintly infer&mdash;Eve's great surrender&mdash; Urging the feet&mdash;that would&mdash;not&mdash;fly&mdash; Children&mdash;matured&mdash;are wiser&mdash;mostly&mdash; Eden&mdash;a legend&mdash;dimly told&mdash; Eve&mdash;and the Anguish&mdash;Grandame's story&mdash; But&mdash;I was telling a tune&mdash;I heard&mdash; Not such a strain&mdash;the Church&mdash;baptizes&mdash; When the last Saint&mdash;goes up the Aisles&mdash; Not such a stanza splits the silence&mdash; When the Redemption strikes her Bells&mdash; Let me not spill&mdash;its smallest cadence&mdash; Humming&mdash;for promise&mdash;when alone&mdash; Humming&mdash;until my faint Rehearsal&mdash; Drop into tune&mdash;around the Throne&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Better—than Music! For I—who heard it


Better—than Music! For I—who heard it—

I was used—to the Birds—before—

This—was different—'Twas Translation—

Of all tunes I knew—and more—

'Twasn't contained—like other stanza—

No one could play it—the second time—

But the Composer—perfect Mozart—

Perish with him—that Keyless Rhyme!

So—Children—told how Brooks in Eden—

Bubbled a better—Melody—

Quaintly infer—Eve's great surrender—

Urging the feet—that would—not—fly—

Children—matured—are wiser—mostly—

Eden—a legend—dimly told—

Eve—and the Anguish—Grandame's story—

But—I was telling a tune—I heard—

Not such a strain—the Church—baptizes—

When the last Saint—goes up the Aisles—

Not such a stanza splits the silence—

When the Redemption strikes her Bells—

Let me not spill—its smallest cadence—

Humming—for promise—when alone—

Humming—until my faint Rehearsal—

Drop into tune—around the Throne—

Emily Dickinson

Bird

A bird came down the walk:

He did not know I saw;

He bit an angle-worm in halves

And ate the fellow, raw.

And then he drank a dew

From a convenient grass,

And the hopped sideways to the wall

To let a beetle pass.

He glanced with rapid eyes

That hurried all abroad, -

They looked like frightened beads, I thought He stirred his velvet head.

Like one in danger; cautious,

I offered him a crumb,

And he unrolled his feathers

And rolled him softer home

Then oars divide the ocean,

Too silver for a seam,

Or butterflies, off banks of noon,

Leap, plashless, as they swim.

Emily Dickinson






Blazing in Gold and quenching in Purple Leaping like Leopards to the Sky

Then at the feet of the old Horizon

Laying her spotted Face to die

Stooping as low as the Otter's Window

Touching the Roof and tinting the Barn Kissing her Bonnet to the Meadow

And the Juggler of Day is gone

Emily Dickinson





Bless God, he went as soldiers


Bless God, he went as soldiers,

His musket on his breast&mdash;

Grant God, he charge the bravest

Of all the martial blest!

Please God, might I behold him

In epauletted white&mdash;

I should not fear the foe then&mdash; I should not fear the fight!

Emily Dickinson

Bring me the sunset in a cup


Bring me the sunset in a cup,

Reckon the morning's flagons up

And say how many Dew,

Tell me how far the morning leaps&mdash; Tell me what time the weaver sleeps

Who spun the breadth of blue!

Write me how many notes there be

In the new Robin's ecstasy

Among astonished boughs&mdash;

How many trips the Tortoise makes&mdash; How many cups the Bee partakes,

The Debauchee of Dews!

Also, who laid the Rainbow's piers,

Also, who leads the docile spheres

By withes of supple blue?

Whose fingers string the stalactite&mdash; Who counts the wampum of the night

To see that none is due?

Who built this little Alban House

And shut the windows down so close

My spirit cannot see?

Who'll let me out some gala day

With implements to fly away,

Passing Pomposity?

Emily Dickinson

By The Sea

I started early, took my dog,

And visited the sea;

The mermaids in the basement

Came out to look at me.

And frigates in the upper floor

Extended hempen hands,

Presuming me to be a mouse

Aground, upon the sands.

But no man moved me till the tide

Went past my simple shoe,

And past my apron and my belt,

And past my bodice too,

And made as he would eat me up

As wholly as a dew

Upon a dandelion's sleeve -

And then I started too.

And he - he followed close behind;

I felt his silver heel

Upon my ankle, - then my shoes

Would overflow with pearl.

Until we met the solid town,

No man he seemed to know;

And bowing with a mighty look

At me, the sea withdrew.

Emily Dickinson





Cat

She sights a Bird - she chuckles -

She flattens - then she crawls -

She runs without the look of feet -

Her eyes increase to Balls -

Her Jaws stir - twitching - hungry -

Her Teeth can hardly stand -

She leaps, but Robin leaped the first -

Ah, Pussy, of the Sand,

The Hopes so juicy ripening -

You almost bathed your Tongue -

When Bliss disclosed a hundred Toes -

And fled with every one -

Emily Dickinson





Chartless

I never saw a moor,

I never saw the sea;

Yet now I know how the heather looks,

And what a wave must be.

I never spoke with God,

Nor visited in Heaven;

Yet certain am I of the spot

As if the chart were given.

Emily Dickinson

Civilization—spurns—the Leopard!


Civilization—spurns—the Leopard!

Was the Leopard—bold?

Deserts—never rebuked her Satin—

Ethiop—her Gold—

Tawny—her Customs—

She was Conscious—

Spotted—her Dun Gown—

This was the Leopard's nature—Signor—

Need—a keeper—frown?

Pity—the Pard—that left her Asia—

Memories—of Palm—

Cannot be stifled—with Narcotic—

Nor suppressed—with Balm—

Emily Dickinson





Cocoon above! Cocoon below!


Cocoon above! Cocoon below!

Stealthy Cocoon, why hide you so

What all the world suspect?

An hour, and gay on every tree

Your secret, perched in ecstasy

Defies imprisonment!

An hour in Chrysalis to pass,

Then gay above receding grass

A Butterfly to go!

A moment to interrogate,

Then wiser than a "Surrogate,"

The Universe to know!

Emily Dickinson

Color—Caste—Denomination


Color—Caste—Denomination—

These—are Time's Affair—

Death's diviner Classifying

Does not know they are—

As in sleep—All Hue forgotten—

Tenets—put behind—

Death's large—Democratic fingers

Rub away the Brand—

If Circassian—He is careless—

If He put away

Chrysalis of Blonde—or Umber—

Equal Butterfly—

They emerge from His Obscuring—

What Death—knows so well—

Our minuter intuitions—

Deem unplausible—

Emily Dickinson





Come Slowly

Come slowly,

Eden

Lips unused to thee.

Bashful, sip thy jasmines,

As the fainting bee,

Reaching late his flower,

Round her chamber hums,

Counts his nectars -alights,

And is lost in balms!

Emily Dickinson

Conjecturing a Climate


Conjecturing a Climate

Of unsuspended Suns&mdash;

Adds poignancy to Winter&mdash;

The Shivering Fancy turns

To a fictitious Country

To palliate a Cold&mdash;

Not obviated of Degree&mdash;

Nor erased&mdash;of Latitude&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Conscious am I in my Chamber


Conscious am I in my Chamber,

Of a shapeless friend&mdash;

He doth not attest by Posture&mdash; Nor Confirm&mdash;by Word&mdash; Neither Place&mdash;need I present Him&mdash; Fitter Courtesy

Hospitable intuition

Of His Company&mdash;

Presence&mdash;is His furthest license&mdash; Neither He to Me

Nor Myself to Him&mdash;by Accent&mdash; Forfeit Probity&mdash;

Weariness of Him, were quainter

Than Monotony

Knew a Particle&mdash;of Space's

Vast Society

Neither if He visit Other&mdash;

Do He dwell&mdash;or Nay&mdash;know I&mdash; But Instinct esteem Him

Immortality&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Could I but ride indefinite


Could I but ride indefinite

As doth the Meadow Bee

And visit only where I liked

And No one visit me

And flirt all Day with Buttercups

And marry whom I may

And dwell a little everywhere

Or better, run away

With no Police to follow

Or chase Him if He do

Till He should jump Peninsulas

To get away from me&mdash;

I said "But just to be a Bee"

Upon a Raft of Air

And row in Nowhere all Day long

And anchor "off the Bar"

What Liberty! So Captives deem

Who tight in Dungeons are.

Emily Dickinson






Could I&mdash;then&mdash;shut the door&mdash; Lest my beseeching face&mdash;at last&mdash; Rejected&mdash;be&mdash;of Her?

Emily Dickinson

Could live&mdash;did live


Could live&mdash;did live&mdash; Could die&mdash;did die&mdash; Could smile upon the whole

Through faith in one he met not,

To introduce his soul.

Could go from scene familiar

To an untraversed spot&mdash;

Could contemplate the journey

With unpuzzled heart&mdash;

Such trust had one among us,

Among us not today&mdash;

We who saw the launching

Never sailed the Bay!

Emily Dickinson

Crisis is a Hair


Crisis is a Hair

Toward which the forces creep

Past which forces retrograde

If it come in sleep

To suspend the Breath

Is the most we can

Ignorant is it Life or Death

Nicely balancing.

Let an instant push

Or an Atom press

Or a Circle hesitate

In Circumference

It&mdash;may jolt the Hand

That adjusts the Hair

That secures Eternity

From presenting&mdash;Here&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Crumbling is not an instant's Act


Crumbling is not an instant's Act

A fundamental pause

Dilapidation's processes

Are organized Decays.

'Tis first a Cobweb on the Soul

A Cuticle of Dust

A Borer in the Axis

An Elemental Rust&mdash;

Ruin is formal&mdash;Devil's work

Consecutive and slow&mdash;

Fail in an instant, no man did

Slipping&mdash;is Crash's law.

Emily Dickinson





Dare you see a Soul at the White Heat?


Dare you see a Soul at the White Heat?

Then crouch within the door&mdash; Red&mdash;is the Fire's common tint&mdash; But when the vivid Ore

Has vanquished Flame's conditions,

It quivers from the Forge

Without a color, but the light

Of unanointed Blaze.

Least Village has its Blacksmith

Whose Anvil's even ring

Stands symbol for the finer Forge

That soundless tugs&mdash;within&mdash; Refining these impatient Ores

With Hammer, and with Blaze

Until the Designated Light

Repudiate the Forge&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Death is a Dialogue between


Death is a Dialogue between

"Dissolve" says Death&mdash;The Spirit "Sir I have another Trust"&mdash;

Death doubts it&mdash;Argues from the Ground&mdash; The Spirit turns away

Just laying off for evidence

An Overcoat of Clay.

Death leaves Us homesick, who behind


Death leaves Us homesick, who behind,

As if it were not born.

Through all their former Places, we

Like Individuals go

Who something lost, the seeking for

Death sets a thing of signigicant

Death sets a thing significant

The eye had hurried by,

Except a perished creature

Entreat us tenderly

To ponder little workmanships

In crayon or in wool,

With 'This was last her fingers did,'

Industrious until

The thimble weighed too heavy,

The stitches stopped themselves,

And then 't was put among the dust

Upon the closet shelves.

A book I have, a friend gave,

Whose pencil, here and there,

Had notched the place that pleased him,--

At rest his fingers are.

Now, when I read, I read not,

For interrupting tears

Obliterate the etchings

Too costly for repairs.

Emily Dickinson
