Delayed till she had ceased to know


Delayed till she had ceased to know&mdash; Delayed till in its vest of snow

Her loving bosom lay&mdash;

An hour behind the fleeting breath&mdash; Later by just an hour than Death&mdash; Oh lagging Yesterday!

Could she have guessed that it would be&mdash; Could but a crier of the joy

Have climbed the distant hill&mdash; Had not the bliss so slow a pace

Who knows but this surrendered face

Were undefeated still?

Oh if there may departing be

Any forgot by Victory

In her imperial round&mdash;

Show them this meek appareled thing

That could not stop to be a king&mdash; Doubtful if it be crowned!

Delight becomes pictorial

Delight becomes pictorial

When viewed through pain,--

More fair, because impossible

That any gain.

The mountaln at a given distance

In amber lies;

Approached, the amber flits a little,--

And that's the skies!

Emily Dickinson





Delight is as the flight


Delight is as the flight&mdash;

Or in the Ratio of it,

As the Schools would say&mdash;

The Rainbow's way&mdash;

A Skein

Flung colored, after Rain,

Would suit as bright,

Except that flight

Were Aliment&mdash;

"If it would last"

I asked the East,

When that Bent Stripe

Struck up my childish

Firmament&mdash;

And I, for glee,

Took Rainbows, as the common way,

And empty Skies

The Eccentricity&mdash;

And so with Lives&mdash;

And so with Butterflies&mdash;

Seen magic&mdash;through the fright That they will cheat the sight&mdash; And Dower latitudes far on&mdash;

Some sudden morn&mdash;

Our portion&mdash;in the fashion&mdash; Done&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

Despair's advantage is achieved

Did you ever stand in a Cavern's Mouth&mdash; Widths out of the Sun&mdash;

And look&mdash;and shudder, and block your breath&mdash; And deem to be alone

In such a place, what horror,

How Goblin it would be&mdash;

And fly, as 'twere pursuing you?

Then Loneliness&mdash;looks so&mdash; Did you ever look in a Cannon's face&mdash; Between whose Yellow eye&mdash;

And yours&mdash;the Judgment intervened&mdash; The Question of "To die"&mdash; Extemporizing in your ear

As cool as Satyr's Drums&mdash;

Distrustful of the Gentian


Distrustful of the Gentian&mdash;

The fluttering of her fringes

Child my perfidy&mdash;

Weary for my&mdash;&mdash;&mdash;&mdash;&mdash; I will singing go&mdash;

Before the breathless Bee&mdash;

On Ears that dying lie&mdash;

To Eyes that Closing go&mdash;

Hangs so distant Heaven&mdash;

To a hand below.

Do People moulder equally,

I do believe a Species

As positively live

As I, who testify it

That there be standing here&mdash; A Sort, that shall not taste of Death&mdash; If Jesus was sincere&mdash;

That statement of the Lord

Is not a controvertible&mdash;

Don't put up my Thread and Needle


Don't put up my Thread and Needle&mdash; I'll begin to Sew

When the Birds begin to whistle&mdash; Better Stitches&mdash;so&mdash; These were bent&mdash;my sight got crooked&mdash; When my mind&mdash;is plain

I'll do seams&mdash;a Queen's endeavor Would not blush to own&mdash;

Doubt Me! My Dim Companion!


Doubt Me! My Dim Companion!

Why, God, would be content

With but a fraction of the Life&mdash; Poured thee, without a stint&mdash; The whole of me&mdash;forever&mdash; What more the Woman can,

Say quick, that I may dower thee

With last Delight I own!

It cannot be my Spirit&mdash;

For that was thine, before&mdash;

I ceded all of Dust I knew&mdash;

What Opulence the more

Had I&mdash;a freckled Maiden,

Whose farthest of Degree,

Was&mdash;that she might&mdash; Some distant Heaven,

Before the Fire's Eyes&mdash;

Winnow her finest fondness&mdash;

But hallow just the snow

Intact, in Everlasting flake&mdash; Oh, Caviler, for you!

Death, the only One

Dying (I heard a fly buzz when I died) I heard a fly buzz when I died;

The stillness round my form

Was like the stillness in the air

Between the heaves of storm.

The eyes beside had wrung them dry,

And breaths were gathering sure

For that last onset, when the king

Be witnessed in his power.

I willed my keepsakes, signed away

What portion of me I

Could make assignable, -- and then

There interposed a fly,

With blue, uncertain, stumbling buzz,

Between the light and me;

And then the windows failed, and then

I could not see to see.

Emily Dickinson

Dying! To be afraid of thee


Dying! To be afraid of thee

One must to thine Artillery

Have left exposed a Friend&mdash;

Than thine old Arrow is a Shot

Delivered straighter to the Heart

The leaving Love behind.

Not for itself, the Dust is shy,

But, enemy, Beloved be

Thy Batteries divorce.

Fight sternly in a Dying eye

Two Armies, Love and Certainty

And Love and the Reverse.

Emily Dickinson





Each life converges to some centre

Each life converges to some centre

Expressed or still;

Exists in every human nature

A goal,

Admitted scarcely to itself, it may be, Too fair

For credibility's temerity

To dare.

Adored with caution, as a brittle heaven, To reach

Were hopeless as the rainbow's raiment To touch,

Yet persevered toward, surer for the distance; How high

Unto the saints' slow diligence

The sky!

Ungained, it may be, by a life's low venture, But then,

Eternity enables the endeavoring

Again.

Emily Dickinson

Teasing with glittering Amend—

Only to aggravate the Dark

Through an expiring—perfect—look—

Emily Dickinson





Faith

"Faith" is a fine invention

When Gentlemen can see—

But Microscopes are prudent

In an Emergency.

Emily Dickinson






Faith&mdash;is the Pierless Bridge Supporting what We see

Unto the Scene that We do not&mdash; Too slender for the eye

It bears the Soul as bold

As it were rocked in Steel

With Arms of Steel at either side&mdash; It joins&mdash;behind the Veil

To what, could We presume

The Bridge would cease to be

To Our far, vacillating Feet

A first Necessity.

Emily Dickinson

Fame is a bee


Fame is a bee.

It has a song&mdash;

It has a sting&mdash;

Ah, too, it has a wing.

Emily Dickinson





Fame is a fickle food


Fame is a fickle food

Upon a shifting plate

Whose table once a

Guest but not

The second time is set.

Whose crumbs the crows inspect

And with ironic caw

Flap past it to the

Farmer's Corn&mdash;

Men eat of it and die.

Emily Dickinson

Finding is the first Act


Finding is the first Act

The second, loss,

Third, Expedition for

The "Golden Fleece"

Finally, no Golden Fleece&mdash;

Jason&mdash;sham&mdash;too.

First Robin

I dreaded that first robin so,

But he is mastered now,

And I'm accustomed to him grown,--

He hurts a little, though.

I thought if I could only live

Till that first shout got by,

Not all pianos in the woods

Had power to mangle me.

I dared not meet the daffodils,

For fear their yellow gown

Would pierce me with a fashion

So foreign to my own.

I wished the grass would hurry,

So when 't was time to see,

He'd be too tall, the tallest one

Could stretch to look at me.

I could not bear the bees should come, I wished they'd stay away

In those dim countries where they go:

What word had they for me?

They're here, though; not a creature failed, No blossom stayed away

In gentle deference to me,

The Queen of Calvary.

Each one salutes me as he goes,

And I my childish plumes

Lift, in bereaved acknowledgment

Of their unthinking drums.

Emily Dickinson





Fitter to see Him, I may be


Fitter to see Him, I may be

For the long Hindrance&mdash;Grace&mdash;to Me&mdash; With Summers, and with Winters, grow,

Some passing Year&mdash;A trait bestow To make Me fairest of the Earth&mdash; The Waiting&mdash;then&mdash;will seem so worth I shall impute with half a pain

The blame that I was chosen&mdash;then&mdash; Time to anticipate His Gaze&mdash; It's first&mdash;Delight&mdash;and then&mdash;Surprise&mdash; The turning o'er and o'er my face

For Evidence it be the Grace&mdash; He left behind One Day&mdash;So less He seek Conviction, That&mdash;be This&mdash; I only must not grow so new

That He'll mistake&mdash;and ask for me Of me&mdash;when first unto the Door I go&mdash;to Elsewhere go no more&mdash; I only must not change so fair

He'll sigh&mdash;"The Other&mdash;She&mdash;is Where?"

The Love, tho', will array me right

I shall be perfect&mdash;in His sight&mdash; If He perceive the other Truth&mdash; Upon an Excellenter Youth&mdash;

How sweet I shall not lack in Vain&mdash; But gain&mdash;thro' loss&mdash;Through Grief&mdash;obtain&mdash; The Beauty that reward Him best&mdash; The Beauty of Demand&mdash;at Rest&mdash; Emily Dickinson






Flowers&mdash;Well&mdash;if anybody Can the ecstasy define&mdash;

Half a transport&mdash;half a trouble&mdash; With which flowers humble men:

Anybody find the fountain

From which floods so contra flow&mdash; I will give him all the Daisies

Which upon the hillside blow.

Too much pathos in their faces

For a simple breast like mine&mdash; Butterflies from St. Domingo

Cruising round the purple line&mdash; Have a system of aesthetics&mdash; Far superior to mine.

Emily Dickinson

For Death&mdash;or rather

For each ecstatic instant

For each ecstatic instant

We must an anguish pay

In keen and quivering ratio

To the ectasty.

For each beloved hour

Sharp pittances of years,

Bitter contested farthings

And coffers heaped with tears.

Emily Dickinson





For every Bird a Nest


For every Bird a Nest&mdash;

Wherefore in timid quest

Some little Wren goes seeking round&mdash; Wherefore when boughs are free&mdash; Households in every tree&mdash;

Pilgrim be found?

Perhaps a home too high&mdash;

Ah Aristocracy!

The little Wren desires&mdash;

Perhaps of twig so fine&mdash;

Of twine e'en superfine,

Her pride aspires&mdash;

The Lark is not ashamed

To build upon the ground

Her modest house&mdash;

Yet who of all the throng

Dancing around the sun

Does so rejoice?

Emily Dickinson





For largest Woman's Hearth I knew


For largest Woman's Hearth I knew&mdash;

'Tis little I can do&mdash;

And yet the largest Woman's Heart

Could hold an Arrow&mdash;too&mdash; And so, instructed by my own,

I tenderer, turn Me to.

Emily Dickinson





For this&mdash;accepted Breath


For this&mdash;accepted Breath&mdash; Through it&mdash;compete with Death&mdash; The fellow cannot touch this Crown&mdash; By it&mdash;my title take&mdash; Ah, what a royal sake

To my necessity&mdash;stooped down!

No Wilderness&mdash;can be

Where this attendeth me&mdash;

No Desert Noon&mdash;

No fear of frost to come

Haunt the perennial bloom&mdash;

But Certain June!

Get Gabriel&mdash;to tell&mdash;the royal syllable&mdash; Get Saints&mdash;with new&mdash;unsteady tongue&mdash; To say what trance below

Most like their glory show&mdash;

Fittest the Crown!

Emily Dickinson





For this—accepted Breath


For this—accepted Breath—

Through it—compete with Death—

The fellow cannot touch this Crown—

By it—my title take—

Ah, what a royal sake

To my necessity—stooped down!

No Wilderness—can be

Where this attendeth me—

No Desert Noon—

No fear of frost to come

Haunt the perennial bloom—

But Certain June!

To say what trance below

Fittest the Crown!

Forever at His side to walk


Forever at His side to walk&mdash; The smaller of the two!

Brain of His Brain&mdash;

Blood of His Blood&mdash;

Two lives&mdash;One Being&mdash;now&mdash; Forever of His fate to taste&mdash; If grief&mdash;the largest part&mdash; If joy&mdash;to put my piece away

For that beloved Heart&mdash;

All life&mdash;to know each other&mdash; Whom we can never learn&mdash;

And bye and bye&mdash;a Change&mdash; Called Heaven&mdash;

Rapt Neighborhoods of Men&mdash;

Just finding out&mdash;what puzzled us&mdash; Without the lexicon!

Forever&mdash;it composed of Nows


Forever&mdash;it composed of Nows&mdash;

No different Our Years would be

From Anno Domini's&mdash;

Forget! The lady with the Amulet


Forget! The lady with the Amulet

Forget she wore it at her Heart

Because she breathed against

Was Treason twixt?

Deny! Did Rose her Bee&mdash;

For Privilege of Play

Or Wile of Butterfly

Or Opportunity&mdash;Her Lord away?

The lady with the Amulet&mdash;will face&mdash; The Bee&mdash;in Mausoleum laid&mdash; Discard his Bride&mdash;

But longer than the little Rill&mdash; That cooled the Forehead of the Hill&mdash; While Other&mdash;went the Sea to fill&mdash; And Other&mdash;went to turn the Mill&mdash; I'll do thy Will&mdash;

Four Trees&mdash;upon a solitary Acre&mdash; Without Design

Or Order, or Apparent Action&mdash; Maintain&mdash;

The Sun&mdash;upon a Morning meets them&mdash; The Wind&mdash;

No nearer Neighbor&mdash;have they&mdash; But God&mdash;

The Acre gives them&mdash;Place&mdash; They&mdash;Him&mdash;Attention of Passer by&mdash; Of Shadow, or of Squirrel, haply&mdash; Or Boy&mdash;

What Deed is Theirs unto the General Nature&mdash; What Plan

They severally&mdash;retard&mdash;or further&mdash; Unknown&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Four Trees—upon a solitary Acre


Four Trees—upon a solitary Acre—

Without Design

Or Order, or Apparent Action—

Maintain—

The Sun—upon a Morning meets them—

The Wind—

No nearer Neighbor—have they—

But God—

The Acre gives them—Place—

They—Him—Attention of Passer by—

Of Shadow, or of Squirrel, haply—

Or Boy—

What Deed is Theirs unto the General Nature—

What Plan

They severally—retard—or further—

Unknown—

Emily Dickinson





Frequently the wood are pink


Frequently the wood are pink&mdash; Frequently are brown.

Frequently the hills undress

Behind my native town.

Oft a head is crested

I was wont to see&mdash;

And as oft a cranny

Where it used to be&mdash;

And the Earth&mdash; they tell me&mdash; On its Axis turned!

Wonderful Rotation!

By but twelve performed!

Emily Dickinson





From Blank to Blank


From Blank to Blank&mdash;

A Threadless Way

I pushed Mechanic feet&mdash;

To stop&mdash;or perish&mdash;or advance&mdash; Alike indifferent&mdash;

If end I gained

It ends beyond

Indefinite disclosed&mdash;

I shut my eyes&mdash;and groped as well

'Twas lighter&mdash;to be Blind&mdash; Emily Dickinson





From Cocoon forth a Butterfly


From Cocoon forth a Butterfly

As Lady from her Door

Emerged&mdash;a Summer Afternoon&mdash; Repairing Everywhere&mdash;

Without Design&mdash;that I could trace Except to stray abroad

On Miscellaneous Enterprise

The Clovers&mdash;understood&mdash; Her pretty Parasol be seen

Contracting in a Field

Where Men made Hay&mdash;

Then struggling hard

With an opposing Cloud&mdash;

Where Parties&mdash;Phantom as Herself&mdash; To Nowhere&mdash;seemed to go

In purposeless Circumference&mdash; As 'twere a Tropic Show&mdash;

And notwithstanding Bee&mdash;that worked&mdash; And Flower&mdash;that zealous blew&mdash; This Audience of Idleness

Disdained them, from the Sky&mdash; Till Sundown crept&mdash;a steady Tide&mdash; And Men that made the Hay&mdash;

And Afternoon&mdash;and Butterfly&mdash; Extinguished&mdash;in the Sea&mdash; Emily Dickinson





From Us She wandered now a Year


From Us She wandered now a Year,

Her tarrying, unknown,

If Wilderness prevent her feet

Or that Ethereal Zone

No eye hath seen and lived

We ignorant must be&mdash;

We only know what time of Year

We took the Mystery.

Emily Dickinson





Funny&mdash;to be a Century

Funny—to be a Century


Funny—to be a Century—

And see the People—going by—

I—should die of the Oddity—

But then—I'm not so staid—as He—

He keeps His Secrets safely—very—

Were He to tell—extremely sorry

This Bashful Globe of Ours would be—

So dainty of Publicity—

Emily Dickinson





Further in Summer than the Birds


Further in Summer than the Birds

Pathetic from the Grass

A minor Nation celebrates

Its unobtrusive Mass.

No Ordinance be seen

So gradual the Grace

A pensive Custom it becomes

Enlarging Loneliness.

Antiquest felt at Noon

When August burning low

Arise this spectral Canticle

Repose to typify

Remit as yet no Grace

No Furrow on the Glow

Yet a Druidic Difference

Enhances Nature now

Emily Dickinson

Glee&mdash;The great storm is over&mdash; Four&mdash;have recovered the Land&mdash; Forty&mdash;gone down together&mdash; Into the boiling Sand&mdash;

Ring&mdash;for the Scant Salvation&mdash; Toll&mdash;for the bonnie Souls&mdash; Neighbor&mdash;and friend&mdash;and Bridegroom&mdash; Spinning upon the Shoals&mdash;

How they will tell the Story&mdash; When Winter shake the Door&mdash;

Till the Children urge&mdash;

But the Forty&mdash;

Did they&mdash;come back no more?

Then a softness&mdash;suffuse the Story&mdash; And a silence&mdash;the Teller's eye&mdash; And the Children&mdash;no further question&mdash; And only the Sea&mdash;reply&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Glee—The great storm is over


Glee—The great storm is over—

Four—have recovered the Land—

Forty—gone down together—

Into the boiling Sand—

Ring—for the Scant Salvation—

Toll—for the bonnie Souls—

Neighbor—and friend—and Bridegroom—

Spinning upon the Shoals—

How they will tell the Story—

When Winter shake the Door—

Till the Children urge—

But the Forty—

Did they—come back no more?

Then a softness—suffuse the Story—

And a silence—the Teller's eye—

And the Children—no further question—

And only the Sea—reply—

Emily Dickinson





Glowing is her Bonnet


Glowing is her Bonnet,

Glowing is her Cheek,

Glowing is her Kirtle,

Yet she cannot speak.

Better as the Daisy

From the Summer hill

Vanish unrecorded

Save by tearful rill&mdash;

Save by loving sunrise

Looking for her face.

Save by feet unnumbered

Pausing at the place.

Emily Dickinson





God gave a loaf to every bird

God gave a loaf to every bird,

But just a crumb to me;

I dare not eat it, though I starve,--

My poignant luxury

To own it, touch it, prove the feat

That made the pellet mine,--

Too happy in my sparrow chance

For ampler coveting.

It might be famine all around,

I could not miss an ear,

Such plenty smiles upon my board,

My garner shows so fair.

I wonder how the rich may feel,--

An Indiaman--an Earl?

I deem that I with but a crumb

Am sovereign of them all.

Emily Dickinson

"Miles", and "Priscilla", were such an One&mdash; But, lest the Soul&mdash;like fair "Priscilla"

God is a distant—stately Lover


God is a distant—stately Lover—

Woos, as He states us—by His Son—

Verily, a Vicarious Courtship—

"Miles", and "Priscilla", were such an One—

But, lest the Soul—like fair "Priscilla"

Choose the Envoy—and spurn the Groom—

Vouches, with hyperbolic archness—

"Miles", and "John Alden" were Synonym—

Emily Dickinson





God made a little Gentian


God made a little Gentian&mdash;

It tried&mdash;to be a Rose&mdash; And failed&mdash;and all the Summer laughed&mdash; But just before the Snows

There rose a Purple Creature&mdash; That ravished all the Hill&mdash;

And Summer hid her Forehead&mdash; And Mockery&mdash;was still&mdash; The Frosts were her condition&mdash; The Tyrian would not come

Until the North&mdash;invoke it&mdash; Creator&mdash;Shall I&mdash;bloom?

Emily Dickinson





God made a little gentian;

God made a little gentian;

It tried to be a rose

And failed, and all the summer laughed.

But just before the snows

There came a purple creature

That ravished all the hill;

And summer hid her forehead,

And mockery was still.

The frosts were her condition;

The Tyrian would not come

Until the North evoked it.

"Creator! shall I bloom?"

Emily Dickinson





God permit industrious angels

God permit industrious angels

Afternoons to play.

I met one, -- forgot my school-mates,

All, for him, straightaway.

God calls home the angels promptly

At the setting sun;

I missed mine. How dreary marbles,

After playing the Crown!

Emily Dickinson





God permits industrious Angels


God permits industrious Angels&mdash; Afternoons&mdash;to play&mdash; I met one&mdash;forgot my Schoolmates&mdash; All&mdash;for Him&mdash;straightway&mdash; God calls home&mdash;the Angels&mdash;promptly&mdash; At the Setting Sun&mdash;

Going to Heaven!


Going to Heaven!

I don't know when&mdash;

Pray do not ask me how!

Indeed I'm too astonished

To think of answering you!

Going to Heaven!

How dim it sounds!

And yet it will be done

As sure as flocks go home at night

Unto the Shepherd's arm!

Perhaps you're going too!

Who knows?

If you should get there first

Save just a little space for me

Close to the two I lost&mdash;

The smallest "Robe" will fit me And just a bit of "Crown"&mdash; For you know we do not mind our dress

When we are going home&mdash;

I'm glad I don't believe it

For it would stop my breath&mdash; And I'd like to look a little more

At such a curious Earth!

I'm glad they did believe it

Whom I have never found

Since the might Autumn afternoon

I left them in the ground.

Emily Dickinson





Going to Him! Happy letter!


Going to Him! Happy letter!

Tell Him&mdash;

Tell Him the page I didn't write&mdash; Tell Him&mdash;I only said the Syntax&mdash; And left the Verb and the pronoun out&mdash; Tell Him just how the fingers hurried&mdash; Then&mdash;how they waded&mdash;slow&mdash;slow&mdash; And then you wished you had eyes in your pages&mdash; So you could see what moved them so&mdash; Tell Him&mdash;it wasn't a Practised Writer&mdash; You guessed&mdash;from the way the sentence toiled&mdash; You could hear the Bodice tug, behind you&mdash; As if it held but the might of a child&mdash; You almost pitied it&mdash;you&mdash;it worked so&mdash; Tell Him&mdash;no&mdash;you may quibble there&mdash; For it would split His Heart, to know it&mdash; And then you and I, were silenter.

Tell Him&mdash;Night finished&mdash;before we finished&mdash; And the Old Clock kept neighing "Day"!

And you&mdash;got sleepy&mdash;and begged to be ended&mdash; What could it hinder so&mdash;to say?

Tell Him&mdash;just how she sealed you&mdash;Cautious!

But&mdash;if He ask where you are hid Until tomorrow&mdash;Happy letter!

Gesture Coquette&mdash;and shake your Head!

Emily Dickinson





Going to him! Happy letter! Tell him--

Going to him! Happy letter! Tell him--

Tell him the page I didn't write;

Tell him I only said the syntax,

And left the verb and the pronoun out.

Tell him just how the fingers hurried

Then how they waded, slow, slow, slow-

And then you wished you had eyes in your pages, So you could see what moved them so.

'Tell him it wasn't a practised writer, You guessed, from the way the sentence toiled; You could hear the bodice tug, behind you, As if it held but the might of a child; You almost pitied it, you, it worked so.

Tell him--No, you may quibble there,

For it would split his heart to know it, And then you and I were silenter.

'Tell him night finished before we finished And the old clock kept neighing 'day!'

And you got sleepy and begged to be ended--

What could it hinder so, to say?

Tell him just how she sealed you, cautious But if he ask where you are hid

Until to-morrow,--happy letter!

Gesture, coquette, and shake your head!'

Emily Dickinson





Good Morning&mdash;Midnight


Good Morning&mdash;Midnight&mdash; I'm coming Home&mdash;

Day&mdash;got tired of Me&mdash; How could I&mdash;of Him?

Sunshine was a sweet place&mdash;

I liked to stay&mdash;

But Morn&mdash;didn't want me&mdash;now&mdash; So&mdash;Goodnight&mdash;Day!

I can look&mdash;can't I&mdash; When the East is Red?

The Hills&mdash;have a way&mdash;then&mdash; That puts the Heart&mdash;abroad&mdash; You&mdash;are not so fair&mdash;Midnight&mdash; I chose&mdash;Day&mdash;

But&mdash;please take a little Girl&mdash; He turned away!

Emily Dickinson





Good Morning—Midnight


Good Morning—Midnight—

I'm coming Home—

Day—got tired of Me—

How could I—of Him?

Sunshine was a sweet place—

I liked to stay—

But Morn—didn't want me—now—

So—Goodnight—Day!

I can look—can't I—

When the East is Red?

The Hills—have a way—then—

That puts the Heart—abroad—

You—are not so fair—Midnight—

I chose—Day—

But—please take a little Girl—

He turned away!

Emily Dickinson





Good night! which put the candle out?

Good night! which put the candle out?

A jealous zephyr, not a doubt.

Ah! friend, you little knew

How long at that celestial wick

The angels labored diligent;

Extinguished, now, for you!

It might have been the lighthouse spark Some sailor, rowing in the dark,

Had importuned to see!

It might have been the waning lamp

That lit the drummer from the camp

To purer reveille!

Emily Dickinson





Good night, because we must


Good night, because we must,

How intricate the dust!

I would go, to know!

Oh incognito!

Saucy, Saucy Seraph

To elude me so!

Father! they won't tell me,

Won't you tell them to?

Emily Dickinson





Good to hide, and hear 'em hunt!


Good to hide, and hear 'em hunt!

Better, to be found,

If one care to, that is,

The Fox fits the Hound&mdash;

Good to know, and not tell,

Best, to know and tell,

Can one find the rare Ear

Not too dull&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






Gratitude&mdash;is not the mention Of a Tenderness,

But its still appreciation

Out of Plumb of Speech.

When the Sea return no Answer

By the Line and Lead

Proves it there's no Sea, or rather

A remoter Bed?

Emily Dickinson

Gratitude—is not the mention

Of a Tenderness,

But its still appreciation

Out of Plumb of Speech.

When the Sea return no Answer

By the Line and Lead

Proves it there's no Sea, or rather

A remoter Bed?

Great Caesar! Condescend


Great Caesar! Condescend

The Daisy, to receive,

Gathered by Cato's Daughter,

With your majestic leave!

Emily Dickinson





Grief is a Mouse


Grief is a Mouse&mdash;

And chooses Wainscot in the Breast

For His Shy House&mdash;

And baffles quest&mdash;

Grief is a Thief&mdash;quick startled&mdash; Pricks His Ear&mdash;report to hear Of that Vast Dark&mdash;

That swept His Being&mdash;back&mdash; Grief is a Juggler&mdash;boldest at the Play&mdash; Lest if He flinch&mdash;the eye that way Pounce on His Bruises&mdash;One&mdash;say&mdash;or Three&mdash; Grief is a Gourmand&mdash;spare His luxury&mdash; Best Grief is Tongueless&mdash;before He'll tell&mdash; Burn Him in the Public Square&mdash; His Ashes&mdash;will

Possibly&mdash;if they refuse&mdash;How then know&mdash; Since a Rack couldn't coax a syllable&mdash;now.

Emily Dickinson






Growth of Man&mdash;like Growth of Nature&mdash; Gravitates within&mdash;

Atmosphere, and Sun endorse it&mdash; Bit it stir&mdash;alone&mdash; Each&mdash;its difficult Ideal

Must achieve&mdash;Itself&mdash; Through the solitary prowess

Of a Silent Life&mdash;

Effort&mdash;is the sole condition&mdash; Patience of Itself&mdash;

Patience of opposing forces&mdash; And intact Belief&mdash;

Looking on&mdash;is the Department Of its Audience&mdash;

But Transaction&mdash;is assisted

By no Countenance&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Growth of Man—like Growth of Nature

Had I not This, or This, I said


Had I not This, or This, I said,

Appealing to Myself,

In moment of prosperity&mdash;

Inadequate&mdash;were Life&mdash;

"Thou hast not Me, nor Me"&mdash;it said, In Moment of Reverse&mdash;

"And yet Thou art industrious&mdash; No need&mdash;hadst Thou&mdash;of us"?

My need&mdash;was all I had&mdash;I said&mdash; The need did not reduce&mdash;

Because the food&mdash;exterminate&mdash; The hunger&mdash;does not cease&mdash; But diligence&mdash;is sharper&mdash; Proportioned to the Chance&mdash;

To feed upon the Retrograde&mdash; Enfeebles&mdash;the Advance&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Had I presumed to hope


Had I presumed to hope&mdash;

The loss had been to Me

A Value&mdash;for the Greatness' Sake&mdash; As Giants&mdash;gone away&mdash; Had I presumed to gain

A Favor so remote&mdash;

The failure but confirm the Grace

In further Infinite&mdash;

'Tis failure&mdash;not of Hope&mdash; But Confident Despair&mdash;

Advancing on Celestial Lists&mdash; With faint&mdash;Terrestial power&mdash;

'Tis Honor&mdash;though I die&mdash; For That no Man obtain

Till He be justified by Death&mdash; This&mdash;is the Second Gain&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Have any like Myself


Have any like Myself

Investigating March,

New Houses on the Hill descried&mdash; And possibly a Church&mdash;

That were not, We are sure&mdash;

As lately as the Snow&mdash;

And are Today&mdash;if We exist&mdash; Though how may this be so?

Have any like Myself

Conjectured Who may be

The Occupants of the Adobes&mdash; So easy to the Sky&mdash;

'Twould seem that God should be

The nearest Neighbor to&mdash;

And Heaven&mdash;a convenient Grace For Show, or Company&mdash;

Have any like Myself

Preserved the Charm secure

By shunning carefully the Place

All Seasons of the Year,

Excepting March&mdash;'Tis then

My Villages be seen&mdash;

And possibly a Steeple&mdash;

Not afterward&mdash;by Men&mdash; Emily Dickinson






Have you got a Brook in your little heart, Where bashful flowers blow,

And blushing birds go down to drink,

And shadows tremble so&mdash;

And nobody knows, so still it flows,

That any brook is there,

And yet your little draught of life

Is daily drunken there&mdash;

Why, look out for the little brook in March, When the rivers overflow,

And the snows come hurrying from the fills, And the bridges often go&mdash;

And later, in August it may be&mdash; When the meadows parching lie,

Beware, lest this little brook of life, Some burning noon go dry!

Emily Dickinson






He forgot&mdash;and I&mdash;remembered&mdash;

'Twas an everyday affair&mdash;

Long ago as Christ and Peter&mdash;

"Warmed them" at the "Temple fire."

"Thou wert with him"&mdash;quoth "the Damsel"?

"No"&mdash;said Peter, 'twasn't me&mdash; Jesus merely "looked" at Peter&mdash; Could I do aught else&mdash;to Thee?

Emily Dickinson





He forgot—and I—remembered


He forgot—and I—remembered—

'Twas an everyday affair—

Long ago as Christ and Peter—

"Warmed them" at the "Temple fire."

"Thou wert with him"—quoth "the Damsel"?

"No"—said Peter, 'twasn't me—

Jesus merely "looked" at Peter—

Could I do aught else—to Thee?

Emily Dickinson






He fought like those Who've nought to lose&mdash; Bestowed Himself to Balls

As One who for a further Life

Had not a further Use&mdash;

Invited Death&mdash;with bold attempt&mdash; But Death was Coy of Him

As Other Men, were Coy of Death&mdash; To Him&mdash;to live&mdash;was Doom&mdash; His Comrades, shifted like the Flakes

When Gusts reverse the Snow&mdash; But He&mdash;was left alive Because Of Greediness to die&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





He found my Being&mdash;set it up


He found my Being&mdash;set it up&mdash; Adjusted it to place&mdash;

Then carved his name&mdash;upon it&mdash; And bade it to the East

Be faithful&mdash;in his absence&mdash; And he would come again&mdash;

With Equipage of Amber&mdash;

That time&mdash;to take it Home&mdash; Emily Dickinson





He found my Being—set it up


He found my Being—set it up—

Adjusted it to place—

Then carved his name—upon it—

And bade it to the East

Be faithful—in his absence—

And he would come again—

With Equipage of Amber—

That time—to take it Home—

Emily Dickinson





He fumbles at your Soul


He fumbles at your Soul

As Players at the Keys

Before they drop full Music on&mdash; He stuns you by degrees&mdash;

Prepares your brittle Nature

For the Ethereal Blow

By fainter Hammers&mdash;further heard&mdash; Then nearer&mdash;Then so slow

Your Breath has time to straighten&mdash; Your Brain&mdash;to bubble Cool&mdash; Deals&mdash;One&mdash;imperial&mdash;Thunderbolt&mdash; That scalps your naked Soul&mdash; When Winds take Forests in the Paws&mdash; The Universe&mdash;is still&mdash; Emily Dickinson





He fumbles at your spirit

He fumbles at your spirit

As players at the keys

Before they drop full music on;

He stuns you by degrees,

Prepares your brittle substance

For the ethereal blow,

By fainter hammers, further heard,

Then nearer, then so slow

Your breath has time to straighten,

Your brain to bubble cool, --

Deals one imperial thunderbolt

That scalps your naked soul.

Emily Dickinson





He gave away his Life


He gave away his Life&mdash;

To Us&mdash;Gigantic Sum&mdash; A trifle&mdash;in his own esteem&mdash; But magnified&mdash;by Fame&mdash; Until it burst the Hearts

That fancied they could hold&mdash; When swift it slipped its limit&mdash; And on the Heavens&mdash;unrolled&mdash;

'Tis Ours&mdash;to wince&mdash;and weep&mdash; And wonder&mdash;and decay

By Blossoms gradual process&mdash; He chose&mdash;Maturity&mdash; And quickening&mdash;as we sowed&mdash; Just obviated Bud&mdash;

And when We turned to note the Growth&mdash; Broke&mdash;perfect&mdash;from the Pod&mdash; Emily Dickinson





He outstripped Time with but a Bout


He outstripped Time with but a Bout,

He outstripped Stars and Sun

And then, unjaded, challenged God

In presence of the Throne.

And He and He in mighty List

Unto this present, run,

The larger Glory for the less

A just sufficient Ring.

Emily Dickinson






He parts Himself&mdash;like Leaves&mdash; And then&mdash;He closes up&mdash; Then stands upon the Bonnet

Of Any Buttercup&mdash;

And then He runs against

And oversets a Rose&mdash;

And then does Nothing&mdash;

Then away upon a Jib&mdash;He goes&mdash; And dangles like a Mote

Suspended in the Noon&mdash;

Uncertain&mdash;to return Below&mdash; Or settle in the Moon&mdash;

What come of Him&mdash;at Night&mdash; The privilege to say

Be limited by Ignorance&mdash;

What come of Him&mdash;That Day&mdash; The Frost&mdash;possess the World&mdash; In Cabinets&mdash;be shown&mdash; A Sepulchre of quaintest Floss&mdash; An Abbey&mdash;a Cocoon&mdash; Emily Dickinson





He parts Himself—like Leaves


He parts Himself—like Leaves—

And then—He closes up—

Then stands upon the Bonnet

Of Any Buttercup—

And then He runs against

And oversets a Rose—

And then does Nothing—

Then away upon a Jib—He goes—

And dangles like a Mote

Suspended in the Noon—

Uncertain—to return Below—

Or settle in the Moon—

What come of Him—at Night—

The privilege to say

Be limited by Ignorance—

What come of Him—That Day—

The Frost—possess the World—

In Cabinets—be shown—

A Sepulchre of quaintest Floss—

An Abbey—a Cocoon—

Emily Dickinson





He put the Belt around my life


He put the Belt around my life

I heard the Buckle snap&mdash;

And turned away, imperial,

My Lifetime folding up&mdash;

Deliberate, as a Duke would do

A Kingdom's Title Deed&mdash;

Henceforth, a Dedicated sort&mdash; A Member of the Cloud.

Yet not too far to come at call&mdash; And do the little Toils

That make the Circuit of the Rest&mdash; And deal occasional smiles

To lives that stoop to notice mine&mdash; And kindly ask it in&mdash;

Whose invitation, know you not

For Whom I must decline?

Emily Dickinson





He strained my faith


He strained my faith&mdash;

Did he find it supple?

Shook my strong trust&mdash;

Did it then&mdash;yield?

Hurled my belief&mdash;

But&mdash;did he shatter&mdash;it?

Racked&mdash;with suspense&mdash; Not a nerve failed!

Wrung me&mdash;with Anguish&mdash; But I never doubted him&mdash;

'Tho' for what wrong

He did never say&mdash;

Stabbed&mdash;while I sued

His sweet forgiveness&mdash;

Jesus&mdash;it's your little "John"!

Don't you know&mdash;me?

Emily Dickinson





He told a homely tale


He told a homely tale

And spotted it with tears&mdash;

Upon his infant face was set

The Cicatrice of years&mdash;

All crumpled was the cheek

No other kiss had known

Than flake of snow, divided with

The Redbreast of the Barn&mdash;

If Mother&mdash;in the Grave&mdash; Or Father&mdash;on the Sea&mdash; Or Father in the Firmament&mdash;

Or Brethren, had he&mdash;

If Commonwealth below,

Or Commonwealth above

Have missed a Barefoot Citizen&mdash; I've ransomed it&mdash;alive&mdash; Emily Dickinson





He touched me, so I live to know


He touched me, so I live to know

That such a day, permitted so,

I groped upon his breast&mdash;

It was a boundless place to me

And silenced, as the awful sea

Puts minor streams to rest.

And now, I'm different from before,

As if I breathed superior air&mdash; Or brushed a Royal Gown&mdash;

My feet, too, that had wandered so&mdash; My Gypsy face&mdash;transfigured now&mdash; To tenderer Renown&mdash;

Into this Port, if I might come,

Rebecca, to Jerusalem,

Would not so ravished turn&mdash;

Nor Persian, baffled at her shrine

Lift such a Crucifixial sign

To her imperial Sun.

Emily Dickinson






He was weak, and I was strong&mdash;then&mdash; So He let me lead him in&mdash;

I was weak, and He was strong then&mdash; So I let him lead me&mdash;Home.

'Twasn't far&mdash;the door was near&mdash;

'Twasn't dark&mdash;for He went&mdash;too&mdash;

'Twasn't loud, for He said nought&mdash; That was all I cared to know.

Day knocked&mdash;and we must part&mdash; Neither&mdash;was strongest&mdash;now&mdash; He strove&mdash;and I strove&mdash;too&mdash; We didn't do it&mdash;tho'!

Emily Dickinson





He was weak, and I was strong—then


He was weak, and I was strong—then—

So He let me lead him in—

I was weak, and He was strong then—

So I let him lead me—Home.

'Twasn't far—the door was near—

'Twasn't dark—for He went—too—

'Twasn't loud, for He said nought—

That was all I cared to know.

Day knocked—and we must part—

Neither—was strongest—now—

He strove—and I strove—too—

We didn't do it—tho'!

Emily Dickinson





He who in Himself believes


He who in Himself believes&mdash;

Fraud cannot presume&mdash;

Faith is Constancy's Result&mdash; And assumes&mdash;from Home&mdash; Cannot perish, though it fail

Every second time&mdash;

But defaced Vicariously&mdash;

For Some Other Shame&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Heart! We will forget him!


Heart! We will forget him!

You and I&mdash;tonight!

You may forget the warmth he gave&mdash; I will forget the light!

When you have done, pray tell me

That I may straight begin!

Haste! lest while you're lagging

I remember him!

Emily Dickinson





Heart, not so heavy as mine


Heart, not so heavy as mine

Wending late home&mdash;

As it passed my window

Whistled itself a tune&mdash;

A careless snatch&mdash;a ballad&mdash;A ditty of the street&mdash; Yet to my irritated Ear

An Anodyne so sweet&mdash;

It was as if a Bobolink

Sauntering this way

Carolled, and paused, and carolled&mdash; Then bubbled slow away!

It was as if a chirping brook

Upon a dusty way&mdash;

Set bleeding feet to minuets

Without the knowing why!

Tomorrow, night will come again&mdash; Perhaps, weary and sore&mdash;

Ah Bugle! By my window

I pray you pass once more.

Emily Dickinson





Heart, We Will Forget Him

Heart, we will forget him,

You and I, tonight!

You must forget the warmth he gave,

I will forget the light.

When you have done pray tell me,

Then I, my thoughts, will dim.

Haste! ‘lest while you’re lagging

I may remember him!

Emily Dickinson





Heaven


"Heaven" has different Signs—to me—

Sometimes, I think that Noon

Is but a symbol of the Place—

And when again, at Dawn,

A mighty look runs round the World

And settles in the Hills—

An Awe if it should be like that

Upon the Ignorance steals—

The Orchard, when the Sun is on—

The Triumph of the Birds

When they together Victory make—

Some Carnivals of Clouds—

The Rapture of a finished Day—

Returning to the West—

All these—remind us of the place

That Men call "paradise"—

Itself be fairer—we suppose—

But how Ourself, shall be

Adorned, for a Superior Grace—

Not yet, our eyes can see—

Emily Dickinson





Heaven has different Signs—to me

"Heaven" has different Signs—to me—

Sometimes, I think that Noon

Is but a symbol of the Place—

And when again, at Dawn,

A mighty look runs round the World

And settles in the Hills—

An Awe if it should be like that

Upon the Ignorance steals—

The Orchard, when the Sun is on—

The Triumph of the Birds

When they together Victory make—

Some Carnivals of Clouds—

The Rapture of a finished Day—

Returning to the West—

All these—remind us of the place

That Men call "paradise"—

Itself be fairer—we suppose—

But how Ourself, shall be

Adorned, for a Superior Grace—

Not yet, our eyes can see—

Emily Dickinson





Heaven is so far of the Mind


Heaven is so far of the Mind

That were the Mind dissolved&mdash; The Site&mdash;of it&mdash;by Architect Could not again be proved&mdash;

'Tis vast&mdash;as our Capacity&mdash; As fair&mdash;as our idea&mdash; To Him of adequate desire

No further 'tis, than Here&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Heaven is what I cannot reach!

Heaven is what I cannot reach!

The apple on the tree,

Provided it do hopelss hang,

That 'heaven' is, to me.

The color on the cruising cloud,

The interdicted ground

Behind the hill, the house behind, --

There Paradise is found!

Emily Dickinson





Heaven—is what I cannot reach!

"Heaven"—is what I cannot reach!

The Apple on the Tree—

Provided it do hopeless—hang—

That—"Heaven" is—to Me!

The Color, on the Cruising Cloud—

The interdicted Land—

Behind the Hill—the House behind—

There—Paradise—is found!

Her teasing Purples—Afternoons—

The credulous—decoy—

Enamored—of the Conjuror—

That spurned us—Yesterday!

Emily Dickinson





Her—


Her—"last Poems"—

Poets—ended—

Silver—perished—with her Tongue—

Not on Record—bubbled other,

Flute—or Woman—

So divine—

Not unto its Summer—Morning

Robin—uttered Half the Tune—

Gushed too free for the Adoring—

From the Anglo-Florentine—

Late—the Praise—

'Tis dull—conferring

On the Head too High to Crown—

Diadem—or Ducal Showing—

Be its Grave—sufficient sign—

Nought—that We—No Poet's Kinsman—

Suffocate—with easy woe—

What, and if, Ourself a Bridegroom—

Put Her down—in Italy?

Emily Dickinson





Her breast is fit for pearls


Her breast is fit for pearls,

But I was not a "Diver"&mdash; Her brow is fit for thrones

But I have not a crest.

Her heart is fit for home&mdash;

I&mdash;a Sparrow&mdash;build there Sweet of twigs and twine

My perennial nest.

Emily Dickinson





Her final Summer was it


Her final Summer was it&mdash;

And yet We guessed it not&mdash;

If tenderer industriousness

Pervaded Her, We thought

A further force of life

Developed from within&mdash;

When Death lit all the shortness up

It made the hurry plain&mdash;

We wondered at our blindness

When nothing was to see

But Her Carrara Guide post&mdash;

At Our Stupidity&mdash;

When duller than our dullness

The Busy Darling lay&mdash;

So busy was she&mdash;finishing&mdash; So leisurely&mdash;were We&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Her final summer was it,

Her final summer was it,

And yet we guessed it not;

If tenderer industriousness

Pervaded her, we thought

A further force of life

Developed from within,--

When Death lit all the shortness up,

And made the hurry plain.

We wondered at our blindness,--

When nothing was to see

But her Carrara guide-post,--

At our stupidity

When, duller than our dulness,

The busy darling lay,

So busy was she, finishing,

So leisurely were we!

Emily Dickinson





Her Grace is all she has—


Her Grace is all she has—

And that, so least displays—

One Art to recognize, must be,

Another Art, to praise.

Emily Dickinson

Her Grace is all she has&mdash;

And that, so least displays&mdash; One Art to recognize, must be,

Another Art, to praise.

Emily Dickinson






Her smile was shaped like other smiles&mdash; The Dimples ran along&mdash;

And still it hurt you, as some Bird

Did hoist herself, to sing,

Then recollect a Ball, she got&mdash; And hold upon the Twig,

Convulsive, while the Music broke&mdash; Like Beads&mdash;among the Bog&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Her Sweet turn to leave the Homestead


Her Sweet turn to leave the Homestead

Came the Darker Way&mdash;

Carriages&mdash;Be Sure&mdash;and Guests&mdash;too&mdash; But for Holiday

'Tis more pitiful Endeavor

Than did Loaded Sea

O'er the Curls attempt to caper

It had cast away&mdash;

Never Bride had such Assembling&mdash; Never kinsmen kneeled

To salute so fair a Forehead&mdash; Garland be indeed&mdash;

Fitter Feet&mdash;of Her before us&mdash; Than whatever Brow

Art of Snow&mdash;or Trick of Lily Possibly bestow

Of Her Father&mdash;Whoso ask Her&mdash; He shall seek as high

As the Palm&mdash;that serve the Desert&mdash; To obtain the Sky&mdash;

Distance&mdash;be Her only Motion&mdash; If 'tis Nay&mdash;or Yes&mdash; Acquiescence&mdash;or Demurral&mdash; Whosoever guess&mdash;

He&mdash;must pass the Crystal Angle That obscure Her face&mdash;

He&mdash;must have achieved in person Equal Paradise&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Her sweet Weight on my Heart a Night


Her sweet Weight on my Heart a Night

Had scarcely deigned to lie&mdash; When, stirring, for Belief's delight,

My Bride had slipped away&mdash;

If 'twas a Dream&mdash;made solid&mdash;just The Heaven to confirm&mdash;

Or if Myself were dreamed of Her&mdash; The power to presume&mdash;

With Him remain&mdash;who unto Me&mdash; Gave&mdash;even as to All&mdash; A Fiction superseding Faith&mdash; By so much&mdash;as 'twas real&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Her&mdash;"last Poems"


Her&mdash;"last Poems"&mdash; Poets&mdash;ended&mdash;

Herein a Blossom lies


Herein a Blossom lies&mdash;

A Sepulchre, between&mdash;

Cross it, and overcome the Bee&mdash; Remain&mdash;'tis but a Rind.

Emily Dickinson





His Bill an Auger is


His Bill an Auger is,

His Head, a Cap and Frill.

He laboreth at every Tree

A Worm, His utmost Goal.

Emily Dickinson





His Feet are shod with Gauze


His Feet are shod with Gauze&mdash; His Helmet, is of Gold,

His Breast, a Single Onyx

With Chrysophrase, inlaid.

His Labor is a Chant&mdash;

His Idleness&mdash;a Tune&mdash; Oh, for a Bee's experience

Of Clovers, and of Noon!

Emily Dickinson





Home

Years I had been from home,

And now, before the door

I dared not open, lest a face

I never saw before

Stare vacant into mine

And ask my business there.

My business, - just a life I left,

Was such still dwelling there?

I fumbled at my nerve,

I scanned the windows near;

The silence like an ocean rolled,

And broke against my ear.

I laughed a wooden laugh

That I could fear a door,

Who danger and the dead had faced,

But never quaked before.

I fitted to the latch

My hand, with trembling care,

Lest back the awful door should spring, And leave me standing there.

I moved my fingers off

As cautiously as glass,

And held my ears, and like a thief

Fled gasping from the house.

Emily Dickinson





Hope is the thing with feathers

Hope is the thing with feathers

That perches in the soul,

And sings the tune without the words,

And never stops at all,

And sweetest in the gale is heard;

And sore must be the storm

That could abash the little bird

That kept so many warm.

I've heard it in the chillest land,

And on the strangest sea;

Yet, never, in extremity,

It asked a crumb of me.

Emily Dickinson





Hope is the thing with feathers—

"Hope" is the thing with feathers—

That perches in the soul—

And sings the tune without the words—

And never stops—at all—

And sweetest—in the Gale—is heard—

And sore must be the storm—

That could abash the little Bird

That kept so many warm—

I've heard it in the chillest land—

And on the strangest Sea—

Yet, never, in Extremity,

It asked a crumb—of Me.

Emily Dickinson





Houses—so the Wise Men tell me—

"Houses"—so the Wise Men tell me—

"Mansions"! Mansions must be warm!

Mansions cannot let the tears in,

Mansions must exclude the storm!

"Many Mansions," by "his Father,"

I don't know him; snugly built!

Could the Children find the way there—

Some, would even trudge tonight!

Emily Dickinson





How far is it to Heaven?


How far is it to Heaven?

As far as Death this way&mdash;

Of River or of Ridge beyond

Was no discovery.

How far is it to Hell?

As far as Death this way&mdash;

How far left hand the Sepulchre

Defies Topography.

Emily Dickinson





How fortunate the Grave


How fortunate the Grave&mdash;

All Prizes to obtain&mdash;

Successful certain, if at last,

First Suitor not in vain.

Emily Dickinson





How happy I was if I could forget


How happy I was if I could forget

To remember how sad I am

Would be an easy adversity

But the recollecting of Bloom

Keeps making November difficult

Till I who was almost bold

Lose my way like a little Child

And perish of the cold.

Emily Dickinson





How happy is the little Stone


How happy is the little Stone

That rambles in the Road alone,

And doesn't care about Careers

And Exigencies never fears&mdash;

Whose Coat of elemental Brown

A passing Universe put on,

And independent as the Sun

Associates or glows alone,

Fulfilling absolute Decree

In casual simplicity&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





How many Flowers fail in Wood


How many Flowers fail in Wood&mdash; Or perish from the Hill&mdash;

Without the privilege to know

That they are Beautiful&mdash;

How many cast a nameless Pod

Upon the nearest Breeze&mdash;

Unconscious of the Scarlet Freight&mdash; It bear to Other Eyes&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






How many times these low feet staggered&mdash; Only the soldered mouth can tell&mdash; Try&mdash;can you stir the awful rivet&mdash; Try&mdash;can you lift the hasps of steel!

Stroke the cool forehead&mdash;hot so often&mdash; Lift&mdash;if you care&mdash;the listless hair&mdash; Handle the adamantine fingers

Never a thimble&mdash;more&mdash;shall wear&mdash; Buzz the dull flies&mdash;on the chamber window&mdash; Brave&mdash;shines the sun through the freckled pane&mdash; Fearless&mdash;the cobweb swings from the ceiling&mdash; Indolent Housewife&mdash;in Daisies&mdash;lain!

Emily Dickinson





How noteless Men, and Pleiads, stand


How noteless Men, and Pleiads, stand,

Until a sudden sky

Reveals the fact that One is rapt

Forever from the Eye&mdash;

Members of the Invisible,

Existing, while we stare,

In Leagueless Opportunity,

O'ertakenless, as the Air&mdash;

Why didn't we detain Them?

The Heavens with a smile,

Sweep by our disappointed Heads

Without a syllable&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






How sick&mdash;to wait&mdash;in any place&mdash;but thine&mdash; I knew last night&mdash;when someone tried to twine&mdash; Thinking&mdash;perhaps&mdash;that I looked tired&mdash;or alone&mdash; Or breaking&mdash;almost&mdash;with unspoken pain&mdash; And I turned&mdash;ducal&mdash; That right&mdash;was thine&mdash; One port&mdash;suffices&mdash;for a Brig&mdash;like mine&mdash; Ours be the tossing&mdash;wild though the sea&mdash; Rather than a Mooring&mdash;unshared by thee.

Ours be the Cargo&mdash;unladed&mdash;here&mdash; Rather than the "spicy isles&mdash;"

And thou&mdash;not there&mdash; Emily Dickinson






How sick—to wait—in any place—but thine—

I knew last night—when someone tried to twine—

Thinking—perhaps—that I looked tired—or alone—

Or breaking—almost—with unspoken pain—

And I turned—ducal—

That right—was thine—

One port—suffices—for a Brig—like mine—

Ours be the tossing—wild though the sea—

Rather than a Mooring—unshared by thee.

Ours be the Cargo—unladed—here—

Rather than the "spicy isles—"

And thou—not there—

Emily Dickinson






How the old Mountains drip with Sunset How the Hemlocks burn&mdash;

How the Dun Brake is draped in Cinder

By the Wizard Sun&mdash;

How the old Steeples hand the Scarlet

Till the Ball is full&mdash;

Have I the lip of the Flamingo

That I dare to tell?

Then, how the Fire ebbs like Billows&mdash; Touching all the Grass

With a departing&mdash;Sapphire&mdash;feature&mdash; As a Duchess passed&mdash;

How a small Dusk crawls on the Village Till the Houses blot

And the odd Flambeau, no men carry

Glimmer on the Street&mdash;

How it is Night&mdash;in Nest and Kennel&mdash; And where was the Wood&mdash;

Just a Dome of Abyss is Bowing

Into Solitude&mdash;

These are the Visions flitted Guido&mdash; Titian&mdash;never told&mdash; Domenichino dropped his pencil&mdash; Paralyzed, with Gold&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





How the Waters closed above Him


How the Waters closed above Him

We shall never know&mdash;

How He stretched His Anguish to us

That&mdash;is covered too&mdash; Spreads the Pond Her Base of Lilies

Bold above the Boy

Whose unclaimed Hat and Jacket

Sum the History&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





How well I knew Her not


How well I knew Her not

Whom not to know has been

A Bounty in prospective, now

Next Door to mine the Pain.

Emily Dickinson





I am alive&mdash;I guess


I am alive&mdash;I guess&mdash; The Branches on my Hand

Are full of Morning Glory&mdash;

And at my finger's end&mdash;

The Carmine&mdash;tingles warm&mdash; And if I hold a Glass

Across my Mouth&mdash;it blurs it&mdash; Physician's&mdash;proof of Breath&mdash; I am alive&mdash;because

I am not in a Room&mdash;

The Parlor&mdash;Commonly&mdash;it is&mdash; So Visitors may come&mdash;

And lean&mdash;and view it sidewise&mdash; And add "How cold&mdash;it grew"&mdash; And "Was it conscious&mdash;when it stepped In Immortality?"

I am alive&mdash;because

I do not own a House&mdash;

Entitled to myself&mdash;precise&mdash; And fitting no one else&mdash;

And marked my Girlhood's name&mdash; So Visitors may know

Which Door is mine&mdash;and not

Emily Dickinson





I am alive—I guess


I am alive—I guess—

The Branches on my Hand

Are full of Morning Glory—

And at my finger's end—

The Carmine—tingles warm—

And if I hold a Glass

Across my Mouth—it blurs it—

Physician's—proof of Breath—

I am alive—because

I am not in a Room—

The Parlor—Commonly—it is—

So Visitors may come—

And lean—and view it sidewise—

And add "How cold—it grew"—

And "Was it conscious—when it stepped In Immortality?"

I am alive—because

I do not own a House—

Entitled to myself—precise—

And fitting no one else—

And marked my Girlhood's name—

So Visitors may know

Which Door is mine—and not

Emily Dickinson





I am ashamed&mdash;I hide


I am ashamed&mdash;I hide&mdash; What right have I&mdash;to be a Bride&mdash; So late a Dowerless Girl&mdash;

Nowhere to hide my dazzled Face&mdash; No one to teach me that new Grace&mdash; Nor introduce&mdash;my Soul&mdash; Me to adorn&mdash;How&mdash;tell&mdash; Trinket&mdash;to make Me beautiful&mdash; Fabrics of Cashmere&mdash;

Never a Gown of Dun&mdash;more&mdash; Raiment instead&mdash;of Pompadour&mdash; For Me&mdash;My soul&mdash;to wear&mdash; Fingers&mdash;to frame my Round Hair Oval&mdash;as Feudal Ladies wore&mdash; Far Fashions&mdash;Fair&mdash; Skill to hold my Brow like an Earl&mdash; Plead&mdash;like a Whippoorwill&mdash; Prove&mdash;like a Pearl&mdash; Then, for Character&mdash;

Fashion My Spirit quaint&mdash;white&mdash; Quick&mdash;like a Liquor&mdash; Gay&mdash;like Light&mdash;

Bring Me my best Pride&mdash;

No more ashamed&mdash;

No more to hide&mdash;

Meek&mdash;let it be&mdash;too proud&mdash;for Pride&mdash; Baptized&mdash;this Day&mdash;a Bride&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I am ashamed—I hide


I am ashamed—I hide—

What right have I—to be a Bride—

So late a Dowerless Girl—

Nowhere to hide my dazzled Face—

No one to teach me that new Grace—

Nor introduce—my Soul—

Me to adorn—How—tell—

Trinket—to make Me beautiful—

Fabrics of Cashmere—

Never a Gown of Dun—more—

Raiment instead—of Pompadour—

For Me—My soul—to wear—

Fingers—to frame my Round Hair

Oval—as Feudal Ladies wore—

Far Fashions—Fair—

Skill to hold my Brow like an Earl—

Plead—like a Whippoorwill—

Prove—like a Pearl—

Then, for Character—

Fashion My Spirit quaint—white—

Quick—like a Liquor—

Gay—like Light—

Bring Me my best Pride—

No more ashamed—

No more to hide—

Meek—let it be—too proud—for Pride—

Baptized—this Day—a Bride—

Emily Dickinson





I asked no other thing


I asked no other thing&mdash;

No other&mdash;was denied&mdash; I offered Being&mdash;for it&mdash; The Mighty Merchant sneered&mdash; Brazil? He twirled a Button&mdash; Without a glance my way&mdash;

"But&mdash;Madam&mdash;is there nothing else&mdash; That We can show&mdash;Today?"

Emily Dickinson





I breathed enough to learn the trick,

I breathed enough to learn the trick,

And now, removed from air,

I simulate the breath so well,

That one, to be quite sure

The lungs are stirless, must descend

Among the cunning cells,

And touch the pantomime himself.

How cool the bellows feels!

Emily Dickinson





I breathed enough to take the Trick


I breathed enough to take the Trick&mdash; And now, removed from Air&mdash;

I simulate the Breath, so well&mdash; That One, to be quite sure&mdash;

The Lungs are stirless&mdash;must descend Among the Cunning Cells&mdash;

And touch the Pantomine&mdash;Himself, How numb, the Bellows feels!

Emily Dickinson





I bring an unaccustomed wine


I bring an unaccustomed wine

To lips long parching

Next to mine,

And summon them to drink;

Crackling with fever, they Essay,

I turn my brimming eyes away,

And come next hour to look.

The hands still hug the tardy glass&mdash; The lips I would have cooled, alas&mdash; Are so superfluous Cold&mdash;

I would as soon attempt to warm

The bosoms where the frost has lain

Ages beneath the mould&mdash;

Some other thirsty there may be

To whom this would have pointed me

Had it remained to speak&mdash;

And so I always bear the cup

If, haply, mine may be the drop

Some pilgrim thirst to slake&mdash; If, haply, any say to me

"Unto the little, unto me,"

When I at last awake.

Emily Dickinson





I Came to buy a smile&mdash;today


I Came to buy a smile&mdash;today&mdash; But just a single smile&mdash;

The smallest one upon your face

Will suit me just as well&mdash;

The one that no one else would miss

It shone so very small&mdash;

I'm pleading at the "counter"&mdash;sir&mdash; Could you afford to sell&mdash;

I've Diamonds&mdash;on my fingers&mdash; You know what Diamonds are?

I've Rubies&mdash;live the Evening Blood&mdash; And Topaz&mdash;like the star!

'Twould be "a Bargain" for a Jew!

Say&mdash;may I have it&mdash;Sir?

Emily Dickinson





I Came to buy a smile—today


I Came to buy a smile—today—

But just a single smile—

The smallest one upon your face

Will suit me just as well—

The one that no one else would miss

It shone so very small—

I can wade Grief


I can wade Grief&mdash;

Whole Pools of it&mdash;

I'm used to that&mdash;

But the least push of Joy

Breaks up my feet&mdash;

And I tip&mdash;drunken&mdash; Let no Pebble&mdash;smile&mdash;

'Twas the New Liquor&mdash;

That was all!

Power is only Pain&mdash;

Stranded, thro' Discipline,

Till Weights&mdash;will hang&mdash; Give Balm&mdash;to Giants&mdash; And they'll wilt, like Men&mdash;

Give Himmaleh&mdash;

They'll Carry&mdash;Him!

Emily Dickinson





I cannot be ashamed


I cannot be ashamed

Because I cannot see

The love you offer&mdash;

Magnitude

Reverses Modesty

And I cannot be proud

Because a Height so high

Involves Alpine

Requirements

And Services of Snow.

Emily Dickinson






I cannot buy it&mdash;'tis not sold&mdash; There is no other in the World&mdash; Mine was the only one

I was so happy I forgot

To shut the Door And it went out

And I am all alone&mdash;

If I could find it Anywhere

I would not mind the journey there

Though it took all my store

But just to look it in the Eye&mdash;

"Did'st thou?" "Thou did'st not mean," to say, Then, turn my Face away.

Emily Dickinson

I cannot dance upon my Toes


I cannot dance upon my Toes&mdash; No Man instructed me&mdash;

But oftentimes, among my mind,

A Glee possesseth me,

That had I Ballet knowledge&mdash; Would put itself abroad

In Pirouette to blanch a Troupe&mdash; Or lay a Prima, mad,

And though I had no Gown of Gauze&mdash; No Ringlet, to my Hair,

Nor hopped to Audiences&mdash;like Birds, One Claw upon the Air,

Nor tossed my shape in Eider Balls,

Nor rolled on wheels of snow

Till I was out of sight, in sound,

The House encore me so&mdash;

Nor any know I know the Art

I mention&mdash;easy&mdash;Here&mdash; Nor any Placard boast me&mdash;

It's full as Opera&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I cannot live with You

I cannot live with You --

It would be Life --

And Life is over there --

Behind the Shelf

The Sexton keeps the Key to --

Putting up

Our Life -- His Porcelain --

Like a Cup --

Discarded of the Housewife --

Quaint -- or Broke --

A newer Sevres pleases --

Old Ones crack --

I could not die -- with You --

For One must wait

To shut the Other's Gaze down --

You -- could not --

And I -- Could I stand by

And see You -- freeze --

Without my Right of Frost --

Death's privilege?

Nor could I rise -- with You --

Because Your Face

Would put out Jesus' --

That New Grace

Glow plain -- and foreign

On my homesick Eye --

Except that You than He

Shone closer by --

They'd judge Us -- How --

For You -- served Heaven -- You know,

Or sought to --

I could not --

Because You saturated Sight --

And I had no more Eyes

For sordid excellence

As Paradise

And were You lost, I would be --

Though My Name

Rang loudest

On the Heavenly fame --

And were You -- saved --

And I -- condemned to be





Where You were not --

That self -- were Hell to Me --

So We must meet apart --

You there -- I -- here --

With just the Door ajar

That Oceans are -- and Prayer --

And that White Sustenance --

Despair --

Emily Dickinson

I cannot live with you,

cannot live with you,

It would be life,

And life is over there

Behind the shelf

The sexton keeps the key to,

Putting up

Our life, his porcelain,

Like a cup

Discarded of the housewife,

Quaint or broken;

A newer Sevres pleases,

Old ones crack.

I could not die with you,

For one must wait

To shut the other's gaze down,--

You could not.

And I, could I stand by

And see you freeze,

Without my right of frost,

Death's privilege?

Nor could I rise with you,

Because your face

Would put out Jesus'.

That new grace

Glow plain and foreign

On my homesick eye,

Except that you, than he

Shone closer by.

They'd judge us--how?

For you served Heaven, you know

Or sought to;

I could not,

Because you saturated sight,

And I had no more eyes

For sordid excellence

As Paradise.

And were you lost, I would be,

Though my name

Rang loudest

On the heavenly fame.

And were you saved,

And I condemned to be





Where you were not,

That self were hell to me.

So we must keep apart,

You there, I here,

With just the door ajar

That oceans are,

And prayer,

And that pale svustenance,

Despair!

Emily Dickinson






I can't tell you&mdash;but you feel it&mdash; Nor can you tell me&mdash;

Saints, with ravished slate and pencil Solve our April Day!

Sweeter than a vanished frolic

From a vanished green!

Swifter than the hoofs of Horsemen

Round a Ledge of dream!

Modest, let us walk among it

With our faces veiled&mdash;

As they say polite Archangels

Do in meeting God!

Not for me&mdash;to prate about it!

Not for you&mdash;to say

To some fashionable Lady

"Charming April Day"!

Rather&mdash;Heaven's "Peter Parley"!

By which Children slow

To sublimer Recitation

Are prepared to go!

Emily Dickinson

I cautious, scanned my little life


I cautious, scanned my little life&mdash; I winnowed what would fade

From what would last till Heads like mine Should be a-dreaming laid.

I put the latter in a Barn&mdash;

The former, blew away.

I went one winter morning

And lo - my priceless Hay

Was not upon the "Scaffold"&mdash; Was not upon the "Beam"&mdash; And from a thriving Farmer&mdash;

A Cynic, I became.

Whether a Thief did it&mdash;

Whether it was the wind&mdash;

Whether Deity's guiltless&mdash;

My business is, to find!

So I begin to ransack!

How is it Hearts, with Thee?

Art thou within the little Barn

Love provided Thee?

Emily Dickinson






I could bring You Jewels&mdash;had I a mind to&mdash; But You have enough&mdash;of those&mdash; I could bring You Odors from St. Domingo&mdash; Colors&mdash;from Vera Cruz&mdash; Berries of the Bahamas&mdash;have I&mdash; But this little Blaze

Flickering to itself&mdash;in the Meadow&mdash; Suits Me&mdash;more than those&mdash; Never a Fellow matched this Topaz&mdash; And his Emerald Swing&mdash;

Dower itself&mdash;for Bobadilo&mdash; Better&mdash;Could I bring?

Emily Dickinson






I could bring You Jewels—had I a mind to—

But You have enough—of those—

I could bring You Odors from St. Domingo—

Colors—from Vera Cruz—

Berries of the Bahamas—have I—

But this little Blaze

Flickering to itself—in the Meadow—

Suits Me—more than those—

Never a Fellow matched this Topaz—

And his Emerald Swing—

Dower itself—for Bobadilo—

Better—Could I bring?

Emily Dickinson





I could die&mdash;to know


I could die&mdash;to know&mdash;

I could die—to know


I could die—to know—

'Tis a trifling knowledge—

News-Boys salute the Door—

Carts—joggle by—

Morning's bold face—stares in the window—

Were but mine—the Charter of the least Fly—

Houses hunch the House

With their Brick Shoulders—

Coals—from a Rolling Load—rattle—how—near—

To the very Square—His foot is passing—

Possibly, this moment—

While I—dream—Here—

Emily Dickinson

Till You had tasted first,

Though cooler than the Water was

The Thoughtfullness of Thirst.

I could not prove the Years had feet


I could not prove the Years had feet&mdash; Yet confident they run

Am I, from symptoms that are past

And Series that are done&mdash;

I find my feet have further Goals&mdash; I smile upon the Aims

That felt so ample&mdash;Yesterday&mdash; Today's&mdash;have vaster claims&mdash; I do not doubt the self I was

Was competent to me&mdash;

But something awkward in the fit&mdash; Proves that&mdash;outgrown&mdash;I see&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I could suffice for Him, I knew


I could suffice for Him, I knew&mdash; He&mdash;could suffice for Me&mdash; Yet Hesitating Fractions&mdash;Both Surveyed Infinity&mdash;

"Would I be Whole" He sudden broached&mdash; My syllable rebelled&mdash;

'Twas face to face with Nature&mdash;forced&mdash;

'Twas face to face with God&mdash; Withdrew the Sun&mdash;to Other Wests&mdash; Withdrew the furthest Star

Before Decision&mdash;stooped to speech&mdash; And then&mdash;be audibler

The Answer of the Sea unto

The Motion of the Moon&mdash;

Herself adjust Her Tides&mdash;unto&mdash; Could I&mdash;do else&mdash;with Mine?

Emily Dickinson





I cried at Pity&mdash;not at Pain


I cried at Pity&mdash;not at Pain&mdash; I heard a Woman say

"Poor Child"&mdash;and something in her voice Convicted me&mdash;of me&mdash; So long I fainted, to myself

It seemed the common way,

And Health, and Laughter, Curious things&mdash; To look at, like a Toy&mdash;

To sometimes hear "Rich people" buy And see the Parcel rolled&mdash;

And carried, I supposed&mdash;to Heaven, For children, made of Gold&mdash;

But not to touch, or wish for,

Or think of, with a sigh&mdash;

And so and so&mdash;had been to me, Had God willed differently.

I wish I knew that Woman's name&mdash; So when she comes this way,

To hold my life, and hold my ears

For fear I hear her say

She's "sorry I am dead"&mdash;again&mdash; Just when the Grave and I&mdash;

Have sobbed ourselves almost to sleep, Our only Lullaby&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I cried at Pity—not at Pain


I cried at Pity—not at Pain—

I heard a Woman say

"Poor Child"—and something in her voice Convicted me—of me—

So long I fainted, to myself

It seemed the common way,

And Health, and Laughter, Curious things—

To look at, like a Toy—

To sometimes hear "Rich people" buy And see the Parcel rolled—

And carried, I supposed—to Heaven,

For children, made of Gold—

But not to touch, or wish for,

Or think of, with a sigh—

And so and so—had been to me,

Had God willed differently.

I wish I knew that Woman's name—

So when she comes this way,

To hold my life, and hold my ears

For fear I hear her say

She's "sorry I am dead"—again—

Just when the Grave and I—

Have sobbed ourselves almost to sleep, Our only Lullaby—

Emily Dickinson





I cross till I am weary


I cross till I am weary

A Mountain&mdash;in my mind&mdash; More Mountains&mdash;then a Sea&mdash; More Seas&mdash;And then

A Desert&mdash;find&mdash;

And My Horizon blocks

With steady&mdash;drifting&mdash;Grains Of unconjectured quantity&mdash;

As Asiatic Rains&mdash;

Nor this&mdash;defeat my Pace&mdash; It hinder from the West

But as an Enemy's Salute

One hurrying to Rest&mdash;

What merit had the Goal&mdash;

Except there intervene

Faint Doubt&mdash;and far Competitor&mdash; To jeopardize the Gain?

At last&mdash;the Grace in sight&mdash; I shout unto my feet&mdash;

I offer them the Whole of Heaven

The instant that we meet&mdash;

They strive&mdash;and yet delay&mdash; They perish&mdash;Do we die&mdash; Or is this Death's Experiment&mdash; Reversed&mdash;in Victory?

Emily Dickinson





I Died For Beauty

I died for beauty, but was scarce

Adjusted in the tomb,

When one who died for truth was lain

In an adjoining room.

He questioned softly why I failed?

"For beauty," I replied.

"And I for truth - the two are one; We brethren are," he said.

And so, as kinsmen met a-night,

We talked between the rooms,

Until the moss had reached our lips,

And covered up our names.

Emily Dickinson

I dreaded that first Robin, so


I dreaded that first Robin, so,

But He is mastered, now,

I'm accustomed to Him grown,

He hurts a little, though&mdash;

I thought If I could only live

Till that first Shout got by&mdash; Not all Pianos in the Woods

Had power to mangle me&mdash;

I dared not meet the Daffodils&mdash; For fear their Yellow Gown

Would pierce me with a fashion

So foreign to my own&mdash;

I wished the Grass would hurry&mdash; So&mdash;when 'twas time to see&mdash; He'd be too tall, the tallest one

Could stretch&mdash;to look at me&mdash; I could not bear the Bees should come, I wished they'd stay away

In those dim countries where they go,

What word had they, for me?

They're here, though; not a creature failed&mdash; No Blossom stayed away

In gentle deference to me&mdash;

The Queen of Calvary&mdash;

Each one salutes me, as he goes,

And I, my childish Plumes,

Lift, in bereaved acknowledgment

Of their unthinking Drums&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I dwell in Possibility


I dwell in Possibility&mdash;

A fairer House than Prose&mdash;

More numerous of Windows&mdash;

Superior&mdash;for Doors&mdash; Of Chambers as the Cedars&mdash;

Impregnable of Eye&mdash;

And for an Everlasting Roof

The Gambrels of the Sky&mdash;

Of Visitors&mdash;the fairest&mdash; For Occupation&mdash;This&mdash; The spreading wide of narrow Hands

To gather Paradise&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I envy Seas, whereon He rides


I envy Seas, whereon He rides&mdash; I envy Spokes of Wheels

Of Chariots, that Him convey&mdash; I envy Crooked Hills

That gaze upon His journey&mdash;

How easy All can see

What is forbidden utterly

As Heaven&mdash;unto me!

I envy Nests of Sparrows&mdash;

That dot His distant Eaves&mdash;

The wealthy Fly, upon His Pane&mdash; The happy&mdash;happy Leaves&mdash; That just abroad His Window

Have Summer's leave to play&mdash; The Ear Rings of Pizarro

Could not obtain for me&mdash;

I envy Light&mdash;that wakes Him&mdash; And Bells&mdash;that boldly ring

To tell Him it is Noon, abroad&mdash; Myself&mdash;be Noon to Him&mdash; Yet interdict&mdash;my Blossom&mdash; And abrogate&mdash;my Bee&mdash; Lest Noon in Everlasting Night&mdash; Drop Gabriel&mdash;and Me&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I fear a Man of frugal Speech


I fear a Man of frugal Speech&mdash; I fear a Silent Man&mdash;

Haranguer&mdash;I can overtake&mdash; Or Babbler&mdash;entertain&mdash; But He who weigheth&mdash;While the Rest&mdash; Expend their furthest pound&mdash; Of this Man&mdash;I am wary&mdash; I fear that He is Grand&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I felt a cleaving in my mind

I felt a cleaving in my mind

As if my brain had split;

I tried to match it, seam by seam,

But could not make them fit.

The thought behind I strove to join

Unto the thought before,

But sequence ravelled out of reach

Like balls upon a floor.

Emily Dickinson





I felt a funeral in my brain,

I felt a funeral in my brain,

And mourners, to and fro,

Kept treading, treading, till it seemed That sense was breaking through.

And when they all were seated,

A service like a drum

Kept beating, beating, till I thought

My mind was going numb

And then I heard them lift a box,

And creak across my soul

With those same boots of lead, again.

Then space began to toll

As all the heavens were a bell,

And being, but an ear,

And I and Silence some strange Race

Wrecked, solitary, here.

Emily Dickinson





I felt a Funeral, in my Brain


I felt a Funeral, in my Brain,

And Mourners to and fro

Kept treading&mdash;treading&mdash;till it seemed That Sense was breaking through&mdash; And when they all were seated,

A Service, like a Drum&mdash;

Kept beating&mdash;beating&mdash;till I thought My Mind was going numb&mdash;

And Finished knowing&mdash;then&mdash; Emily Dickinson






I felt a Funeral, in my Brain,

And Mourners to and fro

Kept treading--treading--till it seemed That Sense was breaking through--

And when they all were seated,

A Service, like a Drum--

Kept beating--beating--till I thought

My Mind was going numb--

And then I heard them lift a Box

And creak across my Soul

With those same Boots of Lead, again,

Then Space--began to toll,

As all the Heavens were a Bell,

And Being, but an Ear,

And I, and Silence, some strange Race

Wrecked, solitary, here--

And then a Plank in Reason, broke,

And I dropped down, and down--

And hit a World, at every plunge,

And Finished knowing--then--

Emily Dickinson





I felt my life with both my hands


I felt my life with both my hands

To see if it was there&mdash;

I held my spirit to the Glass,

To prove it possibler&mdash;

I turned my Being round and round

And paused at every pound

To ask the Owner's name&mdash;

For doubt, that I should know the Sound&mdash; I judged my features&mdash;jarred my hair&mdash; I pushed my dimples by, and waited&mdash; If they&mdash;twinkled back&mdash; Conviction might, of me&mdash;

I told myself, "Take Courage, Friend&mdash; That&mdash;was a former time&mdash; But we might learn to like the Heaven, As well as our Old Home!"

Emily Dickinson





I found the phrase to every thought

I found the phrase to every thought

I ever had, but one;

And that defies me,--as a hand

Did try to chalk the sun

To races nurtured in the dark;--

How would your own begin?

Can blaze be done in cochineal,

Or noon in mazarin?

Emily Dickinson





I found the words to every thought


I found the words to every thought

I ever had&mdash;but One&mdash; And that&mdash;defies me&mdash; As a Hand did try to chalk the Sun

I gained it so


I gained it so&mdash;

By Climbing slow&mdash;

By Catching at the Twigs that grow

Between the Bliss&mdash;and me&mdash; It hung so high

As well the Sky

Attempt by Strategy&mdash;

I said I gained it&mdash;

This&mdash;was all&mdash;

Look, how I clutch it

Lest it fall&mdash;

And I a Pauper go&mdash;

Unfitted by an instant's Grace

For the Contented&mdash;Beggar's face I wore&mdash;an hour ago&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I gave myself to Him


I gave myself to Him&mdash;

And took Himself, for Pay,

The solemn contract of a Life

Was ratified, this way&mdash;

The Wealth might disappoint&mdash; Myself a poorer prove

Than this great Purchaser suspect,

The Daily Own&mdash;of Love

Depreciate the Vision&mdash;

But till the Merchant buy&mdash;

Still Fable&mdash;in the Isles of Spice&mdash; The subtle Cargoes&mdash;lie&mdash; At least&mdash;'tis Mutual&mdash;Risk&mdash; Some&mdash;found it&mdash;Mutual Gain&mdash; Sweet Debt of Life&mdash;Each Night to owe&mdash; Insolvent&mdash;every Noon&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I got so I could take his name


I got so I could take his name&mdash; Without&mdash;Tremendous gain&mdash; That Stop-sensation&mdash;on my Soul&mdash; And Thunder&mdash;in the Room&mdash; I got so I could walk across

That Angle in the floor,

Where he turned so, and I turned&mdash;how&mdash; And all our Sinew tore&mdash;

I got so I could stir the Box&mdash; In which his letters grew

Without that forcing, in my breath&mdash; As Staples&mdash;driven through&mdash; Could dimly recollect a Grace&mdash; I think, they call it "God"&mdash; Renowned to ease Extremity&mdash;

When Formula, had failed&mdash;

And shape my Hands&mdash;

Petition's way,

Tho' ignorant of a word

That Ordination&mdash;utters&mdash; My Business, with the Cloud,

If any Power behind it, be,

Not subject to Despair&mdash;

It care, in some remoter way,

For so minute affair

As Misery&mdash;

Itself, too vast, for interrupting&mdash;more&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I had a guinea golden


I had a guinea golden&mdash;

I lost it in the sand&mdash;

And tho' the sum was simple

And pounds were in the land&mdash; Still, had it such a value

Unto my frugal eye&mdash;

That when I could not find it&mdash; I sat me down to sigh.

I had a crimson Robin&mdash;

Who sang full many a day

But when the woods were painted,

He, too, did fly away&mdash;

Time brought me other Robins&mdash; Their ballads were the same&mdash; Still, for my missing Troubador

I kept the "house at hame."

I had a star in heaven&mdash;

One "Pleiad" was its name&mdash; And when I was not heeding,

It wandered from the same.

And tho' the skies are crowded&mdash; And all the night ashine&mdash;

I do not care about it&mdash;

Since none of them are mine.

My story has a moral&mdash;

I have a missing friend&mdash;

"Pleiad" its name, and Robin, And guinea in the sand.

And when this mournful ditty

Accompanied with tear&mdash;

Shall meet the eye of traitor

In country far from here&mdash;

Grant that repentance solemn

May seize upon his mind&mdash;

And he no consolation

Beneath the sun may find.

Emily Dickinson





I had been hungry all the years-

I had been hungry all the years-

My noon had come, to dine-

I, trembling, drew the table near

And touched the curious wine.

'T was this on tables I had seen

When turning, hungry, lone,

I looked in windows, for the wealth

I could not hope to own.

I did not know the ample bread,

'T was so unlike the crumb

The birds and I had often shared

In Nature's dining-room.

The plenty hurt me, 't was so new,--

Myself felt ill and odd,

As berry of a mountain bush

Transplanted to the road.

Nor was I hungry; so I found

That hunger was a way

Of persons outside windows,

The entering takes away.

Emily Dickinson





I had been hungry, all the Years


I had been hungry, all the Years&mdash; My Noon had Come&mdash;to dine&mdash; I trembling drew the Table near&mdash; And touched the Curious Wine&mdash;

I had no Cause to be awake


I had no Cause to be awake&mdash;

My Best&mdash;was gone to sleep&mdash; And Morn a new politeness took&mdash; And failed to wake them up&mdash;

But called the others&mdash;clear&mdash; And passed their Curtains by&mdash; Sweet Morning&mdash;when I oversleep&mdash; Knock&mdash;Recollect&mdash;to Me&mdash; I looked at Sunrise&mdash;Once&mdash; And then I looked at Them&mdash;

And wishfulness in me arose&mdash; For Circumstance the same&mdash;

'Twas such an Ample Peace&mdash;

It could not hold a Sigh&mdash;

'Twas Sabbath&mdash;with the Bells divorced&mdash;

'Twas Sunset&mdash;all the Day&mdash; So choosing but a Gown&mdash;

And taking but a Prayer&mdash;

The only Raiment I should need&mdash; I struggled&mdash;and was There&mdash; Emily Dickinson

I had no time to Hate&mdash;
