I had no time to hate, because

I had no time to hate, because

The grave would hinder me,

And life was not so ample I

Could finish enmity.

Nor had I time to love, but since

Some industry must be,

The little toil of love, I thought,

Was large enough for me.

I had some things that I called mine


I had some things that I called mine&mdash; And God, that he called his,

Till, recently a rival Claim

Disturbed these amities.

The property, my garden,

Which having sown with care,

He claims the pretty acre,

And sends a Bailiff there.

The station of the parties

Forbids publicity,

But Justice is sublimer

Than arms, or pedigree.

I'll institute an "Action"&mdash; I'll vindicate the law&mdash;

Jove! Choose your counsel&mdash;

I retain "Shaw"!

Emily Dickinson

When lesser Fames invite&mdash;

With one long "Nay"&mdash; Bliss' early shape

Deforming&mdash;Dwindling&mdash;Gulfing up&mdash; Time's possibility.

I have a Bird in spring


I have a Bird in spring

Which for myself doth sing&mdash;

The spring decoys.

And as the summer nears&mdash;

And as the Rose appears,

Robin is gone.

Yet do I not repine

Knowing that Bird of mine

Though flown&mdash;

Learneth beyond the sea

Melody new for me

And will return.

Fast is a safer hand

Held in a truer Land

Are mine&mdash;

And though they now depart,

Tell I my doubting heart

They're thine.

In a serener Bright,

In a more golden light

I see

Each little doubt and fear,

Each little discord here

Removed.

Then will I not repine,

Knowing that Bird of mine

Though flown

Shall in a distant tree

Bright melody for me

Return.

Emily Dickinson





I have a King, who does not speak


I have a King, who does not speak&mdash; So&mdash;wondering&mdash;thro' the hours meek I trudge the day away&mdash;

Half glad when it is night, and sleep, If, haply, thro' a dream, to peep

In parlors, shut by day.

And if I do&mdash;when morning comes&mdash; It is as if a hundred drums

Did round my pillow roll,

And shouts fill all my Childish sky,

And Bells keep saying "Victory"

From steeples in my soul!

And if I don't&mdash;the little Bird Within the Orchard, is not heard,

And I omit to pray

"Father, thy will be done" today For my will goes the other way,

And it were perjury!

Emily Dickinson





I have never seen


I have never seen "Volcanoes"—

But, when Travellers tell

How those old—phlegmatic mountains

Usually so still—

Bear within—appalling Ordnance,

Fire, and smoke, and gun,

Taking Villages for breakfast,

And appalling Men—

If the stillness is Volcanic

In the human face

When upon a pain Titanic

Features keep their place—

If at length the smouldering anguish

Will not overcome—

And the palpitating Vineyard

In the dust, be thrown?

If some loving Antiquary,

On Resumption Morn,

Will not cry with joy "Pompeii"!

To the Hills return!

Emily Dickinson

I haven't told my garden yet


I haven't told my garden yet&mdash; Lest that should conquer me.

I haven't quite the strength now

To break it to the Bee&mdash;

I will not name it in the street

For shops would stare at me&mdash; That one so shy&mdash;so ignorant

Should have the face to die.

The hillsides must not know it&mdash; Where I have rambled so&mdash;

Nor tell the loving forests

The day that I shall go&mdash;

Nor lisp it at the table&mdash;

Nor heedless by the way

Hint that within the Riddle

One will walk today&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I heard a Fly buzz -- when I died --

I heard a Fly buzz -- when I died --

The Stillness in the Room

Was like the Stillness in the Air --

Between the Heaves of Storm --

The Eyes around -- had wrung them dry --

And Breaths were gathering firm

For that last Onset -- when the King

Be witnessed -- in the Room --

I willed my Keepsakes -- signed away

What portion of me be

Assignable -- and then it was

There interposed a Fly --

With Blue -- uncertain stumbling Buzz --

Between the light -- and me --

And then the Windows failed -- and then I could not see to see --

Emily Dickinson

I heard a fly buzz when I died;

I heard a fly buzz when I died;

The stillness round my form

Was like the stillness in the air

Between the heaves of storm.

The eyes beside had wrung them dry,

And breaths were gathering sure

For that last onset, when the king

Be witnessed in his power.

I willed my keepsakes, signed away

What portion of me I

Could make assignable,--and then

There interposed a fly,

With blue, uncertain, stumbling buzz,

Between the light and me;

And then the windows failed, and then

I could not see to see.

Emily Dickinson

I keep my pledge


I keep my pledge.

I was not called&mdash;

Death did not notice me.

I bring my Rose.

I plight again,

By every sainted Bee&mdash;

By Daisy called from hillside&mdash; by Bobolink from lane.

Blossom and I&mdash;

Her oath, and mine&mdash;

Will surely come again.

I know a place where summer strives

I know a place where summer strives

With such a practised frost,

She each year leads her daisies back,

Recording briefly, 'Lost.'

But when the south wind stirs the pools And struggles in the lanes,

Her heart misgives her for her vow,

And she pours soft refrains

Into the lap of adamant,

And spices, and the dew,

That stiffens quietly to quartz

Upon her amber shoe.

Emily Dickinson





I know lives, I could miss


I know lives, I could miss

Without a Misery&mdash;

Others&mdash;whose instant's wanting&mdash; Would be Eternity&mdash;

The last&mdash;a scanty Number&mdash;

'Twould scarcely fill a Two&mdash; The first&mdash;a Gnat's Horizon

Could easily outgrow&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






I know some lonely Houses off the Road A Robber'd like the look of&mdash; Wooden barred,

And Windows hanging low,

Inviting to&mdash;

A Portico,

Where two could creep&mdash;

One&mdash;hand the Tools&mdash; The other peep&mdash;

To make sure All's Asleep&mdash;

Old fashioned eyes&mdash;

Not easy to surprise!

How orderly the Kitchen'd look, by night, With just a Clock&mdash;

But they could gag the Tick&mdash; And Mice won't bark&mdash;

And so the Walls&mdash;don't tell&mdash; None&mdash;will&mdash;

A pair of Spectacles ajar just stir&mdash; An Almanac's aware&mdash;

Was it the Mat&mdash;winked,

Or a Nervous Star?

The Moon&mdash;slides down the stair, To see who's there!

There's plunder&mdash;where&mdash; Tankard, or Spoon&mdash;

Earring&mdash;or Stone&mdash;

A Watch&mdash;Some Ancient Brooch

To match the Grandmama&mdash;

Staid sleeping&mdash;there&mdash; Day&mdash;rattles&mdash;too

Stealth's&mdash;slow&mdash;

The Sun has got as far

As the third Sycamore&mdash;

Screams Chanticleer

"Who's there"?

And Echoes&mdash;Trains away,

Sneer&mdash;"Where"!

While the old Couple, just astir,

Fancy the Sunrise&mdash;left the door ajar!

Emily Dickinson





I know that He exists


I know that He exists.

Somewhere&mdash;in Silence&mdash; He has hid his rare life

From our gross eyes.

'Tis an instant's play.

'Tis a fond Ambush&mdash;

Just to make Bliss

Earn her own surprise!

But&mdash;should the play

Prove piercing earnest&mdash;

Should the glee&mdash;glaze&mdash; In Death's&mdash;stiff&mdash;stare&mdash; Would not the fun

Look too expensive!

Would not the jest&mdash;

Have crawled too far!

Emily Dickinson






I know where Wells grow&mdash;Droughtless Wells&mdash; Deep dug&mdash;for Summer days&mdash; Where Mosses go no more away&mdash; And Pebble&mdash;safely plays&mdash; It's made of Fathoms&mdash;and a Belt&mdash; A Belt of jagged Stone&mdash;

Inlaid with Emerald&mdash;half way down&mdash; And Diamonds&mdash;jumbled on&mdash; It has no Bucket&mdash;Were I rich A Bucket I would buy&mdash;

I'm often thirsty&mdash;but my lips Are so high up&mdash;You see&mdash; I read in an Old fashioned Book

That People "thirst no more"&mdash; The Wells have Buckets to them there&mdash; It must mean that&mdash;I'm sure&mdash; Shall We remember Parching&mdash;then?

Those Waters sound so grand&mdash; I think a little Well&mdash;like Mine&mdash; Dearer to understand&mdash;

I know where Wells grow—Droughtless Wells—

Deep dug—for Summer days—

Where Mosses go no more away—

And Pebble—safely plays—

It's made of Fathoms—and a Belt—

A Belt of jagged Stone—

Inlaid with Emerald—half way down—

And Diamonds—jumbled on—

It has no Bucket—Were I rich

A Bucket I would buy—

I'm often thirsty—but my lips

Are so high up—You see—

I read in an Old fashioned Book

That People "thirst no more"—

The Wells have Buckets to them there—

It must mean that—I'm sure—

Shall We remember Parching—then?

Those Waters sound so grand—

I think a little Well—like Mine—

Dearer to understand—

Emily Dickinson






I learned&mdash;at least&mdash;what Home could be&mdash; How ignorant I had been

Of pretty ways of Covenant&mdash;

How awkward at the Hymn

Round our new Fireside&mdash;but for this&mdash; This pattern&mdash;of the Way&mdash; Whose Memory drowns me, like the Dip

Of a Celestial Sea&mdash;

What Mornings in our Garden&mdash;guessed&mdash; What Bees&mdash;for us&mdash;to hum&mdash; With only Birds to interrupt

The Ripple of our Theme&mdash;

And Task for Both&mdash;

When Play be done&mdash;

Your Problem&mdash;of the Brain&mdash; And mine&mdash;some foolisher effect&mdash; A Ruffle&mdash;or a Tune&mdash; The Afternoons&mdash;Together spent&mdash; And Twilight&mdash;in the Lanes&mdash; Some ministry to poorer lives&mdash; Seen poorest&mdash;thro' our gains&mdash; And then Return&mdash;and Night&mdash;and Home&mdash; And then away to You to pass&mdash; A new&mdash;diviner&mdash;care&mdash; Till Sunrise take us back to Scene&mdash; Transmuted&mdash;Vivider&mdash; This seems a Home&mdash;

I learned—at least—what Home could be


I learned—at least—what Home could be—

How ignorant I had been

Of pretty ways of Covenant—

How awkward at the Hymn

Round our new Fireside—but for this—

This pattern—of the Way—

Whose Memory drowns me, like the Dip

Of a Celestial Sea—

What Mornings in our Garden—guessed—

What Bees—for us—to hum—

With only Birds to interrupt

The Ripple of our Theme—

And Task for Both—

When Play be done—

Your Problem—of the Brain—

And mine—some foolisher effect—

A Ruffle—or a Tune—

The Afternoons—Together spent—

And Twilight—in the Lanes—

Some ministry to poorer lives—

Seen poorest—thro' our gains—

And then Return—and Night—and Home—

And then away to You to pass—

A new—diviner—care—

Till Sunrise take us back to Scene—

Transmuted—Vivider—

This seems a Home—

And Home is not—

But what that Place could be—

Afflicts me—as a Setting Sun—

Where Dawn—knows how to be—

Emily Dickinson





I like a look of Agony


I like a look of Agony,

Because I know it's true&mdash;

Men do not sham Convulsion,

Nor simulate, a Throe&mdash;

The Eyes glaze once&mdash;and that is Death&mdash; Impossible to feign

The Beads upon the Forehead

By homely Anguish strung.

Emily Dickinson





I like to see it lap the Miles


I like to see it lap the Miles&mdash; And lick the Valleys up&mdash;

And stop to feed itself at Tanks&mdash; And then&mdash;prodigious step

Around a Pile of Mountains&mdash;

And supercilious peer

In Shanties&mdash;by the sides of Roads&mdash; And then a Quarry pare

To fit its Ribs

And crawl between

Complaining all the while

In horrid&mdash;hooting stanza&mdash; Then chase itself down Hill&mdash; And neigh like Boanerges&mdash;

Then&mdash;punctual as a Star

Stop&mdash;docile and omnipotent

At its own stable door&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I like to see it lap the miles,

I like to see it lap the miles,

And lick the valleys up,

And stop to feed itself at tanks;

And then, prodigious, step

Around a pile of mountains,

And, supercilious, peer

In shanties by the sides of roads;

And then a quarry pare

To fit its sides, and crawl between,

Complaining all the while

In horrid, hooting stanza;

Then chase itself down hill

And neigh like Boanerges;

Then, punctual as a star,

Stop--docile and omnipotent--

At its own stable door.

Emily Dickinson






I live with Him&mdash;I see His face&mdash; I go no more away

For Visitor&mdash;or Sundown&mdash; Death's single privacy

The Only One&mdash;forestalling Mine&mdash; And that&mdash;by Right that He

Presents a Claim invisible&mdash;

No wedlock&mdash;granted Me&mdash; I live with Him&mdash;I hear His Voice&mdash; I stand alive&mdash;Today&mdash; To witness to the Certainty

Of Immortality&mdash;

Taught Me&mdash;by Time&mdash;the lower Way&mdash; Conviction&mdash;Every day&mdash; That Life like This&mdash;is stopless&mdash; Be Judgment&mdash;what it may&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I live with Him—I see His face


I live with Him—I see His face—

I go no more away

For Visitor—or Sundown—

Death's single privacy

The Only One—forestalling Mine—

And that—by Right that He

Presents a Claim invisible—

No wedlock—granted Me—

I live with Him—I hear His Voice—

I stand alive—Today—

To witness to the Certainty

Of Immortality—

Taught Me—by Time—the lower Way—

Conviction—Every day—

That Life like This—is stopless—

Be Judgment—what it may—

Emily Dickinson





I lived on Dread


I lived on Dread&mdash;

To Those who know

The Stimulus there is

In Danger&mdash;Other impetus

Is numb&mdash;and Vitalless&mdash; As 'twere a Spur&mdash;upon the Soul&mdash; A Fear will urge it where

To go without the Sceptre's aid

Were Challenging Despair.

Emily Dickinson





I lived on dread; to those who know

I lived on dread; to those who know

The stimulus there is

In danger, other impetus

Is numb and vital-less.

As't were a spur upon the soul,

A fear will urge it where

To go without the spectre's aid

Were challenging despair.

Emily Dickinson





I lost a World - the other day!


I lost a World - the other day!

Has Anybody found?

You'll know it by the Row of Stars

Around its forehead bound.

A Rich man&mdash;might not notice it&mdash; Yet&mdash;to my frugal Eye,

Of more Esteem than Ducats&mdash;

Oh find it&mdash;Sir&mdash;for me!

Emily Dickinson





I made slow Riches but my Gain


I made slow Riches but my Gain

Was steady as the Sun

And every Night, it numbered more

Than the preceding One

All Days, I did not earn the same

But my perceiveless Gain

Inferred the less by Growing than

The Sum that it had grown.

Emily Dickinson





I make His Crescent fill or lack


I make His Crescent fill or lack&mdash; His Nature is at Full

Or Quarter&mdash;as I signify&mdash; His Tides&mdash;do I control&mdash; He holds superior in the Sky

Or gropes, at my Command

Behind inferior Clouds&mdash;or round A Mist's slow Colonnade&mdash;

But since We hold a Mutual Disc&mdash; And front a Mutual Day&mdash;

Which is the Despot, neither knows&mdash; Nor Whose&mdash;the Tyranny&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I many times thought Peace had come


I many times thought Peace had come

When Peace was far away&mdash;

As Wrecked Men&mdash;deem they sight the Land&mdash; At Centre of the Sea&mdash;

And struggle slacker&mdash;but to prove As hopelessly as I&mdash;

How many the fictitious Shores&mdash; Before the Harbor be&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I meant to find Her when I came


I meant to find Her when I came&mdash; Death&mdash;had the same design&mdash; But the Success&mdash;was His&mdash;it seems&mdash; And the Surrender&mdash;Mine&mdash; I meant to tell Her how I longed

For just this single time&mdash;

But Death had told Her so the first&mdash; And she had past, with Him&mdash;

To wander&mdash;now&mdash;is my Repose&mdash; To rest&mdash;To rest would be

A privilege of Hurricane

To Memory&mdash;and Me.

Emily Dickinson





I meant to have but modest needs


I meant to have but modest needs&mdash; Such as Content&mdash;and Heaven&mdash; Within my income&mdash;these could lie And Life and I&mdash;keep even&mdash; But since the last&mdash;included both&mdash; It would suffice my Prayer

But just for One&mdash;to stipulate&mdash; And Grace would grant the Pair&mdash; And so&mdash;upon this wise&mdash;I prayed&mdash; Great Spirit&mdash;Give to me

A Heaven not so large as Yours,

But large enough&mdash;for me&mdash; A Smile suffused Jehovah's face&mdash; The Cherubim&mdash;withdrew&mdash; Grave Saints stole out to look at me&mdash; And showed their dimples&mdash;too&mdash; I left the Place, with all my might&mdash; I threw my Prayer away&mdash;

The Quiet Ages picked it up&mdash; And Judgment&mdash;twinkled&mdash;too&mdash; Tat one so honest&mdash;be extant&mdash; It take the Tale for true&mdash;

That "Whatsoever Ye shall ask&mdash; Itself be given You"&mdash;

But I, grown shrewder&mdash;scan the Skies With a suspicious Air&mdash;

As Children&mdash;swindled for the first All Swindlers&mdash;be&mdash;infer&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I measure every grief I meet

I measure every grief I meet

With analytic eyes;

I wonder if it weighs like mine,

Or has an easier size.

I wonder if they bore it long,

Or did it just begin?

I could not tell the date of mine,

It feels so old a pain.

I wonder if it hurts to live,

And if they have to try,

And whether, could they choose between, They would not rather die.

I wonder if when years have piled--

Some thousands--on the cause

Of early hurt, if such a lapse

Could give them any pause;

Or would they go on aching still

Through centuries above,

Enlightened to a larger pain

By contrast with the love.

The grieved are many, I am told;

The reason deeper lies,--

Death is but one and comes but once

And only nails the eyes.

There's grief of want, and grief of cold,--

A sort they call 'despair,'

There's banishment from native eyes,

In sight of native air.

And though I may not guess the kind

Correctly yet to me

A piercing comfort it affords

In passing Calvary,

To note the fashions of the cross

Of those that stand alone

Still fascinated to presume

That some are like my own.

Emily Dickinson






I measure every Grief I meet

With narrow, probing, Eyes--

I wonder if It weighs like Mine--

Or has an Easier size.

I wonder if They bore it long--

Or did it just begin--

I could not tell the Date of Mine--

It feels so old a pain--

I wonder if it hurts to live--

And if They have to try--

And whether--could They choose between--

It would not be--to die--

I note that Some--gone patient long--

At length, renew their smile--

An imitation of a Light

That has so little Oil--

I wonder if when Years have piled--

Some Thousands--on the Harm--

That hurt them early--such a lapse

Could give them any Balm--

Or would they go on aching still

Through Centuries of Nerve--

Enlightened to a larger Pain--

In Contrast with the Love--

The Grieved--are many--I am told--

There is the various Cause--

Death--is but one--and comes but once--

And only nails the eyes--

There's Grief of Want--and grief of Cold--

A sort they call &quot;Despair&quot;--

There's Banishment from native Eyes--

In Sight of Native Air--

And though I may not guess the kind--

Correctly--yet to me

A piercing Comfort it affords

In passing Calvary--

To note the fashions--of the Cross--

And how they're mostly worn--

Still fascinated to presume

That Some--are like My Own--

Emily Dickinson





I ment to find her when I came;

I meant to find her when I came;

Death had the same design;

But the success was his, it seems,

And the discomfit mine.

I meant to tell her how I longed

For just this single time;

But Death had told her so the first,

And she had hearkened him.

To wander now is my abode;

To rest,--to rest would be

A privilege of hurricane

To memory and me.

Emily Dickinson





I met a King this afternoon!


I met a King this afternoon!

He had not on a Crown indeed,

A little Palmleaf Hat was all,

And he was barefoot, I'm afraid!

But sure I am he Ermine wore

Beneath his faded Jacket's blue&mdash; And sure I am, the crest he bore

Within that Jacket's pocket too!

For 'twas too stately for an Earl&mdash; A Marquis would not go so grand!

'Twas possibly a Czar petite&mdash; A Pope, or something of that kind!

If I must tell you, of a Horse

My freckled Monarch held the rein&mdash; Doubtless an estimable Beast,

But not at all disposed to run!

And such a wagon! While I live

Dare I presume to see

Another such a vehicle

As then transported me!

Two other ragged Princes

His royal state partook!

Doubtless the first excursion

These sovereigns ever took!

I question if the Royal Coach

Round which the Footmen wait

Has the significance, on high,

Of this Barefoot Estate!

Emily Dickinson





I never felt at Home&mdash;Below


I never felt at Home&mdash;Below&mdash;-

And in the Handsome Skies

I shall not feel at Home&mdash;I know&mdash; I don't like Paradise&mdash;

Because it's Sunday&mdash;all the time&mdash; And Recess&mdash;never comes&mdash; And Eden'll be so lonesome

Bright Wednesday Afternoons&mdash; If God could make a visit&mdash;

Or ever took a Nap&mdash;

So not to see us&mdash;but they say Himself&mdash;a Telescope

Perennial beholds us&mdash;

Myself would run away

From Him&mdash;and Holy Ghost&mdash;and All&mdash; But there's the "Judgement Day"!

Emily Dickinson

By soldiers battered down,

But I tug childish at my bars, --

Only to fail again!

I never lost as much but twice


I never lost as much but twice,

And that was in the sod.

Twice have I stood a beggar

Before the door of God!

Angels&mdash;twice descending

Reimbursed my store&mdash;

Burglar! Banker&mdash;Father!

I am poor once more!

Emily Dickinson





I Never Saw a Moor

I never saw a moor;

I never saw the sea,

Yet know I how the heather looks

And what a billow be.

I never spoke with God,

Nor visited in heaven.

Yet certain am I of the spot

As if the checks were given.

Emily Dickinson





I never saw a moor,

I never saw a moor,

I never saw the sea;

Yet know I how the heather looks,

And what a wave must be.

I never spoke with God,

Nor visited in heaven;

Yet certain am I of the spot

As if the chart were given.

Emily Dickinson





I never told the buried gold


I never told the buried gold

Upon the hill&mdash;that lies&mdash; I saw the sun&mdash;his plunder done Crouch low to guard his prize.

He stood as near

As stood you here&mdash;

A pace had been between&mdash;

Did but a snake bisect the brake

My life had forfeit been.

That was a wondrous booty&mdash;

I hope 'twas honest gained.

Those were the fairest ingots

That ever kissed the spade!

Whether to keep the secret&mdash;

Whether to reveal&mdash;

Whether as I ponder

Kidd will sudden sail&mdash;

Could a shrewd advise me

We might e'en divide&mdash;

Should a shrewd betray me&mdash;

Atropos decide!

Emily Dickinson





I often passed the village


I often passed the village

When going home from school&mdash; And wondered what they did there&mdash; And why it was so still&mdash;

I did not know the year then&mdash; In which my call would come&mdash; Earlier, by the Dial,

Than the rest have gone.

It's stiller than the sundown.

It's cooler than the dawn&mdash;

The Daisies dare to come here&mdash; And birds can flutter down&mdash;

So when you are tired&mdash;

Or perplexed&mdash;or cold&mdash; Trust the loving promise

Underneath the mould,

Cry "it's I," "take Dollie,"

And I will enfold!

Emily Dickinson

It near as I can guess&mdash;

I play at Riches&mdash;to appease


I play at Riches&mdash;to appease

The Clamoring for Gold&mdash;

It kept me from a Thief, I think,

For often, overbold

With Want, and Opportunity&mdash;

I could have done a Sin

And been Myself that easy Thing

An independent Man&mdash;

But often as my lot displays

Too hungry to be borne

I deem Myself what I would be&mdash; And novel Comforting

My Poverty and I derive&mdash;

We question if the Man&mdash;

Who own&mdash;Esteem the Opulence&mdash; As We&mdash;Who never Can&mdash; Should ever these exploring Hands

Chance Sovereign on a Mine&mdash;

Or in the long&mdash;uneven term

To win, become their turn&mdash;

How fitter they will be&mdash;for Want&mdash; Enlightening so well&mdash;

I know not which, Desire, or Grant&mdash; Be wholly beautiful&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

I prayed, at first, a little Girl


I prayed, at first, a little Girl,

Because they told me to&mdash;

But stopped, when qualified to guess

How prayer would feel&mdash;to me&mdash; If I believed God looked around,

Each time my Childish eye

Fixed full, and steady, on his own

In Childish honesty&mdash;

And told him what I'd like, today,

And parts of his far plan

That baffled me&mdash;

The mingled side

Of his Divinity&mdash;

And often since, in Danger,

I count the force 'twould be

To have a God so strong as that

To hold my life for me

Till I could take the Balance

That tips so frequent, now,

It takes me all the while to poise&mdash; And then&mdash;it doesn't stay&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I read my sentence&mdash;steadily


I read my sentence&mdash;steadily&mdash; Reviewed it with my eyes,

To see that I made no mistake

In its extremest clause&mdash;

The Date, and manner, of the shame&mdash; And then the Pious Form

That "God have mercy" on the Soul The Jury voted Him&mdash;

I made my soul familiar&mdash;with her extremity&mdash; That at the last, it should not be a novel Agony&mdash; But she, and Death, acquainted&mdash; Meet tranquilly, as friends&mdash; Salute, and pass, without a Hint&mdash; And there, the Matter ends&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

I reason, Earth is short


I reason, Earth is short&mdash;

And Anguish&mdash;absolute&mdash; And many hurt,

But, what of that?

I reason, we could die&mdash;

The best Vitality

Cannot excel Decay,

But, what of that?

I reason, that in Heaven&mdash;

Somehow, it will be even&mdash;

Some new Equation, given&mdash;

But, what of that?

I reckon&mdash;when I count it all&mdash; First&mdash;Poets&mdash;Then the Sun&mdash; Then Summer&mdash;Then the Heaven of God&mdash; And then&mdash;the List is done&mdash; But, looking back&mdash;the First so seems To Comprehend the Whole&mdash;

The Others look a needless Show&mdash; So I write&mdash;Poets&mdash;All&mdash; Their Summer&mdash;lasts a Solid Year&mdash; They can afford a Sun

The East&mdash;would deem extravagant&mdash; And if the Further Heaven&mdash;

Be Beautiful as they prepare

For Those who worship Them&mdash;

It is too difficult a Grace&mdash; To justify the Dream&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I reckon—when I count it all


I reckon—when I count it all—

First—Poets—Then the Sun—

Then Summer—Then the Heaven of God—

And then—the List is done—

But, looking back—the First so seems

To Comprehend the Whole—

The Others look a needless Show—

So I write—Poets—All—

Their Summer—lasts a Solid Year—

They can afford a Sun

The East—would deem extravagant—

And if the Further Heaven—

Be Beautiful as they prepare

For Those who worship Them—

It is too difficult a Grace—

To justify the Dream—

Emily Dickinson

Brought out their Burs and mosses

My fantasy to please.

I rose&mdash;because He sank


I rose&mdash;because He sank&mdash; I thought it would be opposite&mdash; But when his power dropped&mdash;

My Soul grew straight.

I cheered my fainting Prince&mdash; I sang firm&mdash;even&mdash;Chants&mdash; I helped his Film&mdash;with Hymn&mdash; And when the Dews drew off

That held his Forehead stiff&mdash; I met him&mdash;

Balm to Balm&mdash;

I told him Best&mdash;must pass

Through this low Arch of Flesh&mdash; No Casque so brave

It spurn the Grave&mdash;

I told him Worlds I knew

Where Emperors grew&mdash;

Who recollected us

If we were true&mdash;

And so with Thews of Hymn&mdash;

And Sinew from within&mdash;

And ways I knew not that I knew&mdash;till then&mdash; I lifted Him&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

I saw no Way&mdash;The Heavens were stitched&mdash; I felt the Columns close&mdash;

The Earth reversed her Hemispheres&mdash; I touched the Universe&mdash;

And back it slid&mdash;and I alone&mdash; A Speck upon a Ball&mdash;

Went out upon Circumference&mdash; Beyond the Dip of Bell&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






I saw no Way—The Heavens were stitched—

I felt the Columns close—

The Earth reversed her Hemispheres—

I touched the Universe—

And back it slid—and I alone—

A Speck upon a Ball—

Went out upon Circumference—

Beyond the Dip of Bell—

Emily Dickinson






I see thee better&mdash;in the Dark&mdash; I do not need a Light&mdash;

The Love of Thee&mdash;a Prism be&mdash; Excelling Violet&mdash;

I see thee better for the Years

That hunch themselves between&mdash; The Miner's Lamp&mdash;sufficient be&mdash; To nullify the Mine&mdash;

And in the Grave&mdash;I see Thee best&mdash; Its little Panels be

Aglow&mdash;All ruddy&mdash;with the Light I held so high, for Thee&mdash;

What need of Day&mdash;

To Those whose Dark&mdash;hath so&mdash;surpassing Sun&mdash; It deem it be&mdash;Continually&mdash; At the Meridian?

Emily Dickinson





I see thee better—in the Dark

I see thee better—in the Dark—

I do not need a Light—

The Love of Thee—a Prism be—

Excelling Violet—

I see thee better for the Years

That hunch themselves between—

The Miner's Lamp—sufficient be—

To nullify the Mine—

And in the Grave—I see Thee best—

Its little Panels be

Aglow—All ruddy—with the Light

I held so high, for Thee—

What need of Day—

To Those whose Dark—hath so—surpassing Sun—

It deem it be—Continually—

At the Meridian?

Emily Dickinson





I send Two Sunsets


I send Two Sunsets&mdash;

Day and I&mdash;in competition ran&mdash; I finished Two&mdash;and several Stars&mdash; While He&mdash;was making One&mdash; His own was ampler&mdash;but as I

Was saying to a friend&mdash;

Mine&mdash;is the more convenient

To Carry in the Hand&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I shall keep singing!


I shall keep singing!

Birds will pass me

On their way to Yellower Climes&mdash; Each&mdash;with a Robin's expectation&mdash; I&mdash;with my Redbreast&mdash; And my Rhymes&mdash;

Late&mdash;when I take my place in summer&mdash; But&mdash;I shall bring a fuller tune&mdash; Vespers&mdash;are sweeter than Matins&mdash;Signor&mdash; Morning&mdash;only the seed of Noon&mdash; Emily Dickinson






I shall know why&mdash;when Time is over&mdash; And I have ceased to wonder why&mdash; Christ will explain each separate anguish In the fair schoolroom of the sky&mdash; He will tell me what "Peter" promised&mdash; And I&mdash;for wonder at his woe&mdash; I shall forget the drop of Anguish

That scalds me now&mdash;that scalds me now!

Emily Dickinson





I shall know why—when Time is over


I shall know why—when Time is over—

And I have ceased to wonder why—

Christ will explain each separate anguish In the fair schoolroom of the sky—

He will tell me what "Peter" promised—

And I—for wonder at his woe—

I shall forget the drop of Anguish

That scalds me now—that scalds me now!

Emily Dickinson





I should have been too glad, I see


I should have been too glad, I see&mdash; Too lifted&mdash;for the scant degree Of Life's penurious Round&mdash;

My little Circuit would have shamed

This new Circumference&mdash;have blamed&mdash; The homelier time behind.

I should have been too saved&mdash;I see&mdash; Too rescued&mdash;Fear too dim to me That I could spell the Prayer

I knew so perfect&mdash;yesterday&mdash; That Scalding One&mdash;Sabachthani&mdash; Recited fluent&mdash;here&mdash; Earth would have been too much&mdash;I see&mdash; And Heaven&mdash;not enough for me&mdash; I should have had the Joy

Without the Fear&mdash;to justify&mdash; The Palm&mdash;without the Calvary&mdash; So Savior&mdash;Crucify&mdash; Defeat&mdash;whets Victory&mdash;they say&mdash; The Reefs&mdash;in old Gethsemane&mdash; Endear the Coast&mdash;beyond!

'Tis Beggars&mdash;Banquets&mdash;can define&mdash;

'Tis Parching&mdash;vitalizes Wine&mdash;

"Faith" bleats&mdash;to understand!

Emily Dickinson





I should not dare to leave my friend


I should not dare to leave my friend,

Because&mdash;because if he should die While I was gone&mdash;and I&mdash;too late&mdash; Should reach the Heart that wanted me&mdash; If I should disappoint the eyes

That hunted&mdash;hunted so&mdash;to see&mdash; And could not bear to shut until

They "noticed" me&mdash;they noticed me&mdash; If I should stab the patient faith

So sure I'd come&mdash;so sure I'd come&mdash; It listening&mdash;listening&mdash;went to sleep&mdash; Telling my tardy name&mdash;

My Heart would wish it broke before&mdash; Since breaking then&mdash;since breaking then&mdash; Were useless as next morning's sun&mdash; Where midnight frosts&mdash;had lain!

Emily Dickinson





I showed her Heights she never saw


I showed her Heights she never saw&mdash;

"Would'st Climb," I said?

She said&mdash;"Not so"&mdash;

"With me&mdash;" I said&mdash;With me?

I showed her Secrets&mdash;Morning's Nest&mdash; The Rope the Nights were put across&mdash; And now&mdash;"Would'st have me for a Guest?"

She could not find her Yes&mdash;

And then, I brake my life&mdash;And Lo, A Light, for her, did solemn glow,

The larger, as her face withdrew&mdash; And could she, further, "No"?

Emily Dickinson





I sing to use the Waiting


I sing to use the Waiting

My Bonnet but to tie

And shut the Door unto my House

No more to do have I

Till His best step approaching

We journey to the Day

And tell each other how We sung

To Keep the Dark away.

Emily Dickinson





I sometimes drop it, for a Quick


I sometimes drop it, for a Quick&mdash; The Thought to be alive&mdash;

Anonymous Delight to know&mdash;

And Madder&mdash;to conceive&mdash; Consoles a Woe so monstrous

That did it tear all Day,

Without an instant's Respite&mdash;

'Twould look too far&mdash;to Die&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I started Early - Took my Dog

I started Early - Took my Dog -

And visited the Sea -

The Mermaids in the Basement

Came out to look at me -

And Frigates - in the Upper Floor

Extended Hempen Hands -

Presuming Me to be a Mouse -

Aground - upon the Sands -

But no Man moved Me - till the Tide

Went past my simple Shoe -

And past my Apron - and my Belt

And past my Bodice - too -

And made as He would eat me up -

As wholly as a Dew

Upon a Dandelion's Sleeve -

And then - I started - too -

And He - He followed - close behind -

I felt His Silver Heel

Upon my Ankle - Then my Shoes

Would overflow with Pearl -

Until We met the Solid Town -

No One He seemed to know -

And bowing - with a Mighty look -

At me - The Sea withdrew -

Emily Dickinson

I stepped from plank to plank

I stepped from plank to plank

So slow and cautiously;

The stars about my head I felt,

About my feet the sea.

I knew not but the next

Would be my final inch,--

This gave me that precarious gait

Some call experience.

Emily Dickinson





I stole them from a Bee


I stole them from a Bee&mdash;

Because&mdash;Thee&mdash;

Sweet plea&mdash;

He pardoned me!

Emily Dickinson





I taste a liquor never brewed

I taste a liquor never brewed,

From tankards scooped in pearl;

Not all the vats upon the Rhine

Yield such an alcohol!

Inebriate of air am I,

And debauchee of dew,

Reeling, through endless summer days,

From inns of molten blue.

When the landlord turn the drunken bee Out of the foxglove's door,

When butterflies renounce their drams, I shall but drink the more!

Till seraphs swing their snowy hats,

And saints to windows run,

To see the little tippler

Leaning against the sun!

Emily Dickinson





I tend my flowers for thee


I tend my flowers for thee&mdash;

Bright Absentee!

My Fuchsia's Coral Seams

Rip&mdash;while the Sower&mdash;dreams&mdash; Geraniums&mdash;tint&mdash;and spot&mdash; Low Daisies&mdash;dot&mdash;

My Cactus&mdash;splits her Beard

To show her throat&mdash;

Carnations&mdash;tip their spice&mdash; And Bees&mdash;pick up&mdash;

A Hyacinth&mdash;I hid&mdash;

Puts out a Ruffled Head&mdash;

And odors fall

From flasks&mdash;so small&mdash; You marvel how they held&mdash;

Globe Roses&mdash;break their satin glake&mdash; Upon my Garden floor&mdash;

Yet&mdash;thou&mdash;not there&mdash; I had as lief they bore

No Crimson&mdash;more&mdash;

Thy flower&mdash;be gay&mdash; Her Lord&mdash;away!

It ill becometh me&mdash;

I'll dwell in Calyx&mdash;Gray&mdash; How modestly&mdash;alway&mdash; Thy Daisy&mdash;

Draped for thee!

Emily Dickinson





I think I was enchanted


I think I was enchanted

When first a sombre Girl&mdash;

I read that Foreign Lady&mdash;

The Dark&mdash;felt beautiful&mdash; And whether it was noon at night&mdash; Or only Heaven&mdash;at Noon&mdash; For very Lunacy of Light

I had not power to tell&mdash;

The Bees&mdash;became as Butterflies&mdash; The Butterflies&mdash;as Swans&mdash; Approached&mdash;and spurned the narrow Grass&mdash; And just the meanest Tunes

That Nature murmured to herself

To keep herself in Cheer&mdash;

I took for Giants&mdash;practising Titanic Opera&mdash;

The Days&mdash;to Mighty Metres stept&mdash; The Homeliest&mdash;adorned

As if unto a Jubilee

'Twere suddenly confirmed&mdash;

I could not have defined the change&mdash; Conversion of the Mind

Like Sanctifying in the Soul&mdash; Is witnessed&mdash;not explained&mdash;

'Twas a Divine Insanity&mdash;

The Danger to be Sane

Should I again experience&mdash;

'Tis Antidote to turn&mdash;

To Tomes of solid Witchcraft&mdash; Magicians be asleep&mdash;

But Magic&mdash;hath an Element

Like Deity&mdash;to keep&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I think just how my shape will rise


I think just how my shape will rise&mdash; When I shall be "forgiven"&mdash; Till Hair&mdash;and Eyes&mdash;and timid Head&mdash; Are out of sight&mdash;in Heaven&mdash; I think just how my lips will weigh&mdash; With shapeless&mdash;quivering&mdash;prayer&mdash; That you&mdash;so late&mdash;"Consider" me&mdash; The "Sparrow" of your Care&mdash; I mind me that of Anguish&mdash;sent&mdash; Some drifts were moved away&mdash; Before my simple bosom&mdash;broke&mdash; And why not this&mdash;if they?

And so I con that thing&mdash;"forgiven"&mdash; Until&mdash;delirious&mdash;borne&mdash; By my long bright&mdash;and longer&mdash;trust&mdash; I drop my Heart&mdash;unshriven!

Emily Dickinson





I think the Hemlock likes to stand


I think the Hemlock likes to stand

Upon a Marge of Snow&mdash;

It suits his own Austerity&mdash;

And satisfies an awe

That men, must slake in Wilderness&mdash; And in the Desert&mdash;cloy&mdash; An instinct for the Hoar, the Bald&mdash; Lapland's&mdash;necessity&mdash; The Hemlock's nature thrives&mdash;on cold&mdash; The Gnash of Northern winds

Is sweetest nutriment&mdash;to him&mdash; His best Norwegian Wines&mdash;

To satin Races&mdash;he is nought&mdash; But Children on the Don,

Beneath his Tabernacles, play,

And Dnieper Wrestlers, run.

Emily Dickinson





I think the longest Hour of all


I think the longest Hour of all

Is when the Cars have come&mdash;

And we are waiting for the Coach&mdash; It seems as though the Time

Indignant&mdash;that the Joy was come&mdash; Did block the Gilded Hands&mdash;

And would not let the Seconds by&mdash; But slowest instant&mdash;ends&mdash; The Pendulum begins to count&mdash; Like little Scholars&mdash;loud&mdash; The steps grow thicker&mdash;in the Hall&mdash; The Heart begins to crowd&mdash;

Then I&mdash;my timid service done&mdash; Tho' service 'twas, of Love&mdash; Take up my little Violin&mdash;

And further North&mdash;remove.

Emily Dickinson






I think to Live&mdash;may be a Bliss To those who dare to try&mdash;

Beyond my limit to conceive&mdash; My lip&mdash;to testify&mdash; I think the Heart I former wore

Could widen&mdash;till to me

The Other, like the little Bank

Appear&mdash;unto the Sea&mdash; I think the Days&mdash;could every one In Ordination stand&mdash;

And Majesty&mdash;be easier&mdash; Than an inferior kind&mdash;

No numb alarm&mdash;lest Difference come&mdash; No Goblin&mdash;on the Bloom&mdash; No start in Apprehension's Ear,

No Bankruptcy&mdash;no Doom&mdash; But Certainties of Sun&mdash;

Midsummer&mdash;in the Mind&mdash; A steadfast South&mdash;upon the Soul&mdash; Her Polar time&mdash;behind&mdash; The Vision&mdash;pondered long&mdash; So plausible becomes

That I esteem the fiction&mdash;real&mdash; The Real&mdash;fictitious seems&mdash; How bountiful the Dream&mdash;

What Plenty&mdash;it would be&mdash; Had all my Life but been Mistake

Just rectified&mdash;in Thee

Emily Dickinson





I think to Live—may be a Bliss


I think to Live—may be a Bliss

To those who dare to try—

Beyond my limit to conceive—

My lip—to testify—

I think the Heart I former wore

Could widen—till to me

The Other, like the little Bank

Appear—unto the Sea—

I think the Days—could every one

In Ordination stand—

And Majesty—be easier—

Than an inferior kind—

No numb alarm—lest Difference come—

No Goblin—on the Bloom—

No start in Apprehension's Ear,

No Bankruptcy—no Doom—

But Certainties of Sun—

Midsummer—in the Mind—

A steadfast South—upon the Soul—

Her Polar time—behind—

The Vision—pondered long—

So plausible becomes

That I esteem the fiction—real—

The Real—fictitious seems—

How bountiful the Dream—

What Plenty—it would be—

Had all my Life but been Mistake

Just rectified—in Thee

Emily Dickinson






I tie my Hat&mdash;I crease my Shawl&mdash; Life's little duties do&mdash;precisely&mdash; As the very least

Were infinite&mdash;to me&mdash; I put new Blossoms in the Glass&mdash; And throw the old&mdash;away&mdash; I push a petal from my gown

That anchored there&mdash;I weigh

The time 'twill be till six o'clock

I have so much to do&mdash;

And yet&mdash;Existence&mdash;some way back&mdash; Stopped&mdash;struck&mdash;my tickling&mdash;through&mdash; We cannot put Ourself away

As a completed Man

Or Woman&mdash;When the Errand's done We came to Flesh&mdash;upon&mdash; There may be&mdash;Miles on Miles of Nought&mdash; Of Action&mdash;sicker far&mdash; To simulate&mdash;is stinging work&mdash; To cover what we are

From Science&mdash;and from Surgery&mdash; Too Telescopic Eyes

To bear on us unshaded&mdash;

For their&mdash;sake&mdash;not for Ours&mdash;

'Twould start them&mdash;

We&mdash;could tremble&mdash;

But since we got a Bomb&mdash;

And held it in our Bosom&mdash;

Nay&mdash;Hold it&mdash;it is calm&mdash; Therefore&mdash;we do life's labor&mdash; Though life's Reward&mdash;be done&mdash; With scrupulous exactness&mdash;

To hold our Senses&mdash;on&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I tie my Hat—I crease my Shawl


I tie my Hat—I crease my Shawl—

Life's little duties do—precisely—

As the very least

Were infinite—to me—

I put new Blossoms in the Glass—

And throw the old—away—

I push a petal from my gown

That anchored there—I weigh

The time 'twill be till six o'clock

I have so much to do—

And yet—Existence—some way back—

Stopped—struck—my tickling—through—

We cannot put Ourself away

As a completed Man

Or Woman—When the Errand's done

We came to Flesh—upon—

There may be—Miles on Miles of Nought—

Of Action—sicker far—

To simulate—is stinging work—

To cover what we are

From Science—and from Surgery—

Too Telescopic Eyes

To bear on us unshaded—

For their—sake—not for Ours—

'Twould start them—

We—could tremble—

But since we got a Bomb—

And held it in our Bosom—

Nay—Hold it—it is calm—

Therefore—we do life's labor—

Though life's Reward—be done—

With scrupulous exactness—

To hold our Senses—on—

Emily Dickinson





I took my Power in my Hand


I took my Power in my Hand&mdash;

And went against the World&mdash;

'Twas not so much as David&mdash;had&mdash; But I&mdash;was twice as bold&mdash; I aimed by Pebble&mdash;but Myself Was all the one that fell&mdash;

Was it Goliath&mdash;was too large&mdash; Or was myself&mdash;too small?

Emily Dickinson





I tried to think a lonelier Thing


I tried to think a lonelier Thing

Than any I had seen&mdash;

Some Polar Expiation&mdash;An Omen in the Bone Of Death's tremendous nearness&mdash; I probed Retrieverless things

My Duplicate&mdash;to borrow&mdash; A Haggard Comfort springs

From the belief that Somewhere&mdash; Within the Clutch of Thought&mdash; There dwells one other Creature

Of Heavenly Love&mdash;forgot&mdash; I plucked at our Partition

As One should pry the Walls&mdash; Between Himself&mdash;and Horror's Twin&mdash; Within Opposing Cells&mdash;

I almost strove to clasp his Hand,

Such Luxury&mdash;it grew&mdash; That as Myself&mdash;could pity Him&mdash; Perhaps he&mdash;pitied me&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I want—it pleaded—All its life—

"I want"—it pleaded—All its life—

I want—was chief it said

When Skill entreated it—the last—

And when so newly dead—

I could not deem it late—to hear

That single—steadfast sigh—

The lips had placed as with a "Please"

Toward Eternity—

Emily Dickinson





I was the slightest in the House


I was the slightest in the House&mdash; I took the smallest Room&mdash;

At night, my little Lamp, and Book&mdash; And one Geranium&mdash;

So stationed I could catch the Mint

That never ceased to fall&mdash;

And just my Basket&mdash;

Let me think&mdash;I'm sure&mdash; That this was all&mdash;

I never spoke&mdash;unless addressed&mdash; And then, 'twas brief and low&mdash; I could not bear to live&mdash;aloud&mdash; The Racket shamed me so&mdash;

And if it had not been so far&mdash; And any one I knew

Were going&mdash;I had often thought How noteless&mdash;I could die&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I watched the Moon around the House


I watched the Moon around the House

Until upon a Pane&mdash;

She stopped&mdash;a Traveller's privilege&mdash;for Rest&mdash; And there upon

I gazed&mdash;as at a stranger&mdash; The Lady in the Town

Doth think no incivility

To lift her Glass&mdash;upon&mdash; But never Stranger justified

The Curiosity

Like Mine&mdash;for not a Foot&mdash;nor Hand&mdash; Nor Formula&mdash;had she&mdash; But like a Head&mdash;a Guillotine Slid carelessly away&mdash;

Did independent, Amber&mdash;

Sustain her in the sky&mdash;

Or like a Stemless Flower&mdash;

Upheld in rolling Air

By finer Gravitations&mdash;

Than bind Philosopher&mdash;

No Hunger&mdash;had she&mdash;nor an Inn&mdash; Her Toilette&mdash;to suffice&mdash; Nor Avocation&mdash;nor Concern

For little Mysteries

As harass us&mdash;like Life&mdash;and Death&mdash; And Afterwards&mdash;or Nay&mdash; But seemed engrossed to Absolute&mdash; With shining&mdash;and the Sky&mdash; The privilege to scrutinize

Was scarce upon my Eyes

When, with a Silver practise&mdash; She vaulted out of Gaze&mdash;

And next&mdash;I met her on a Cloud&mdash; Myself too far below

To follow her superior Road&mdash; Or its advantage&mdash;Blue&mdash; Emily Dickinson






Until upon a Pane --

She stopped -- a Traveller's privilege -- for Rest --

And there upon

I gazed -- as at a stranger --

The Lady in the Town

Doth think no incivility

To lift her Glass -- upon --

But never Stranger justified

The Curiosity

Like Mine -- for not a Foot -- nor Hand --

Nor Formula -- had she --

But like a Head -- a Guillotine

Slid carelessly away --

Did independent, Amber --

Sustain her in the sky --

Or like a Stemless Flower --

Upheld in rolling Air

By finer Gravitations --

Than bind Philosopher --

No Hunger -- had she -- nor an Inn --

Her Toilette -- to suffice --

Nor Avocation nor Concern

for little Mysteries

As harass us -- like Life -- and Death --

And Afterwards -- or Nay --

But seemed engrossed to Absolute --

With shining -- and the Sky --

The privilege to scrutinize

Was scarce upon my Eyes

When, with a Silver practise --

She vaulted out of Gaze --

And next -- I met her on a Cloud --

Myself too far below

To follow her superior Road --

Or its advantage -- Blue --

Emily Dickinson





I went to Heaven


I went to Heaven&mdash;

'Twas a small Town&mdash;

Lit&mdash;with a Ruby&mdash;

Lathed&mdash;with Down&mdash;

Stiller&mdash;than the fields

At the full Dew&mdash;

Beautiful&mdash;as Pictures&mdash; No Man drew.

People&mdash;like the Moth&mdash; Of Mechlin&mdash;frames&mdash; Duties&mdash;of Gossamer&mdash; And Eider&mdash;names&mdash;

Almost&mdash;contented&mdash;

I&mdash;could be&mdash;

'Mong such unique

Society&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I went to heaven,--

I went to heaven,--

'T was a small town,

Lit with a ruby,

Lathed with down.

Stiller than the fields

At the full dew,

Beautiful as pictures

No man drew.

People like the moth,

Of mechlin, frames,

Duties of gossamer,

And eider names.

Almost contented

I could be

'Mong such unique

Society.

Emily Dickinson





I went to thank Her


I went to thank Her&mdash;

But She Slept&mdash;

Her Bed&mdash;a funneled Stone&mdash; With Nosegays at the Head and Foot&mdash; That Travellers&mdash;had thrown&mdash; Who went to thank Her&mdash;

But She Slept&mdash;

'Twas Short&mdash;to cross the Sea&mdash; To look upon Her like&mdash;alive&mdash; But turning back&mdash;'twas slow&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I would distil a cup


I would distil a cup,

And bear to all my friends,

Drinking to her no more astir,

By beck, or burn, or moor!

Emily Dickinson





I would not paint&mdash;a picture


I would not paint&mdash;a picture&mdash; I'd rather be the One

Its bright impossibility

To dwell&mdash;delicious&mdash;on&mdash; And wonder how the fingers feel

Whose rare&mdash;celestial&mdash;stir&mdash; Evokes so sweet a Torment&mdash;

Such sumptuous&mdash;Despair&mdash; I would not talk, like Cornets&mdash; I'd rather be the One

Raised softly to the Ceilings&mdash; And out, and easy on&mdash;

Through Villages of Ether&mdash;

Myself endued Balloon

By but a lip of Metal&mdash;

The pier to my Pontoon&mdash;

Nor would I be a Poet&mdash;

It's finer&mdash;own the Ear&mdash; Enamored&mdash;impotent&mdash;content&mdash; The License to revere,

A privilege so awful

What would the Dower be,

Had I the Art to stun myself

With Bolts of Melody!

Emily Dickinson





I would not paint—a picture


I would not paint—a picture—

I'd rather be the One

Its bright impossibility

To dwell—delicious—on—

And wonder how the fingers feel

Whose rare—celestial—stir—

Evokes so sweet a Torment—

Such sumptuous—Despair—

I would not talk, like Cornets—

I'd rather be the One

Raised softly to the Ceilings—

And out, and easy on—

Through Villages of Ether—

Myself endued Balloon

By but a lip of Metal—

The pier to my Pontoon—

Nor would I be a Poet—

It's finer—own the Ear—

Enamored—impotent—content—

The License to revere,

A privilege so awful

What would the Dower be,

Had I the Art to stun myself

With Bolts of Melody!

Emily Dickinson





I Years had been from Home


I Years had been from Home

And now before the Door

I dared not enter, lest a Face

I never saw before

Stare solid into mine

And ask my Business there&mdash;

"My Business but a Life I left

Was such remaining there?"

I leaned upon the Awe&mdash;

I lingered with Before&mdash;

The Second like an Ocean rolled

And broke against my ear&mdash;

I laughed a crumbling Laugh

That I could fear a Door

Who Consternation compassed

And never winced before.

I fitted to the Latch

My Hand, with trembling care

Lest back the awful Door should spring And leave me in the Floor&mdash;

Then moved my Fingers off

As cautiously as Glass

And held my ears, and like a Thief

Fled gasping from the House&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I years had been from home,

I years had been from home,

And now, before the door,

I dared not open, lest a face

I never saw before

Stare vacant into mine

And ask my business there.

My business,--just a life I left,

Was such still dwelling there?

I fumbled at my nerve,

I scanned the windows near;

The silence like an ocean rolled,

And broke against my ear.

I laughed a wooden laugh

That I could fear a door,

Who danger and the dead had faced,

But never quaked before.

I fitted to the latch

My hand, with trembling care,

Lest back the awful door should spring, And leave me standing there.

I moved my fingers off

As cautiously as glass,

And held my ears, and like a thief

Fled gasping from the house.

Emily Dickinson





I’ll tell you how the sun rose

I’ll tell you how the sun rose, -

A ribbon at a time.

The steeples swam in amethyst,

The news like squirrels ran.

The hills untied their bonnets,

The bobolinks begun.

Then I said softly to myself,

"That must have been the sun!"

But how he set, I know not.

There seemed a purple stile.

Which little yellow boys and girls

Were climbing all the while

Till when they reached the other side, A dominie in gray

Put gently up the evening bars,

And led the flock away.

Emily Dickinson





Ideals are the Fairly Oil


Ideals are the Fairly Oil

With which we help the Wheel

But when the Vital Axle turns

The Eye rejects the Oil.

Emily Dickinson






If any sink, assure that this, now standing&mdash; Failed like Themselves&mdash;and conscious that it rose&mdash; Grew by the Fact, and not the Understanding How Weakness passed&mdash;or Force&mdash;arose&mdash; Tell that the Worst, is easy in a Moment&mdash; Dread, but the Whizzing, before the Ball&mdash; When the Ball enters, enters Silence&mdash; Dying&mdash;annuls the power to kill.

Emily Dickinson





If anybody's friend be dead


If anybody's friend be dead

It's sharpest of the theme

The thinking how they walked alive&mdash; At such and such a time&mdash;

Their costume, of a Sunday,

Some manner of the Hair&mdash;

A prank nobody knew but them

Lost, in the Sepulchre&mdash;

How warm, they were, on such a day,

You almost feel the date&mdash;

So short way off it seems&mdash;

And now&mdash;they're Centuries from that&mdash; How pleased they were, at what you said&mdash; You try to touch the smile

And dip your fingers in the frost&mdash; When was it&mdash;Can you tell&mdash; You asked the Company to tea&mdash; Acquaintance&mdash;just a few&mdash; And chatted close with this Grand Thing That don't remember you&mdash;

Past Bows, and Invitations&mdash;

Past Interview, and Vow&mdash;

Past what Ourself can estimate&mdash; That&mdash;makes the Quick of Woe!

Emily Dickinson






If Blame be my side&mdash;forfeit Me&mdash; But doom me not to forfeit Thee&mdash; To forfeit Thee? The very name

Is sentence from Belief&mdash;and House&mdash; Emily Dickinson





If Blame be my side—forfeit Me


If Blame be my side—forfeit Me—

But doom me not to forfeit Thee—

To forfeit Thee? The very name

Is sentence from Belief—and House—

Emily Dickinson






If He dissolve&mdash;then&mdash;there is nothing&mdash;more&mdash; Eclipse&mdash;at Midnight&mdash; It was dark&mdash;before&mdash; Sunset&mdash;at Easter&mdash;

Blindness&mdash;on the Dawn&mdash; Faint Star of Bethlehem&mdash;

Gone down!

Would but some God&mdash;inform Him&mdash; Or it be too late!

Say&mdash;that the pulse just lisps&mdash; The Chariots wait&mdash;

Say&mdash;that a little life&mdash;for His&mdash; Is leaking&mdash;red&mdash;

His little Spaniel&mdash;tell Him!

Will He heed?

Emily Dickinson





If He dissolve—then—there is nothing


If He dissolve—then—there is nothing—more—

Eclipse—at Midnight—

It was dark—before—

Sunset—at Easter—

Blindness—on the Dawn—

Faint Star of Bethlehem—

Gone down!

Would but some God—inform Him—

Or it be too late!

Say—that the pulse just lisps—

The Chariots wait—

Say—that a little life—for His—

Is leaking—red—

His little Spaniel—tell Him!

Will He heed?

Emily Dickinson






If He were living&mdash;dare I ask&mdash; And how if He be dead&mdash;

And so around the Words I went&mdash; Of meeting them&mdash;afraid&mdash; I hinted Changes&mdash;Lapse of Time&mdash; The Surfaces of Years&mdash;

I touched with Caution&mdash;lest they crack&mdash; And show me to my fears&mdash;

Reverted to adjoining Lives&mdash; Adroitly turning out

Wherever I suspected Graves&mdash;

'Twas prudenter&mdash;I thought&mdash; And He&mdash;I pushed&mdash;with sudden force&mdash; In face of the Suspense&mdash;

"Was buried"&mdash;"Buried"! "He!"

My Life just holds the Trench&mdash; Emily Dickinson





If He were living—dare I ask


If He were living—dare I ask—

And how if He be dead—

And so around the Words I went—

Of meeting them—afraid—

I hinted Changes—Lapse of Time—

The Surfaces of Years—

I touched with Caution—lest they crack—

And show me to my fears—

Reverted to adjoining Lives—

Adroitly turning out

Wherever I suspected Graves—

'Twas prudenter—I thought—

And He—I pushed—with sudden force—

In face of the Suspense—

"Was buried"—"Buried"! "He!"

My Life just holds the Trench—

Emily Dickinson





If I Can Stop One Heart from Breaking

If I can stop one heart from breaking, I shall not live in vain;

If I can ease one life the aching,

Or cool one pain,

Or help one fainting robin

Unto his nest again,

I shall not live in vain.

Emily Dickinson





If I can stop one heart from breaking, If I can stop one heart from breaking, I shall not live in vain;

If I can ease one life the aching,

Or cool one pain,

Or help one fainting robin

Unto his nest again,

I shall not live in vain.

Emily Dickinson





If I could bribe them by a Rose


If I could bribe them by a Rose

I'd bring them every flower that grows From Amherst to Cashmere!

I would not stop for night, or storm&mdash; Or frost, or death, or anyone&mdash; My business were so dear!

If they would linger for a Bird

My Tambourin were soonest heard

Among the April Woods!

Unwearied, all the summer long,

Only to break in wilder song

When Winter shook the boughs!

What if they hear me!

Who shall say

That such an importunity

May not at last avail?

That, weary of this Beggar's face&mdash; They may not finally say, Yes&mdash; To drive her from the Hall?

Emily Dickinson





If I may have it, when it's dead


If I may have it, when it's dead,

I'll be contented&mdash;so&mdash; If just as soon as Breath is out

It shall belong to me&mdash;

Until they lock it in the Grave,

'Tis Bliss I cannot weigh&mdash;

For tho' they lock Thee in the Grave,

Myself&mdash;can own the key&mdash; Think of it Lover! I and Thee

Permitted&mdash;face to face to be&mdash; After a Life&mdash;a Death&mdash;We'll say&mdash; For Death was That&mdash;

And this&mdash;is Thee&mdash;

I'll tell Thee All&mdash;how Bald it grew&mdash; How Midnight felt, at first&mdash;to me&mdash; How all the Clocks stopped in the World&mdash; And Sunshine pinched me&mdash;'Twas so cold&mdash; Then how the Grief got sleepy&mdash;some&mdash; As if my Soul were deaf and dumb&mdash; Just making signs&mdash;across&mdash;to Thee&mdash; That this way&mdash;thou could'st notice me&mdash; I'll tell you how I tried to keep

A smile, to show you, when this Deep

All Waded&mdash;We look back for Play, At those Old Times&mdash;in Calvary, Forgive me, if the Grave come slow&mdash; For Coveting to look at Thee&mdash; Forgive me, if to stroke thy frost

Outvisions Paradise!

Emily Dickinson





If I should cease to bring a Rose


If I should cease to bring a Rose

Upon a festal day,

'Twill be because beyond the Rose

I have been called away&mdash;

If I should cease to take the names

My buds commemorate&mdash;

'Twill be because Death's finger

Claps my murmuring lip!

Emily Dickinson





If I should die


If I should die,

And you should live&mdash;

And time should gurgle on&mdash;

And morn should beam&mdash;

And noon should burn&mdash;

As it has usual done&mdash;

If Birds should build as early

And Bees as bustling go&mdash;

One might depart at option

From enterprise below!

'Tis sweet to know that stocks will stand When we with Daisies lie&mdash;

That Commerce will continue&mdash; And Trades as briskly fly&mdash;

It makes the parting tranquil

And keeps the soul serene&mdash;

That gentlemen so sprightly

Conduct the pleasing scene!

Emily Dickinson





If I shouldn't be alive


If I shouldn't be alive

When the Robins come,

Give the one in Red Cravat,

A Memorial crumb.

If I couldn't thank you,

Being fast asleep,

You will know I'm trying

Why my Granite lip!

Emily Dickinson





If I'm lost&mdash;now


If I'm lost&mdash;now

That I was found&mdash;

Shall still my transport be&mdash; That once&mdash;on me&mdash;those Jasper Gates Blazed open&mdash;suddenly&mdash; That in my awkward&mdash;gazing&mdash;face&mdash; The Angels&mdash;softly peered&mdash; And touched me with their fleeces,

Almost as if they cared&mdash;

I'm banished&mdash;now&mdash;you know it&mdash; How foreign that can be&mdash;

You'll know&mdash;Sir&mdash;when the Savior's face Turns so&mdash;away from you&mdash; Emily Dickinson





If I'm lost—now


If I'm lost—now

That I was found—

Shall still my transport be—

That once—on me—those Jasper Gates

Blazed open—suddenly—

That in my awkward—gazing—face—

The Angels—softly peered—

And touched me with their fleeces,

Almost as if they cared—

I'm banished—now—you know it—

How foreign that can be—

You'll know—Sir—when the Savior's face Turns so—away from you—

Emily Dickinson





If it had no pencil


If it had no pencil

Would it try mine&mdash;

Worn&mdash;now&mdash;and dull&mdash;sweet, Writing much to thee.

If it had no word,

Would it make the Daisy,

Most as big as I was,

When it plucked me?

Emily Dickinson





If pain for peace prepares


If pain for peace prepares

Lo, what "Augustan" years

Our feet await!

If springs from winter rise,

Can the Anemones

Be reckoned up?

If night stands fast&mdash;then noon To gird us for the sun,

What gaze!

When from a thousand skies

On our developed eyes

Noons blaze!

Emily Dickinson





If recollecting were forgetting


If recollecting were forgetting,

Then I remember not.

And if forgetting, recollecting,

How near I had forgot.

And if to miss, were merry,

And to mourn, were gay,

How very blithe the fingers

That gathered this, Today!

Emily Dickinson





If she had been the Mistletoe


If she had been the Mistletoe

And I had been the Rose&mdash;

How gay upon your table

My velvet life to close&mdash;

Since I am of the Druid,

And she is of the dew&mdash;

I'll deck Tradition's buttonhole&mdash; And send the Rose to you.

Emily Dickinson





If the foolish, call them


If the foolish, call them "flowers"—

Need the wiser, tell?

If the Savants "Classify" them It is just as well!

Those who read the "Revelations"

Must not criticize

Those who read the same Edition—

With beclouded Eyes!

Could we stand with that Old "Moses"—

"Canaan" denied—

Scan like him, the stately landscape

On the other side—

Doubtless, we should deem superfluous

Many Sciences,

Not pursued by learned Angels

In scholastic skies!

Low amid that glad Belles lettres

Grant that we may stand,

Stars, amid profound Galaxies—

At that grand "Right hand"!

Emily Dickinson

If this is "fading"


If this is "fading"

Oh let me immediately "fade"!

If this is "dying"

Bury me, in such a shroud of red!

If this is "sleep,"

On such a night

How proud to shut the eye!

Good Evening, gentle Fellow men!

Peacock presumes to die!

Emily Dickinson





If those I loved were lost


If those I loved were lost

The Crier's voice would tell me&mdash; If those I loved were found

The bells of Ghent would ring&mdash; Did those I loved repose

The Daisy would impel me.

Philip&mdash;when bewildered

Bore his riddle in!

Emily Dickinson

If you were coming in the Fall


If you were coming in the Fall,

I'd brush the Summer by

With half a smile, and half a spurn,

As Housewives do, a Fly.

If I could see you in a year,

I'd wind the months in balls&mdash; And put them each in separate Drawers, For fear the numbers fuse&mdash;

If only Centuries, delayed,

I'd count them on my Hand,

Subtracting, till my fingers dropped

Into Van Dieman's Land.

If certain, when this life was out&mdash; That yours and mine, should be

I'd toss it yonder, like a Rind,

And take Eternity&mdash;

But, now, uncertain of the length

Of this, that is between,

It goads me, like the Goblin Bee&mdash; That will not state&mdash;its sting.

Emily Dickinson





If you were coming in the fall,

If you were coming in the fall,

I'd brush the summer by

With half a smile and half a spum,

As housewives do a fly.

If I could see you in a year,

I'd wind the months in balls,

And put them each in separate drawers, Until their time befalls.

If only centuries delayed,

I'd count them on my hand,

Subtracting till my fingers dropped

Into Van Diemen's land.

If certain, when this life was out,

That yours and mine should be,

I'd toss it yonder like a rind,

And taste eternity.

But now, all ignorant of the length

Of time's uncertain wing,

It goads me, like the goblin bee,

That will not state its sting.

Emily Dickinson





If your Nerve, deny you


If your Nerve, deny you&mdash;

Go above your Nerve&mdash;

He can lean against the Grave,

If he fear to swerve&mdash;

That's a steady posture&mdash;

Never any bend

Held of those Brass arms&mdash;

Best Giant made&mdash;

If your Soul seesaw&mdash;

Lift the Flesh door&mdash;

The Poltroon wants Oxygen&mdash;

Nothing more&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I'll clutch&mdash;and clutch


I'll clutch&mdash;and clutch&mdash; Next&mdash;One&mdash;Might be the golden touch&mdash; Could take it&mdash;

Diamonds&mdash;Wait&mdash;

I'm diving&mdash;just a little late&mdash; But stars&mdash;go slow&mdash;for night&mdash; I'll string you&mdash;in fine Necklace&mdash; Tiaras&mdash;make&mdash;of some&mdash; Wear you on Hem&mdash;

Loop up a Countess&mdash;with you&mdash; Make&mdash;a Diadem&mdash;and mend my old One&mdash; Count&mdash;Hoard&mdash;then lose&mdash; And doubt that you are mine&mdash; To have the joy of feeling it&mdash;again&mdash; I'll show you at the Court&mdash;

Bear you&mdash;for Ornament

Where Women breathe&mdash;

That every sigh&mdash;may lift you Just as high&mdash;as I&mdash; And&mdash;when I die&mdash;

In meek array&mdash;display you&mdash; Still to show&mdash;how rich I go&mdash; Lest Skies impeach a wealth so wonderful&mdash; And banish me&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I'll clutch—and clutch


I'll clutch—and clutch—

Next—One—Might be the golden touch—

Could take it—

Diamonds—Wait—

I'm diving—just a little late—

But stars—go slow—for night—

I'll string you—in fine Necklace—

Tiaras—make—of some—

Wear you on Hem—

Loop up a Countess—with you—

Make—a Diadem—and mend my old One—

Count—Hoard—then lose—

And doubt that you are mine—

To have the joy of feeling it—again—

I'll show you at the Court—

Bear you—for Ornament

Where Women breathe—

That every sigh—may lift you

Just as high—as I—

And—when I die—

In meek array—display you—

Still to show—how rich I go—

Lest Skies impeach a wealth so wonderful—

And banish me—

Emily Dickinson





I'll send the feather from my Hat!


I'll send the feather from my Hat!

Who knows&mdash;but at the sight of that My Sovereign will relent?

As trinket&mdash;worn by faded Child&mdash; Confronting eyes long&mdash;comforted&mdash; Blisters the Adamant!

Emily Dickinson





I'll tell you how the Sun rose


I'll tell you how the Sun rose&mdash; A Ribbon at a time&mdash;

The Steeples swam in Amethyst&mdash; The news, like Squirrels, ran&mdash; The Hills untied their Bonnets&mdash; The Bobolinks&mdash;begun&mdash; Then I said softly to myself&mdash;

That little Yellow boys and girls

I'll tell you how the sun rose, --

I'll tell you how the sun rose, --

A ribbon at a time.

The steeples swam in amethyst,

The news like squirrels ran.

The hill untied their bonnets,

The bobolinks begun.

Then I said softly to myself,

'That must have been the sun!'

...................................

But how he set, I know not.

There seemed a purple stile

Which little yellow boys and girls

Were climbing all the while

Till when they reached the other side, A dominie in gray

Put gently up the evening bars, --

And led the flock away.

Emily Dickinson





I'm


I'm "wife"—I've finished that—

That other state—

I'm Czar—I'm "Woman" now—

It's safer so—

How odd the Girl's life looks

Behind this soft Eclipse—

I think that Earth feels so

To folks in Heaven—now—

This being comfort—then

That other kind—was pain—

But why compare?

I'm "Wife"! Stop there!

Emily Dickinson






I'm "wife"&mdash;I've finished that&mdash; That other state&mdash;

I'm Czar&mdash;I'm "Woman" now&mdash; It's safer so&mdash;

How odd the Girl's life looks

Behind this soft Eclipse&mdash;

I think that Earth feels so

To folks in Heaven&mdash;now&mdash; This being comfort&mdash;then

That other kind&mdash;was pain&mdash; But why compare?

I'm "Wife"! Stop there!

Emily Dickinson






I'm ceded&mdash;I've stopped being Theirs&mdash; The name They dropped upon my face

With water, in the country church

Is finished using, now,

And They can put it with my Dolls,

My childhood, and the string of spools, I've finished threading&mdash;too&mdash; Baptized, before, without the choice,

But this time, consciously, of Grace&mdash; Unto supremest name&mdash;

Called to my Full&mdash;The Crescent dropped&mdash; Existence's whole Arc, filled up,

With one small Diadem.

My second Rank&mdash;too small the first&mdash; Crowned&mdash;Crowing&mdash;on my Father's breast&mdash; A half unconscious Queen&mdash;

But this time&mdash;Adequate&mdash;Erect, With Will to choose, or to reject,

And I choose, just a Crown&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I'm ceded—I've stopped being Theirs


I'm ceded—I've stopped being Theirs—

The name They dropped upon my face

With water, in the country church

Is finished using, now,

And They can put it with my Dolls,

My childhood, and the string of spools, I've finished threading—too—

Baptized, before, without the choice,

But this time, consciously, of Grace—

Unto supremest name—

Called to my Full—The Crescent dropped—

Existence's whole Arc, filled up,

With one small Diadem.

My second Rank—too small the first—

Crowned—Crowing—on my Father's breast—

A half unconscious Queen—

But this time—Adequate—Erect,

With Will to choose, or to reject,

And I choose, just a Crown—

Emily Dickinson





I'm nobody! Who are you?

I'm nobody! Who are you?

Are you nobody, too?

Then there's a pair of us -- don't tell!

They'd advertise -- you know!

How dreary to be somebody!

How public like a frog

To tell one's name the livelong day

To an admiring bog!

Emily Dickinson






I'm Nobody! Who are you?

Are you--Nobody--too?

Then there's a pair of us?

Don't tell! they'd advertise--you know!

How dreary--to be--Somebody!

How public--like a Frog--

To tell one's name--the livelong June--

To an admiring Bog!

Emily Dickinson





I'm saying every day


I'm saying every day

"If I should be a Queen, tomorrow"&mdash; I'd do this way&mdash;

And so I deck, a little,

If it be, I wake a Bourbon,

None on me, bend supercilious&mdash; With "This was she&mdash;

Begged in the Market place&mdash;

Yesterday."

Court is a stately place&mdash;

I've heard men say&mdash;

So I loop my apron, against the Majesty With bright Pins of Buttercup&mdash; That not too plain&mdash;

Rank&mdash;overtake me&mdash;

And perch my Tongue

On Twigs of singing&mdash;rather high&mdash; But this, might be my brief Term

To qualify&mdash;

Put from my simple speech all plain word&mdash; Take other accents, as such I heard

Though but for the Cricket&mdash;just, And but for the Bee&mdash;

Not in all the Meadow&mdash;

One accost me&mdash;

Better to be ready&mdash;

Than did next morn

Meet me in Aragon&mdash;

My old Gown&mdash;on&mdash;

And the surprised Air

Rustics&mdash;wear&mdash;

Summoned&mdash;unexpectedly&mdash; To Exeter&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






I'm sorry for the Dead&mdash;Today&mdash; It's such congenial times

Old Neighbors have at fences&mdash; It's time o' year for Hay.

And Broad&mdash;Sunburned Acquaintance Discourse between the Toil&mdash;

And laugh, a homely species

That makes the Fences smile&mdash; It seems so straight to lie away

From all of the noise of Fields&mdash; The Busy Carts&mdash;the fragrant Cocks&mdash; The Mower's Metre&mdash;Steals&mdash; A Trouble lest they're homesick&mdash; Those Farmers&mdash;and their Wives&mdash; Set separate from the Farming&mdash; And all the Neighbors' lives&mdash; A Wonder if the Sepulchre

Don't feel a lonesome way&mdash;

When Men&mdash;and Boys&mdash;and Carts&mdash;and June, Go down the Fields to "Hay"&mdash; Emily Dickinson





I'm sorry for the Dead—Today


I'm sorry for the Dead—Today—

It's such congenial times

Old Neighbors have at fences—

It's time o' year for Hay.

And Broad—Sunburned Acquaintance

Discourse between the Toil—

And laugh, a homely species

That makes the Fences smile—

It seems so straight to lie away

From all of the noise of Fields—

The Busy Carts—the fragrant Cocks—

The Mower's Metre—Steals—

A Trouble lest they're homesick—

Those Farmers—and their Wives—

Set separate from the Farming—

And all the Neighbors' lives—

A Wonder if the Sepulchre

Don't feel a lonesome way—

When Men—and Boys—and Carts—and June,

Go down the Fields to "Hay"—

Emily Dickinson





I'm the little


I'm the little "Heart's Ease"!

I don't care for pouting skies!

If the Butterfly delay

Can I, therefore, stay away?

If the Coward Bumble Bee

In his chimney corner stay,

I, must resoluter be!

Who'll apologize for me?

Dear, Old fashioned, little flower!

Eden is old fashioned, too!

Birds are antiquated fellows!

Heaven does not change her blue.

Nor will I, the little Heart's Ease—

Ever be induced to do!

Emily Dickinson

Heaven does not change her blue.

Nor will I, the little Heart's Ease&mdash; Ever be induced to do!

Emily Dickinson





Impossibility, like Wine


Impossibility, like Wine

Exhilarates the Man

Who tastes it; Possibility

Is flavorless&mdash;Combine

A Chance's faintest Tincture

And in the former Dram

Enchantment makes ingredient

As certainly as Doom&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





In Ebon Box, when years have flown


In Ebon Box, when years have flown

To reverently peer,

Wiping away the velvet dust

Summers have sprinkled there!

To hold a letter to the light&mdash; Grown Tawny now, with time&mdash;

To con the faded syllables

That quickened us like Wine!

Perhaps a Flower's shrivelled check

Among its stores to find&mdash;

Plucked far away, some morning&mdash; By gallant&mdash;mouldering hand!

A curl, perhaps, from foreheads

Our Constancy forgot&mdash;

Perhaps, an Antique trinket&mdash; In vanished fashions set!

And then to lay them quiet back&mdash; And go about its care&mdash;

As if the little Ebon Box

Were none of our affair!

Emily Dickinson





In falling Timbers buried


In falling Timbers buried&mdash;

There breathed a Man&mdash;

Outside&mdash;the spades&mdash;were plying&mdash; The Lungs&mdash;within&mdash;

Could He&mdash;know&mdash;they sought Him&mdash; Could They&mdash;know&mdash;He breathed&mdash; Horrid Sand Partition&mdash;

Neither&mdash;could be heard&mdash; Never slacked the Diggers&mdash;

But when Spades had done&mdash;

Oh, Reward of Anguish,

It was dying&mdash;Then&mdash; Many Things&mdash;are fruitless&mdash;

'Tis a Baffling Earth&mdash;

But there is no Gratitude

Like the Grace&mdash;of Death&mdash; Emily Dickinson






In lands I never saw&mdash;they say Immortal Alps look down&mdash;

Whose Bonnets touch the firmament&mdash; Whose Sandals touch the town&mdash; Meek at whose everlasting feet

A Myriad Daisy play&mdash;

Which, Sir, are you and which am I

Upon an August day?

Emily Dickinson

In rags mysterious as these


In rags mysterious as these

The shining Courtiers go&mdash;

Veiling the purple, and the plumes&mdash; Veiling the ermine so.

Smiling, as they request an alms&mdash; At some imposing door!

Smiling when we walk barefoot

Upon their golden floor!

Emily Dickinson





In Winter in my Room


In Winter in my Room

I came upon a Worm&mdash;

Pink, lank and warm&mdash;

But as he was a worm

And worms presume

Not quite with him at home&mdash;

Secured him by a string

To something neighboring

And went along.

A Trifle afterward

A thing occurred

I'd not believe it if I heard

But state with creeping blood&mdash; A snake with mottles rare

Surveyed my chamber floor

In feature as the worm before

But ringed with power&mdash;

The very string with which

I tied him&mdash;too

When he was mean and new

That string was there&mdash;

I shrank&mdash;"How fair you are"!

Propitiation's claw&mdash;

"Afraid," he hissed

"Of me"?

"No cordiality"&mdash;

He fathomed me&mdash;

Then to a Rhythm Slim

Secreted in his Form

As Patterns swim

Projected him.

That time I flew

Both eyes his way

Lest he pursue

Nor ever ceased to run

Till in a distant Town

Towns on from mine

I set me down

This was a dream.

Emily Dickinson





Inconceivably solemn!


Inconceivably solemn!

Things go gay

Pierce&mdash;by the very Press

Of Imagery&mdash;

Their far Parades&mdash;order on the eye With a mute Pomp&mdash;

A pleading Pageantry&mdash;

Flags, are a brave sight&mdash;

But no true Eye

Ever went by One&mdash;

Steadily&mdash;

Music's triumphant&mdash;

But the fine Ear

Winces with delight

Are Drums too near&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Is Bliss then, such Abyss


Is Bliss then, such Abyss,

I must not put my foot amiss

For fear I spoil my shoe?

I'd rather suit my foot

Than save my Boot&mdash;

For yet to buy another Pair

Is possible,

At any store&mdash;

But Bliss, is sold just once.

The Patent lost

None buy it any more&mdash;

Say, Foot, decide the point&mdash; The Lady cross, or not?

Verdict for Boot!

Emily Dickinson





Is it dead&mdash;Find it


Is it dead&mdash;Find it&mdash; Out of sound&mdash;Out of sight&mdash;

"Happy"? Which is wiser&mdash; You, or the Wind?

"Conscious"? Won't you ask that&mdash; Of the low Ground?

"Homesick"? Many met it&mdash; Even through them&mdash;This

Cannot testify&mdash;

Themself&mdash;as dumb&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

Is it true, dear Sue?


Is it true, dear Sue?

Are there two?

I shouldn't like to come

For fear of joggling Him!

If I could shut him up

In a Coffee Cup,

Or tie him to a pin

Till I got in&mdash;

Or make him fast

To "Toby's" fist&mdash;

Hist! Whist! I'd come!

It always felt to me&mdash;a wrong To that Old Moses&mdash;done&mdash; To let him see&mdash;the Canaan&mdash; Without the entering&mdash;

And tho' in soberer moments&mdash; No Moses there can be

I'm satisfied&mdash;the Romance

In point of injury&mdash;

Surpasses sharper stated&mdash;

Of Stephen&mdash;or of Paul&mdash; For these&mdash;were only put to death&mdash; While God's adroiter will

On Moses&mdash;seemed to fasten

With tantalizing Play

As Boy&mdash;should deal with lesser Boy&mdash; To prove ability.

The fault&mdash;was doubtless Israel's&mdash; Myself&mdash;had banned the Tribes&mdash; And ushered Grand Old Moses

In Pentateuchal Robes

Upon the Broad Possession

'Twas little&mdash;But titled Him&mdash;to see&mdash; Old Man on Nebo! Late as this&mdash; My justice bleeds&mdash;for Thee!

Emily Dickinson





It always felt to me—a wrong


It always felt to me—a wrong

To that Old Moses—done—

To let him see—the Canaan—

Without the entering—

And tho' in soberer moments—

No Moses there can be

I'm satisfied—the Romance

In point of injury—

Surpasses sharper stated—

Of Stephen—or of Paul—

For these—were only put to death—

While God's adroiter will

On Moses—seemed to fasten

With tantalizing Play

As Boy—should deal with lesser Boy—

To prove ability.

Myself—had banned the Tribes—

And ushered Grand Old Moses

In Pentateuchal Robes

Upon the Broad Possession
