It bloomed and dropt, a Single Noon


It bloomed and dropt, a Single Noon&mdash; The Flower&mdash;distinct and Red&mdash; I, passing, thought another Noon

Another in its stead

Will equal glow, and thought no More

But came another Day

To find the Species disappeared&mdash; The Same Locality&mdash;

The Sun in place&mdash;no other fraud On Nature's perfect Sum&mdash;

Had I but lingered Yesterday&mdash; Was my retrieveless blame&mdash;

Much Flowers of this and further Zones Have perished in my Hands

For seeking its Resemblance&mdash; But unapproached it stands&mdash;

The single Flower of the Earth

That I, in passing by

Unconscious was&mdash;Great Nature's Face Passed infinite by Me&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





It can't be


It can't be "Summer"!

That—got through!

It's early—yet—for "Spring"!

There's that long town of White—to cross—

Before the Blackbirds sing!

It can't be "Dying"!

It's too Rouge—

The Dead shall go in White—

So Sunset shuts my question down

With Cuffs of Chrysolite!

Emily Dickinson

It ceased to hurt me, though so slow


It ceased to hurt me, though so slow

I could not feel the Anguish go&mdash; But only knew by looking back&mdash; That something&mdash;had benumbed the Track&mdash; Nor when it altered, I could say,

For I had worn it, every day,

As constant as the Childish frock&mdash; I hung upon the Peg, at night.

But not the Grief&mdash;that nestled close As needles&mdash;ladies softly press To Cushions Cheeks&mdash;

To keep their place&mdash;

Nor what consoled it, I could trace&mdash; Except, whereas 'twas Wilderness&mdash; It's better&mdash;almost Peace&mdash; Emily Dickinson





It did not surprise me


It did not surprise me&mdash;

So I said&mdash;or thought&mdash; She will stir her pinions

And the nest forgot,

Traverse broader forests&mdash;

Build in gayer boughs,

Breathe in Ear more modern

God's old fashioned vows&mdash;

This was but a Birdling&mdash;

What and if it be

One within my bosom

Had departed me?

This was but a story&mdash;

What and if indeed

There were just such coffin

In the heart instead?

Emily Dickinson






It don't sound so terrible&mdash;quite&mdash;as it did&mdash; I run it over&mdash;"Dead", Brain, "Dead."

Put it in Latin&mdash;left of my school&mdash; Seems it don't shriek so&mdash;under rule.

Turn it, a little&mdash;full in the face A Trouble looks bitterest&mdash;

Shift it&mdash;just&mdash;

Say "When Tomorrow comes this way&mdash; I shall have waded down one Day."

I suppose it will interrupt me some

Till I get accustomed&mdash;but then the Tomb Like other new Things&mdash;shows largest&mdash;then&mdash; And smaller, by Habit&mdash;

It's shrewder then

Put the Thought in advance&mdash;a Year&mdash; How like "a fit"&mdash;then&mdash; Murder&mdash;wear!

Emily Dickinson






It don't sound so terrible—quite—as it did—

I run it over—"Dead", Brain, "Dead."

Put it in Latin—left of my school—

Seems it don't shriek so—under rule.

Turn it, a little—full in the face

A Trouble looks bitterest—

Shift it—just—

Say "When Tomorrow comes this way—

I shall have waded down one Day."

I suppose it will interrupt me some

Till I get accustomed—but then the Tomb Like other new Things—shows largest—then—

And smaller, by Habit—

It's shrewder then

Put the Thought in advance—a Year—

How like "a fit"—then—

Murder—wear!

Emily Dickinson





It Dropped So Low -- In My Regard --

It dropped so low -- in my Regard --

I heard it hit the Ground --

And go to pieces on the Stones

At bottom of my Mind --

Yet blamed the Fate that flung it -- less Than I denounced Myself,

For entertaining Plated Wares

Upon My Silver Shelf --

Emily Dickinson

Upon my silver shelf.

It feels a shame to be Alive


It feels a shame to be Alive&mdash; When Men so brave&mdash;are dead&mdash; One envies the Distinguished Dust&mdash; Permitted&mdash;such a Head&mdash; The Stone&mdash;that tells defending Whom This Spartan put away

What little of Him we&mdash;possessed In Pawn for Liberty&mdash;

The price is great&mdash;Sublimely paid&mdash; Do we deserve&mdash;a Thing&mdash; That lives&mdash;like Dollars&mdash;must be piled Before we may obtain?

Are we that wait&mdash;sufficient worth&mdash; That such Enormous Pearl

As life&mdash;dissolved be&mdash;for Us&mdash; In Battle's&mdash;horrid Bowl?

It may be&mdash;a Renown to live&mdash; I think the Man who die&mdash;

Those unsustained&mdash;Saviors&mdash; Present Divinity&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





It is a lonesome Glee


It is a lonesome Glee&mdash;

A Bird to overhear

A matter of the Skies.

Emily Dickinson

It knew no Medicine


It knew no Medicine&mdash;

It was not Sickness&mdash;then&mdash; Nor any need of Surgery&mdash;

And therefore&mdash;'twas not Pain&mdash; It moved away the Cheeks&mdash;

A Dimple at a time&mdash;

And left the Profile&mdash;plainer&mdash; And in the place of Bloom

It left the little Tint

That never had a Name&mdash;

You've seen it on a Cast's face&mdash; Was Paradise&mdash;to blame&mdash; If momently ajar&mdash;

Temerity&mdash;drew near&mdash; And sickened&mdash;ever afterward

For Somewhat that it saw?

It makes no difference abroad


It makes no difference abroad&mdash; The Seasons&mdash;fit&mdash;the same&mdash; The Mornings blossom into Noons&mdash; And split their Pods of Flame&mdash; Wild flowers&mdash;kindle in the Woods&mdash; The Brooks slam&mdash;all the Day&mdash; No Black bird bates his Banjo&mdash; For passing Calvary&mdash;

Auto da Fe&mdash;and Judgment&mdash; Are nothing to the Bee&mdash;

His separation from His Rose&mdash; To Him&mdash;sums Misery&mdash; Emily Dickinson





It might be lonelier


It might be lonelier

Without the Loneliness&mdash;

I'm so accustomed to my Fate&mdash; Perhaps the Other&mdash;Peace&mdash; Would interrupt the Dark&mdash;

And crowd the little Room&mdash;

Too scant&mdash;by Cubits&mdash;to contain The Sacrament&mdash;of Him&mdash; I am not used to Hope&mdash;

It might intrude upon&mdash;

Its sweet parade&mdash;blaspheme the place&mdash; Ordained to Suffering&mdash;

It sifts from Leaden Sieves


It sifts from Leaden Sieves&mdash; It powders all the Wood.

It fills with Alabaster Wool

The Wrinkles of the Road&mdash;

It makes an Even Face

Of Mountain, and of Plain&mdash;

Unbroken Forehead from the East

Unto the East again&mdash;

It reaches to the Fence&mdash;

It wraps it Rail by Rail

Till it is lost in Fleeces&mdash;

It deals Celestial Vail

To Stump, and Stack&mdash;and Stem&mdash; A Summer's empty Room&mdash;

Acres of Joints, where Harvests were,

Recordless, but for them--

It Ruffles Wrists of Posts

As Ankles of a Queen&mdash;

Then stills its Artisans&mdash;like Ghosts&mdash; Denying they have been&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





It struck me every day

It struck me every day

The lightning was as new

As if the cloud that instant slit

And let the fire through.

It burned me in the night,

It blistered in my dream;

It sickened fresh upon my sight

With every morning's beam.

I thought that storm was brief,--

The maddest, quickest by;

But Nature lost the date of this,

And left it in the sky.

Emily Dickinson

It troubled me as once I was


It troubled me as once I was&mdash; For I was once a Child&mdash;

Concluding how an Atom&mdash;fell&mdash; And yet the Heavens&mdash;held&mdash; The Heavens weighed the most&mdash;by far&mdash; Yet Blue&mdash;and solid&mdash;stood&mdash; Without a Bolt&mdash;that I could prove&mdash; Would Giants&mdash;understand?

It was a Grave, yet bore no Stone


It was a Grave, yet bore no Stone

Enclosed 'twas not of Rail

A Consciousness its Acre, and

It held a Human Soul.

Entombed by whom, for what offence

If Home or Foreign born&mdash;

Had I the curiosity

'Twere not appeased of men

Till Resurrection, I must guess

Denied the small desire

A Rose upon its Ridge to sow

Or take away a Briar.

Emily Dickinson





It was given to me by the Gods


It was given to me by the Gods&mdash; When I was a little Girl&mdash;

They given us Presents most&mdash;you know&mdash; When we are new&mdash;and small.

I kept it in my Hand&mdash;

I never put it down&mdash;

I did not dare to eat&mdash;or sleep&mdash; For fear it would be gone&mdash;

I heard such words as "Rich"&mdash; When hurrying to school&mdash;

From lips at Corners of the Streets&mdash; And wrestled with a smile.

Rich! 'Twas Myself&mdash;was rich&mdash; To take the name of Gold&mdash;

And Gold to own&mdash;in solid Bars&mdash; The Difference&mdash;made me bold&mdash; Emily Dickinson





It was not Death, for I stood up


It was not Death, for I stood up,

And all the Dead, lie down&mdash;

It was not Night, for all the Bells

Put out their Tongues, for Noon.

It was not Frost, for on my Flesh

I felt Siroccos&mdash;crawl&mdash; Nor Fire&mdash;for just my Marble feet Could keep a Chancel, cool&mdash;

And yet, it tasted, like them all,

The Figures I have seen

Set orderly, for Burial,

Reminded me, of mine&mdash;

As if my life were shaven,

And fitted to a frame,

And could not breathe without a key,

And 'twas like Midnight, some -

When everything that ticked&mdash;has stopped&mdash; And Space stares all around&mdash; Or Grisly frosts&mdash;first Autumn morns, Repeal the Beating Ground&mdash;

But, most, like Chaos - Stopless&mdash;cool&mdash; Without a Change, or Spar&mdash;

Or even a Report of Land&mdash;

To justify&mdash;Despair.

Emily Dickinson





It was not death, for I stood up,

It was not death, for I stood up,

And all the dead lie down;

It was not night, for all the bells

Put out their tongues, for noon.

It was not frost, for on my flesh

I felt siroccos crawl,--

Nor fire, for just my marble feet

Could keep a chancel cool.

And yet it tasted like them all;

The figures I have seen

Set orderly, for burial,

Reminded me of mine,

As if my life were shaven

And fitted to a frame,

And could not breathe without a key;

And 't was like midnight, some,

When everything that ticked has stopped, And space stares, all around,

Or grisly frosts, first autumn morns,

Repeal the beating ground.

But most like chaos,--stopless, cool,--

Without a chance or spar,--

Or even a report of land

To justify despair.

Emily Dickinson

Ladies&mdash;with parasols&mdash; Sauntering Gentlemen&mdash;with Canes&mdash; And little Girls&mdash;with Dolls&mdash; Will tint the pallid landscape&mdash; As 'twere a bright Bouquet&mdash;

It will be Summer—eventually


It will be Summer—eventually.

Ladies—with parasols—

Sauntering Gentlemen—with Canes—

And little Girls—with Dolls—

Will tint the pallid landscape—

As 'twere a bright Bouquet—

Thro' drifted deep, in Parian—

The Village lies—today—

The Lilacs—bending many a year—

Will sway with purple load—

The Bees—will not despise the tune—

Their Forefathers—have hummed—

The Wild Rose—redden in the Bog—

The Aster—on the Hill

Her everlasting fashion—set—

And Covenant Gentians—frill—

Till Summer folds her miracle—

As Women—do—their Gown—

Of Priests—adjust the Symbols—

When Sacrament—is done—

Emily Dickinson





It would have starved a Gnat


It would have starved a Gnat&mdash; To live so small as I&mdash;

And yet I was a living Child&mdash; With Food's necessity

Upon me&mdash;like a Claw&mdash; I could no more remove

Than I could coax a Leech away&mdash; Or make a Dragon&mdash;move&mdash; Not like the Gnat&mdash;had I&mdash; The privilege to fly

And seek a Dinner for myself&mdash; How mightier He&mdash;than I&mdash; Nor like Himself&mdash;the Art

Upon the Window Pane

To gad my little Being out&mdash;

And not begin&mdash;again&mdash; Emily Dickinson






It would never be Common&mdash;more&mdash;I said&mdash; Difference&mdash;had begun&mdash; Many a bitterness&mdash;had been&mdash; But that old sort&mdash;was done&mdash; Or&mdash;if it sometime&mdash;showed&mdash;as 'twill&mdash; Upon the Downiest&mdash;Morn&mdash; Such bliss&mdash;had I&mdash;for all the years&mdash;

'Twould give an Easier&mdash;pain&mdash; I'd so much joy&mdash;I told it&mdash;Red&mdash; Upon my simple Cheek&mdash;

I felt it publish&mdash;in my Eye&mdash;

'Twas needless&mdash;any speak&mdash; I walked&mdash;as wings&mdash;my body bore&mdash; The feet&mdash;I former used&mdash; Unnecessary&mdash;now to me&mdash; As boots&mdash;would be&mdash;to Birds&mdash; I put my pleasure all abroad&mdash; I dealth a word of Gold

To every Creature&mdash;that I met&mdash; And Dowered&mdash;all the World&mdash; When&mdash;suddenly&mdash;my Riches shrank&mdash; A Goblin&mdash;drank my Dew&mdash; My Palaces&mdash;dropped tenantless&mdash; Myself&mdash;was beggared&mdash;too&mdash; I clutched at sounds&mdash;

I groped at shapes&mdash;

I touched the tops of Films&mdash; I felt the Wilderness roll back

Along my Golden lines&mdash;

The Sackcloth&mdash;hangs upon the nail&mdash; The Frock I used to wear&mdash;

But where my moment of Brocade&mdash; My&mdash;drop&mdash;of India?

Emily Dickinson





It would never be Common—more—I said


It would never be Common—more—I said—

Difference—had begun—

Many a bitterness—had been—

But that old sort—was done—

Or—if it sometime—showed—as 'twill—

Upon the Downiest—Morn—

Such bliss—had I—for all the years—

'Twould give an Easier—pain—

I'd so much joy—I told it—Red—

Upon my simple Cheek—

I felt it publish—in my Eye—

'Twas needless—any speak—

I walked—as wings—my body bore—

The feet—I former used—

Unnecessary—now to me—

As boots—would be—to Birds—

I put my pleasure all abroad—

I dealth a word of Gold

To every Creature—that I met—

And Dowered—all the World—

When—suddenly—my Riches shrank—

A Goblin—drank my Dew—

My Palaces—dropped tenantless—

Myself—was beggared—too—

I clutched at sounds—

I groped at shapes—

I touched the tops of Films—

I felt the Wilderness roll back

Along my Golden lines—

The Sackcloth—hangs upon the nail—

The Frock I used to wear—

But where my moment of Brocade—

My—drop—of India?

Emily Dickinson





It's all I have to bring today


It's all I have to bring today&mdash; This, and my heart beside&mdash;

This, and my heart, and all the fields&mdash; And all the meadows wide&mdash;

Be sure you count&mdash;should I forget Some one the sum could tell&mdash; This, and my heart, and all the Bees

Which in the Clover dwell.

Emily Dickinson





It's All I have to bring to-day,

It's All I have to bring to-day,

This, and my heart beside,

This, and my heart, and all the fields, And all the meadows wide.

Be sure you count, should I forget, --

Some one the sum could tell, --

This, and my heart, and all the bees

Which in the clover dwell.

Emily Dickinson






It's coming&mdash;the postponeless Creature&mdash; It gains the Block&mdash;and now&mdash;it gains the Door&mdash; Chooses its latch, from all the other fastenings&mdash; Enters&mdash;with a "You know Me&mdash;Sir"?

Simple Salute&mdash;and certain Recognition&mdash; Bold&mdash;were it Enemy&mdash;Brief&mdash;were it friend&mdash; Dresses each House in Crape, and Icicle&mdash; And carries one&mdash;out of it&mdash;to God&mdash; Emily Dickinson





It's coming—the postponeless Creature


It's coming—the postponeless Creature—

It gains the Block—and now—it gains the Door—

Chooses its latch, from all the other fastenings—

Enters—with a "You know Me—Sir"?

Simple Salute—and certain Recognition—

Bold—were it Enemy—Brief—were it friend—

Dresses each House in Crape, and Icicle—

And carries one—out of it—to God—

Emily Dickinson





It's easy to invent a Life


It's easy to invent a Life&mdash;

God does it&mdash;every Day&mdash; Creation&mdash;but the Gambol

Of His Authority&mdash;

It's easy to efface it&mdash;

The thrifty Deity

Could scarce afford Eternity

To Spontaneity&mdash;

The Perished Patterns murmur&mdash; But His Perturbless Plan

Proceed&mdash;inserting Here&mdash;a Sun&mdash; There&mdash;leaving out a Man&mdash; Emily Dickinson





It's like the Light


It's like the Light&mdash;

A fashionless Delight&mdash;

It's like the Bee&mdash;

A dateless&mdash;Melody&mdash; It's like the Woods&mdash;

Private&mdash;Like the Breeze&mdash; Phraseless&mdash;yet it stirs

The proudest Trees&mdash;

It's like the Morning&mdash;

Best&mdash;when it's done&mdash; And the Everlasting Clocks&mdash;

Chime&mdash;Noon!

Emily Dickinson





It's like the light, --

It's like the light, --

A fashionless delight

It's like the bee, --

A dateless melody.

It's like the woods,

Private like breeze,

Phraseless, yet it stirs

The proudest trees.

It's like the morning, --

Best when it's done, --

The everlasting clocks

Chime noon.

Emily Dickinson





It's such a little thing to weep


It's such a little thing to weep&mdash; So short a thing to sigh&mdash;

And yet&mdash;by Trades&mdash;the size of these We men and women die!

Emily Dickinson






It's thoughts&mdash;and just One Heart&mdash; And Old Sunshine&mdash;about&mdash; Make frugal&mdash;Ones&mdash;Content&mdash; And two or three&mdash;for Company&mdash; Upon a Holiday&mdash;

Crowded&mdash;as Sacrament&mdash; Books&mdash;when the Unit&mdash; Spare the Tenant&mdash;long eno'&mdash; A Picture&mdash;if it Care&mdash; Itself&mdash;a Gallery too rare&mdash; For needing more&mdash;

Flowers&mdash;to keep the Eyes&mdash;from going awkward&mdash; When it snows&mdash;

A Bird&mdash;if they&mdash;prefer&mdash; Though Winter fire&mdash;sing clear as Plover&mdash; To our&mdash;ear&mdash;

A Landscape&mdash;not so great

To suffocate the Eye&mdash;

A Hill&mdash;perhaps&mdash;

Perhaps&mdash;the profile of a Mill Turned by the Wind&mdash;

Tho' such&mdash;are luxuries&mdash; It's thoughts&mdash;and just two Heart&mdash; And Heaven&mdash;about&mdash;

At least&mdash;a Counterfeit&mdash; We would not have Correct&mdash;

And Immortality&mdash;can be almost&mdash; Not quite&mdash;Content&mdash; Emily Dickinson





It's thoughts—and just One Heart

It's thoughts—and just One Heart—

And Old Sunshine—about—

Make frugal—Ones—Content—

And two or three—for Company—

Upon a Holiday—

Crowded—as Sacrament—

Books—when the Unit—

Spare the Tenant—long eno'—

A Picture—if it Care—

Itself—a Gallery too rare—

For needing more—

Flowers—to keep the Eyes—from going awkward—

When it snows—

A Bird—if they—prefer—

Though Winter fire—sing clear as Plover—

To our—ear—

A Landscape—not so great

To suffocate the Eye—

A Hill—perhaps—

Perhaps—the profile of a Mill

Turned by the Wind—

Tho' such—are luxuries—

It's thoughts—and just two Heart—

And Heaven—about—

At least—a Counterfeit—

We would not have Correct—

And Immortality—can be almost—

Not quite—Content—

Emily Dickinson





I've heard an Organ talk, sometimes


I've heard an Organ talk, sometimes

In a Cathedral Aisle,

And understood no word it said&mdash; Yet held my breath, the while&mdash; And risen up&mdash;and gone away,

A more Berdardine Girl&mdash;

Yet&mdash;know not what was done to me In that old Chapel Aisle.

Emily Dickinson





I've known a Heaven, like a Tent


I've known a Heaven, like a Tent&mdash; To wrap its shining Yards&mdash;

Pluck up its stakes, and disappear&mdash; Without the sound of Boards

Or Rip of Nail&mdash;Or Carpenter&mdash; But just the miles of Stare&mdash; That signalize a Show's Retreat&mdash; In North America&mdash;

No Trace&mdash;no Figment of the Thing That dazzled, Yesterday,

No Ring&mdash;no Marvel&mdash; Men, and Feats&mdash;

Dissolved as utterly&mdash;

As Bird's far Navigation

Discloses just a Hue&mdash;

A plash of Oars, a Gaiety&mdash;

Then swallowed up, of View.

Emily Dickinson





I've none to tell me to but Thee


I've none to tell me to but Thee

So when Thou failest, nobody.

It was a little tie&mdash;

It just held Two, nor those it held

Since Somewhere thy sweet Face has spilled Beyond my Boundary&mdash;

If things were opposite&mdash;and Me And Me it were&mdash;that ebbed from Thee On some unanswering Shore&mdash;

Would'st Thou seek so&mdash;just say That I the Answer may pursue

Unto the lips it eddied through&mdash; So&mdash;overtaking Thee&mdash; Emily Dickinson






I've nothing else&mdash;to bring, You know&mdash; So I keep bringing These&mdash;

Just as the Night keeps fetching Stars To our familiar eyes&mdash;

Maybe, we shouldn't mind them&mdash; Unless they didn't come&mdash;

Then&mdash;maybe, it would puzzle us To find our way Home&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





I've nothing else—to bring, You know


I've nothing else—to bring, You know—

So I keep bringing These—

Just as the Night keeps fetching Stars To our familiar eyes—

Maybe, we shouldn't mind them—

Unless they didn't come—

Then—maybe, it would puzzle us

To find our way Home—

Emily Dickinson





I've seen a Dying Eye


I've seen a Dying Eye

Run round and round a Room&mdash;

In search of Something&mdash;as it seemed&mdash; Then Cloudier become&mdash;

And then&mdash;obscure with Fog&mdash; And then&mdash;be soldered down

Without disclosing what it be

'Twere blessed to have seen&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Jesus! thy Crucifix


Jesus! thy Crucifix

Enable thee to guess

The smaller size!

Jesus! thy second face

Mind thee in Paradise

Of ours!

Emily Dickinson





Joy to have merited the Pain


Joy to have merited the Pain&mdash; To merit the Release&mdash;

Joy to have perished every step&mdash; To Compass Paradise&mdash;

Pardon&mdash;to look upon thy face&mdash; With these old fashioned Eyes&mdash; Better than new&mdash;could be&mdash;for that&mdash; Though bought in Paradise&mdash;

Because they looked on thee before&mdash; And thou hast looked on them&mdash; Prove Me&mdash;My Hazel Witnesses

The features are the same&mdash;

So fleet thou wert, when present&mdash; So infinite&mdash;when gone&mdash; An Orient's Apparition&mdash;

Remanded of the Morn&mdash;

The Height I recollect&mdash;

'Twas even with the Hills&mdash;

The Depth upon my Soul was notched&mdash; As Floods&mdash;on Whites of Wheels&mdash; To Haunt&mdash;till Time have dropped His last Decade away,

And Haunting actualize&mdash;to last At least&mdash;Eternity&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Just as He spoke it from his Hands


Just as He spoke it from his Hands

This Edifice remain&mdash;

A Turret more, a Turret less

Dishonor his Design&mdash;

According as his skill prefer

It perish, or endure&mdash;

Content, soe'er, it ornament

His absent character.

Emily Dickinson





Just lost, when I was saved!


Just lost, when I was saved!

Just felt the world go by!

Just girt me for the onset with Eternity, When breath blew back,

And on the other side

I heard recede the disappointed tide!

Therefore, as One returned, I feel

Odd secrets of the line to tell!

Some Sailor, skirting foreign shores&mdash; Some pale Reporter, from the awful doors Before the Seal!

Next time, to stay!

Next time, the things to see

By Ear unheard,

Unscrutinized by Eye&mdash;

Next time, to tarry,

While the Ages steal&mdash;

Slow tramp the Centuries,

And the Cycles wheel!

Emily Dickinson






Just so&mdash;Jesus&mdash;raps&mdash; He&mdash;doesn't weary&mdash;

Last&mdash;at the Knocker&mdash; And first&mdash;at the Bell.

Then&mdash;on divinest tiptoe&mdash;standing&mdash; Might He but spy the lady's soul&mdash; When He&mdash;retires&mdash;

Chilled&mdash;or weary&mdash;

It will be ample time for&mdash;me&mdash; Patient&mdash;upon the steps&mdash;until then&mdash; Hears! I am knocking&mdash;low at thee.

Emily Dickinson

Kill your Balm&mdash;and its Odors bless you&mdash; Bare your Jessamine&mdash;to the storm&mdash; And she will fling her maddest perfume&mdash; Haply&mdash;your Summer night to Charm&mdash; Stab the Bird&mdash;that built in your bosom&mdash; Oh, could you catch her last Refrain&mdash; Bubble! "forgive"&mdash;"Some better"&mdash;Bubble!

"Carol for Him&mdash;when I am gone"!

Emily Dickinson






Kill your Balm—and its Odors bless you—

Bare your Jessamine—to the storm—

And she will fling her maddest perfume—

Haply—your Summer night to Charm—

Stab the Bird—that built in your bosom—

Oh, could you catch her last Refrain—

Bubble! "forgive"—"Some better"—Bubble!

"Carol for Him—when I am gone"!

Emily Dickinson





Knows how to forget!


Knows how to forget!

But could It teach it?

Easiest of Arts, they say

When one learn how

Dull Hearts have died

In the Acquisition

Sacrificed for Science

Is common, though, now&mdash;

I went to School

But was not wiser

Globe did not teach it

Nor Logarithm Show

"How to forget"!

Say&mdash;some&mdash;Philosopher!

Ah, to be erudite

Enough to know!

Is it in a Book?

So, I could buy it&mdash;

Is it like a Planet?

Telescopes would know&mdash;

If it be invention

It must have a Patent.

Rabbi of the Wise Book

Don't you know?

Emily Dickinson





Least Bee that brew


Least Bee that brew&mdash;

A Honey's Weight

Content Her smallest fraction help

The Amber Quantity&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






Least Rivers&mdash;docile to some sea.

My Caspian&mdash;thee.

Emily Dickinson





Least Rivers—docile to some sea


Least Rivers—docile to some sea.

My Caspian—thee.

Emily Dickinson





Let Us play Yesterday


Let Us play Yesterday&mdash;

I&mdash;the Girl at school&mdash; You&mdash;and Eternity&mdash;the Untold Tale&mdash;

Easing my famine

At my Lexicon&mdash;

Logarithm&mdash;had I&mdash;for Drink&mdash;

'Twas a dry Wine&mdash;

Somewhat different&mdash;must be&mdash; Dreams tint the Sleep&mdash;

Cunning Reds of Morning

Make the Blind&mdash;leap&mdash; Still at the Egg-life&mdash;

Chafing the Shell&mdash;

When you troubled the Ellipse&mdash; And the Bird fell&mdash;

Manacles be dim&mdash;they say&mdash; To the new Free&mdash;

Liberty&mdash;Commoner&mdash;

Never could&mdash;to me&mdash;

'Twas my last gratitude

When I slept&mdash;at night&mdash;

'Twas the first Miracle

Let in&mdash;with Light&mdash; Can the Lark resume the Shell&mdash; Easier&mdash;for the Sky&mdash; Wouldn't Bonds hurt more

Than Yesterday?

Wouldn't Dungeons sorer frate

On the Man&mdash;free&mdash;

Just long enough to taste&mdash;

Then&mdash;doomed new&mdash;

God of the Manacle

As of the Free&mdash;

Take not my Liberty

Away from Me&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Life&mdash;is what we make of it


Life&mdash;is what we make of it&mdash; Death&mdash;we do not know&mdash; Christ's acquaintance with Him

Justify Him&mdash;though&mdash; He&mdash;would trust no stranger&mdash; Other&mdash;could betray&mdash; Just His own endorsement&mdash;

That&mdash;sufficeth Me&mdash; All the other Distance

He hath traversed first&mdash;

No New Mile remaineth&mdash;

Far as Paradise&mdash;

His sure foot preceding&mdash;

Tender Pioneer&mdash;

Base must be the Coward

Dare not venture&mdash;now&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Life, and Death, and Giants


Life, and Death, and Giants&mdash; Such as These&mdash;are still&mdash; Minor&mdash;Apparatus&mdash;Hopper of the Mill&mdash; Beetle at the Candle&mdash;

Or a Fife's Fame&mdash;

Maintain&mdash;by Accident that they proclaim&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Life—is what we make of it


Life—is what we make of it—

Death—we do not know—

Christ's acquaintance with Him

Justify Him—though—

He—would trust no stranger—

Other—could betray—

Just His own endorsement—

That—sufficeth Me—

All the other Distance

He hath traversed first—

No New Mile remaineth—

Far as Paradise—

His sure foot preceding—

Tender Pioneer—

Base must be the Coward

Dare not venture—now—

Emily Dickinson





Light is sufficient to itself


Light is sufficient to itself&mdash; If Others want to see

It can be had on Window Panes

Some Hours in the Day.

But not for Compensation&mdash;

It holds as large a Glow

To Squirrel in the Himmaleh

Precisely, as to you.

Emily Dickinson





Like eyes that looked on Wastes


Like eyes that looked on Wastes&mdash; Incredulous of Ought

But Blank&mdash;and steady Wilderness&mdash; Diversified by Night&mdash;

Just Infinites of Nought&mdash;

As far as it could see&mdash;

So looked the face I looked upon&mdash; So looked itself&mdash;on Me&mdash; I offered it no Help&mdash;

Because the Cause was Mine&mdash;

The Misery a Compact

As hopeless&mdash;as divine&mdash; Neither&mdash;would be absolved&mdash; Neither would be a Queen

Without the Other&mdash;Therefore&mdash; We perish&mdash;tho' We reign&mdash; Emily Dickinson






Like Flowers, that heard the news of Dews, But never deemed the dripping prize

Awaited their&mdash;low Brows&mdash; Or Bees&mdash;that thought the Summer's name Some rumor of Delirium,

No Summer&mdash;could&mdash;for Them&mdash; Or Arctic Creatures, dimly stirred&mdash; By Tropic Hint&mdash;some Travelled Bird Imported to the Wood&mdash;

Or Wind's bright signal to the Ear&mdash; Making that homely, and severe,

Contented, known, before&mdash;

The Heaven&mdash;unexpected come,

To Lives that thought the Worshipping

A too presumptuous Psalm&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Like her the Saints retire


Like her the Saints retire,

In their Chapeaux of fire,

Martial as she!

Like her the Evenings steal

Purple and Cochineal

After the Day!

"Departed"&mdash;both&mdash;they say!

i.e. gathered away,

Not found,

Argues the Aster still&mdash;

Reasons the Daffodil

Profound!

Emily Dickinson






Like Mighty Foot Lights&mdash;burned the Red At Bases of the Trees&mdash;

The far Theatricals of Day

Exhibiting&mdash;to These&mdash;

'Twas Universe&mdash;that did applaud&mdash; While Chiefest&mdash;of the Crowd&mdash; Enabled by his Royal Dress&mdash;

Myself distinguished God&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






Like Mighty Foot Lights—burned the Red At Bases of the Trees—

The far Theatricals of Day

Exhibiting—to These—

'Twas Universe—that did applaud—

While Chiefest—of the Crowd—

Enabled by his Royal Dress—

Myself distinguished God—

Emily Dickinson





Like Some Old fashioned Miracle


Like Some Old fashioned Miracle

When Summertime is done&mdash;

Seems Summer's Recollection

And the Affairs of June

As infinite Tradition

As Cinderella's Bays&mdash;

Or Little John&mdash;of Lincoln Green&mdash; Or Blue Beard's Galleries&mdash;

Her Bees have a fictitious Hum&mdash; Her Blossoms, like a Dream&mdash;

Elate us&mdash;till we almost weep&mdash; So plausible&mdash;they seem&mdash; Her Memories like Strains&mdash;Review&mdash; When Orchestra is dumb&mdash;

The Violin in Baize replaced&mdash; And Ear&mdash;and Heaven&mdash;numb&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Like trains of cars on tracks of plush Like trains of cars on tracks of plush I hear the level bee:

A jar across the flowers goes,

Their velvet masonry

Withstands until the sweet assault

Their chivalry consumes,

While he, victorious, tilts away

To vanquish other blooms.

His feet are shod with gauze,

His helmet is of gold;

His breast, a single onyx

With chrysoprase, inlaid.

His labor is a chant,

His idleness a tune;

Oh, for a bee's experience

Of clovers and of noon!

Emily Dickinson






Love reckons by itself&mdash;alone&mdash;

"As large as I"&mdash;relate the Sun To One who never felt it blaze&mdash; Itself is all the like it has&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Love reckons by itself—alone


Love reckons by itself—alone—

"As large as I"—relate the Sun To One who never felt it blaze—

Itself is all the like it has—

Emily Dickinson





Love&mdash;is anterior to Life


Love&mdash;is anterior to Life&mdash; Posterior&mdash;to Death&mdash; Initial of Creation, and

The Exponent of Earth&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






Love&mdash;is that later Thing than Death&mdash; More previous&mdash;than Life&mdash; Confirms it at its entrance&mdash;And Usurps it&mdash;of itself&mdash; Tastes Death&mdash;the first&mdash;to hand the sting The Second&mdash;to its friend&mdash; Disarms the little interval&mdash; Deposits Him with God&mdash;

Then hovers&mdash;an inferior Guard&mdash; Lest this Beloved Charge

Need&mdash;once in an Eternity&mdash; A smaller than the Large&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Love&mdash;thou art high


Love&mdash;thou art high&mdash; I cannot climb thee&mdash;

But, were it Two&mdash;

Who know but we&mdash;

Taking turns&mdash;at the Chimborazo&mdash; Ducal&mdash;at last&mdash;stand up by thee&mdash; Love&mdash;thou are deep&mdash; I cannot cross thee&mdash;

But, were there Two

Instead of One&mdash;

Rower, and Yacht&mdash;some sovereign Summer&mdash; Who knows&mdash;but we'd reach the Sun?

Love&mdash;thou are Veiled&mdash; A few&mdash;behold thee&mdash; Smile&mdash;and alter&mdash;and prattle&mdash;and die&mdash; Bliss&mdash;were an Oddity&mdash;without thee&mdash; Nicknamed by God&mdash;

Eternity&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Love—is anterior to Life


Love—is anterior to Life—

Posterior—to Death—

Initial of Creation, and

The Exponent of Earth—

Emily Dickinson





Love—is that later Thing than Death


Love—is that later Thing than Death—

More previous—than Life—

Confirms it at its entrance—And

Usurps it—of itself—

Tastes Death—the first—to hand the sting The Second—to its friend—

Disarms the little interval—

Deposits Him with God—

Then hovers—an inferior Guard—

Lest this Beloved Charge

Need—once in an Eternity—

A smaller than the Large—

Emily Dickinson





Love—thou art high


Love—thou art high—

I cannot climb thee—

But, were it Two—

Who know but we—

Taking turns—at the Chimborazo—

Ducal—at last—stand up by thee—

Love—thou are deep—

I cannot cross thee—

But, were there Two

Instead of One—

Rower, and Yacht—some sovereign Summer—

Who knows—but we'd reach the Sun?

Love—thou are Veiled—

A few—behold thee—

Smile—and alter—and prattle—and die—

Bliss—were an Oddity—without thee—

Nicknamed by God—

Eternity—

Emily Dickinson





Low at my problem bending


Low at my problem bending,

Another problem comes&mdash;

Larger than mine&mdash;Serener&mdash; Involving statelier sums.

I check my busy pencil,

My figures file away.

Wherefore, my baffled fingers

They perplexity?

Emily Dickinson





Make me a picture of the sun


Make me a picture of the sun&mdash; So I can hang it in my room&mdash; And make believe I'm getting warm

When others call it "Day"!

Draw me a Robin&mdash;on a stem&mdash; So I am hearing him, I'll dream,

And when the Orchards stop their tune&mdash; Put my pretense&mdash;away&mdash; Say if it's really&mdash;warm at noon&mdash; Whether it's Buttercups&mdash;that "skim"&mdash; Or Butterflies&mdash;that "bloom"?

Then&mdash;skip&mdash;the frost&mdash;upon the lea&mdash; And skip the Russet&mdash;on the tree&mdash; Let's play those&mdash;never come!

Emily Dickinson





Mama never forgets her birds


Mama never forgets her birds,

Though in another tree&mdash;

She looks down just as often

And just as tenderly

As when her little mortal nest

With cunning care she wove&mdash;

If either of her "sparrows fall,"

She "notices," above.

Emily Dickinson






Many a phrase has the English language&mdash; I have heard but one&mdash;

Low as the laughter of the Cricket,

Loud, as the Thunder's Tongue&mdash; Murmuring, like old Caspian Choirs,

When the Tide's a' lull&mdash;

Saying itself in new infection&mdash; Like a Whippoorwill&mdash;

Breaking in bright Orthography

On my simple sleep&mdash;

Thundering its Prospective&mdash;

Till I stir, and weep&mdash;

Not for the Sorrow, done me&mdash; But the push of Joy&mdash;

Say it again, Saxton!

Hush&mdash;Only to me!

Emily Dickinson





Many cross the Rhine


Many cross the Rhine

In this cup of mine.

Sip old Frankfort air

From my brown Cigar.

Emily Dickinson





Me from Myself&mdash;to banish


Me from Myself&mdash;to banish&mdash; Had I Art&mdash;

Impregnable my Fortress

Unto All Heart&mdash;

But since Myself&mdash;assault Me&mdash; How have I peace

Except by subjugating

Consciousness?

And since We're mutual Monarch

How this be

Except by Abdication&mdash;

Me&mdash;of Me?

Emily Dickinson

Me prove it now&mdash;Whoever doubt Me stop to prove it&mdash;now&mdash; Make haste&mdash;the Scruple! Death be scant For Opportunity&mdash;

The River reaches to my feet&mdash; As yet&mdash;My Heart be dry&mdash; Oh Lover&mdash;Life could not convince&mdash; Might Death&mdash;enable Thee&mdash; The River reaches to My Breast&mdash; Still&mdash;still&mdash;My Hands above Proclaim with their remaining Might&mdash; Dost recognize the Love?

The River reaches to my Mouth&mdash; Remember&mdash;when the Sea

Swept by my searching eyes&mdash;the last&mdash; Themselves were quick&mdash;with Thee!

Emily Dickinson





Me prove it now—Whoever doubt


Me prove it now—Whoever doubt

Me stop to prove it—now—

Make haste—the Scruple! Death be scant For Opportunity—

The River reaches to my feet—

As yet—My Heart be dry—

Oh Lover—Life could not convince—

Might Death—enable Thee—

The River reaches to My Breast—

Still—still—My Hands above

Proclaim with their remaining Might—

Dost recognize the Love?

The River reaches to my Mouth—

Remember—when the Sea

Swept by my searching eyes—the last—

Themselves were quick—with Thee!

Emily Dickinson





Me! Come! My dazzled face

Me! Come! My dazzled face

In such a shining place!

Me! Hear! My foreign ear

The sounds of welcome near!

The saints shall meet

Our bashful feet.

My holiday shall be

That they remember me;

My paradise, the fame

That they pronounce my name.

Emily Dickinson

More Life&mdash;went out&mdash;when He went Than Ordinary Breath&mdash;

Lit with a finer Phosphor&mdash;

Requiring in the Quench&mdash;

A Power of Renowned Cold,

The Climate of the Grave

A Temperature just adequate

So Anthracite, to live&mdash;

For some&mdash;an Ampler Zero&mdash; A Frost more needle keen

Is necessary, to reduce

The Ethiop within.

Others&mdash;extinguish easier&mdash; A Gnat's minutest Fan

Sufficient to obliterate

A Tract of Citizen&mdash;

Whose Peat lift&mdash;amply vivid&mdash; Ignores the solemn News

That Popocatapel exists&mdash;

Or Etna's Scarlets, Choose&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

Morning—means

"Morning"—means "Milking"—to the Farmer—

Dawn—to the Teneriffe—

Dice—to the Maid—

Morning means just Risk—to the Lover—

Just revelation—to the Beloved—

Epicures—date a Breakfast—by it—

Brides—an Apocalypse—

Worlds—a Flood—

Faint-going Lives—Their Lapse from Sighing—

Faith—The Experiment of Our Lord

Emily Dickinson





Morns like these&mdash;we parted


Morns like these&mdash;we parted&mdash; Noons like these&mdash;she rose&mdash; Fluttering first&mdash;then firmer To her fair repose.

Never did she lisp it&mdash;

It was not for me&mdash;

She&mdash;was mute from transport&mdash; I&mdash;from agony&mdash;

Till&mdash;the evening nearing

One the curtains drew&mdash;

Quick! A Sharper rustling!

And this linnet flew!

Emily Dickinson

Morns like these—we parted—

To her fair repose.

Most she touched me by her muteness


Most she touched me by her muteness&mdash; Most she won me by the way

She presented her small figure&mdash; Plea itself&mdash;for Charity&mdash; Were a Crumb my whole possession&mdash; Were there famine in the land&mdash; Were it my resource from starving&mdash; Could I such a plea withstand&mdash; Not upon her knee to thank me

Sank this Beggar from the Sky&mdash; But the Crumb partook&mdash;departed&mdash; And returned On High&mdash;

I supposed&mdash;when sudden

Such a Praise began

'Twas as Space sat singing

To herself&mdash;and men&mdash;

'Twas the Winged Beggar&mdash;

Afterward I learned

To her Benefactor

Making Gratitude

Emily Dickinson





Much Madness is divinest Sense

Much Madness is divinest Sense -

To a discerning Eye -

Much Sense - the starkest Madness -

`Tis the Majority

In this, as All, prevail -

Assent - and you are sane -

Demur - yoùre straightaway dangerous -

And handled with a Chain -

Musicians wrestle everywhere


Musicians wrestle everywhere&mdash; All day&mdash;among the crowded air I hear the silver strife&mdash;

And&mdash;walking&mdash;long before the morn&mdash; Such transport breaks upon the town

I think it that "New Life"!

If is not Bird&mdash;it has no nest&mdash; Nor "Band"&mdash;in brass and scarlet&mdash;drest&mdash; Nor Tamborin&mdash;nor Man&mdash; It is not Hymn from pulpit read&mdash; The "Morning Stars" the Treble led On Time's first Afternoon!

Some&mdash;say&mdash;it is "the Spheres"&mdash;at play!

Some say that bright Majority

Of vanished Dames&mdash;and Men!

Some&mdash;think it service in the place Where we&mdash;with late&mdash;celestial face&mdash; Please God&mdash;shall Ascertain!

Emily Dickinson





Must be a Woe


Must be a Woe&mdash;

A loss or so&mdash;

To bend the eye

Best Beauty's way&mdash;

But&mdash;once aslant

It notes Delight

As difficult

As Stalactite

A Common Bliss

Were had for less&mdash;

The price&mdash;is

Even as the Grace&mdash;

Our lord&mdash;thought no

Extravagance

To pay&mdash;a Cross&mdash;

My constant&mdash;reverential Face Sufficient Courtesy.

My Faith is larger than the Hills


My Faith is larger than the Hills&mdash; So when the Hills decay&mdash;

My Faith must take the Purple Wheel

To show the Sun the way&mdash;

'Tis first He steps upon the Vane&mdash; And then&mdash;upon the Hill&mdash; And then abroad the World He go

To do His Golden Will&mdash;

And if His Yellow feet should miss&mdash; The Bird would not arise&mdash;

The Flowers would slumber on their Stems&mdash; No Bells have Paradise&mdash;

How dare I, therefore, stint a faith

On which so vast depends&mdash;

Lest Firmament should fail for me&mdash; The Rivet in the Bands

Emily Dickinson






My first well Day&mdash;since many ill&mdash; I asked to go abroad,

And take the Sunshine in my hands,

And see the things in Pod&mdash;

A 'blossom just when I went in

To take my Chance with pain&mdash; Uncertain if myself, or He,

Should prove the strongest One.

The Summer deepened, while we strove&mdash; She put some flowers away&mdash;

And Redder cheeked Ones&mdash;in their stead&mdash; A fond&mdash;illusive way&mdash; To cheat Herself, it seemed she tried&mdash; As if before a child

To fade&mdash;Tomorrow&mdash;Rainbows held The Sepulchre, could hide.

She dealt a fashion to the Nut&mdash; She tied the Hoods to Seeds&mdash; She dropped bright scraps of Tint, about&mdash; And left Brazilian Threads

On every shoulder that she met&mdash; Then both her Hands of Haze

Put up&mdash;to hide her parting Grace From our unfitted eyes.

My loss, by sickness&mdash;Was it Loss?

Or that Ethereal Gain

One earns by measuring the Grave&mdash; Then&mdash;measuring the Sun&mdash; Emily Dickinson





My first well Day—since many ill


My first well Day—since many ill—

I asked to go abroad,

And take the Sunshine in my hands,

And see the things in Pod—

A 'blossom just when I went in

To take my Chance with pain—

Uncertain if myself, or He,

Should prove the strongest One.

The Summer deepened, while we strove—

She put some flowers away—

And Redder cheeked Ones—in their stead—

A fond—illusive way—

To cheat Herself, it seemed she tried—

As if before a child

To fade—Tomorrow—Rainbows held

The Sepulchre, could hide.

She dealt a fashion to the Nut—

She tied the Hoods to Seeds—

She dropped bright scraps of Tint, about—

And left Brazilian Threads

On every shoulder that she met—

Then both her Hands of Haze

Put up—to hide her parting Grace

From our unfitted eyes.

My loss, by sickness—Was it Loss?

Or that Ethereal Gain

One earns by measuring the Grave—

Then—measuring the Sun—

Emily Dickinson





My friend attacks my friend!


My friend attacks my friend!

Oh Battle picturesque!

Then I turn Soldier too,

And he turns Satirist!

How martial is this place!

Had I a mighty gun

I think I'd shoot the human race

And then to glory run!

Emily Dickinson

Ah, curious friend!

Thou puzzlest me!

My life closed twice

Parting is all we know of heaven,

And all we need of hell.

My life had stood

My life had stood--a Loaded Gun--

In Corners--till a Day

The Owner passed--identified--

And carried Me away--

And now We roam in Sovereign Woods--

And now We hunt the Doe--

And every time I speak for Him--

The Mountains straight reply--

And do I smile, such cordial light

Upon the Valley glow--

It is as a Vesuvian face

Had let its pleasure through--

And when at Night--Our good Day done--

I guard My Master's Head--

'Tis better than the Eider-Duck's

Deep Pillow--to have shared--

To foe of His--I'm deadly foe--

None stir the second time--

On whom I lay a Yellow Eye--

Or an emphatic Thumb--

Though I than He--may longer live

He longer must--than I--

For I have but the power to kill,

Without--the power to die--

Emily Dickinson

My nosegays are for Captives


My nosegays are for Captives&mdash; Dim&mdash;expectant eyes,

Fingers denied the plucking,

Patient till Paradise.

To such, if they should whisper

Of morning and the moor,

They bear no other errand,

And I, no other prayer.

Emily Dickinson

My nosegays are for captives;

Dim, long-expectant eyes,

My period had come for Prayer


My period had come for Prayer&mdash; No other Art&mdash;would do&mdash; My Tactics missed a rudiment&mdash; Creator&mdash;Was it you?

God grows above&mdash;so those who pray Horizons&mdash;must ascend&mdash; And so I stepped upon the North

To see this Curious Friend&mdash;

His House was not&mdash;no sign had He&mdash; By Chimney&mdash;nor by Door

Could I infer his Residence&mdash; Vast Prairies of Air

Unbroken by a Settler&mdash;

Were all that I could see&mdash;

Infinitude&mdash;Had'st Thou no Face That I might look on Thee?

The Silence condescended&mdash;

Creation stopped&mdash;for Me&mdash; But awed beyond my errand&mdash;

I worshipped&mdash;did not "pray"&mdash; Emily Dickinson





My Portion is Defeat&mdash;today


My Portion is Defeat&mdash;today&mdash; A paler luck than Victory&mdash;

Less Paeans&mdash;fewer Bells&mdash; The Drums don't follow Me&mdash;with tunes&mdash; Defeat&mdash;a somewhat slower&mdash;means&mdash; More Arduous than Balls&mdash;

'Tis populous with Bone and stain&mdash; And Men too straight to stoop again&mdash;, And Piles of solid Moan&mdash;

And Chips of Blank&mdash;in Boyish Eyes&mdash; And scraps of Prayer&mdash;

And Death's surprise,

Stamped visible&mdash;in Stone&mdash; There's somewhat prouder, over there&mdash; The Trumpets tell it to the Air&mdash; How different Victory

To Him who has it&mdash;and the One Who to have had it, would have been

Contender&mdash;to die&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





My Portion is Defeat—today


My Portion is Defeat—today—

A paler luck than Victory—

Less Paeans—fewer Bells—

The Drums don't follow Me—with tunes—

Defeat—a somewhat slower—means—

More Arduous than Balls—

'Tis populous with Bone and stain—

And Men too straight to stoop again—,

And Piles of solid Moan—

And Chips of Blank—in Boyish Eyes—

And scraps of Prayer—

And Death's surprise,

Stamped visible—in Stone—

There's somewhat prouder, over there—

The Trumpets tell it to the Air—

How different Victory

To Him who has it—and the One

Who to have had it, would have been

Contender—to die—

Emily Dickinson





My Reward for Being, was This


My Reward for Being, was This.

My premium&mdash;My Bliss&mdash; An Admiralty, less&mdash;

A Sceptre&mdash;penniless&mdash; And Realms&mdash;just Dross&mdash; When Thrones accost my Hands&mdash; With "Me, Miss, Me"&mdash; I'll unroll Thee&mdash;

Dominions dowerless&mdash;beside this Grace&mdash; Election&mdash;Vote&mdash;

The Ballots of Eternity, will show just that.

Emily Dickinson

My Soul—accused me—And I quailed


My Soul—accused me—And I quailed—

As Tongue of Diamond had reviled

All else accused me—and I smiled—

My Soul—that Morning—was My friend—

Her favor—is the best Disdain

Toward Artifice of Time—or Men—

But Her Disdain—'twere lighter bear

A finger of Enamelled Fire—

Emily Dickinson





My wheel is in the dark


My wheel is in the dark!

I cannot see a spoke

Yet know its dripping feet

Go round and round.

My foot is on the Tide!

An unfrequented road&mdash;

Yet have all roads

A clearing at the end&mdash;

Some have resigned the Loom&mdash; Some in the busy tomb

Find quaint employ&mdash;

Some with new&mdash;stately feet&mdash; Pass royal through the gate&mdash; Flinging the problem back

At you and I!

Emily Dickinson





My Worthiness is all my Doubt


My Worthiness is all my Doubt&mdash; His Merit&mdash;all my fear&mdash; Contrasting which, my quality

Do lowlier&mdash;appear&mdash; Lest I should insufficient prove

For His beloved Need&mdash;

The Chiefest Apprehension

Upon my thronging Mind&mdash;

'Tis true&mdash;that Deity to stoop Inherently incline&mdash;

For nothing higher than Itself

Itself can rest upon&mdash;

So I&mdash;the undivine abode

Of His Elect Content&mdash;

Conform my Soul&mdash;as 'twere a Church, Unto Her Sacrament&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






Myself was formed&mdash;a Carpenter&mdash; An unpretending time

Myself was formed—a Carpenter


Myself was formed—a Carpenter—

An unpretending time

My Plane—and I, together wrought

Before a Builder came—

To measure our attainments—

Had we the Art of Boards

Sufficiently developed—He'd hire us

At Halves—

My Tools took Human—Faces—

The Bench, where we had toiled—

Against the Man—persuaded—

We—Temples build—I said—

Emily Dickinson

As Herschel's private interest

Or Mercury's affair&mdash;

Nature is what we see—

"Nature" is what we see—

The Hill—the Afternoon—

Squirrel—Eclipse—the Bumble bee—

Nay—Nature is Heaven—

Nature is what we hear—

The Bobolink—the Sea—

Thunder—the Cricket—

Nay—Nature is Harmony—

Nature is what we know—

Yet have no art to say—

So impotent Our Wisdom is

To her Simplicity.

Emily Dickinson





Nature rarer uses yellow

Nature rarer uses yellow

Than another hue;

Saves she all of that for sunsets,--

Prodigal of blue,

Spending scarlet like a woman,

Yellow she affords

Only scantly and selectly,

Like a lover's words.

Emily Dickinson





Nature the gentlest mother is

Nature the gentlest mother is,

Impatient of no child,

The feeblest of the waywardest.

Her admonition mild

In forest and the hill

By traveller be heard,

Restraining rampant squirrel

Or too impetuous bird.

How fair her conversation

A summer afternoon,

Her household her assembly;

And when the sun go down,

Her voice among the aisles

Incite the timid prayer

Of the minutest cricket,

The most unworthy flower.

When all the children sleep,

She turns as long away

As will suffice tolight her lamps,

Then bending from the sky

With infinite affection

An infiniter care,

Her golden finger on her lip,

Wills silence everywhere.

Emily Dickinson






Nature&mdash;sometimes sears a Sapling&mdash; Sometimes&mdash;scalps a Tree&mdash; Her Green People recollect it

When they do not die&mdash;

Fainter Leaves&mdash;to Further Seasons&mdash; Dumbly testify&mdash;

We&mdash;who have the Souls&mdash; Die oftener&mdash;Not so vitally&mdash; Emily Dickinson

As will suffice to light Her lamps&mdash; Then bending from the Sky&mdash;

With infinite Affection&mdash;

And infiniter Care&mdash;

Her Golden finger on Her lip&mdash; Wills Silence&mdash;Everywhere&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Nature, the gentlest mother,

Nature, the gentlest mother,

Impatient of no child,

The feeblest or the waywardest,

Her admonition mild

In forest and the hill

By traveller is heard,

Restraining rampant squirrel

Or too impetuous bird.

How fair her conversation,

A summer afternoon,--

Her household, her assembly;

And when the sun goes down

Her voice among the aisles

Incites the timid prayer

Of the minutest cricket,

The most unworthy flower.

When all the children sleep

She turns as long away

As will suffice to light her lamps;

Then, bending from the sky

With infinite affection

And infiniter care,

Her golden finger on her lip,

Wills silence everywhere.

Emily Dickinson





Nature—sometimes sears a Sapling


Nature—sometimes sears a Sapling—

Sometimes—scalps a Tree—

Her Green People recollect it

When they do not die—

Fainter Leaves—to Further Seasons—

Dumbly testify—

We—who have the Souls—

Die oftener—Not so vitally—

Emily Dickinson

Never for Society

No Crowd that has occurred

No Notice gave She, but a Change


No Notice gave She, but a Change&mdash; No Message, but a Sigh&mdash;

For Whom, the Time did not suffice

That She should specify.

She was not warm, though Summer shone

Nor scrupulous of cold

Though Rime by Rime, the steady Frost

Upon Her Bosom piled&mdash;

Of shrinking ways&mdash;she did not fright Though all the Village looked&mdash; But held Her gravity aloft&mdash;

And met the gaze&mdash;direct&mdash; And when adjusted like a Seed

In careful fitted Ground

Unto the Everlasting Spring

And hindered but a Mound

Her Warm return, if so she chose&mdash; And We&mdash;imploring drew&mdash; Removed our invitation by

As Some She never knew&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

No Rack can torture me

No easier divest&mdash;

And gain the Sky

Than mayest Thou&mdash;

Except Thyself may be

Captivity is Consciousness&mdash;

So's Liberty.

Not in this world to see his face

Not in this world to see his face

Sounds long, until I read the place

Where this is said to be

But just the primer to a life

Unopened, rare, upon the shelf,

Clasped yet to him and me.

I would not choose a book to know

Than that, be sweeter wise;

Might some one else so learned be.

And leave me just my A B C,

Himself could have the skies.

Not probable—The barest Chance


Not probable—The barest Chance—

A smile too few—a word too much

And far from Heaven as the Rest—

The Soul so close on Paradise—

What if the Bird from journey far—

Confused by Sweets—as Mortals—are—

Forget the secret of His wing

And perish—but a Bough between—

Oh, Groping feet—

Oh Phantom Queen!

Emily Dickinson

Of all the souls that stand create

Of all the souls that stand create

I have elected one.

When sense from spirit files away,

And subterfuge is done;

When that which is and that which was

Apart, intrinsic, stand,

And this brief tragedy of flesh

Is shifted like a sand;

When figures show their royal front

And mists are carved sway,--

Behold the atom I Feferred

To all the lists of clay!

Emily Dickinson





Of all the Sounds despatched abroad


Of all the Sounds despatched abroad,

There's not a Charge to me

Like that old measure in the Boughs&mdash; That phraseless Melody&mdash;

The Wind does&mdash;working like a Hand, Whose fingers Comb the Sky&mdash;

Then quiver down&mdash;with tufts of Tune&mdash; Permitted Gods, and me&mdash;

Inheritance, it is, to us&mdash;

Beyond the Art to Earn&mdash;

Beyond the trait to take away

By Robber, since the Gain

Is gotten not of fingers&mdash;

And inner than the Bone&mdash;

Hid golden, for the whole of Days,

And even in the Urn,

I cannot vouch the merry Dust

Do not arise and play

In some odd fashion of its own,

Some quainter Holiday,

When Winds go round and round in Bands&mdash; And thrum upon the door,

And Birds take places, overhead,

To bear them Orchestra.

I crave Him grace of Summer Boughs,

If such an Outcast be&mdash;

Who never heard that fleshless Chant&mdash; Rise&mdash;solemn&mdash;on the Tree, As if some Caravan of Sound

Off Deserts, in the Sky,

Had parted Rank,

Then knit, and swept&mdash;

In Seamless Company&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Of Being is a Bird


Of Being is a Bird

The likest to the Down

An Easy Breeze do put afloat

The General Heavens&mdash;upon&mdash; It soars&mdash;and shifts&mdash;and whirls&mdash; And measures with the Clouds

In easy&mdash;even&mdash;dazzling pace&mdash; No different the Birds&mdash;

Except a Wake of Music

Accompany their feet&mdash;

As did the Down emit a Tune&mdash; For Ecstasy&mdash;of it

Emily Dickinson





Of Bronze&mdash;and Blaze


Of Bronze&mdash;and Blaze&mdash; The North&mdash;Tonight&mdash; So adequate&mdash;it forms&mdash; So preconcerted with itself&mdash; So distant&mdash;to alarms&mdash; And Unconcern so sovereign

To Universe, or me&mdash;

Infects my simple spirit

With Taints of Majesty&mdash;

Till I take vaster attitudes&mdash; And strut upon my stem&mdash;

Disdaining Men, and Oxygen,

For Arrogance of them&mdash;

My Splendors, are Menagerie&mdash; But their Completeless Show

Will entertain the Centuries

When I, am long ago,

An Island in dishonored Grass&mdash; Whom none but Beetles&mdash;know.

Emily Dickinson

Of Brussels&mdash;it was not

Of nearness to her sundered Things


Of nearness to her sundered Things

The Soul has special times&mdash;

When Dimness&mdash;looks the Oddity&mdash; Distinctness&mdash;easy&mdash;seems&mdash; The Shapes we buried, dwell about,

Familiar, in the Rooms&mdash;

Untarnished by the Sepulchre,

The Mouldering Playmate comes&mdash; In just the Jacket that he wore&mdash; Long buttoned in the Mold

Since we&mdash;old mornings, Children&mdash;played&mdash; Divided&mdash;by a world&mdash; The Grave yields back her Robberies&mdash; The Years, our pilfered Things&mdash; Bright Knots of Apparitions

Salute us, with their wings&mdash; As we&mdash;it were&mdash;that perished&mdash; Themself&mdash;had just remained till we rejoin them&mdash; And 'twas they, and not ourself

That mourned.

Emily Dickinson

Of Silken Speech and Specious Shoe

His service to the newest Grace

Present continually

His Suit a chance

His Troth a Term

Protracted as the Breeze

Continual Ban propoundeth He

Continual Divorce.

Of Tribulation, these are They


Of Tribulation, these are They,

The Spangled Gowns, a lesser Rank

Of Victors&mdash;designate&mdash; All these&mdash;did conquer&mdash; But the ones who overcame most times&mdash; Wear nothing commoner than Snow&mdash; No Ornament, but Palms&mdash;

Surrender&mdash;is a sort unknown&mdash; On this superior soil&mdash;

Defeat&mdash;an outgrown Anguish&mdash; Remembered, as the Mile

On such a night, or such a night


On such a night, or such a night,

Would anybody care

If such a little figure

Slipped quiet from its chair&mdash; So quiet&mdash;Oh how quiet,

That nobody might know

But that the little figure

Rocked softer&mdash;to and fro&mdash; On such a dawn, or such a dawn&mdash; Would anybody sigh

That such a little figure

Too sound asleep did lie

For Chanticleer to wake it&mdash;

Or stirring house below&mdash;

Or giddy bird in orchard&mdash;

Or early task to do?

There was a little figure plump

For every little knoll&mdash;

Busy needles, and spools of thread&mdash; And trudging feet from school&mdash; Playmates, and holidays, and nuts&mdash; And visions vast and small&mdash;

Strange that the feet so precious charged Should reach so small a goal!

Emily Dickinson

One Blessing had I than the rest


One Blessing had I than the rest

So larger to my Eyes

That I stopped gauging&mdash;satisfied&mdash; For this enchanted size&mdash;

It was the limit of my Dream&mdash; The focus of my Prayer&mdash;

A perfect&mdash;paralyzing Bliss&mdash; Contented as Despair&mdash;

I knew no more of Want&mdash;or Cold&mdash; Phantasms both become

For this new Value in the Soul&mdash; Supremest Earthly Sum&mdash;

The Heaven below the Heaven above&mdash; Obscured with ruddier Blue&mdash;

Life's Latitudes leant over&mdash;full&mdash; The Judgment perished&mdash;too&mdash; Why Bliss so scantily disburse&mdash; Why Paradise defer&mdash;

Why Floods be served to Us&mdash;in Bowls&mdash; I speculate no more&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

One Day is there of the Series


One Day is there of the Series

Termed Thanksgiving Day.

Celebrated part at Table

Part in Memory.

Neither Patriarch nor Pussy

I dissect the Play

Seems it to my Hooded thinking

Reflex Holiday.

Had there been no sharp Subtraction

From the early Sum&mdash;

Not an Acre or a Caption

Where was once a Room&mdash;

Not a Mention, whose small Pebble

Wrinkled any Sea,

Unto Such, were such Assembly

'Twere Thanksgiving Day.

Emily Dickinson





One dignity delays for all


One dignity delays for all&mdash;

One mitred Afternoon&mdash;

None can avoid this purple&mdash;

None evade this Crown!

Coach, it insures, and footmen&mdash; Chamber, and state, and throng&mdash; Bells, also, in the village

As we ride grand along!

What dignified Attendants!

What service when we pause!

How loyally at parting

Their hundred hats they raise!

Her pomp surpassing ermine

When simple You, and I,

Present our meek escutheon

And claim the rank to die!

Emily Dickinson





One Life of so much Consequence!


One Life of so much Consequence!

Yet I&mdash;for it&mdash;would pay&mdash; My Soul's entire income&mdash;

In ceaseless&mdash;salary&mdash; One Pearl&mdash;to me&mdash;so signal&mdash; That I would instant dive&mdash;

Although&mdash;I knew&mdash;to take it&mdash; Would cost me&mdash;just a life!

The Sea is full&mdash;I know it!

That&mdash;does not blur my Gem!

It burns&mdash;distinct from all the row&mdash; Intact&mdash;in Diadem!

The life is thick&mdash;I know it!

Yet&mdash;not so dense a crowd&mdash; But Monarchs&mdash;are perceptible&mdash; Far down the dustiest Road!

Emily Dickinson





One need not be a chamber to be haunted, One need not be a chamber to be haunted, One need not be a house;

The brain has corridors surpassing

Material place.

Far safer, of a midnight meeting

External ghost,

Than an interior confronting

That whiter host.

Far safer through an Abbey gallop,

The stones achase,

Than, moonless, one's own self encounter In lonesome place.

Ourself, behind ourself concealed,

Should startle most;

Assassin, hid in our apartment,

Be horror's least.

The prudent carries a revolver,

He bolts the door,

O'erlooking a superior spectre

More near.

Emily Dickinson






One need not be a Chamber&mdash;to be Haunted&mdash; One need not be a House&mdash;

The Brain has Corridors&mdash;surpassing Material Place&mdash;

Far safer, of a Midnight Meeting

External Ghost

Than its interior Confronting&mdash; That Cooler Host.

Far safer, through an Abbey gallop,

The Stones a'chase&mdash;

Than Unarmed, one's a'self encounter&mdash; In lonesome Place&mdash;

Ourself behind ourself, concealed&mdash; Should startle most&mdash;

Assassin hid in our Apartment

Be Horror's least.

The Body&mdash;borrows a Revolver&mdash; He bolts the Door&mdash;

O'erlooking a superior spectre&mdash; Or More&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






One need not be a Chamber—to be Haunted—

One need not be a House—

The Brain has Corridors—surpassing

Material Place—

Far safer, of a Midnight Meeting

External Ghost

Than its interior Confronting—

That Cooler Host.

Far safer, through an Abbey gallop,

The Stones a'chase—

Than Unarmed, one's a'self encounter—

In lonesome Place—

Ourself behind ourself, concealed—

Should startle most—

Assassin hid in our Apartment

Be Horror's least.

The Body—borrows a Revolver—

He bolts the Door—

O'erlooking a superior spectre—

Or More—

Emily Dickinson





One Sister have I in our house


One Sister have I in our house,

And one, a hedge away.

There's only one recorded,

But both belong to me.

One came the road that I came&mdash; And wore my last year's gown&mdash; The other, as a bird her nest,

Builded our hearts among.

She did not sing as we did&mdash;

It was a different tune&mdash;

Herself to her a music

As Bumble bee of June.

Today is far from Childhood&mdash; But up and down the hills

I held her hand the tighter&mdash; Which shortened all the miles&mdash; And still her hum

The years among,

Deceives the Butterfly;

Still in her Eye

The Violets lie

Mouldered this many May.

I spilt the dew&mdash;

But took the morn&mdash;

I chose this single star

From out the wide night's numbers&mdash; Sue - forevermore!

Emily Dickinson





One Year ago&mdash;jots what?


One Year ago&mdash;jots what?

God&mdash;spell the word! I&mdash;can't&mdash; Was't Grace? Not that&mdash;

Was't Glory? That&mdash;will do&mdash; Spell slower&mdash;Glory&mdash; Such Anniversary shall be&mdash;

Sometimes&mdash;not often&mdash;in Eternity&mdash; When farther Parted, than the Common Woe&mdash; Look&mdash;feed upon each other's faces&mdash;so&mdash; In doubtful meal, if it be possible

Their Banquet's true&mdash;

I tasted&mdash;careless&mdash;then&mdash; I did not know the Wine

Came once a World&mdash;Did you?

Oh, had you told me so&mdash;

This Thirst would blister&mdash;easier&mdash;now&mdash; You said it hurt you&mdash;most&mdash; Mine&mdash;was an Acorn's Breast&mdash; And could not know how fondness grew

In Shaggier Vest&mdash;

Perhaps&mdash;I couldn't&mdash; But, had you looked in&mdash;

A Giant&mdash;eye to eye with you, had been&mdash; No Acorn&mdash;then&mdash;

So&mdash;Twelve months ago&mdash; We breathed&mdash;

Then dropped the Air&mdash;

Which bore it best?

Was this&mdash;the patientest&mdash; Because it was a Child, you know&mdash; And could not value&mdash;Air?

If to be "Elder"&mdash;mean most pain&mdash; I'm old enough, today, I'm certain&mdash;then&mdash; As old as thee&mdash;how soon?

One&mdash;Birthday more&mdash;or Ten?

Let me&mdash;choose!

Ah, Sir, None!

Emily Dickinson





One Year ago—jots what?


One Year ago—jots what?

God—spell the word! I—can't—

Was't Grace? Not that—

Was't Glory? That—will do—

Spell slower—Glory—

Such Anniversary shall be—

Sometimes—not often—in Eternity—

When farther Parted, than the Common Woe—

Look—feed upon each other's faces—so—

In doubtful meal, if it be possible

Their Banquet's true—

I tasted—careless—then—

I did not know the Wine

Came once a World—Did you?

Oh, had you told me so—

This Thirst would blister—easier—now—

You said it hurt you—most—

Mine—was an Acorn's Breast—

And could not know how fondness grew

In Shaggier Vest—

Perhaps—I couldn't—

But, had you looked in—

A Giant—eye to eye with you, had been—

No Acorn—then—

So—Twelve months ago—

We breathed—

Then dropped the Air—

Which bore it best?

Was this—the patientest—

Because it was a Child, you know—

And could not value—Air?

If to be "Elder"—mean most pain—

I'm old enough, today, I'm certain—then—

As old as thee—how soon?

One—Birthday more—or Ten?

Let me—choose!

Ah, Sir, None!

Emily Dickinson





Only a Shrine, but Mine


Only a Shrine, but Mine&mdash;

I made the Taper shine&mdash;

Madonna dim, to whom all Feet may come, Regard a Nun&mdash;

Thou knowest every Woe&mdash;

Needless to tell thee&mdash;so&mdash; But can'st thou do

The Grace next to it&mdash;heal?

That looks a harder skill to us&mdash; Still&mdash;just as easy, if it be thy Will To thee&mdash;Grant me&mdash;

Thou knowest, though, so Why tell thee?

Emily Dickinson





Only God&mdash;detect the Sorrow


Only God&mdash;detect the Sorrow&mdash; Only God&mdash;

The Jehovahs&mdash;are no Babblers&mdash; Unto God&mdash;

God the Son&mdash;Confide it&mdash; Still secure&mdash;

God the Spirit's Honor&mdash;

Just as sure&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Only God—detect the Sorrow


Only God—detect the Sorrow—

Only God—

The Jehovahs—are no Babblers—

Unto God—

God the Son—Confide it—

God the Spirit's Honor—

Our journey had advanced


Our journey had advanced&mdash;

Our feet were almost come

To that odd Fork in Being's Road&mdash; Eternity&mdash;by Term&mdash;

Our pace took sudden awe&mdash;

Our feet&mdash;reluctant&mdash;led&mdash; Before&mdash;were Cities&mdash;but Between&mdash; The Forest of the Dead&mdash;

Retreat&mdash;was out of Hope&mdash; Behind&mdash;a Sealed Route&mdash; Eternity's White Flag&mdash;Before&mdash; And God&mdash;at every Gate&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Our journey had advanced;

Our journey had advanced;

Our feet were almost come

To that odd fork in Being's road,

Eternity by term.

Our pace took sudden awe,

Our feet reluctant led.

Before were cities, but between,

The forest of the dead.

Retreat was out of hope,--

Behind, a sealed route,

Eternity's white flag before,

And God at every gate.

Emily Dickinson






Our little Kinsmen&mdash;after Rain In plenty may be seen,

A Pink and Pulpy multitude

The tepid Ground upon.

A needless life, it seemed to me

Until a little Bird

As to a Hospitality

Advanced and breakfasted.

As I of He, so God of Me

I pondered, may have judged,

And left the little Angle Worm

With Modesties enlarged.

Emily Dickinson

Our little Kinsmen—after Rain

Our Lives Are Swiss

Our lives are Swiss --

So still -- so Cool --

Till some odd afternoon

The Alps neglect their Curtains

And we look farther on!

Italy stands the other side!

While like a guard between --

The solemn Alps --

The siren Alps

Forever intervene!

Emily Dickinson

Our share of night to bear


Our share of night to bear&mdash;

Our share of morning&mdash;

Our blank in bliss to fill

Our blank in scorning&mdash;

Here a star, and there a star,

Some lose their way!

Here a mist, and there a mist,

Afterwards&mdash;Day!

Emily Dickinson






Ourselves were wed one summer&mdash;dear&mdash; Your Vision&mdash;was in June&mdash; And when Your little Lifetime failed,

I wearied&mdash;too&mdash;of mine&mdash; And overtaken in the Dark&mdash;

Where You had put me down&mdash;

By Some one carrying a Light&mdash; I&mdash;too&mdash;received the Sign.

'Tis true&mdash;Our Futures different lay&mdash; Your Cottage&mdash;faced the sun&mdash; While Oceans&mdash;and the North must be&mdash; On every side of mine

'Tis true, Your Garden led the Bloom,

For mine&mdash;in Frosts&mdash;was sown&mdash; And yet, one Summer, we were Queens&mdash; But You&mdash;were crowned in June&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Ourselves were wed one summer—dear


Ourselves were wed one summer—dear—

Your Vision—was in June—

And when Your little Lifetime failed,

I wearied—too—of mine—

And overtaken in the Dark—

Where You had put me down—

By Some one carrying a Light—

I—too—received the Sign.

'Tis true—Our Futures different lay—

Your Cottage—faced the sun—

While Oceans—and the North must be—

On every side of mine

'Tis true, Your Garden led the Bloom,

For mine—in Frosts—was sown—

And yet, one Summer, we were Queens—

But You—were crowned in June—

Emily Dickinson





Out of sight? What of that?


Out of sight? What of that?

See the Bird&mdash;reach it!

Curve by Curve&mdash;Sweep by Sweep&mdash; Round the Steep Air&mdash;

Danger! What is that to Her?

Better 'tis to fail&mdash;there&mdash; Than debate&mdash;here&mdash;

Blue is Blue&mdash;the World through&mdash; Amber&mdash;Amber&mdash;Dew&mdash;Dew&mdash; Seek&mdash;Friend&mdash;and see&mdash; Heaven is shy of Earth&mdash;that's all&mdash; Bashful Heaven&mdash;thy Lovers small&mdash; Hide&mdash;too&mdash;from thee&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Over and over, like a Tune


Over and over, like a Tune&mdash;

The Recollection plays&mdash;

Drums off the Phantom Battlements

Cornets of Paradise&mdash;

Snatches, from Baptized Generations&mdash; Cadences too grand

But for the Justified Processions

At the Lord's Right hand.

Emily Dickinson





Over the fence


Over the fence&mdash;

Strawberries&mdash;grow&mdash; Over the fence&mdash;

I could climb&mdash;if I tried, I know&mdash; Berries are nice!

But&mdash;if I stained my Apron&mdash; God would certainly scold!

Oh, dear,&mdash;I guess if He were a Boy&mdash; He'd&mdash;climb&mdash;if He could!

Emily Dickinson





Pain

Pain--has an Element of Blank--

It cannot recollect

When it begun--or if there were

A time when it was not--

It has no Future--but itself--

Its Infinite Contain

Its Past--enlightened to perceive

New Periods--of Pain.

Emily Dickinson





Pain Has An Element

Pain has an element of blank;

It cannot recollect

When it began, or if there were

A day when it was not.

It has no future but itself,

Its infinite realms contain

Its past, enlightened to perceive

New periods of pain.

Emily Dickinson





Pain has an element of blank;

Pain has an element of blank;

It cannot recollect

When it began, or if there were

A day when it was not.

It has no future but itself,

Its infinite realms contain

Its past, enlightened to perceive

New periods of pain.

Emily Dickinson





Pain&mdash;expands the Time


Pain&mdash;expands the Time&mdash; Ages coil within

The minute Circumference

Of a single Brain&mdash;

Pain contracts&mdash;the Time&mdash; Occupied with Shot

Gamuts of Eternities

Are as they were not&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

Papa above!


Papa above!

Regard a Mouse

O'erpowered by the Cat!

Reserve within thy kingdom

A "Mansion" for the Rat!

Snug in seraphic Cupboards

To nibble all the day

While unsuspecting Cycles

Wheel solemnly away!

Emily Dickinson

Abstemiously.

In Sicily.

Emily Dickinson





Patience&mdash;has a quiet Outer


Patience&mdash;has a quiet Outer&mdash; Patience&mdash;Look within&mdash; Is an Insect's futile forces

Infinites&mdash;between&mdash;

'Scaping one&mdash;against the other Fruitlesser to fling&mdash;

Patience&mdash;is the Smile's exertion Through the quivering&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Patience—has a quiet Outer


Patience—has a quiet Outer—

Patience—Look within—

Is an Insect's futile forces

Infinites—between—

'Scaping one—against the other

Fruitlesser to fling—

Patience—is the Smile's exertion

Through the quivering—

Emily Dickinson





Peace is a fiction of our Faith


Peace is a fiction of our Faith&mdash; The Bells a Winter Night

Bearing the Neighbor out of Sound

That never did alight.

Emily Dickinson





Perhaps I Asked Too Large

Perhaps I asked too large --

I take -- no less than skies --

For Earths, grow thick as

Berries, in my native town --

My Basked holds -- just -- Firmaments --

Those -- dangle easy -- on my arm,

But smaller bundles -- Cram.

Emily Dickinson





Perhaps you think me stooping


Perhaps you think me stooping

I'm not ashamed of that

Christ&mdash;stooped until He touched the Grave&mdash; Do those at Sacrament

Commemorative Dishonor

Or love annealed of love

Until it bend as low as Death

Redignified, above?

Emily Dickinson





Perhaps you'd like to buy a flower


Perhaps you'd like to buy a flower,

But I could never sell&mdash;

If you would like to borrow,

Until the Daffodil

Unties her yellow Bonnet

Beneath the village door,

Until the Bees, from Clover rows

Their Hock, and Sherry, draw,

Why, I will lend until just then,

But not an hour more!

Emily Dickinson





Pigmy seraphs&mdash;gone astray


Pigmy seraphs&mdash;gone astray&mdash; Velvet people from Vevay&mdash;

Balles from some lost summer day&mdash; Bees exclusive Coterie&mdash;

Paris could not lay the fold

Belted down with Emerald&mdash;

Venice could not show a check

Of a tint so lustrous meek&mdash;

Never such an Ambuscade

As of briar and leaf displayed

For my little damask maid&mdash;

I had rather wear her grace

Than an Earl's distinguished face&mdash; I had rather dwell like her

Than be "Duke of Exeter"&mdash; Royalty enough for me

To subdue the Bumblebee.

Emily Dickinson

Poor little Heart!


Poor little Heart!

Did they forget thee?

Then dinna care! Then dinna care!

Proud little Heart!

Did they forsake thee?

Be debonnaire! Be debonnaire!

Frail little Heart!

I would not break thee&mdash;

Could'st credit me? Could'st credit me?

Gay little Heart&mdash;

Like Morning Glory!

Wind and Sun&mdash;wilt thee array!

Emily Dickinson





Portraits are to daily faces


Portraits are to daily faces

As an Evening West,

To a fine, pedantic sunshine&mdash; In a satin Vest!

Emily Dickinson





Prayer is the little implement


Prayer is the little implement

Through which Men reach

Where Presence&mdash;is denied them.

They fling their Speech

By means of it&mdash;in God's Ear&mdash; If then He hear&mdash;

This sums the Apparatus

Comprised in Prayer&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






Precious to Me&mdash;She still shall be&mdash; Though She forget the name I bear&mdash; The fashion of the Gown I wear&mdash; The very Color of My Hair&mdash;

So like the Meadows&mdash;now&mdash; I dared to show a Tress of Theirs

If haply&mdash;She might not despise A Buttercup's Array&mdash;

I know the Whole&mdash;obscures the Part&mdash; The fraction&mdash;that appeased the Heart Till Number's Empery&mdash;

Remembered&mdash;as the Millner's flower When Summer's Everlasting Dower&mdash; Confronts the dazzled Bee.

Emily Dickinson





Precious to Me—She still shall be


Precious to Me—She still shall be—

Though She forget the name I bear—

The fashion of the Gown I wear—

The very Color of My Hair—

So like the Meadows—now—

I dared to show a Tress of Theirs

If haply—She might not despise

A Buttercup's Array—

I know the Whole—obscures the Part—

The fraction—that appeased the Heart

Till Number's Empery—

Remembered—as the Millner's flower

When Summer's Everlasting Dower—

Confronts the dazzled Bee.

Emily Dickinson

Promise This&mdash;When You be Dying&mdash; Some shall summon Me&mdash;

Mine belong Your latest Sighing&mdash; Mine&mdash;to Belt Your Eye&mdash; Not with Coins&mdash;though they be Minted From an Emperor's Hand&mdash;

Be my lips&mdash;the only Buckle

Your low Eyes&mdash;demand&mdash; Mine to stay&mdash;when all have wandered&mdash; To devise once more

If the Life be too surrendered&mdash; Life of Mine&mdash;restore&mdash; Poured like this&mdash;My Whole Libation&mdash; Just that You should see

Bliss of Death&mdash;Life's Bliss extol thro'

Imitating You&mdash;

Mine&mdash;to guard Your Narrow Precinct&mdash; To seduce the Sun

Longest on Your South, to linger,

Largest Dews of Morn

To demand, in Your low favor

Lest the Jealous Grass

Greener lean&mdash;Or fonder cluster Round some other face&mdash;

Mine to supplicate Madonna&mdash;

If Madonna be

Could behold so far a Creature&mdash; Christ&mdash;omitted&mdash;Me&mdash; Just to follow Your dear future&mdash; Ne'er so far behind&mdash;

For My Heaven&mdash;

Had I not been

Most enough&mdash;denied?

Emily Dickinson





Promise This—When You be Dying


Promise This—When You be Dying—

Some shall summon Me—

Mine belong Your latest Sighing—

Mine—to Belt Your Eye—

Not with Coins—though they be Minted

From an Emperor's Hand—

Be my lips—the only Buckle

Your low Eyes—demand—

Mine to stay—when all have wandered—

To devise once more

If the Life be too surrendered—

Life of Mine—restore—

Poured like this—My Whole Libation—

Just that You should see

Bliss of Death—Life's Bliss extol thro'

Imitating You—

Mine—to guard Your Narrow Precinct—

To seduce the Sun

Longest on Your South, to linger,

Largest Dews of Morn

To demand, in Your low favor

Lest the Jealous Grass

Greener lean—Or fonder cluster

Round some other face—

Mine to supplicate Madonna—

If Madonna be

Could behold so far a Creature—

Christ—omitted—Me—

Just to follow Your dear future—

Ne'er so far behind—

For My Heaven—

Had I not been

Most enough—denied?

Emily Dickinson





Publication

Publication -- is the Auction

Of the Mind of Man --

Poverty -- be justifying

For so foul a thing

Possibly -- but We -- would rather

From Our Garret go

White -- Unto the White Creator --

Than invest -- Our Snow --

Thought belong to Him who gave it --

Then -- to Him Who bear

Its Corporeal illustration -- Sell

The Royal Air --

In the Parcel -- Be the Merchant

Of the Heavenly Grace --

But reduce no Human Spirit

To Disgrace of Price --

Emily Dickinson
