Put up my lute!


Put up my lute!

What of&mdash;my Music!

Since the sole ear I cared to charm&mdash; Passive&mdash;as Granite&mdash;laps My Music&mdash; Sobbing&mdash;will suit&mdash;as well as psalm!

Would but the "Memnon" of the Desert&mdash; Teach me the strain

That vanquished Him&mdash;

When He&mdash;surrendered to the Sunrise&mdash; Maybe&mdash;that&mdash;would awaken&mdash;them!

Emily Dickinson






Read&mdash;Sweet&mdash;how others&mdash;strove&mdash; Till we&mdash;are stouter&mdash; What they&mdash;renounced&mdash; Till we&mdash;are less afraid&mdash; How many times they&mdash;bore the faithful witness&mdash; Till we&mdash;are helped&mdash; As if a Kingdom&mdash;cared!

Read then&mdash;of faith&mdash; That shone above the fagot&mdash;

Clear strains of Hymn

The River could not drown&mdash;

Brave names of Men&mdash;

And Celestial Women&mdash;

Passed out&mdash;of Record

Into&mdash;Renown!

Emily Dickinson





Read—Sweet—how others—strove


Read—Sweet—how others—strove—

Till we—are stouter—

What they—renounced—

Till we—are less afraid—

How many times they—bore the faithful witness—

Till we—are helped—

As if a Kingdom—cared!

Read then—of faith—

That shone above the fagot—

Clear strains of Hymn

The River could not drown—

Brave names of Men—

And Celestial Women—

Passed out—of Record

Into—Renown!

Emily Dickinson





Rehearsal to Ourselves


Rehearsal to Ourselves

Of a Withdrawn Delight&mdash;

Affords a Bliss like Murder&mdash; Omnipotent&mdash;Acute&mdash;

We will not drop the Dirk&mdash;

Because We love the Wound

The Dirk Commemorate&mdash;Itself

Remind Us that we died.

Emily Dickinson





Remorse

Remorse -- is Memory -- awake --

Her Parties all astir --

A Presence of Departed Acts --

At window -- and at Door --

Its Past -- set down before the Soul

And lighted with a Match --

Perusal -- to facilitate --

And help Belief to stretch --

Remorse is cureless -- the Disease

Not even God -- can heal --

For 'tis His institution -- and

The Adequate of Hell --

Emily Dickinson

Removed from Accident of Loss


Removed from Accident of Loss

By Accident of Gain

Befalling not my simple Days&mdash; Myself had just to earn&mdash;

Of Riches&mdash;as unconscious

As is the Brown Malay

Of Pearls in Eastern Waters,

Marked His&mdash;What Holiday

Would stir his slow conception&mdash; Had he the power to dream

That put the Dower's fraction&mdash; Awaited even&mdash;Him&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Renunciation

Renunciation -- is a piercing Virtue --

The letting go

A Presence -- for an Expectation --

Not now --

The putting out of Eyes --

Just Sunrise --

Lest Day --

Day's Great Progenitor --

Outvie

Renunciation -- is the Choosing

Against itself --

Itself to justify

Unto itself --

When larger function --

Make that appear --

Smaller -- that Covered Vision -- Here --

Emily Dickinson

Reverse cannot befall


Reverse cannot befall

Whose Sources are interior&mdash;

Ribbons of the Year


Ribbons of the Year&mdash;

Multitude Brocade&mdash;

Worn to Nature's Party once

Then, as flung aside

As a faded Bead

Or a Wrinkled Pearl

Who shall charge the Vanity

Of the Maker's Girl?

Emily Dickinson






Robbed by Death&mdash;but that was easy&mdash; To the failing Eye

I could hold the latest Glowing&mdash; Robbed by Liberty

For Her Jugular Defences&mdash;

This, too, I endured&mdash;

Hint of Glory&mdash;it afforded&mdash; For the Brave Beloved&mdash;

Fraud of Distance&mdash;Fraud of Danger, Fraud of Death&mdash;to bear&mdash; It is Bounty&mdash;to Suspense's

Vague Calamity&mdash;

Stalking our entire Possession

On a Hair's result&mdash;

Then&mdash;seesawing&mdash;coolly&mdash;on it&mdash; Trying if it split&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Robbed by Death—but that was easy


Robbed by Death—but that was easy—

To the failing Eye

I could hold the latest Glowing—

Robbed by Liberty

For Her Jugular Defences—

This, too, I endured—

Hint of Glory—it afforded—

For the Brave Beloved—

Fraud of Distance—Fraud of Danger,

Vague Calamity—

Stalking our entire Possession

On a Hair's result—

Then—seesawing—coolly—on it—

Trying if it split—

Emily Dickinson





Safe in Their Alabaster Chambers

Safe in their Alabaster Chambers --

Untouched by Morning

And untouched by Noon --

Sleep the meek members of the Resurrection --

Rafter of satin,

And Roof of stone.

Light laughs the breeze

In her Castle above them --

Babbles the Bee in a stolid Ear,

Pipe the Sweet Birds in ignorant cadence --

Ah, what sagacity perished here!

Emily Dickinson





Safe in their alabaster chambers,

Safe in their alabaster chambers,

Untouched by morning and untouched by noon, Sleep the meek members of the resurrection, Rafter of satin, and roof of stone.

Light laughs the breeze in her castle of sunshine; Babbles the bee in a stolid ear;

Pipe the sweet birds in ignorant cadences, --

Ah, what sagacity perished here!

Grand go the years in the crescent above them; Worlds scoop their arcs, and firmaments row, Diadems drop and Doges surrender,

Soundless as dots on a disk of snow.

Emily Dickinson





Savior! I've no one else to tell


Savior! I've no one else to tell&mdash; And so I trouble thee.

I am the one forgot thee so&mdash; Dost thou remember me?

Nor, for myself, I came so far&mdash; That were the little load&mdash;

I brought thee the imperial Heart

I had not strength to hold&mdash;

The Heart I carried in my own&mdash; Till mine too heavy grew&mdash;

Yet&mdash;strangest&mdash;heavier since it went&mdash; Is it too large for you?

Emily Dickinson





Severer Service of myself


Severer Service of myself

I&mdash;hastened to demand

To fill the awful Vacuum

Your life had left behind&mdash;

I worried Nature with my Wheels

When Hers had ceased to run&mdash; When she had put away Her Work

My own had just begun.

I strove to weary Brain and Bone&mdash; To harass to fatigue

The glittering Retinue of nerves&mdash; Vitality to clog

To some dull comfort Those obtain

Who put a Head away

They knew the Hair to&mdash;

And forget the color of the Day&mdash; Affliction would not be appeased&mdash; The Darkness braced as firm

As all my stratagem had been

The Midnight to confirm&mdash;

No Drug for Consciousness&mdash;can be&mdash; Alternative to die

Is Nature's only Pharmacy

For Being's Malady&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Sexton! My Master's sleeping here


Sexton! My Master's sleeping here.

Pray lead me to his bed!

I came to build the Bird's nest,

And sow the Early seed&mdash;

That when the snow creeps slowly

From off his chamber door&mdash;

Daisies point the way there&mdash; And the Troubadour.

Emily Dickinson





She bore it till the simple veins


She bore it till the simple veins

Traced azure on her hand&mdash;

Til pleading, round her quiet eyes

The purple Crayons stand.

Till Daffodils had come and gone

I cannot tell the sum,

And then she ceased to bear it&mdash; And with the Saints sat down.

No more her patient figure

At twilight soft to meet&mdash;

No more her timid bonnet

Upon the village street&mdash;

But Crowns instead, and Courtiers&mdash; And in the midst so fair,

Whose but her shy&mdash;immortal face Of whom we're whispering here?

Emily Dickinson






She dealt her pretty words like Blades&mdash; How glittering they shone&mdash;

And every One unbared a Nerve

Or wantoned with a Bone&mdash;

She never deemed&mdash;she hurt&mdash; That&mdash;is not Steel's Affair&mdash; A vulgar grimace in the Flesh&mdash; How ill the Creatures bear&mdash;

To Ache is human&mdash;not polite&mdash; The Film upon the eye

Mortality's old Custom&mdash;

Just locking up&mdash;to Die.

Emily Dickinson





She died at play


She died at play,

Gambolled away

Her lease of spotted hours,

Then sank as gaily as a Turn

Upon a Couch of flowers.

Her ghost strolled softly o'er the hill Yesterday, and Today,

Her vestments as the silver fleece&mdash; Her countenance as spray.

Emily Dickinson






She died&mdash;this was the way she died.

And when her breath was done

Took up her simple wardrobe

And started for the sun.

Her little figure at the gate

The Angels must have spied,

Since I could never find her

Upon the mortal side.

Emily Dickinson

She dwelleth in the Ground


She dwelleth in the Ground&mdash;

Where Daffodils&mdash;abide&mdash; Her Maker&mdash;Her Metropolis&mdash; The Universe&mdash;Her Maid&mdash; To fetch Her Grace&mdash;and Hue&mdash; And Fairness&mdash;and Renown&mdash; The Firmament's&mdash;To Pluck Her&mdash; And fetch Her Thee&mdash;be mine&mdash; Emily Dickinson





She hideth Her the last


She hideth Her the last&mdash;

And is the first, to rise&mdash;

Her Night doth hardly recompense

The Closing of Her eyes&mdash;

She doth Her Purple Work&mdash;

And putteth Her away

In low Apartments in the Sod -

As worthily as We.

To imitate her life

As impotent would be

As make of Our imperfect Mints,

The Julep&mdash;of the Bee&mdash; Emily Dickinson





She lay as if at play


She lay as if at play

Her life had leaped away&mdash;

Intending to return&mdash;

But not so soon&mdash;

Her merry Arms, half dropt&mdash;

As if for lull of sport&mdash;

An instant had forgot&mdash;

The Trick to start&mdash;

Her dancing Eyes&mdash;ajar&mdash; As if their Owner were

Still sparkling through

For fun&mdash;at you&mdash;

Her Morning at the door&mdash;

Devising, I am sure&mdash;

To force her sleep&mdash;

So light&mdash;so deep&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





She rose to His Requirement


She rose to His Requirement&mdash;dropt The Playthings of Her Life

To take the honorable Work

Of Woman, and of Wife&mdash;

If ought She missed in Her new Day,

Of Amplitude, or Awe&mdash;

Or first Prospective&mdash;Or the Gold In using, wear away,

It lay unmentioned&mdash;as the Sea Develop Pearl, and Weed,

But only to Himself&mdash;be known The Fathoms they abide&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

She rose to his requirement, dropped

She rose to his requirement, dropped

The playthings of her life

To take the honorable work

Of woman and of wife.

If aught she missed in her new day

Of amplitude, or awe,

Or first prospective, or the gold

In using wore away,

It lay unmentioned, as the sea

Develops pearl and weed,

But only to himself is known

The fathoms they abide.

Emily Dickinson






She sights a Bird&mdash;she chuckles&mdash; She flattens&mdash;then she crawls&mdash; She runs without the look of feet&mdash; Her eyes increase to Balls&mdash;

Her Jaws stir&mdash;twitching&mdash;hungry&mdash; Her Teeth can hardly stand&mdash;

She leaps, but Robin leaped the first&mdash; Ah, Pussy, of the Sand,

The Hopes so juicy ripening&mdash; You almost bather your Tongue&mdash; When Bliss disclosed a hundred Toes&mdash; And fled with every one&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





She sights a Bird—she chuckles


She sights a Bird—she chuckles—

She flattens—then she crawls—

She runs without the look of feet—

Her eyes increase to Balls—

Her Jaws stir—twitching—hungry—

Her Teeth can hardly stand—

She leaps, but Robin leaped the first—

Ah, Pussy, of the Sand,

The Hopes so juicy ripening—

You almost bather your Tongue—

When Bliss disclosed a hundred Toes—

And fled with every one—

Emily Dickinson





She slept beneath a tree


She slept beneath a tree&mdash;

Remembered but by me.

She recognized the foot&mdash;

Put on her carmine suit

And see!

Emily Dickinson





She sped as Petals of a Rose


She sped as Petals of a Rose

Offended by the Wind&mdash;

A frail Aristocrat of Time

Indemnity to find&mdash;

Leaving on nature&mdash;a Default

As Cricket or as Bee&mdash;

But Andes in the Bosoms where

She had begun to lie&mdash;

She sweeps with many-colored Brooms


She sweeps with many-colored Brooms&mdash; And leaves the Shreds behind&mdash; Oh Housewife in the Evening West&mdash; Come back, and dust the Pond!

You dropped a Purple Ravelling in&mdash; You dropped an Amber thread&mdash; And how you've littered all the East

With duds of Emerald!

Till Brooms fade softly into stars&mdash; And then I come away&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





She sweeps with many-colored brooms,

She sweeps with many-colored brooms,

And leaves the shreds behind;

Oh, housewife in the evening west,

Come back, and dust the pond!

You dropped a purple ravelling in,

You dropped an amber thread;

And now you've littered all the East

With duds of emerald!

And still she plies her spotted brooms, And still the aprons fly,

Till brooms fade softly into stars --

And then I come away.

Emily Dickinson





She went as quiet as the Dew


She went as quiet as the Dew

From an Accustomed flower.

Not like the Dew, did she return

At the Accustomed hour!

She dropt as softly as a star

From out my summer's Eve&mdash;

Less skillful than Le Verriere

It's sorer to believe!

Emily Dickinson

She's happy, with a new Content

Sic transit gloria mundi


"Sic transit gloria mundi,"

"How doth the busy bee,"

"Dum vivimus vivamus,"

I stay mine enemy!

Oh "veni, vidi, vici!"

Oh caput cap-a-pie!

And oh "memento mori"

When I am far from thee!

Hurrah for Peter Parley!

Hurrah for Daniel Boone!

Three cheers, sir, for the gentleman

Who first observed the moon!

Peter, put up the sunshine;

Patti, arrange the stars;

Tell Luna, tea is waiting,

And call your brother Mars!

Put down the apple, Adam,

And come away with me,

So shalt thou have a pippin

From off my father's tree!

I climb the "Hill of Science,"

I "view the landscape o'er;"

Such transcendental prospect,

I ne'er beheld before!

Unto the Legislature

My country bids me go;

I'll take my india rubbers,

In case the wind should blow!

During my education,

It was announced to me

That gravitation, stumbling,

Fell from an apple tree!

The earth upon an axis

Was once supposed to turn,

By way of a gymnastic

In honor of the sun!

It was the brave Columbus,

A sailing o'er the tide,

Who notified the nations

Of where I would reside!





Mortality is fatal&mdash;

Gentility is fine,

Rascality, heroic,

Insolvency, sublime!

Our Fathers being weary,

Laid down on Bunker Hill;

And tho' full many a morning,

Yet they are sleeping still,&mdash; The trumpet, sir, shall wake them,

In dreams I see them rise,

Each with a solemn musket

A marching to the skies!

A coward will remain, Sir,

Until the fight is done;

But an immortal hero

Will take his hat, and run!

Good bye, Sir, I am going;

My country calleth me;

Allow me, Sir, at parting,

To wipe my weeping e'e.

In token of our friendship

Accept this "Bonnie Doon,"

And when the hand that plucked it

Hath passed beyond the moon,

The memory of my ashes

Will consolation be;

Then, farewell, Tuscarora,

And farewell, Sir, to thee!

Emily Dickinson






Size circumscribes&mdash;it has no room For petty furniture&mdash;

The Giant tolerates no Gnat

For Ease of Gianture&mdash;

Repudiates it, all the more&mdash; Because intrinsic size

Ignores the possibility

Of Calumnies&mdash;or Flies.

Emily Dickinson

Sleep is supposed to be


Sleep is supposed to be

By souls of sanity

The shutting of the eye.

Sleep is the station grand

Down which, on either hand

The hosts of witness stand!

Morn is supposed to be

By people of degree

The breaking of the Day.

Morning has not occurred!

That shall Aurora be&mdash;

East of Eternity&mdash;

One with the banner gay&mdash;

One in the red array&mdash;

That is the break of Day!

Emily Dickinson





Smiling back from Coronation


Smiling back from Coronation

May be Luxury&mdash;

On the Heads that started with us&mdash; Being's Peasantry&mdash;

Recognizing in Procession

Ones We former knew&mdash;

When Ourselves were also dusty&mdash; Centuries ago&mdash;

Had the Triumph no Conviction

Of how many be&mdash;

Stimulated&mdash;by the Contrast&mdash; Unto Misery&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

Snow beneath whose chilly softness

We so new bestow

Than thine acclimated Creature

Snow flakes


Snow flakes.

I counted till they danced so

Their slippers leaped the town,

And then I took a pencil

To note the rebels down.

And then they grew so jolly

I did resign the prig,

And ten of my once stately toes

Are marshalled for a jig!

Emily Dickinson





So bashful when I spied her!

And bore her struggling, blushing,

Her simple haunts beyond!

But I shall never tell!

Some Keep the Sabbath Going to Church

Some keep the Sabbath going to Church --

I keep it, staying at Home --

With a Bobolink for a Chorister --

And an Orchard, for a Dome --

Some keep the Sabbath in Surplice --

I just wear my Wings --

And instead of tolling the Bell, for Church, Our little Sexton -- sings.

God preaches, a noted Clergyman --

And the sermon is never long,

So instead of getting to Heaven, at least --

I'm going, all along.

Emily Dickinson





Some Rainbow&mdash;coming from the Fair!


Some Rainbow&mdash;coming from the Fair!

Some Vision of the World Cashmere&mdash; I confidently see!

Or else a Peacock's purple Train

Feather by feather&mdash;on the plain Fritters itself away!

The dreamy Butterflies bestir!

Lethargic pools resume the whir

Of last year's sundered tune!

From some old Fortress on the sun

Baronial Bees&mdash;march&mdash;one by one&mdash; In murmuring platoon!

The Robins stand as thick today

As flakes of snow stood yesterday&mdash; On fence&mdash;and Roof&mdash;and Twig!

The Orchis binds her feather on

For her old lover - Don the Sun!

Revisiting the Bog!

Without Commander! Countless! Still!

The Regiments of Wood and Hill

In bright detachment stand!

Behold! Whose Multitudes are these?

The children of whose turbaned seas&mdash; Or what Circassian Land?

Emily Dickinson

Some Rainbow—coming from the Fair!

Behold! Whose Multitudes are these?

The children of whose turbaned seas—

Or what Circassian Land?

Emily Dickinson





Some such Butterfly be seen


Some such Butterfly be seen

On Brazilian Pampas&mdash;

Just at noon&mdash;no later&mdash;Sweet&mdash; Then&mdash;the License closes&mdash; Some such Spice&mdash;express and pass&mdash; Subject to Your Plucking&mdash;

As the Stars&mdash;You knew last Night&mdash; Foreigners&mdash;This Morning&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Some things that fly there be


Some things that fly there be&mdash; Birds&mdash;Hours&mdash;the Bumblebee&mdash; Of these no Elegy.

Some things that stay there be&mdash; Grief&mdash;Hills&mdash;Eternity&mdash; Nor this behooveth me.

There are that resting, rise.

Can I expound the skies?

How still the Riddle lies!

Emily Dickinson





Some&mdash;Work for Immortality


Some&mdash;Work for Immortality&mdash; The Chiefer part, for Time&mdash;

He&mdash;Compensates&mdash;immediately&mdash; The former&mdash;Checks&mdash;on Fame&mdash; Slow Gold&mdash;but Everlasting&mdash; The Bullion of Today&mdash;

Contrasted with the Currency

Of Immortality&mdash;

A Beggar&mdash;Here and There&mdash; Is gifted to discern

Beyond the Broker's insight&mdash; One's&mdash;Money&mdash;One's&mdash;the Mine&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Some, too fragile for winter winds


Some, too fragile for winter winds

The thoughtful grave encloses&mdash; Tenderly tucking them in from frost

Before their feet are cold.

Never the treasures in her nest

The cautious grave exposes,

Building where schoolboy dare not look, And sportsman is not bold.

This covert have all the children

Early aged, and often cold,

Sparrow, unnoticed by the Father&mdash; Lambs for whom time had not a fold.

Emily Dickinson





Some—Work for Immortality


Some—Work for Immortality—

The Chiefer part, for Time—

He—Compensates—immediately—

The former—Checks—on Fame—

Slow Gold—but Everlasting—

The Bullion of Today—

Contrasted with the Currency

Of Immortality—

A Beggar—Here and There—

Is gifted to discern

Beyond the Broker's insight—

One's—Money—One's—the Mine—

Emily Dickinson





Soto! Explore thyself!


Soto! Explore thyself!

Therein thyself shalt find

The "Undiscovered Continent"&mdash; No Settler had the Mind.

Emily Dickinson





Soul, Wilt thou toss again?


Soul, Wilt thou toss again?

By just such a hazard

Hundreds have lost indeed&mdash;

But tens have won an all&mdash;

Angel's breathless ballot

Lingers to record thee&mdash;

Imps in eager Caucus

Raffle for my Soul!

Emily Dickinson





South Winds jostle them


South Winds jostle them&mdash;

Bumblebees come&mdash;

Hover&mdash;hesitate&mdash;

Drink, and are gone&mdash;

Butterflies pause

On their passage Cashmere&mdash;

I&mdash;softly plucking,

Present them here!

Emily Dickinson





Sown in dishonor


"Sown in dishonor"!

Ah! Indeed!

May this "dishonor" be?

If I were half so fine myself

I'd notice nobody!

"Sown in corruption"!

Not so fast!

Apostle is askew!


A Circumstance or two!

Emily Dickinson





Speech—is a prank of Parliament—

"Speech"—is a prank of Parliament—

"Tears"—is a trick of the nerve—

But the Heart with the heaviest freight on—

Doesn't—always—move—

Emily Dickinson





Split the Lark

Split the Lark -- and you'll find the Music --

Bulb after Bulb, in Silver rolled --

Scantilly dealt to the Summer Morning

Saved for your Ear when Lutes be old.

Loose the Flood -- you shall find it patent --

Gush after Gush, reserved for you --

Scarlet Experiment! Sceptic Thomas!

Now, do you doubt that your Bird was true?

Emily Dickinson






Split the Lark&mdash;and you'll find the Music&mdash; Bulb after Bulb, in Silver rolled&mdash; Scantilly dealt to the Summer Morning

Saved for your Ear when Lutes be old.

Loose the Flood&mdash;you shall find it patent&mdash; Gush after Gush, reserved for you&mdash; Scarlet Experiment! Sceptic Thomas!

Split the Lark—and you'll find the Music—

Bulb after Bulb, in Silver rolled—

Scantilly dealt to the Summer Morning

Saved for your Ear when Lutes be old.

Loose the Flood—you shall find it patent—

Gush after Gush, reserved for you—

Scarlet Experiment! Sceptic Thomas!

Now, do you doubt that your Bird was true?

Emily Dickinson





Spring is the Period


Spring is the Period

Express from God.

Among the other seasons

Himself abide,

But during March and April

None stir abroad

Without a cordial interview

With God.

Emily Dickinson






Strong Draughts of Their Refreshing Minds To drink&mdash;enables Mine

Through Desert or the Wilderness

As bore it Sealed Wine&mdash;

To go elastic&mdash;Or as One

The Camel's trait&mdash;attained&mdash; How powerful the Stimulus

Of an Hermetic Mind&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Struck, was I, not yet by Lightning


Struck, was I, not yet by Lightning&mdash; Lightning&mdash;lets away

Power to perceive His Process

With Vitality.

Maimed&mdash;was I&mdash;yet not by Venture&mdash; Stone of stolid Boy&mdash;

Nor a Sportsman's Peradventure&mdash; Who mine Enemy?

Robbed&mdash;was I&mdash;intact to Bandit&mdash; All my Mansion torn&mdash;

Sun&mdash;withdrawn to Recognition&mdash; Furthest shining&mdash;done&mdash; Yet was not the foe&mdash;of any&mdash; Not the smallest Bird

In the nearest Orchard dwelling

Be of Me&mdash;afraid.

Most&mdash;I love the Cause that slew Me.

Often as I die

Its beloved Recognition

Holds a Sun on Me&mdash;

Best&mdash;at Setting&mdash;as is Nature's&mdash; Neither witnessed Rise

Till the infinite Aurora

In the other's eyes.

Emily Dickinson





Success is Counted Sweetest

Success is counted sweetest

By those who ne'er succeed.

To comprehend a nectar

Requires sorest need.

Not one of all the purple Host

Who took the Flag today

Can tell the definition

So clear of Victory

As he defeated--dying--

On whose forbidden ear

The distant strains of triumph

Burst agonized and clear!

Emily Dickinson





Such is the Force of Happiness


Such is the Force of Happiness&mdash; The Least&mdash;can lift a Ton

Assisted by its stimulus&mdash;

Who Misery&mdash;sustain&mdash; No Sinew can afford&mdash;

The Cargo of Themselves&mdash;

Too infinite for Consciousness'

Slow capabilities.

Emily Dickinson





Summer for thee, grant I may be


Summer for thee, grant I may be

When Summer days are flown!

Thy music still, when Whipporwill

And Oriole&mdash;are done!

For thee to bloom, I'll skip the tomb

And row my blossoms o'er!

Pray gather me&mdash;

Anemone&mdash;

Thy flower&mdash;forevermore!

Emily Dickinson





Summer Shower

A drop fell on the apple tree,

Another on the roof;

A half a dozen kissed the eaves,

And made the gables laugh.

A few went out to help the brook,

That went to help the sea.

Myself conjectured, Were they pearls,

What necklaces could be!

The dust replaced in hoisted roads,

The birds jocoser sung;

The sunshine threw his hat away,

The orchards spangles hung.

The breezes brought dejected lutes,

And bathed them in the glee;

The East put out a single flag,

And signed the fete away.

Emily Dickinson





Sunset at Night&mdash;is natural


Sunset at Night&mdash;is natural&mdash; But Sunset on the Dawn

Reverses Nature&mdash;Master&mdash; So Midnight's&mdash;due&mdash;at Noon.

Eclipses be&mdash;predicted&mdash; And Science bows them in&mdash;

But do one face us suddenly&mdash; Jehovah's Watch&mdash;is wrong.

Emily Dickinson





Sunset at Night—is natural


Sunset at Night—is natural—

But Sunset on the Dawn

Reverses Nature—Master—

So Midnight's—due—at Noon.

Eclipses be—predicted—

And Science bows them in—

But do one face us suddenly—

Jehovah's Watch—is wrong.

Emily Dickinson





Superfluous were the Sun


Superfluous were the Sun

When Excellence be dead

He were superfluous every Day

For every Day be said

That syllable whose Faith

Just saves it from Despair

And whose "I'll meet You" hesitates If Love inquire "Where"?

Upon His dateless Fame

Our Periods may lie

As Stars that drop anonymous

From an abundant sky.

Emily Dickinson





Surgeons must be very careful


Surgeons must be very careful

When they take the knife!

Underneath their fine incisions

Stirs the Culprit&mdash;Life!

Emily Dickinson






Suspense&mdash;is Hostiler than Death&mdash; Death&mdash;tho'soever Broad,

Is Just Death, and cannot increase&mdash; Suspense&mdash;does not conclude&mdash; But perishes&mdash;to live anew&mdash; But just anew to die&mdash;

Annihilation&mdash;plated fresh

With Immortality&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Suspense—is Hostiler than Death


Suspense—is Hostiler than Death—

Death—tho'soever Broad,

Is Just Death, and cannot increase—

Suspense—does not conclude—

But perishes—to live anew—

But just anew to die—

Annihilation—plated fresh

With Immortality—

Emily Dickinson






Sweet Mountains&mdash;Ye tell Me no lie&mdash; Never deny Me&mdash;Never fly&mdash; Those same unvarying Eyes

Turn on Me&mdash;when I fail&mdash;or feign, Or take the Royal names in vain&mdash; Their far&mdash;slow&mdash;Violet Gaze&mdash; My Strong Madonnas&mdash;Cherish still&mdash; The Wayward Nun&mdash;beneath the Hill&mdash; Whose service&mdash;is to You&mdash; Her latest Worship&mdash;When the Day Fades from the Firmament away&mdash; To lift Her Brows on You&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Sweet Mountains—Ye tell Me no lie


Sweet Mountains—Ye tell Me no lie—

Never deny Me—Never fly—

Those same unvarying Eyes

Turn on Me—when I fail—or feign,

Or take the Royal names in vain—

Their far—slow—Violet Gaze—

My Strong Madonnas—Cherish still—

The Wayward Nun—beneath the Hill—

Whose service—is to You—

Her latest Worship—When the Day

Fades from the Firmament away—

To lift Her Brows on You—

Emily Dickinson





Sweet&mdash;safe&mdash;Houses


Sweet&mdash;safe&mdash;Houses&mdash; Glad&mdash;gay&mdash;Houses&mdash; Sealed so stately tight&mdash;

Lids of Steel&mdash;on Lids of Marble&mdash; Locking Bare feet out&mdash;

Brooks of Plush&mdash;in Banks of Satin Not so softly fall

As the laughter&mdash;and the whisper&mdash; From their People Pearl&mdash;

No Bald Death&mdash;affront their Parlors&mdash; No Bold Sickness come

To deface their Stately Treasures&mdash; Anguish&mdash;and the Tomb&mdash; Hum by&mdash;in Muffled Coaches&mdash; Lest they&mdash;wonder Why&mdash; Any&mdash;for the Press of Smiling&mdash; Interrupt&mdash;to die&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






Sweet&mdash;You forgot&mdash;but I remembered Every time&mdash;for Two&mdash; So that the Sum be never hindered

Through Decay of You&mdash;

Say if I erred? Accuse my Farthings&mdash; Blame the little Hand

Happy it be for You&mdash;a Beggar's&mdash; Seeking More&mdash;to spend&mdash; Just to be Rich&mdash;to waste my Guineas On so Best a Heart&mdash;

Just to be Poor&mdash;for Barefoot Vision You&mdash;Sweet&mdash;Shut me out&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Sweet, to have had them lost


Sweet, to have had them lost

For news that they be saved&mdash; The nearer they departed Us

The nearer they, restored,

Shall stand to Our Right Hand&mdash; Most precious and the Dead&mdash;

Next precious

Those that rose to go&mdash;

Then thought of Us, and stayed.

Emily Dickinson





Sweet—safe—Houses


Sweet—safe—Houses—

Glad—gay—Houses—

Sealed so stately tight—

Lids of Steel—on Lids of Marble—

Locking Bare feet out—

Brooks of Plush—in Banks of Satin

Not so softly fall

As the laughter—and the whisper—

From their People Pearl—

No Bald Death—affront their Parlors—

No Bold Sickness come

To deface their Stately Treasures—

Anguish—and the Tomb—

Hum by—in Muffled Coaches—

Lest they—wonder Why—

Any—for the Press of Smiling—

Interrupt—to die—

Emily Dickinson





Sweet—You forgot—but I remembered


Sweet—You forgot—but I remembered

Every time—for Two—

So that the Sum be never hindered

Through Decay of You—

Say if I erred? Accuse my Farthings—

Blame the little Hand

Happy it be for You—a Beggar's—

Seeking More—to spend—

Just to be Rich—to waste my Guineas

On so Best a Heart—

Just to be Poor—for Barefoot Vision

You—Sweet—Shut me out—

Emily Dickinson





T was just this time last year I died.

'T was just this time last year I died.

I know I heard the corn,

When I was carried by the farms,--

It had the tassels on.

I thought how yellow it would look

When Richard went to mill;

And then I wanted to get out,

But something held my will.

I thought just how red apples wedged

The stubble's joints between;

And carts went stooping round the fields To take the pumpkins in.

I wondered which would miss me least,

And when Thanksgiving came,

If father'd multiply the plates

To make an even sum.

And if my stocking hung too high,

Would it blur the Christmas glee,

That not a Santa Claus could reach

The altitude of me?

But this sort grieved myself, and so

I thought how it would be

When just this time, some perfect year, Themselves should come to me.

Emily Dickinson

'T was just this time last year I died.

When I was carried by the farms,--

It had the tassels on.

I thought just how red apples wedged

The stubble's joints between;

And carts went stooping round the fields To take the pumpkins in.

I wondered which would miss me least,

And when Thanksgiving came,

If father'd multiply the plates

To make an even sum.

And if my stocking hung too high,

Would it blur the Christmas glee,

That not a Santa Claus could reach

The altitude of me?

But this sort grieved myself, and so

I thought how it would be

Emily Dickinson





Take your Heaven further on


Take your Heaven further on&mdash; This&mdash;to Heaven divine Has gone&mdash; Had You earlier blundered in

Possibly, e'en You had seen

An Eternity&mdash;put on&mdash; Now&mdash;to ring a Door beyond

Is the utmost of Your Hand&mdash;

To the Skies&mdash;apologize&mdash; Nearer to Your Courtesies

Than this Sufferer polite&mdash;

Dressed to meet You&mdash;

See&mdash;in White!

Emily Dickinson





Taking up the fair Ideal


Taking up the fair Ideal,

Just to cast her down

When a fracture&mdash;we discover&mdash; Or a splintered Crown&mdash;

Makes the Heavens portable&mdash;

And the Gods&mdash;a lie&mdash; Doubtless&mdash;"Adam"&mdash;scowled at Eden&mdash; For his perjury!

Cherishing&mdash;our pool Ideal&mdash; Till in purer dress&mdash;

We behold her&mdash;glorified&mdash; Comforts&mdash;search&mdash;like this&mdash; Till the broken creatures&mdash;

We adored&mdash;for whole&mdash; Stains&mdash;all washed&mdash; Transfigured&mdash;mended&mdash; Meet us&mdash;with a smile&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Talk with prudence to a Beggar


Talk with prudence to a Beggar

Of "Potose," and the mines!

Reverently, to the Hungry

Of your viands, and your wines!

Cautious, hint to any Captive

You have passed enfranchised feet!

Anecdotes of air in Dungeons

Have sometimes proved deadly sweet!

Emily Dickinson






Teach Him&mdash;When He makes the names&mdash; Such an one&mdash;to say&mdash; On his babbling&mdash;Berry&mdash;lips&mdash; As should sound&mdash;to me&mdash; Were my Ear&mdash;as near his nest&mdash; As my thought&mdash;today&mdash; As should sound&mdash;

"Forbid us not"&mdash;

Some like "Emily."

Emily Dickinson





Teach Him—When He makes the names


Teach Him—When He makes the names—

Such an one—to say—

On his babbling—Berry—lips—

As should sound—to me—

Were my Ear—as near his nest—

As my thought—today—

As should sound—

"Forbid us not"—

Some like "Emily."

Emily Dickinson





Tell All The Truth

Tell all the truth but tell it slant,

Success in circuit lies,

Too bright for our infirm delight

The truth's superb surprise;

As lightning to the children eased

With explanation kind,

The truth must dazzle gradually

Or every man be blind.

Emily Dickinson





Tell all the Truth but tell it slant


Tell all the Truth but tell it slant&mdash; Success in Circuit lies

Too bright for our infirm Delight

The Truth's superb surprise

As Lightning to the Children eased

With explanation kind

The Truth must dazzle gradually

Or every man be blind&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






That after Horror&mdash;that 'twas us&mdash; That passed the mouldering Pier&mdash; Just as the Granite Crumb let go&mdash; Our Savior, by a Hair&mdash;

A second more, had dropped too deep

For Fisherman to plumb&mdash;

The very profile of the Thought

Puts Recollection numb&mdash;

The possibility&mdash;to pass

Without a Moment's Bell&mdash;

Into Conjecture's presence&mdash;

Is like a Face of Steel&mdash;

That suddenly looks into ours

With a metallic grin&mdash;

The Cordiality of Death&mdash;

Who drills his Welcome in&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





That after Horror—that 'twas us


That after Horror—that 'twas us—

That passed the mouldering Pier—

Just as the Granite Crumb let go—

Our Savior, by a Hair—

A second more, had dropped too deep

For Fisherman to plumb—

The very profile of the Thought

Puts Recollection numb—

The possibility—to pass

Without a Moment's Bell—

Into Conjecture's presence—

Is like a Face of Steel—

That suddenly looks into ours

With a metallic grin—

The Cordiality of Death—

Who drills his Welcome in—

Emily Dickinson





That Distance was between Us


That Distance was between Us

That is not of Mile or Main&mdash; The Will it is that situates&mdash; Equator&mdash;never can&mdash; Emily Dickinson






That first Day, when you praised Me, Sweet, And said that I was strong&mdash;

And could be mighty, if I liked&mdash; That Day&mdash;the Days among&mdash; Glows Central&mdash;like a Jewel

Between Diverging Golds&mdash;

The Minor One&mdash;that gleamed behind&mdash; And Vaster&mdash;of the World's.

Emily Dickinson





That I did always love


That I did always love

I bring thee Proof

That till I loved

I never lived&mdash;Enough&mdash; That I shall love alway&mdash;

I argue thee

That love is life&mdash;

And life hath Immortality&mdash;

This&mdash;dost thou doubt&mdash;Sweet&mdash; Then have I

Nothing to show

But Calvary&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





That is solemn we have ended


That is solemn we have ended

Be it but a Play

Or a Glee among the Garret

Or a Holiday

Or a leaving Home, or later,

Parting with a World

We have understood for better

Still to be explained.

Emily Dickinson






The Admirations&mdash;and Contempts&mdash;of time&mdash; Show justest&mdash;through an Open Tomb&mdash; The Dying&mdash;as it were a Height Reorganizes Estimate

And what We saw not

We distinguish clear&mdash;

And mostly&mdash;see not

What We saw before&mdash;

'Tis Compound Vision&mdash;

Light&mdash;enabling Light&mdash; The Finite&mdash;furnished

With the Infinite&mdash;

Convex&mdash;and Concave Witness&mdash; Back&mdash;toward Time&mdash;

And forward&mdash;

Toward the God of Him&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Admirations—and Contempts—of time


The Admirations—and Contempts—of time—

Show justest—through an Open Tomb—

The Dying—as it were a Height

Reorganizes Estimate

And what We saw not

We distinguish clear—

And mostly—see not

What We saw before—

'Tis Compound Vision—

Light—enabling Light—

The Finite—furnished

With the Infinite—

Convex—and Concave Witness—

Back—toward Time—

And forward—

Toward the God of Him—

Emily Dickinson





The Angle of a Landscape


The Angle of a Landscape&mdash;

That every time I wake&mdash;

Between my Curtain and the Wall

Upon an ample Crack&mdash;

Like a Venetian&mdash;waiting&mdash; Accosts my open eye&mdash;

Is just a Bough of Apples&mdash;

Held slanting, in the Sky&mdash;

The Pattern of a Chimney&mdash;

The Forehead of a Hill&mdash;

Sometimes&mdash;a Vane's Forefinger&mdash; But that's&mdash;Occasional&mdash; The Seasons&mdash;shift&mdash;my Picture&mdash; Upon my Emerald Bough,

I wake&mdash;to find no&mdash;Emeralds&mdash; Then&mdash;Diamonds&mdash;which the Snow From Polar Caskets&mdash;fetched me&mdash; The Chimney&mdash;and the Hill&mdash; And just the Steeple's finger&mdash; These&mdash;never stir at all&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The Battle fought between the Soul


The Battle fought between the Soul

And No Man&mdash;is the One

Of all the Battles prevalent&mdash; By far the Greater One&mdash;

No News of it is had abroad&mdash; Its Bodiless Campaign

Establishes, and terminates&mdash; Invisible&mdash;Unknown&mdash; Nor History&mdash;record it&mdash; As Legions of a Night

The Sunrise scatters&mdash;These endure&mdash; Enact&mdash;and terminate&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The Bee is not afraid of me


The Bee is not afraid of me.

I know the Butterfly.

The pretty people in the Woods

Receive me cordially&mdash;

The Brooks laugh louder when I come&mdash; The Breezes madder play;

Wherefore mine eye thy silver mists,

Wherefore, Oh Summer's Day?

Emily Dickinson





The Beggar Lad&mdash;dies early


The Beggar Lad&mdash;dies early&mdash; It's Somewhat in the Cold&mdash;

And Somewhat in the Trudging feet&mdash; And haply, in the World&mdash;

The Cruel&mdash;smiling&mdash;bowing World&mdash; That took its Cambric Way&mdash;

Nor heard the timid cry for "Bread"&mdash;

"Sweet Lady&mdash;Charity"&mdash; Among Redeemed Children

If Trudging feet may stand

The Barefoot time forgotten&mdash;so&mdash; The Sleet&mdash;the bitter Wind&mdash; The Childish Hands that teased for Pence Lifted adoring&mdash;them&mdash; To Him whom never Ragged&mdash;Coat Did supplicate in vain&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

The Bible is an antique Volume


The Bible is an antique Volume&mdash; Written by faded men

At the suggestion of Holy Spectres&mdash; Subjects&mdash;Bethlehem&mdash; Eden&mdash;the ancient Homestead&mdash; Satan&mdash;the Brigadier&mdash; Judas&mdash;the Great Defaulter&mdash; David&mdash;the Troubador&mdash; Sin&mdash;a distinguished Precipice Others must resist&mdash;

Boys that "believe" are very lonesome&mdash; Other Boys are "lost"&mdash; Had but the Tale a warbling Teller&mdash; All the Boys would come&mdash;

Orpheus' Sermon captivated&mdash;

It did not condemn&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Bird must sing to earn the Crumb


The Bird must sing to earn the Crumb

What merit have the Tune

No Breakfast if it guaranty

The Rose content may bloom

To gain renown of Lady's Drawer

But if the Lady come

But once a Century, the Rose

Superfluous become&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Birds begun at Four o'clock


The Birds begun at Four o'clock&mdash; Their period for Dawn&mdash;

A Music numerous as space&mdash;

But neighboring as Noon&mdash;

I could not count their Force&mdash; Their Voices did expend

As Brook by Brook bestows itself

To multiply the Pond.

Their Witnesses were not&mdash;

Except occasional man&mdash;

In homely industry arrayed&mdash;

To overtake the Morn&mdash;

Nor was it for applause&mdash;

That I could ascertain&mdash;

But independent Ecstasy

Of Deity and Men&mdash;

By Six, the Flood had done&mdash;

No Tumult there had been

Of Dressing, or Departure&mdash;

And yet the Band was gone&mdash;

The Sun engrossed the East&mdash;

The Day controlled the World&mdash; The Miracle that introduced

Forgotten, as fulfilled.

Emily Dickinson





The Birds reported from the South


The Birds reported from the South&mdash; A News express to Me&mdash;

A spicy Charge, My little Posts&mdash; But I am deaf&mdash;Today&mdash; The Flowers&mdash;appealed&mdash;a timid Throng&mdash; I reinforced the Door&mdash;

Go blossom for the Bees&mdash;I said&mdash; And trouble Me&mdash;no More&mdash; The Summer Grace, for Notice strove&mdash; Remote&mdash;Her best Array&mdash; The Heart&mdash;to stimulate the Eye Refused too utterly&mdash;

At length, a Mourner, like Myself,

She drew away austere&mdash;

Her frosts to ponder&mdash;then it was I recollected Her&mdash;

She suffered Me, for I had mourned&mdash; I offered Her no word&mdash;

My Witness&mdash;was the Crape I bore&mdash; Her&mdash;Witness&mdash;was Her Dead&mdash; Thenceforward&mdash;We&mdash;together dwelt&mdash; I never questioned Her&mdash;

Our Contract

A Wiser Sympathy

Emily Dickinson






The Black Berry&mdash;wears a Thorn in his side&mdash; But no Man heard Him cry&mdash;

He offers His Berry, just the same

To Partridge&mdash;and to Boy&mdash; He sometimes holds upon the Fence&mdash; Or struggles to a Tree&mdash;

Or clasps a Rock, with both His Hands&mdash; But not for Sympathy&mdash;

We&mdash;tell a Hurt&mdash;to cool it&mdash; This Mourner&mdash;to the Sky

A little further reaches&mdash;instead&mdash; Brave Black Berry&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Black Berry—wears a Thorn in his side The Black Berry—wears a Thorn in his side—

But no Man heard Him cry—

He offers His Berry, just the same

To Partridge—and to Boy—

He sometimes holds upon the Fence—

Or struggles to a Tree—

Or clasps a Rock, with both His Hands—

But not for Sympathy—

We—tell a Hurt—to cool it—

This Mourner—to the Sky

A little further reaches—instead—

Brave Black Berry—

Emily Dickinson





The Body grows without


The Body grows without&mdash;

The more convenient way&mdash;

That if the Spirit&mdash;like to hide Its Temple stands, alway,

Ajar&mdash;secure&mdash;inviting&mdash; It never did betray

The Soul that asked its shelter

In solemn honesty

Emily Dickinson






The Brain&mdash;is wider than the Sky&mdash; For&mdash;put them side by side&mdash; The one the other will contain

With ease&mdash;and You&mdash;beside&mdash; The Brain is deeper than the sea&mdash; For&mdash;hold them&mdash;Blue to Blue&mdash; The one the other will absorb&mdash; As Sponges&mdash;Buckets&mdash;do&mdash; The Brain is just the weight of God&mdash; For&mdash;Heft them&mdash;Pound for Pound&mdash; And they will differ&mdash;if they do&mdash; As Syllable from Sound&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Brain, within its Groove


The Brain, within its Groove

Runs evenly&mdash;and true&mdash; But let a Splinter swerve&mdash;

'Twere easier for You&mdash;

To put a Current back&mdash;

When Floods have slit the Hills&mdash; And scooped a Turnpike for Themselves&mdash; And trodden out the Mills&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The braind within its groove

The brain within its groove

Runs evenly and true;

But let a splinter swerve,

'T were easier for you

To put the water back

When floods have slit the hills,

And scooped a turnpike for themselves, And blotted out the mills!

Emily Dickinson





The Brain—is wider than the Sky


The Brain—is wider than the Sky—

For—put them side by side—

The one the other will contain

With ease—and You—beside—

The Brain is deeper than the sea—

For—hold them—Blue to Blue—

The one the other will absorb—

As Sponges—Buckets—do—

The Brain is just the weight of God—

For—Heft them—Pound for Pound—

And they will differ—if they do—

As Syllable from Sound—

Emily Dickinson





The bustle in a house

The bustle in a house

The morning after death

Is solemnest of industries

Enacted upon earth,--

The sweeping up the heart,

And putting love away

We shall not want to use again

Until eternity.

Emily Dickinson





The Chemical conviction


The Chemical conviction

That Nought be lost

Enable in Disaster

My fractured Trust&mdash;

The Faces of the Atoms

If I shall see

How more the Finished Creatures

Departed me!

Emily Dickinson





The Child's faith is new


The Child's faith is new&mdash;

Whole&mdash;like His Principle&mdash; Wide&mdash;like the Sunrise

On fresh Eyes&mdash;

Never had a Doubt&mdash;

Laughs&mdash;at a Scruple&mdash; Believes all sham

But Paradise&mdash;

Credits the World&mdash;

Deems His Dominion

Broadest of Sovereignties&mdash;

And Caesar&mdash;mean&mdash;

In the Comparison&mdash;

Baseless Emperor&mdash;

Ruler of Nought&mdash;

Yet swaying all&mdash;

Grown bye and bye

To hold mistaken

His pretty estimates

Of Prickly Things

He gains the skill

Sorrowful&mdash;as certain&mdash; Men&mdash;to anticipate

Instead of Kings&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Color of a Queen, is this


The Color of a Queen, is this&mdash; The Color of a Sun

At setting&mdash;this and Amber&mdash; Beryl&mdash;and this, at Noon&mdash; And when at night&mdash;Auroran widths Fling suddenly on men&mdash;

'Tis this&mdash;and Witchcraft&mdash;nature keeps A Rank&mdash;for Iodine&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The Color of the Grave is Green


The Color of the Grave is Green&mdash; The Outer Grave&mdash;I mean&mdash; You would not know it from the Field&mdash; Except it own a Stone&mdash;

To help the fond&mdash;to find it&mdash; Too infinite asleep

To stop and tell them where it is&mdash; But just a Daisy&mdash;deep&mdash; The Color of the Grave is white&mdash; The outer Grave&mdash;I mean&mdash; You would not know it from the Drifts&mdash; In Winter&mdash;till the Sun&mdash; Has furrowed out the Aisles&mdash; Then&mdash;higher than the Land

The little Dwelling Houses rise

Where each&mdash;has left a friend&mdash; The Color of the Grave within&mdash; The Duplicate&mdash;I mean&mdash; Not all the Snows could make it white&mdash; Not all the Summers&mdash;Green&mdash; You've seen the Color&mdash;maybe&mdash; Upon a Bonnet bound&mdash;

When that you met it with before&mdash; The Ferret&mdash;cannot find&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The Court is far away


The Court is far away&mdash;

No Umpire&mdash;have I&mdash;

My Sovereign is offended&mdash;

To gain his grace&mdash;I'd die!

I'll seek his royal feet&mdash;

I'll say&mdash;Remember&mdash;King&mdash; Thou shalt&mdash;thyself&mdash;one day&mdash;a Child&mdash; Implore a larger&mdash;thing&mdash; That Empire&mdash;is of Czars&mdash; As small&mdash;they say&mdash;as I&mdash; Grant me&mdash;that day&mdash;the royalty&mdash; To intercede&mdash;for Thee&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The cricket sang,

The cricket sang,

And set the sun,

And workmen finished, one by one,

Their seam the day upon.

The low grass loaded with the dew,

The twilight stood as strangers do

With hat in hand, polite and new,

To stay as if, or go.

A vastness, as a neighbor, came,--

A wisdom without face or name,

A peace, as hemispheres at home,--

And so the night became.

Emily Dickinson





The Daisy follows soft the Sun


The Daisy follows soft the Sun&mdash; And when his golden walk is done&mdash; Sits shyly at his feet&mdash;

He&mdash;waking&mdash;finds the flower there&mdash; Wherefore&mdash;Marauder&mdash;art thou here?

Because, Sir, love is sweet!

We are the Flower&mdash;Thou the Sun!

Forgive us, if as days decline&mdash; We nearer steal to Thee!

Enamored of the parting West&mdash; The peace&mdash;the flight&mdash;the Amethyst&mdash; Night's possibility!

Emily Dickinson





The Day Came Slow

The day came slow, till five o'clock,

Then sprang before the hills,

Like hindered rubies, or the light,

A sudden musket spills.

The purple could not keep the east.

The sunrise shook from fold.

Like breadths of topaz, packed a night, The lady just unrolled.

The happy winds their timbrels took;

The birds in docile rows,

Arranged themselves around their prince.

(The wind is prince of those.)

The orchard sparkled like a Jew,---

How mighty 'twas to stay,

A guest in this stupendous place,

The parlor of the day.

Emily Dickinson






The Day came slow&mdash;till Five o'clock&mdash; Then sprang before the Hills

Like Hindered Rubies&mdash;or the Light A Sudden Musket&mdash;spills&mdash; The Purple could not keep the East&mdash; The Sunrise shook abroad

Like Breadths of Topaz&mdash;packed a Night&mdash; The Lady just unrolled&mdash;

The Happy Winds&mdash;their Timbrels took&mdash; The Birds&mdash;in docile Rows

Arranged themselves around their Prince The Wind&mdash;is Prince of Those&mdash; The Orchard sparkled like a Jew&mdash; How mighty 'twas&mdash;to be

A Guest in this stupendous place&mdash; The Parlor&mdash;of the Day&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The day came slow, till five o' clock

The day came slow, till five o'clock

Then sprang before the hills

Like hindered rubies, or the light

A sudden musket spills

The purple could not keep the east,

The sunrise shook from fold,

Like breadths of topaz, packed a night, The lady just unrolled.

The happy winds their timbrels took;

The birds, in docile rows,

Arranged themselves around their prince (The wind is prince of those).

The orchard sparkled like a Jew, --

How mighty 't was, to stay

A guest in this stupendous place,

The parlor of the day!

Emily Dickinson





The Day that I was crowned


The Day that I was crowned

Was like the other Days&mdash;

Until the Coronation came&mdash;

And then&mdash;'twas Otherwise&mdash; As Carbon in the Coal

And Carbon in the Gem

Are One&mdash;and yet the former

Were dull for Diadem&mdash;

I rose, and all was plain&mdash;

But when the Day declined

Myself and It, in Majesty

Were equally&mdash;adorned&mdash; The Grace that I&mdash;was chose&mdash; To Me&mdash;surpassed the Crown

That was the Witness for the Grace&mdash;

'Twas even that 'twas Mine&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Day undressed&mdash;Herself


The Day undressed&mdash;Herself&mdash; Her Garter&mdash;was of Gold&mdash; Her Petticoat&mdash;of Purple plain&mdash; Her Dimities&mdash;as old

Exactly&mdash;as the World&mdash; And yet the newest Star&mdash;

Enrolled upon the Hemisphere

Be wrinkled&mdash;much as Her&mdash; Too near to God&mdash;to pray&mdash; Too near to Heaven&mdash;to fear&mdash; The Lady of the Occident

Retired without a care&mdash;

Her Candle so expire

The flickering be seen

On Ball of Mast in Bosporus&mdash; And Dome&mdash;and Window Pane&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The Definition of Beauty is


The Definition of Beauty is

That Definition is none&mdash;

Of Heaven, easing Analysis,

Since Heaven and He are one.

Emily Dickinson





The difference between Despair


The difference between Despair

And Fear&mdash;is like the One

Between the instant of a Wreck

And when the Wreck has been&mdash; The Mind is smooth&mdash;no Motion&mdash; Contented as the Eye

Upon the Forehead of a Bust&mdash; That knows&mdash;it cannot see&mdash; Emily Dickinson






The Doomed&mdash;regard the Sunrise With different Delight&mdash;

Because&mdash;when next it burns abroad They doubt to witness it&mdash;

The Man&mdash;to die&mdash;tomorrow&mdash; Harks for the Meadow Bird&mdash;

Because its Music stirs the Axe

That clamors for his head&mdash;

Joyful&mdash;to whom the Sunrise

Precedes Enamored&mdash;Day&mdash; Joyful&mdash;for whom the Meadow Bird Has ought but Elegy!

Emily Dickinson





The Doomed—regard the Sunrise


The Doomed—regard the Sunrise

With different Delight—

Because—when next it burns abroad

They doubt to witness it—

The Man—to die—tomorrow—

Harks for the Meadow Bird—

Because its Music stirs the Axe

That clamors for his head—

Joyful—to whom the Sunrise

Precedes Enamored—Day—

Joyful—for whom the Meadow Bird

Has ought but Elegy!

Emily Dickinson





The Drop, that wrestles in the Sea


The Drop, that wrestles in the Sea&mdash; Forgets her own locality&mdash;

As I&mdash;toward Thee&mdash;

She knows herself an incense small&mdash; Yet small&mdash;she sighs&mdash;if All&mdash;is All&mdash; How larger&mdash;be?

The Ocean&mdash;smiles&mdash;at her Conceit&mdash; But she, forgetting Amphitrite&mdash; Pleads&mdash;"Me"?

Emily Dickinson





The Dust behind I strove to join


The Dust behind I strove to join

Unto the Disk before&mdash;

But Sequence ravelled out of Sound

Like Balls upon a Floor&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The dying need but little, dear,--

The dying need but little, dear,--

A glass of water's all,

A flower's unobtrusive face

To punctuate the wall,

A fan, perhaps, a friend's regret,

And certainly that one

No color in the rainbow

Perceives when you are gone.

Emily Dickinson






The face I carry with me&mdash;last&mdash; When I go out of Time&mdash;

To take my Rank&mdash;by&mdash;in the West&mdash; That face&mdash;will just be thine&mdash; I'll hand it to the Angel&mdash;

That&mdash;Sir&mdash;was my Degree&mdash; In Kingdoms&mdash;you have heard the Raised&mdash; Refer to&mdash;possibly.

He'll take it&mdash;scan it&mdash;step aside&mdash; Return&mdash;with such a crown

As Gabriel&mdash;never capered at&mdash; And beg me put it on&mdash;

And then&mdash;he'll turn me round and round&mdash; To an admiring sky&mdash;

As one that bore her Master's name&mdash; Sufficient Royalty!

Emily Dickinson





The face I carry with me—last


The face I carry with me—last—

When I go out of Time—

To take my Rank—by—in the West—

That face—will just be thine—

I'll hand it to the Angel—

That—Sir—was my Degree—

In Kingdoms—you have heard the Raised—

Refer to—possibly.

He'll take it—scan it—step aside—

Return—with such a crown

As Gabriel—never capered at—

And beg me put it on—

And then—he'll turn me round and round—

To an admiring sky—

As one that bore her Master's name—

Sufficient Royalty!

Emily Dickinson





The feet of people walking home


The feet of people walking home

With gayer sandals go&mdash;

The Crocus&mdash; til she rises

The Vassal of the snow&mdash;

The lips at Hallelujah

Long years of practise bore

Til bye and bye these Bargemen

Walked singing on the shore.

Pearls are the Diver's farthings

Extorted from the Sea&mdash;

Pinions&mdash; the Seraph's wagon

Pedestrian once&mdash; as we&mdash; Night is the morning's Canvas

Larceny&mdash; legacy&mdash;

Death, but our rapt attention

To Immortality.

My figures fail to tell me

How far the Village lies&mdash;

Whose peasants are the Angels&mdash; Whose Cantons dot the skies&mdash; My Classics veil their faces&mdash; My faith that Dark adores&mdash;

Which from its solemn abbeys

Such ressurection pours.

Emily Dickinson





The Fingers of the Light


The Fingers of the Light

Tapped soft upon the Town

With "I am great and cannot wait

So therefore let me in."

"You're soon," the Town replied,

"My Faces are asleep&mdash;

But swear, and I will let you by,

You will not wake them up."

The easy Guest complied

But once within the Town

The transport of His Countenance

Awakened Maid and Man

The Neighbor in the Pool

Upon His Hip elate

Made loud obeisance and the Gnat

Held up His Cup for Light.

Emily Dickinson





The first Day that I was a Life


The first Day that I was a Life

I recollect it&mdash;How still&mdash; That last Day that I was a Life

I recollect it&mdash;as well&mdash;

'Twas stiller&mdash;though the first Was still&mdash;

"Twas empty&mdash;but the first Was full&mdash;

This&mdash;was my finallest Occasion&mdash; But then

My tenderer Experiment

Toward Men&mdash;

"Which choose I"?

That&mdash;I cannot say&mdash;

"Which choose They"?

Question Memory!

Emily Dickinson





The first Day's Night had come


The first Day's Night had come&mdash; And grateful that a thing

So terrible&mdash;had been endured&mdash; I told my Soul to sing&mdash;

She said her Strings were snapt&mdash; Her Bow&mdash;to Atoms blown&mdash; And so to mend her&mdash;gave me work Until another Morn&mdash;

And then&mdash;a Day as huge

As Yesterdays in pairs,

Unrolled its horror in my face&mdash; Until it blocked my eyes&mdash;

My Brain&mdash;begun to laugh&mdash; I mumbled&mdash;like a fool&mdash; And tho' 'tis Years ago&mdash;that Day&mdash; My Brain keeps giggling&mdash;still.

And Something's odd&mdash;within&mdash; That person that I was&mdash;

And this One&mdash;do not feel the same&mdash; Could it be Madness&mdash;this?

Emily Dickinson





The Flower must not blame the Bee


The Flower must not blame the Bee&mdash; That seeketh his felicity

Too often at her door&mdash;

But teach the Footman from Vevay&mdash; Mistress is "not at home"&mdash;to say&mdash; To people&mdash;any more!

Emily Dickinson





The Future&mdash;never spoke


The Future&mdash;never spoke&mdash; Nor will He&mdash;like the Dumb&mdash; Reveal by sign&mdash;a syllable

Of His Profound To Come&mdash;

But when the News be ripe&mdash;

Presents it&mdash;in the Act&mdash; Forestalling Preparation&mdash;

Escape&mdash;or Substitute&mdash; Indifference to Him&mdash;

The Dower&mdash;as the Doom&mdash; His Office&mdash;but to execute

Fate's&mdash;Telegram&mdash;to Him&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The Future—never spoke


The Future—never spoke—

Nor will He—like the Dumb—

Reveal by sign—a syllable

Of His Profound To Come—

But when the News be ripe—

Presents it—in the Act—

Forestalling Preparation—

Escape—or Substitute—

Indifference to Him—

The Dower—as the Doom—

His Office—but to execute

Fate's—Telegram—to Him—

Emily Dickinson





The Gentian weaves her fringes


The Gentian weaves her fringes&mdash; The Maple's loom is red&mdash;

My departing blossoms

Obviate parade.

A brief, but patient illness&mdash; An hour to prepare,

And one below this morning

Is where the angels are&mdash;

It was a short procession,

The Bobolink was there&mdash;

An aged Bee addressed us&mdash;

And then we knelt in prayer&mdash; We trust that she was willing&mdash; We ask that we may be.

Summer&mdash;Sister&mdash;Seraph!

Let us go with thee!

In the name of the Bee&mdash;

And of the Butterfly&mdash;

And of the Breeze&mdash;Amen!

Emily Dickinson





The good Will of a Flower


The good Will of a Flower

The Man who would possess

Must first present

Certificate

Of minted Holiness.

Emily Dickinson






The Grace&mdash;Myself&mdash;might not obtain&mdash; Confer upon My flower&mdash;

Refracted but a Countenance&mdash; For I&mdash;inhabit Her&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The Grace—Myself—might not obtain


The Grace—Myself—might not obtain—

Confer upon My flower—

Refracted but a Countenance—

For I—inhabit Her—

Emily Dickinson





The Grass so little has to do

The Grass so little has to do –

A Sphere of simple Green –

With only Butterflies to brood

And Bees to entertain –

And stir all day to pretty Tunes

The Breezes fetch along –

And hold the Sunshine in its lap

And bow to everything –

And thread the Dews, all night, like Pearls –

And make itself so fine

A Duchess were too common

For such a noticing –

And even when it dies – to pass

In Odors so divine –

Like Lowly spices, lain to sleep –

Or Spikenards, perishing –

And then, in Sovereign Barns to dwell –

And dream the Days away,

The Grass so little has to do

I wish I were a Hay –

Emily Dickinson





The Guest is gold and crimson


The Guest is gold and crimson&mdash; An Opal guest and gray&mdash;

Of Ermine is his doublet&mdash;

His Capuchin gay&mdash;

He reaches town at nightfall&mdash; He stops at every door&mdash;

Who looks for him at morning

I pray him too&mdash;explore

The Lark's pure territory&mdash;

Or the Lapwing's shore!

Emily Dickinson





The hallowing of Pain


The hallowing of Pain

Like hallowing of Heaven,

Obtains at a corporeal cost&mdash; The Summit is not given

To Him who strives severe

At middle of the Hill&mdash;

But He who has achieved the Top&mdash; All&mdash;is the price of All&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The heart asks pleasure first

The heart asks pleasure first

And then, excuse from pain-

And then, those little anodynes

That deaden suffering;

And then, to go to sleep;

And then, if it should be

The will of its Inquisitor,

The liberty to die.

Emily Dickinson






The Heart asks Pleasure&mdash;first&mdash; And then&mdash;Excuse from Pain&mdash; And then&mdash;those little Anodyness That deaden suffering&mdash;

And then&mdash;to go to sleep&mdash; And then&mdash;if it should be

The will of its Inquisitor

The privilege to die&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Heart has narrow Banks


The Heart has narrow Banks

It measures like the Sea

In mighty&mdash;unremitting Bass

And Blue Monotony

Till Hurricane bisect

And as itself discerns

Its sufficient Area

The Heart convulsive learns

That Calm is but a Wall

Of unattempted Gauze

An instant's Push demolishes

A Questioning&mdash;dissolves.

Emily Dickinson





The Heaven vests for Each


The Heaven vests for Each

In that small Deity

It craved the grace to worship

Some bashful Summer's Day&mdash;

Half shrinking from the Glory

It importuned to see

Till these faint Tabernacles drop

In full Eternity&mdash;

How imminent the Venture&mdash;

As one should sue a Star&mdash;

For His mean sake to leave the Row

And entertain Despair&mdash;

A Clemency so common&mdash;

We almost cease to fear&mdash;

Enabling the minutest&mdash;

And furthest&mdash;to adore&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The Himmaleh was known to stoop


The Himmaleh was known to stoop

Unto the Daisy low&mdash;

Transported with Compassion

That such a Doll should grow

Where Tent by Tent&mdash;Her Universe Hung out its Flags of Snow&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Hollows round His eager Eyes


The Hollows round His eager Eyes

Were Pages where to read

Pathetic Histories&mdash;although

Himself had not complained.

Biography to All who passed

Of Unobtrusive Pain

Except for the italic Face

Endured, unhelped&mdash;unknown.

Emily Dickinson





The Judge is like the Owl


The Judge is like the Owl&mdash;

I've heard my Father tell&mdash;

And Owls do build in Oaks&mdash;

So here's an Amber Sill&mdash;

That slanted in my Path&mdash;

When going to the Barn&mdash;

And if it serve You for a House&mdash; Itself is not in vain&mdash;

About the price&mdash;'tis small&mdash; I only ask a Tune

At Midnight&mdash;Let the Owl select His favorite Refrain.

Emily Dickinson





The Juggler's Hat her Country is


The Juggler's Hat her Country is&mdash; The Mountain Gorse&mdash;the Bee's!

Emily Dickinson





The Lady feeds Her little Bird


The Lady feeds Her little Bird

At rarer intervals&mdash;

The little Bird would not dissent

But meekly recognize

The Gulf between the Hand and Her

And crumbless and afar

And fainting, on Her yellow Knee

Fall softly, and adore&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Lamp burns sure&mdash;within


The Lamp burns sure&mdash;within&mdash; Tho' Serfs&mdash;supply the Oil&mdash; It matters not the busy Wick&mdash; At her phosphoric toil!

The Slave&mdash;forgets&mdash;to fill&mdash; The Lamp&mdash;burns golden&mdash;on&mdash; Unconscious that the oil is out&mdash; As that the Slave&mdash;is gone.

Emily Dickinson





The Lamp burns sure—within


The Lamp burns sure—within—

Tho' Serfs—supply the Oil—

It matters not the busy Wick—

At her phosphoric toil!

The Slave—forgets—to fill—

The Lamp—burns golden—on—

Unconscious that the oil is out—

As that the Slave—is gone.

Emily Dickinson





The last Night that She lived


The last Night that She lived

It was a Common Night

Except the Dying&mdash;this to Us

Made Nature different

We noticed smallest things&mdash;

Things overlooked before

By this great light upon our Minds

Italicized&mdash;as 'twere.

As We went out and in

Between Her final Room

And Rooms where Those to be alive

Tomorrow were, a Blame

That Others could exist

While She must finish quite

A Jealousy for Her arose

So nearly infinite&mdash;

We waited while She passed&mdash;

It was a narrow time&mdash;

Too jostled were Our Souls to speak

At length the notice came.

She mentioned, and forgot&mdash;

Then lightly as a Reed

Bent to the Water, struggled scarce&mdash; Consented, and was dead&mdash;

And We&mdash;We placed the Hair&mdash; And drew the Head erect&mdash;

And then an awful leisure was

Belief to regulate&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Leaves like Women interchange


The Leaves like Women interchange

Exclusive Confidence&mdash;

Somewhat of nods and somewhat

Portentous inference.

The Parties in both cases

Enjoining secrecy&mdash;

Inviolable compact

To notoriety.

Emily Dickinson






The Lightning playeth&mdash;all the while&mdash; But when He singeth&mdash;then&mdash; Ourselves are conscious He exist&mdash; And we approach Him&mdash;stern&mdash; With Insulators&mdash;and a Glove&mdash; Whose short&mdash;sepulchral Bass

Alarms us&mdash;tho' His Yellow feet May pass&mdash;and counterpass&mdash; Upon the Ropes&mdash;above our Head&mdash; Continual&mdash;with the News&mdash; Nor We so much as check our speech&mdash; Nor stop to cross Ourselves&mdash; Emily Dickinson

The Loneliness One dare not sound


The Loneliness One dare not sound&mdash; And would as soon surmise

As in its Grave go plumbing

To ascertain the size&mdash;

The Loneliness whose worst alarm

Is lest itself should see&mdash;

And perish from before itself

For just a scrutiny&mdash;

The Horror not to be surveyed&mdash; But skirted in the Dark&mdash;

With Consciousness suspended&mdash; And Being under Lock&mdash;

I fear me this&mdash;is Loneliness&mdash; The Maker of the soul

Its Caverns and its Corridors

Illuminate&mdash;or seal&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The lonesome for they know not What


The lonesome for they know not What&mdash; The Eastern Exiles&mdash;be&mdash; Who strayed beyond the Amber line

Some madder Holiday&mdash;

And ever since&mdash;the purple Moat They strive to climb&mdash;in vain&mdash; As Birds&mdash;that tumble from the clouds Do fumble at the strain&mdash;

The Blessed Ether&mdash;taught them&mdash; Some Transatlantic Morn&mdash;

When Heaven&mdash;was too common&mdash;to miss&mdash; Too sure&mdash;to dote upon!

Emily Dickinson





The Love a Life can show Below


The Love a Life can show Below

Is but a filament, I know,

Of that diviner thing

That faints upon the face of Noon&mdash; And smites the Tinder in the Sun&mdash; And hinders Gabriel's Wing&mdash;

'Tis this&mdash;in Music&mdash;hints and sways&mdash; And far abroad on Summer days&mdash; Distils uncertain pain&mdash;

'Tis this enamors in the East&mdash; And tints the Transit in the West

With harrowing Iodine&mdash;

'Tis this&mdash;invites&mdash;appalls&mdash;endows&mdash; Flits&mdash;glimmers&mdash;proves&mdash;dissolves&mdash; Returns&mdash;suggests&mdash;convicts&mdash;enchants&mdash; Then&mdash;flings in Paradise&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The Luxury to apprehend


The Luxury to apprehend

The Luxury 'twould be

To look at Thee a single time

An Epicure of Me

In whatsoever Presence makes

Till for a further Food

I scarcely recollect to starve

So first am I supplied&mdash;

The Luxury to meditate

The Luxury it was

To banguet on thy Countenance

A Sumptuousness bestows

On plainer Days, whose Table far

As Certainty can see

Is laden with a single Crumb

The Consciousness of Thee.

Emily Dickinson





The Malay&mdash;took the Pearl


The Malay&mdash;took the Pearl&mdash; Not&mdash;I&mdash;the Earl&mdash; I&mdash;feared the Sea&mdash;too much Unsanctified&mdash;to touch&mdash; Praying that I might be

Worthy&mdash;the Destiny&mdash; The Swarthy fellow swam&mdash;

And bore my Jewel&mdash;Home&mdash; Home to the Hut! What lot

Had I&mdash;the Jewel&mdash;got&mdash; Borne on a Dusky Breasty&mdash;

I had not deemed a Vest

Of Amber&mdash;fit&mdash;

The Negro never knew

I&mdash;wooed it&mdash;too&mdash; To gain, or be undone&mdash;

Alike to Him&mdash;One&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Malay—took the Pearl


The Malay—took the Pearl—

Not—I—the Earl—

I—feared the Sea—too much

Unsanctified—to touch—

Praying that I might be

Worthy—the Destiny—

The Swarthy fellow swam—

And bore my Jewel—Home—

Home to the Hut! What lot

Had I—the Jewel—got—

Borne on a Dusky Breasty—

I had not deemed a Vest

Of Amber—fit—

The Negro never knew

I—wooed it—too—

To gain, or be undone—

Alike to Him—One—

Emily Dickinson





The Manner of its Death


The Manner of its Death

When Certain it must die&mdash;

'Tis deemed a privilege to choose&mdash;

'Twas Major Andre's Way&mdash;

When Choice of Life&mdash;is past&mdash; There yet remains a Love

Its little Fate to stipulate&mdash; How small in those who live&mdash; The Miracle to tease

With Bable of the styles&mdash;

How "they are Dying mostly&mdash;now"&mdash; And Customs at "St. James"!

Emily Dickinson






The Martyr Poets&mdash;did not tell&mdash; But wrought their Pang in syllable&mdash; That when their mortal name be numb&mdash; Their mortal fate&mdash;encourage Some&mdash; The Martyr Painters&mdash;never spoke&mdash; Bequeathing&mdash;rather&mdash;to their Work&mdash; That when their conscious fingers cease&mdash; Some seek in Art&mdash;the Art of Peace&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The Martyr Poets—did not tell


The Martyr Poets—did not tell—

But wrought their Pang in syllable—

That when their mortal name be numb—

Their mortal fate—encourage Some—

The Martyr Painters—never spoke—

Bequeathing—rather—to their Work—

That when their conscious fingers cease—

Some seek in Art—the Art of Peace—

Emily Dickinson






The Missing All&mdash;prevented Me From missing minor Things.

If nothing larger than a World's

Departure from a Hinge&mdash;

Or Sun's extinction, be observed&mdash;

'Twas not so large that I

Could lift my Forehead from my work

For Curiosity.

Emily Dickinson

The Months have ends&mdash;the Years&mdash;a knot&mdash; No Power can untie

To stretch a little further

A Skein of Misery&mdash;

The Earth lays back these tired lives

In her mysterious Drawers&mdash;

Too tenderly, that any doubt

An ultimate Repose&mdash;

The manner of the Children&mdash;

Who weary of the Day&mdash;

Themself&mdash;the noisy Plaything They cannot put away&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

The Moon is distant from the Sea


The Moon is distant from the Sea&mdash; And yet, with Amber Hands&mdash;

She leads Him&mdash;docile as a Boy&mdash; Along appointed Sands&mdash;

He never misses a Degree&mdash;

Obedient to Her Eye

He comes just so far&mdash;toward the Town&mdash; Just so far&mdash;goes away&mdash; Oh, Signor, Thine, the Amber Hand&mdash; And mine&mdash;the distant Sea&mdash; Obedient to the least command

Thine eye impose on me&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Moon was but a Chin of Gold


The Moon was but a Chin of Gold

A Night or two ago&mdash;

And now she turns Her perfect Face

Upon the World below&mdash;

Her Forehead is of Amplest Blonde&mdash; Her Cheek&mdash;a Beryl hewn&mdash; Her Eye unto the Summer Dew

The likest I have known&mdash;

Her Lips of Amber never part&mdash; But what must be the smile

Upon Her Friend she could confer

Were such Her Silver Will&mdash;

And what a privilege to be

But the remotest Star&mdash;

For Certainty She take Her Way

Beside Your Palace Door&mdash;

Her Bonnet is the Firmament&mdash; The Universe&mdash;Her Shoe&mdash; The Stars&mdash;the Trinkets at Her Belt&mdash; Her Dimities&mdash;of Blue&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The Morning after Woe


The Morning after Woe&mdash;

'Tis frequently the Way&mdash;

Surpasses all that rose before&mdash; For utter Jubilee&mdash;

As Nature did not care&mdash;

And piled her Blossoms on&mdash;

And further to parade a Joy

Her Victim stared upon&mdash;

The Birds declaim their Tunes&mdash; Pronouncing every word

Like Hammers&mdash;Did they know they fell Like Litanies of Lead&mdash;

On here and there&mdash;a creature&mdash; They'd modify the Glee

To fit some Crucifixal Clef&mdash; Some Key of Calvary&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The morns are meeker than they were


The morns are meeker than they were&mdash; The nuts are getting brown&mdash;

The berry's cheek is plumper&mdash; The Rose is out of town.

The Maple wears a gayer scarf&mdash; The field a scarlet gown&mdash;

Lest I should be old fashioned

I'll put a trinket on.

Emily Dickinson





The Mountain sat upon the Plain


The Mountain sat upon the Plain

In his tremendous Chair&mdash;

His observation omnifold,

His inquest, everywhere&mdash;

The Seasons played around his knees

Like Children round a sire&mdash;

Grandfather of the Days is He

Of Dawn, the Ancestor&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

Looks long&mdash;and last&mdash;and golden&mdash; For fellowship&mdash;at night&mdash; Emily Dickinson





The Mountains—grow unnoticed


The Mountains—grow unnoticed—

Their Purple figures rise

Without attempt—Exhaustion—

Assistance—or Applause—

In Their Eternal Faces

The Sun—with just delight

Looks long—and last—and golden—

For fellowship—at night—

Emily Dickinson





The Murmur of a Bee


The Murmur of a Bee

A Witchcraft&mdash;yieldeth me&mdash; If any ask me why&mdash;

'Twere easier to die&mdash;

Than tell&mdash;

The Red upon the Hill

Taketh away my will&mdash;

If anybody sneer&mdash;

Take care&mdash;for God is here&mdash; That's all.

The Breaking of the Day

Addeth to my Degree&mdash;

If any ask me how&mdash;

Artist&mdash;who drew me so&mdash; Must tell!

Emily Dickinson





The Mystery of Pain

Pain has an element of blank;

It cannot recollect

When it began, or if there were

A day when it was not.

It has no future but itself,

Its infinite realms contain

Its past, enlightened to perceive

New periods of pain.

Emily Dickinson





The name&mdash;of it&mdash;is "Autumn"


The name&mdash;of it&mdash;is "Autumn"&mdash; The hue&mdash;of it&mdash;is Blood&mdash; An Artery&mdash;upon the Hill&mdash; A Vein&mdash;along the Road&mdash; Great Globules&mdash;in the Alleys&mdash; And Oh, the Shower of Stain&mdash; When Winds&mdash;upset the Basin&mdash; And spill the Scarlet Rain&mdash;

It sprinkles Bonnets&mdash;far below&mdash; It gathers ruddy Pools&mdash;

Then&mdash;eddies like a Rose&mdash;away&mdash; Upon Vermilion Wheels&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The name—of it—is


The name—of it—is "Autumn"—

The hue—of it—is Blood—

An Artery—upon the Hill—

A Vein—along the Road—

Great Globules—in the Alleys—

And Oh, the Shower of Stain—

When Winds—upset the Basin—

And spill the Scarlet Rain—

It sprinkles Bonnets—far below—

It gathers ruddy Pools—

Then—eddies like a Rose—away—

Upon Vermilion Wheels—

Emily Dickinson






The nearest Dream recedes&mdash;unrealized&mdash; The Heaven we chase,

Like the June Bee&mdash;before the School Boy, Invites the Race&mdash;

Stoops&mdash;to an easy Clover&mdash; Dips&mdash;evades&mdash;teases&mdash;deploys&mdash; Then&mdash;to the Royal Clouds

Lifts his light Pinnace&mdash;

Heedless of the Boy&mdash;

Staring&mdash;bewildered&mdash;at the mocking sky&mdash; Homesick for steadfast Honey&mdash; Ah, the Bee flies not

That brews that rare variety!

Emily Dickinson





The nearest dream recedes, unrealized

The nearest dream recedes, unrealized.

The heaven we chase

Like the June bee

Before the school-boy

Invites the race;

Stoops to an easy clover

Dips--evades--teases--deploys;

Then to the royal clouds

Lifts his light pinnace

Heedless of the boy

Staring, bewildered, at the mocking sky.

Homesick for steadfast honey,

Ah! the bee flies not

That brews that rare variety.

Emily Dickinson

The Night was wide, and furnished scant With but a single Star&mdash;

That often as a Cloud it met&mdash; Blew out itself&mdash;for fear&mdash; The Wind pursued the little Bush&mdash; And drove away the Leaves

November left&mdash;then clambered up And fretted in the Eaves&mdash;

No Squirrel went abroad&mdash;

A Dog's belated feet

Like intermittent Plush, he heard

Adown the empty Street&mdash;

To feel if Blinds be fast&mdash;

And closer to the fire&mdash;

Her little Rocking Chair to draw&mdash; And shiver for the Poor&mdash;

The Housewife's gentle Task&mdash; How pleasanter&mdash;said she

Unto the Sofa opposite&mdash;

The Sleet&mdash;than May, no Thee&mdash; Emily Dickinson






The One who could repeat the Summer day&mdash; Were greater than itself&mdash;though He Minutest of Mankind should be&mdash; And He&mdash;could reproduce the Sun&mdash; At period of going down&mdash;

The Lingering&mdash;and the Stain&mdash;I mean&mdash; When Orient have been outgrown

And Occident&mdash;become Unknown&mdash; His Name&mdash;remain&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The only ghost I ever saw

The only ghost I ever saw

Was dressed in mechlin, --so;

He wore no sandal on his foot,

And stepped like flakes of snow.

His gait was soundless, like the bird, But rapid, like the roe;

His fashions quaint, mosaic,

Or, haply, mistletoe.

Hi conversation seldom,

His laughter like the breeze

That dies away in dimples

Among the pensive trees.

Our interview was transient, --

Of me, himself was shy;

And God forbid I look behind

Since that appalling day!

Emily Dickinson





The Only News I know


The Only News I know

Is Bulletins all Day

From Immortality.

The Only Shows I see&mdash;

Tomorrow and Today&mdash;

Perchance Eternity&mdash;

The Only One I meet

Is God&mdash;The Only Street&mdash; Existence&mdash;This traversed

If Other News there be&mdash;

Or Admirable Show&mdash;

I'll tell it You&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





The Outer&mdash;from the Inner


The Outer&mdash;from the Inner

Derives its Magnitude&mdash;

'Tis Duke, or Dwarf, according

As is the Central Mood&mdash;

The fine&mdash;unvarying Axis

That regulates the Wheel&mdash;

Though Spokes&mdash;spin&mdash;more conspicuous And fling a dust&mdash;the while.

The Inner&mdash;paints the Outer&mdash; The Brush without the Hand&mdash;

Its Picture publishes&mdash;precise&mdash; As is the inner Brand&mdash;

On fine&mdash;Arterial Canvas&mdash; A Cheek&mdash;perchance a Brow&mdash; The Star's whole Secret&mdash;in the Lake&mdash; Eyes were not meant to know.

Emily Dickinson





The Outer—from the Inner


The Outer—from the Inner

Derives its Magnitude—

'Tis Duke, or Dwarf, according

As is the Central Mood—

The fine—unvarying Axis

That regulates the Wheel—

Though Spokes—spin—more conspicuous

And fling a dust—the while.

The Inner—paints the Outer—

The Brush without the Hand—

Its Picture publishes—precise—

As is the inner Brand—

On fine—Arterial Canvas—

A Cheek—perchance a Brow—

The Star's whole Secret—in the Lake—

Eyes were not meant to know.

Emily Dickinson
