'Twas the old&mdash;road&mdash;through pain&mdash; That unfrequented&mdash;one&mdash; With many a turn&mdash;and thorn&mdash; That stops&mdash;at Heaven&mdash; This&mdash;was the Town&mdash;she passed&mdash; There&mdash;where she&mdash;rested&mdash;last&mdash; Then&mdash;stepped more fast&mdash; The little tracks&mdash;close prest&mdash; Then&mdash;not so swift&mdash; Slow&mdash;slow&mdash;as feet did weary&mdash;grow&mdash; Then&mdash;stopped&mdash;no other track!

Wait! Look! Her little Book&mdash; The leaf&mdash;at love&mdash;turned back&mdash; Her very Hat&mdash;

And this worn shoe just fits the track&mdash; Herself&mdash;though&mdash;fled!

Another bed&mdash;a short one&mdash; Women make&mdash;tonight&mdash; In Chambers bright&mdash;

Too out of sight&mdash;though&mdash; For our hoarse Good Night&mdash;

To touch her Head!

Emily Dickinson





'Twas the old—road—through pain


'Twas the old—road—through pain—

That unfrequented—one—

With many a turn—and thorn—

That stops—at Heaven—

This—was the Town—she passed—

There—where she—rested—last—

Then—stepped more fast—

The little tracks—close prest—

Then—not so swift—

Slow—slow—as feet did weary—grow—

Then—stopped—no other track!

Wait! Look! Her little Book—

The leaf—at love—turned back—

Her very Hat—

And this worn shoe just fits the track—

Herself—though—fled!

Another bed—a short one—

Women make—tonight—

In Chambers bright—

Too out of sight—though—

For our hoarse Good Night—

To touch her Head!

Emily Dickinson






'Twas warm&mdash;at first&mdash;like Us&mdash; Until there crept upon

A Chill&mdash;like frost upon a Glass&mdash; Till all the scene&mdash;be gone.

The Forehead copied Stone&mdash;

The Fingers grew too cold

To ache&mdash;and like a Skater's Brook&mdash; The busy eyes&mdash;congealed&mdash; It straightened&mdash;that was all&mdash; It crowded Cold to Cold&mdash;

It multiplied indifference&mdash;

As Pride were all it could&mdash;

And even when with Cords&mdash;

'Twas lowered, like a Weight&mdash; It made no Signal, nor demurred,

But dropped like Adamant.

Emily Dickinson





'Twas warm—at first—like Us


'Twas warm—at first—like Us—

Until there crept upon

A Chill—like frost upon a Glass—

Till all the scene—be gone.

The Forehead copied Stone—

The Fingers grew too cold

To ache—and like a Skater's Brook—

The busy eyes—congealed—

It straightened—that was all—

It crowded Cold to Cold—

It multiplied indifference—

As Pride were all it could—

And even when with Cords—

'Twas lowered, like a Weight—

It made no Signal, nor demurred,

But dropped like Adamant.

Emily Dickinson





Twice had Summer her fair Verdure


Twice had Summer her fair Verdure

Proffered to the Plain&mdash;

Twice a Winter's silver Fracture

On the Rivers been&mdash;

Two full Autumns for the Squirrel

Bounteous prepared&mdash;

Nature, Had'st thou not a Berry

For thy wandering Bird?

Emily Dickinson





Two butterflies went out at noon

Two butterflies went out at noon

And waltzed above a stream,

Then stepped straight through the firmament And rested on a beam;

And then together bore away

Upon a shining sea,--

Though never yet, in any port

Their coming mentioned be.

If spoken by the distant bird,

If met in ether sea

By frigate or by merchantman,

Report was not to me.

Emily Dickinson





Two swimmers wrestled on the spar


Two swimmers wrestled on the spar&mdash; Until the morning sun&mdash;

When One&mdash;turned smiling to the land&mdash; Oh God! the Other One!

The stray ships&mdash;passing&mdash; Spied a face&mdash;

Upon the waters borne&mdash;

With eyes in death&mdash;still begging raised&mdash; And hands&mdash;beseeching&mdash;thrown!

Emily Dickinson





Two Travellers perishing in Snow


Two Travellers perishing in Snow

The Forests as they froze

Together heard them strengthening

Each other with the words

That Heaven if Heaven&mdash;must contain What Either left behind

And then the cheer too solemn grew

For language, and the wind

Long steps across the features took

That Love had touched the Morn

With reverential Hyacinth&mdash;

The taleless Days went on

Till Mystery impatient drew

And those They left behind

Led absent, were procured of Heaven

As Those first furnished, said&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Two&mdash;were immortal twice


Two&mdash;were immortal twice&mdash; The privilege of few&mdash;

Eternity&mdash;obtained&mdash;in Time&mdash; Reversed Divinity&mdash;

That our ignoble Eyes

The quality conceive

Of Paradise superlative&mdash;

Through their Comparative.

Emily Dickinson





'Twould ease&mdash;a Butterfly

Her least attention raise on me&mdash; Emily Dickinson

Into Divinity.

Under the Light, yet under


Under the Light, yet under,

Under the Grass and the Dirt,

Under the Beetle's Cellar

Under the Clover's Root,

Further than Arm could stretch

Were it Giant long,

Further than Sunshine could

Were the Day Year long,

Over the Light, yet over,

Over the Arc of the Bird&mdash;

Over the Comet's chimney&mdash;

Over the Cubit's Head,

Further than Guess can gallop

Further than Riddle ride&mdash;

Oh for a Disc to the Distance

Between Ourselves and the Dead!

Emily Dickinson






Undue Significance a starving man attaches To Food&mdash;

Far off&mdash;He sighs&mdash;and therefore&mdash;Hopeless&mdash; And therefore&mdash;Good&mdash; Partaken&mdash;it relieves&mdash;indeed&mdash; But proves us

That Spices fly

In the Receipt&mdash;It was the Distance&mdash; Was Savory&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

Unit, like Death, for Whom?


Unit, like Death, for Whom?

True, like the Tomb,

Who tells no secret

Told to Him&mdash;

The Grave is strict&mdash;

Tickets admit

Just two&mdash;the Bearer&mdash; And the Borne&mdash;

And seat&mdash;just One&mdash; The Living&mdash;tell&mdash;

The Dying&mdash;but a Syllable&mdash; The Coy Dead&mdash;None&mdash; No Chatter&mdash;here&mdash;no tea&mdash; So Babbler, and Bohea&mdash;stay there&mdash; But Gravity&mdash;and Expectation&mdash;and Fear&mdash; A tremor just, that All's not sure.

Emily Dickinson






Unto like Story&mdash;Trouble has enticed me&mdash; How Kinsmen fell&mdash;

Brothers and Sister&mdash;who preferred the Glory&mdash; And their young will

Bent to the Scaffold, or in Dungeons&mdash;chanted&mdash; Till God's full time&mdash;

When they let go the ignominy&mdash;smiling&mdash; And Shame went still&mdash;

Unto guessed Crests, my moaning fancy, leads me, Worn fair

By Heads rejected&mdash;in the lower country&mdash; Of honors there&mdash;

Such spirit makes her perpetual mention, That I&mdash;grown bold&mdash; Step martial&mdash;at my Crucifixion&mdash; As Trumpets&mdash;rolled&mdash; Feet, small as mine&mdash;have marched in Revolution Firm to the Drum&mdash;

Hands&mdash;not so stout&mdash;hoisted them&mdash;in witness&mdash; When Speech went numb&mdash;

Let me not shame their sublime deportments&mdash; Drilled bright&mdash;

Beckoning&mdash;Etruscan invitation&mdash; Toward Light&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






Unto like Story—Trouble has enticed me—

How Kinsmen fell—

Brothers and Sister—who preferred the Glory—

And their young will

Bent to the Scaffold, or in Dungeons—chanted—

Till God's full time—

When they let go the ignominy—smiling—

And Shame went still—

Unto guessed Crests, my moaning fancy, leads me, Worn fair

By Heads rejected—in the lower country—

Of honors there—

Such spirit makes her perpetual mention, That I—grown bold—

Step martial—at my Crucifixion—

As Trumpets—rolled—

Feet, small as mine—have marched in Revolution Firm to the Drum—

Hands—not so stout—hoisted them—in witness—

When Speech went numb—

Let me not shame their sublime deportments—

Drilled bright—

Beckoning—Etruscan invitation—

Toward Light—

Emily Dickinson





Unto Me? I do not know you—

"Unto Me?" I do not know you—

Where may be your House?

"I am Jesus—Late of Judea—

Now—of Paradise"—

Wagons—have you—to convey me?

This is far from Thence—

"Arms of Mine—sufficient Phaeton—

Trust Omnipotence"—

I am spotted—"I am Pardon"—

I am small—"The Least

Is esteemed in Heaven the Chiefest—

Occupy my House"—

Emily Dickinson

It half endears the Abstinence&mdash; And Pain&mdash;is missed&mdash;in Praise&mdash; As Flavors&mdash;cheer Retarded Guests With Banquettings to be&mdash;

So Spices&mdash;stimulate the time Till my small Library&mdash;

It may be Wilderness&mdash;without&mdash; Far feet of failing Men&mdash;

Enamor&mdash;in Prospective&mdash; And satisfy&mdash;obtained&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Unto my Books—so good to turn


Unto my Books—so good to turn—

Far ends of tired Days—

It half endears the Abstinence—

And Pain—is missed—in Praise—

As Flavors—cheer Retarded Guests

With Banquettings to be—

So Spices—stimulate the time

Till my small Library—

It may be Wilderness—without—

Far feet of failing Men—

But Holiday—excludes the night—

And it is Bells—within—

I thank these Kinsmen of the Shelf—

Their Countenances Kid

Enamor—in Prospective—

And satisfy—obtained—

Emily Dickinson





Upon Concluded Lives


Upon Concluded Lives

To Ears the Dying Side&mdash;

'Tis Coronal&mdash;and Funeral&mdash; Saluting&mdash;in the Road&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Victory comes late


Victory comes late&mdash;

And is held low to freezing lips&mdash; Too rapt with frost

To take it&mdash;

How sweet it would have tasted&mdash; Just a Drop&mdash;

Was God so economical?

His Table's spread too high for Us&mdash; Unless We dine on tiptoe&mdash;

Crumbs&mdash;fit such little mouths&mdash; Cherries&mdash;suit Robbins&mdash; The Eagle's Golden Breakfast strangles&mdash;Them&mdash; God keep His Oath to Sparrows&mdash; Who of little Love&mdash;know how to starve&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Victory comes late,

Victory comes late,

And is held low to freezing lips

Too rapt with frost

To take it.

How sweet it would have tasted,

Just a drop!

Was God so economical?

His table's spread too high for us

Unless we dine on tip-toe.

Crumbs fit such little mouths,

Cherries suit robins;

The eagle's golden breakfast

Strangles them.

God keeps his oath to sparrows,

Who of little love

Know how to starve!

Emily Dickinson





Wait till the Majesty of Death


Wait till the Majesty of Death

Invests so mean a brow!

Almost a powdered Footman

Might dare to touch it now!

Wait till in Everlasting Robes

That Democrat is dressed,

Then prate about "Preferment"&mdash; And "Station," and the rest!

Around this quiet Courtier

Obsequious Angels wait!

Full royal is his Retinue!

Full purple is his state!

A Lord, might dare to lift the Hat

To such a Modest Clay

Since that My Lord, "the Lord of Lords"

Receives unblushingly!

Emily Dickinson





Water, is taught by thirst


Water, is taught by thirst.

Land&mdash;by the Oceans passed.

Transport&mdash;by throe&mdash; Peace&mdash;by its battles told&mdash; Love, by Memorial Mold&mdash;

Birds, by the Snow.

Emily Dickinson





We can but follow to the Sun


We can but follow to the Sun&mdash; As oft as He go down

He leave Ourselves a Sphere behind&mdash;

'Tis mostly&mdash;following&mdash; We go no further with the Dust

Than to the Earthen Door&mdash;

And then the Panels are reversed&mdash; And we behold&mdash;no more.

Emily Dickinson





We Cover Thee&mdash;Sweet Face


We Cover Thee&mdash;Sweet Face&mdash; Not that We tire of Thee&mdash;

But that Thyself fatigue of Us&mdash; Remember&mdash;as Thou go&mdash; We follow Thee until

Thou notice Us&mdash;no more&mdash; And then&mdash;reluctant&mdash;turn away To Con Thee o'er and o'er&mdash;

And blame the scanty love

We were Content to show&mdash;

Augmented&mdash;Sweet&mdash;a Hundred fold&mdash; If Thou would'st take it&mdash;now&mdash; Emily Dickinson





We Cover Thee—Sweet Face


We Cover Thee—Sweet Face—

Not that We tire of Thee—

But that Thyself fatigue of Us—

Remember—as Thou go—

We follow Thee until

Thou notice Us—no more—

And then—reluctant—turn away

To Con Thee o'er and o'er—

And blame the scanty love

We were Content to show—

Augmented—Sweet—a Hundred fold—

If Thou would'st take it—now—

Emily Dickinson





We do not play on Graves


We do not play on Graves&mdash;

Because there isn't Room&mdash;

Besides&mdash;it isn't even&mdash;it slants And People come&mdash;

And put a Flower on it&mdash;

And hang their faces so&mdash;

We're fearing that their Hearts will drop&mdash; And crush our pretty play&mdash;

And so we move as far

As Enemies&mdash;away&mdash;

Just looking round to see how far

It is&mdash;Occasionally&mdash; Emily Dickinson





We don't cry&mdash;Tim and I


We don't cry&mdash;Tim and I,

We are far too grand&mdash;

But we bolt the door tight

To prevent a friend&mdash;

Then we hide our brave face

Deep in our hand&mdash;

Not to cry&mdash;Tim and I&mdash; We are far too grand&mdash;

Nor to dream&mdash;he and me&mdash; Do we condescend&mdash;

We just shut our brown eye

To see to the end&mdash;

Tim&mdash;see Cottages&mdash;

But, Oh, so high!

Then&mdash;we shake&mdash;Tim and I&mdash; And lest I&mdash;cry&mdash;

Tim&mdash;reads a little Hymn&mdash; And we both pray&mdash;

Please, Sir, I and Tim&mdash;

Always lost the way!

We must die&mdash;by and by&mdash; Clergymen say&mdash;

Tim&mdash;shall&mdash;if I&mdash;do&mdash; I&mdash;too&mdash;if he&mdash; How shall we arrange it&mdash;

Tim&mdash;was&mdash;so&mdash;shy?

Take us simultaneous&mdash;Lord&mdash; I&mdash;"Tim"&mdash;and Me!

Emily Dickinson





We don't cry—Tim and I


We don't cry—Tim and I,

We are far too grand—

But we bolt the door tight

To prevent a friend—

Then we hide our brave face

Deep in our hand—

Not to cry—Tim and I—

We are far too grand—

Nor to dream—he and me—

Do we condescend—

We just shut our brown eye

To see to the end—

Tim—see Cottages—

But, Oh, so high!

Then—we shake—Tim and I—

And lest I—cry—

Tim—reads a little Hymn—

And we both pray—

Please, Sir, I and Tim—

Always lost the way!

We must die—by and by—

Clergymen say—

Tim—shall—if I—do—

I—too—if he—

How shall we arrange it—

Tim—was—so—shy?

Take us simultaneous—Lord—

I—"Tim"—and Me!

Emily Dickinson






We dream&mdash;it is good we are dreaming&mdash; It would hurt us&mdash;were we awake&mdash; But since it is playing&mdash;kill us, And we are playing&mdash;shriek&mdash; What harm? Men die&mdash;externally&mdash; It is a truth&mdash;of Blood&mdash; But we&mdash;are dying in Drama&mdash; And Drama&mdash;is never dead&mdash; Cautious&mdash;We jar each other&mdash; And either&mdash;open the eyes&mdash; Lest the Phantasm&mdash;prove the Mistake&mdash; And the livid Surprise

Cool us to Shafts of Granite&mdash; With just an Age&mdash;and Name&mdash; And perhaps a phrase in Egyptian&mdash; It's prudenter&mdash;to dream&mdash; Emily Dickinson





We dream—it is good we are dreaming


We dream—it is good we are dreaming—

It would hurt us—were we awake—

But since it is playing—kill us,

And we are playing—shriek—

What harm? Men die—externally—

It is a truth—of Blood—

But we—are dying in Drama—

And Drama—is never dead—

Cautious—We jar each other—

And either—open the eyes—

Lest the Phantasm—prove the Mistake—

And the livid Surprise

Cool us to Shafts of Granite—

With just an Age—and Name—

And perhaps a phrase in Egyptian—

It's prudenter—to dream—

Emily Dickinson





We Grow Accustomed to the Dark

We grow accustomed to the Dark --

When light is put away --

As when the Neighbor holds the Lamp

To witness her Goodbye --

A Moment -- We uncertain step

For newness of the night --

Then -- fit our Vision to the Dark --

And meet the Road -- erect --

And so of larger -- Darkness --

Those Evenings of the Brain --

When not a Moon disclose a sign --

Or Star -- come out -- within --

The Bravest -- grope a little --

And sometimes hit a Tree

Directly in the Forehead --

But as they learn to see --

Either the Darkness alters --

Or something in the sight

Adjusts itself to Midnight --

And Life steps almost straight.

Emily Dickinson





We learned the Whole of Love


We learned the Whole of Love&mdash; The Alphabet&mdash;the Words&mdash; A Chapter&mdash;then the mighty Book&mdash; Then&mdash;Revelation closed&mdash; But in Each Other's eyes

An Ignorance beheld&mdash;

Diviner than the Childhood's&mdash; And each to each, a Child&mdash;

Attempted to expound

What Neither&mdash;understood&mdash; Alas, that Wisdom is so large&mdash; And Truth&mdash;so manifold!

Emily Dickinson





We like march, his shoes are purple,

We like March, his shoes are purple,

He is new and high;

Makes he mud for dog and peddler,

Makes he forest dry;

Knows the adder's tongue his coming,

And begets her spot.

Stands the sun so close and mighty

That our minds are hot.

News is he of all the others;

Bold it were to die

With the blue-birds buccaneering

On his British sky.

Emily Dickinson





We lose&mdash;because we win


We lose&mdash;because we win&mdash; Gamblers&mdash;recollecting which

Toss their dice again!

Emily Dickinson





We lose—because we win


We lose—because we win—

Gamblers—recollecting which

Toss their dice again!

Emily Dickinson






We met as Sparks&mdash;Diverging Flints Sent various&mdash;scattered ways&mdash; We parted as the Central Flint

Were cloven with an Adze&mdash;

Subsisting on the Light We bore

Before We felt the Dark&mdash;

A Flint unto this Day&mdash;perhaps&mdash; But for that single Spark.

Emily Dickinson





We met as Sparks—Diverging Flints


We met as Sparks—Diverging Flints

Sent various—scattered ways—

We parted as the Central Flint

Were cloven with an Adze—

Subsisting on the Light We bore

Before We felt the Dark—

A Flint unto this Day—perhaps—

But for that single Spark.

Emily Dickinson





We miss Her, not because We see


We miss Her, not because We see&mdash; The Absence of an Eye&mdash;

Except its Mind accompany

Abridge Society

As slightly as the Routes of Stars&mdash; Ourselves&mdash;asleep below&mdash; We know that their superior Eyes

Include Us&mdash;as they go&mdash; Emily Dickinson





We outgrow love like other things

We outgrow love like other things

And put it in the drawer,

Till it an antique fashion shows

Like costumes grandsires wore.

Emily Dickinson





We outgrow love, like other things


We outgrow love, like other things

And put it in the Drawer&mdash;

Till it an Antique fashion shows&mdash; Like Costumes Grandsires wore.

Emily Dickinson





We play at Paste


We play at Paste&mdash;

Till qualified, for Pearl&mdash;

Then, drop the Paste&mdash;

And deem ourself a fool&mdash;

The Shapes&mdash;though&mdash;were similar&mdash; And our new Hands

Learned Gem-Tactics&mdash;

Practicing Sands&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





We play at paste,

We play at paste,

Till qualified for pearl,

Then drop the paste,

And deem ourself a fool.

The shapes, though, were similar,

And our new hands

Learned gem-tactics

Practising sands.

Emily Dickinson





We pray&mdash;to Heaven


We pray&mdash;to Heaven&mdash; We prate&mdash;of Heaven&mdash; Relate&mdash;when Neighbors die&mdash; At what o'clock to heaven&mdash;they fled&mdash; Who saw them&mdash;Wherefore fly?

Is Heaven a Place&mdash;a Sky&mdash;a Tree?

Location's narrow way is for Ourselves&mdash; Unto the Dead

There's no Geography&mdash;

But State&mdash;Endowal&mdash;Focus&mdash; Where&mdash;Omnipresence&mdash;fly?

Emily Dickinson





We see&mdash;Comparatively


We see&mdash;Comparatively&mdash; The Thing so towering high

We could not grasp its segment

Unaided&mdash;Yesterday&mdash; This Morning's finer Verdict&mdash; Makes scarcely worth the toil&mdash; A furrow&mdash;Our Cordillera&mdash; Our Apennine&mdash;a Knoll&mdash; Perhaps 'tis kindly&mdash;done us&mdash; The Anguish&mdash;and the loss&mdash; The wrenching&mdash;for His Firmament The Thing belonged to us&mdash;

To spare these Striding Spirits

Some Morning of Chagrin&mdash;

The waking in a Gnat's&mdash;embrace&mdash; Our Giants&mdash;further on&mdash; Emily Dickinson





We should not mind so small a flower


We should not mind so small a flower&mdash; Except it quiet bring

Our little garden that we lost

Back to the Lawn again.

So spicy her Carnations nod&mdash; So drunken, reel her Bees&mdash;

So silver steal a hundred flutes

From out a hundred trees&mdash;

That whoso sees this little flower

By faith may clear behold

The Bobolinks around the throne

And Dandelions gold.

Emily Dickinson





We talked as Girls do


We talked as Girls do&mdash;

Fond, and late&mdash;

We speculated fair, on every subject, but the Grave&mdash; Of ours, none affair&mdash;

We handled Destinies, as cool&mdash; As we&mdash;Disposers&mdash;be&mdash; And God, a Quiet Party

To our Authority&mdash;

But fondest, dwelt upon Ourself

As we eventual&mdash;be&mdash; When Girls to Women, softly raised

We&mdash;occupy&mdash;Degree&mdash; We parted with a contract

To cherish, and to write

But Heaven made both, impossible

Before another night.

Emily Dickinson






We thirst at first&mdash;'tis Nature's Act&mdash; And later&mdash;when we die&mdash; A little Water supplicate&mdash;

Of fingers going by&mdash;

It intimates the finer want&mdash; Whose adequate supply

Is that Great Water in the West&mdash; Termed Immortality&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





We thirst at first—'tis Nature's Act


We thirst at first—'tis Nature's Act—

And later—when we die—

A little Water supplicate—

Of fingers going by—

It intimates the finer want—

Whose adequate supply

Is that Great Water in the West—

Termed Immortality—

Emily Dickinson






We&mdash;Bee and I&mdash;live by the quaffing&mdash;

'Tisn't all Hock&mdash;with us&mdash; Life has its Ale&mdash;

But it's many a lay of the Dim Burgundy&mdash; We chant&mdash;for cheer&mdash;when the Wines&mdash;fail&mdash; Do we "get drunk"?

Ask the jolly Clovers!

Do we "beat" our "Wife"?

I&mdash;never wed&mdash;

Bee&mdash;pledges his&mdash;in minute flagons&mdash; Dainty&mdash;as the trees&mdash;on our deft Head&mdash; While runs the Rhine&mdash;

He and I&mdash;revel&mdash;

First&mdash;at the vat&mdash;and latest at the Vine&mdash; Noon&mdash;our last Cup&mdash;

"Found dead"&mdash;"of Nectar"&mdash; By a humming Coroner&mdash;

In a By-Thyme!

Emily Dickinson





We—Bee and I—live by the quaffing


We—Bee and I—live by the quaffing—

'Tisn't all Hock—with us—

Life has its Ale—

But it's many a lay of the Dim Burgundy—

We chant—for cheer—when the Wines—fail—

Do we "get drunk"?

Ask the jolly Clovers!

Do we "beat" our "Wife"?

I—never wed—

Bee—pledges his—in minute flagons—

Dainty—as the trees—on our deft Head—

While runs the Rhine—

He and I—revel—

First—at the vat—and latest at the Vine—

Noon—our last Cup—

"Found dead"—"of Nectar"—

By a humming Coroner—

In a By-Thyme!

Emily Dickinson





We'll pass without the parting


We'll pass without the parting

So to spare

Certificate of Absence&mdash;

Deeming where

I left Her I could find Her

If I tried&mdash;

This way, I keep from missing

Those that died.

Emily Dickinson





Went up a year this evening!


Went up a year this evening!

I recollect it well!

Amid no bells nor bravoes

The bystanders will tell!

Cheerful&mdash;as to the village&mdash; Tranquil&mdash;as to repose&mdash; Chastened&mdash;as to the Chapel

This humble Tourist rose!

Did not talk of returning!

Alluded to no time

When, were the gales propitious&mdash; We might look for him!

Was grateful for the Roses

In life's diverse bouquet&mdash;

Talked softly of new species

To pick another day;

Beguiling thus the wonder

The wondrous nearer drew&mdash;

Hands bustled at the moorings&mdash; The crown respectful grew&mdash;

Ascended from our vision

To Countenances new!

A Difference&mdash;A Daisy&mdash; Is all the rest I knew!

Emily Dickinson






Wert Thou but ill&mdash;that I might show thee How long a Day I could endure

Though thine attention stop not on me

Nor the least signal, Me assure&mdash; Wert Thou but Stranger in ungracious country&mdash; And Mine&mdash;the Door

Thou paused at, for a passing bounty&mdash; No More&mdash;

Accused&mdash;wert Thou&mdash;and Myself&mdash;Tribunal&mdash; Convicted&mdash;Sentenced&mdash;Ermine&mdash;not to Me Half the Condition, thy Reverse&mdash;to follow&mdash; Just to partake&mdash;the infamy&mdash; The Tenant of the Narrow Cottage, wert Thou&mdash; Permit to be

The Housewife in thy low attendance

Contenteth Me&mdash;

No Service hast Thou, I would not achieve it&mdash; To die&mdash;or live&mdash;

The first&mdash;Sweet, proved I, ere I saw thee&mdash; For Life&mdash;be Love&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






Wert Thou but ill—that I might show thee How long a Day I could endure

Though thine attention stop not on me

Nor the least signal, Me assure—

Wert Thou but Stranger in ungracious country—

And Mine—the Door

Thou paused at, for a passing bounty—

No More—

Accused—wert Thou—and Myself—Tribunal—

Convicted—Sentenced—Ermine—not to Me

Half the Condition, thy Reverse—to follow—

Just to partake—the infamy—

The Tenant of the Narrow Cottage, wert Thou—

Permit to be

The Housewife in thy low attendance

Contenteth Me—

No Service hast Thou, I would not achieve it—

To die—or live—

The first—Sweet, proved I, ere I saw thee—

For Life—be Love—

Emily Dickinson





What care the Dead, for Chanticleer


What care the Dead, for Chanticleer&mdash; What care the Dead for Day?

'Tis late your Sunrise vex their face&mdash; And Purple Ribaldry&mdash;of Morning Pour as blank on them

As on the Tier of Wall

The Mason builded, yesterday,

And equally as cool&mdash;

What care the Dead for Summer?

The Solstice had no Sun

Could waste the Snow before their Gate&mdash; And knew One Bird a Tune&mdash;

Could thrill their Mortised Ear

Of all the Birds that be&mdash;

This One&mdash;beloved of Mankind

Henceforward cherished be&mdash;

What care the Dead for Winter?

Themselves as easy freeze&mdash;

June Noon&mdash;as January Night&mdash; As soon the South&mdash;her Breeze Of Sycamore&mdash;or Cinnamon&mdash; Deposit in a Stone

And put a Stone to keep it Warm&mdash; Give Spices&mdash;unto Men&mdash; Emily Dickinson





What did They do since I saw Them?


What did They do since I saw Them?

Were They industrious?

So many questions to put Them

Have I the eagerness

That could I snatch Their Faces

That could Their lips reply

Not till the last was answered

Should They start for the Sky.

Not if Their Party were waiting,

Not if to talk with Me

Were to Them now, Homesickness

After Eternity.

Not if the Just suspect me

And offer a Reward

Would I restore my Booty

To that Bold Person, God&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





What I can do&mdash;I will


What I can do&mdash;I will&mdash; Though it be little as a Daffodil&mdash; That I cannot&mdash;must be

Unknown to possibility&mdash;

Emily Dickinson

What I see not, I better see


What I see not, I better see&mdash; Through Faith&mdash;my Hazel Eye

Has periods of shutting&mdash;

But, No lid has Memory&mdash;

For frequent, all my sense obscured

I equally behold

As someone held a light unto

The Features so beloved&mdash;-

And I arise&mdash;and in my Dream&mdash; Do Thee distinguished Grace&mdash; Till jealous Daylight interrupt&mdash; And mar thy perfectness&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





What if I say I shall not wait!


What if I say I shall not wait!

What if I burst the fleshly Gate&mdash; And pass escaped&mdash;to thee!

What if I file this Mortal&mdash;off&mdash; See where it hurt me&mdash;That's enough&mdash; And wade in Liberty!

They cannot take me&mdash;any more!

Dungeons can call&mdash;and Guns implore Unmeaning&mdash;now&mdash;to me&mdash; As laughter&mdash;was&mdash;an hour ago&mdash; Or Laces&mdash;or a Travelling Show&mdash; Or who died&mdash;yesterday!

Emily Dickinson





What Inn is this


What Inn is this

Where for the night

Peculiar Traveller comes?

Who is the Landlord?

Where the maids?

Behold, what curious rooms!

No ruddy fires on the hearth&mdash; No brimming Tankards flow&mdash;

Necromancer! Landlord!

Who are these below?

Emily Dickinson





What is—


What is—"Paradise"—

Who live there—

Are they "Farmers"—

Do they "hoe"—

Do they know that this is "Amherst"—

And that I—am coming—too—

Do they wear "new shoes"—in "Eden"—

Is it always pleasant—there—

Won't they scold us—when we're homesick—

Or tell God—how cross we are—

You are sure there's such a person

As "a Father"—in the sky—

So if I get lost—there—ever—

Or do what the Nurse calls "die"—

I shan't walk the "Jasper"—barefoot—

Ransomed folks—won't laugh at me—

Maybe—"Eden" a'n't so lonesome As New England used to be!

Emily Dickinson





What is&mdash;"Paradise"


What is&mdash;"Paradise"&mdash; Who live there&mdash;

Are they "Farmers"&mdash; Do they "hoe"&mdash;

As "a Father"&mdash;in the sky&mdash; So if I get lost&mdash;there&mdash;ever&mdash; Or do what the Nurse calls "die"&mdash; I shan't walk the "Jasper"&mdash;barefoot&mdash; Ransomed folks&mdash;won't laugh at me&mdash; Maybe&mdash;"Eden" a'n't so lonesome As New England used to be!

What shall I do when the Summer troubles&mdash; What, when the Rose is ripe&mdash; What when the Eggs fly off in Music

From the Maple Keep?

What shall I do when the Skies a'chirrup Drop a Tune on me&mdash;

When the Bee hangs all Noon in the Buttercup What will become of me?

Oh, when the Squirrel fills His Pockets And the Berries stare

How can I bear their jocund Faces

Thou from Here, so far?

'Twouldn't afflict a Robin&mdash;

All His Goods have Wings&mdash;

I&mdash;do not fly, so wherefore

My Perennial Things?

Emily Dickinson






What shall I do&mdash;it whimpers so&mdash; This little Hound within the Heart

All day and night with bark and start&mdash; And yet, it will not go&mdash;

Would you untie it, were you me&mdash; Would it stop whining&mdash;if to Thee&mdash; I sent it&mdash;even now?

It should not tease you&mdash;

By your chair&mdash;or, on the mat&mdash; Or if it dare&mdash;to climb your dizzy knee&mdash; Or&mdash;sometimes at your side to run&mdash; When you were willing&mdash;

Shall it come?

Tell Carlo&mdash;

He'll tell me!

Emily Dickinson





What shall I do—it whimpers so


What shall I do—it whimpers so—

This little Hound within the Heart

All day and night with bark and start—

And yet, it will not go—

Would you untie it, were you me—

Would it stop whining—if to Thee—

I sent it—even now?

It should not tease you—

By your chair—or, on the mat—

Or if it dare—to climb your dizzy knee—

Or—sometimes at your side to run—

When you were willing—

Shall it come?

Tell Carlo—

He'll tell me!

Emily Dickinson






What Soft&mdash;Cherubic Creatures&mdash; These Gentlewomen are&mdash;

One would as soon assault a Plush&mdash; Or violate a Star&mdash;

Such Dimity Convictions&mdash;

A Horror so refined

Of freckled Human Nature&mdash;

Of Deity&mdash;ashamed&mdash;

It's such a common&mdash;Glory&mdash; A Fisherman's&mdash;Degree&mdash; Redemption&mdash;Brittle Lady&mdash; Be so&mdash;ashamed of Thee&mdash; Emily Dickinson





What Soft—Cherubic Creatures


What Soft—Cherubic Creatures—

These Gentlewomen are—

One would as soon assault a Plush—

Or violate a Star—

Such Dimity Convictions—

A Horror so refined

Of freckled Human Nature—

Of Deity—ashamed—

It's such a common—Glory—

A Fisherman's—Degree—

Redemption—Brittle Lady—

Be so—ashamed of Thee—

Emily Dickinson





What would I give to see his face?


What would I give to see his face?

I'd give&mdash;I'd give my life&mdash;of course&mdash; But that is not enough!

Stop just a minute&mdash;let me think!

I'd give my biggest Bobolink!

That makes two&mdash;Him&mdash;and Life!

You know who "June" is&mdash; I'd give her&mdash;

Roses a day from Zanzibar&mdash;

And Lily tubes&mdash;like Wells&mdash; Bees&mdash;by the furlong&mdash; Straits of Blue

Navies of Butterflies&mdash;sailed thro'&mdash; And dappled Cowslip Dells&mdash;

Then I have "shares" in Primrose "Banks"&mdash; Daffodil Dowries&mdash;spicy "Stocks"&mdash; Dominions&mdash;broad as Dew&mdash; Bags of Doublons&mdash;adventurous Bees Brought me&mdash;from firmamental seas&mdash; And Purple&mdash;from Peru&mdash; Now&mdash;have I bought it&mdash;

"Shylock"? Say!

Sign me the Bond!

"I vow to pay

To Her&mdash;who pledges this&mdash; One hour&mdash;of her Sovereign's face"!

Ecstatic Contract!

Niggard Grace!

My Kingdom's worth of Bliss!

Emily Dickinson






When Bells stop ringing&mdash;Church&mdash;begins The Positive&mdash;of Bells&mdash; When Cogs&mdash;stop&mdash;that's Circumference&mdash; The Ultimate&mdash;of Wheels.

Emily Dickinson





When Bells stop ringing—Church—begins


When Bells stop ringing—Church—begins

The Positive—of Bells—

When Cogs—stop—that's Circumference—

The Ultimate—of Wheels.

Emily Dickinson





When Diamonds are a Legend


When Diamonds are a Legend,

And Diadems&mdash;a Tale&mdash; I Brooch and Earrings for Myself,

Do sow, and Raise for sale&mdash;

And tho' I'm scarce accounted,

My Art, a Summer Day&mdash;had Patrons&mdash; Once&mdash;it was a Queen&mdash; And once&mdash;a Butterfly&mdash; Emily Dickinson





When I count the seeds


When I count the seeds

That are sown beneath,

To bloom so, bye and bye&mdash;

When I con the people

Lain so low,

To be received as high&mdash;

When I believe the garden

Mortal shall not see&mdash;

Pick by faith its blossom

And avoid its Bee,

I can spare this summer, unreluctantly.

Emily Dickinson





When I have seen the Sun emerge


When I have seen the Sun emerge

From His amazing House&mdash;

And leave a Day at every Door

A Deed, in every place&mdash;

Without the incident of Fame

Or accident of Noise&mdash;

The Earth has seemed to me a Drum,

Pursued of little Boys

Emily Dickinson





When I hoped, I recollect


When I hoped, I recollect

Just the place I stood&mdash;

At a Window facing West&mdash;

Roughest Air&mdash;was good&mdash; Not a Sleet could bite me&mdash;

Not a frost could cool&mdash;

Hope it was that kept me warm&mdash; Not Merino shawl&mdash;

When I feared&mdash;I recollect

Just the Day it was&mdash;

Worlds were lying out to Sun&mdash; Yet how Nature froze&mdash;

Icicles upon my soul

Prickled Blue and Cool&mdash;

Bird went praising everywhere&mdash; Only Me&mdash;was still&mdash; And the Day that I despaired&mdash; This&mdash;if I forget

Nature will&mdash;that it be Night After Sun has set&mdash;

Darkness intersect her face&mdash; And put out her eye&mdash;

Nature hesitate&mdash;before

Memory and I&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





When I was small, a Woman died


When I was small, a Woman died&mdash; Today&mdash;her Only Boy

Went up from the Potomac&mdash;

His face all Victory

To look at her&mdash;How slowly

The Seasons must have turned

Till Bullets clipt an Angle

And He passed quickly round&mdash; If pride shall be in Paradise&mdash; Ourself cannot decide&mdash;

Of their imperial Conduct&mdash;

No person testified&mdash;

But, proud in Apparition&mdash;

That Woman and her Boy

Pass back and forth, before my Brain

As even in the sky&mdash;

I'm confident that Bravoes&mdash;

Perpetual break abroad

For Braveries, remote as this

In Scarlet Maryland&mdash;

Emily Dickinson






When Katie walks, this simple pair accompany her side, When Katie runs unwearied they follow on the road, When Katie kneels, their loving hands still clasp her pious knee&mdash; Ah! Katie! Smile at Fortune, with two so knit to thee!

Emily Dickinson





When Night is almost done


When Night is almost done&mdash;

And Sunrise grows so near

That we can touch the Spaces&mdash; It's time to smooth the Hair&mdash; And get the Dimples ready&mdash;

And wonder we could care

For that old&mdash;faded Midnight&mdash; That frightened&mdash;but an Hour&mdash; Emily Dickinson





When One has given up One's life


When One has given up One's life

The parting with the rest

Feels easy, as when Day lets go

Entirely the West

The Peaks, that lingered last

Remain in Her regret

As scarcely as the Iodine

Upon the Cataract.

Emily Dickinson





When Roses cease to bloom, Sir


When Roses cease to bloom, Sir,

And Violets are done&mdash;

When Bumblebees in solemn flight

Have passed beyond the Sun&mdash;

The hand that paused to gather

Upon this Summer's day

Will idle lie&mdash;in Auburn&mdash; Then take my flowers&mdash;pray!

Emily Dickinson





When the Astronomer stops seeking


When the Astronomer stops seeking

For his Pleiad's Face&mdash;

When the lone British Lady

Forsakes the Arctic Race

When to his Covenant Needle

The Sailor doubting turns&mdash;

It will be amply early

To ask what treason means.

Emily Dickinson





When we stand on the tops of Things


When we stand on the tops of Things&mdash; And like the Trees, look down&mdash; The smoke all cleared away from it&mdash; And Mirrors on the scene&mdash;

Just laying light&mdash;no soul will wink Except it have the flaw&mdash;

The Sound ones, like the Hills&mdash;shall stand&mdash; No Lighting, scares away&mdash;

The Perfect, nowhere be afraid&mdash; They bear their dauntless Heads,

Where others, dare not go at Noon,

Protected by their deeds&mdash;

The Stars dare shine occasionally

Upon a spotted World&mdash;

And Suns, go surer, for their Proof,

As if an Axle, held&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Where bells no more affright the morn


Where bells no more affright the morn&mdash; Where scrabble never comes&mdash;

Where very nimble Gentlemen

Are forced to keep their rooms&mdash; Where tired Children placid sleep

Thro' Centuries of noon

This place is Bliss&mdash;this town is Heaven&mdash; Please, Pater, pretty soon!

"Oh could we climb where Moses stood, And view the Landscape o'er"

Not Father's bells&mdash;nor Factories, Could scare us any more!

Emily Dickinson





Where I have lost, I softer tread


Where I have lost, I softer tread&mdash; I sow sweet flower from garden bed&mdash; I pause above that vanished head

And mourn.

Whom I have lost, I pious guard

From accent harsh, or ruthless word&mdash; Feeling as if their pillow heard,

Though stone!

When I have lost, you'll know by this&mdash; A Bonnet black&mdash;A dusk surplice&mdash; A little tremor in my voice

Like this!

Why, I have lost, the people know

Who dressed in flocks of purest snow

Went home a century ago

Next Bliss!

Emily Dickinson






Where Ships of Purple&mdash;gently toss&mdash; On Seas of Daffodil&mdash;

Fantastic Sailors&mdash;mingle&mdash; And then&mdash;the Wharf is still!

Emily Dickinson

Where Ships of Purple—gently toss—

On Seas of Daffodil—

Fantastic Sailors—mingle—

And then—the Wharf is still!

Emily Dickinson






Where Thou art&mdash;that&mdash;is Home&mdash; Cashmere&mdash;or Calvary&mdash;the same&mdash; Degree&mdash;or Shame&mdash;

I scarce esteem Location's Name&mdash; So I may Come&mdash;

What Thou dost&mdash;is Delight&mdash; Bondage as Play&mdash;be sweet&mdash; Imprisonment&mdash;Content&mdash; And Sentence&mdash;Sacrament&mdash; Just We two&mdash;meet&mdash;

Where Thou art not&mdash;is Woe&mdash; Tho' Bands of Spices&mdash;row&mdash; What Thou dost not&mdash;Despair&mdash; Tho' Gabriel&mdash;praise me&mdash;Sire&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Where Thou art—that—is Home


Where Thou art—that—is Home—

Cashmere—or Calvary—the same—

Degree—or Shame—

I scarce esteem Location's Name—

So I may Come—

What Thou dost—is Delight—

Bondage as Play—be sweet—

Imprisonment—Content—

And Sentence—Sacrament—

Just We two—meet—

Where Thou art not—is Woe—

Tho' Bands of Spices—row—

What Thou dost not—Despair—

Tho' Gabriel—praise me—Sire—

Emily Dickinson





Whether my bark went down at sea


Whether my bark went down at sea&mdash; Whether she met with gales&mdash;

Whether to isles enchanted

She bent her docile sails&mdash;

By what mystic mooring

She is held today&mdash;

This is the errand of the eye

Out upon the Bay.

Emily Dickinson

While it is alive


While it is alive

Until Death touches it

While it and I lap one Air

Dwell in one Blood

Under one Sacrament

Show me Division can split or pare&mdash; Love is like Life&mdash;merely longer Love is like Death, during the Grave

Love is the Fellow of the Resurrection Scooping up the Dust and chanting "Live"!

Emily Dickinson





Who Court obtain within Himself


Who Court obtain within Himself

Sees every Man a King&mdash;

And Poverty of Monarchy

Is an interior thing&mdash;

No Man depose

Whom Fate Ordain&mdash;

And Who can add a Crown

To Him who doth continual

Conspire against His Own

Emily Dickinson





Who Giants know, with lesser Men


Who Giants know, with lesser Men

Are incomplete, and shy&mdash;

For Greatness, that is ill at ease

In minor Company&mdash;

A Smaller, could not be perturbed&mdash; The Summer Gnat displays&mdash;

Unconscious that his single Fleet

Do not comprise the skies&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Who never lost, are unprepared


Who never lost, are unprepared

A Coronet to find!

Who never thirsted

Flagons, and Cooling Tamarind!

Who never climbed the weary league&mdash; Can such a foot explore

The purple territories

On Pizarro's shore?

How many Legions overcome&mdash;

The Emperor will say?

How many Colors taken

On Revolution Day?

How many Bullets bearest?

Hast Thou the Royal scar?

Angels! Write "Promoted"

On this Soldier's brow!

Emily Dickinson





Who occupies this House?


Who occupies this House?

A Stranger I must judge

Since No one know His Circumstance&mdash;

'Tis well the name and age

Are writ upon the Door

Or I should fear to pause

Where not so much as Honest Dog

Approach encourages.

It seems a curious Town&mdash;

Some Houses very old,

Some&mdash;newly raised this Afternoon, Were I compelled to build

It should not be among

Inhabitants so still

But where the Birds assemble

And Boys were possible.

Before Myself was born

'Twas settled, so they say,

A Territory for the Ghosts&mdash;

And Squirrels, formerly.

Until a Pioneer, as

Settlers often do

Liking the quiet of the Place

Attracted more unto&mdash;

And from a Settlement

A Capital has grown

Distinguished for the gravity

Of every Citizen.

The Owner of this House

A Stranger He must be&mdash;

Eternity's Acquaintances

Are mostly so&mdash;to me.

Emily Dickinson






Whole Gulfs&mdash;of Red, and Fleets&mdash;of Red&mdash; And Crews&mdash;of solid Blood&mdash; Did place upon the West&mdash;Tonight&mdash; As 'twere specific Ground&mdash;

And They&mdash;appointed Creatures&mdash; In Authorized Arrays&mdash;

Due&mdash;promptly&mdash;as a Drama&mdash; That bows&mdash;and disappears&mdash; Emily Dickinson





Whole Gulfs—of Red, and Fleets—of Red


Whole Gulfs—of Red, and Fleets—of Red—

And Crews—of solid Blood—

Did place upon the West—Tonight—

As 'twere specific Ground—

And They—appointed Creatures—

In Authorized Arrays—

Due—promptly—as a Drama—

That bows—and disappears—

Emily Dickinson





Whose are the little beds, I asked


Whose are the little beds, I asked

Which in the valleys lie?

Some shook their heads, and others smiled&mdash; And no one made reply.

Perhaps they did not hear, I said,

I will inquire again&mdash;

Whose are the beds&mdash;the tiny beds So thick upon the plain?

'Tis Daisy, in the shortest&mdash; A little further on&mdash;

Nearest the door&mdash;to wake the Ist&mdash; Little Leontoden.

'Tis Iris, Sir, and Aster&mdash;

Anemone, and Bell&mdash;

Bartsia, in the blanket red&mdash; And chubby Daffodil.

Meanwhile, at many cradles

Her busy foot she plied&mdash;

Humming the quaintest lullaby

That ever rocked a child.

Hush! Epigea wakens!

The Crocus stirs her lids&mdash;

Rhodora's cheek is crimson,

She's dreaming of the woods!

Then turning from them reverent&mdash; Their bedtime 'tis, she said&mdash; The Bumble bees will wake them

When April woods are red.

Emily Dickinson





Whose cheek is this?


Whose cheek is this?

What rosy face

Has lost a blush today?

I found her&mdash;"pleiad"&mdash;in the woods And bore her safe away.

Robins, in the tradition

Did cover such with leaves,

But which the cheek&mdash;

And which the pall

My scrutiny deceives.

Emily Dickinson





Why do I love You, Sir?

"Why do I love" You, Sir?

Because—

The Wind does not require the Grass

To answer—Wherefore when He pass

She cannot keep Her place.

Because He knows—and

Do not You—

And We know not—

Enough for Us

The Wisdom it be so—

The Lightning—never asked an Eye

Wherefore it shut—when He was by—

Because He knows it cannot speak—

And reasons not contained—

—Of Talk—

There be—preferred by Daintier Folk—

The Sunrise—Sire—compelleth Me—

Because He's Sunrise—and I see—

Therefore—Then—

I love Thee—

Emily Dickinson






Why make it doubt&mdash;it hurts it so&mdash; So sick&mdash;to guess&mdash;

So strong&mdash;to know&mdash; So brave&mdash;upon its little Bed To tell the very last They said

Unto Itself&mdash;and smile&mdash;And shake&mdash; For that dear&mdash;distant&mdash;dangerous&mdash;Sake&mdash; But&mdash;the Instead&mdash;the Pinching fear That Something&mdash;it did do&mdash;or dare&mdash; Offend the Vision&mdash;and it flee&mdash; And They no more remember me&mdash; Nor ever turn to tell me why&mdash; Oh, Master, This is Misery&mdash;

Emily Dickinson





Why make it doubt—it hurts it so


Why make it doubt—it hurts it so—

So sick—to guess—

So strong—to know—

So brave—upon its little Bed

To tell the very last They said

Unto Itself—and smile—And shake—

For that dear—distant—dangerous—Sake—

But—the Instead—the Pinching fear

That Something—it did do—or dare—

Offend the Vision—and it flee—

And They no more remember me—

Nor ever turn to tell me why—

Oh, Master, This is Misery—

Emily Dickinson





Why&mdash;do they shut Me out of Heaven?

But&mdash;I can say a little "Minor"

Timid as a Bird!

Wouldn't the Angels try me&mdash;

Just&mdash;once&mdash;more&mdash; Just&mdash;see&mdash;if I troubled them&mdash; But don't&mdash;shut the door!

Wild Nights - Wild Nights!

Wild nights - wild nights!

Were I with thee,

Wild nights should be

Our luxury.

Futile the winds

To a heart in port

Done with the compass,

Done with the chart.

Rowing in Eden -

Ah, the sea!

Might I but moor tonight

In thee.

Will there really be a


Will there really be a "Morning"?

Is there such a thing as "Day"?

Could I see it from the mountains

If I were as tall as they?

Has it feet like Water lilies?

Has it feathers like a Bird?

Is it brought from famous countries

Of which I have never heard?

Oh some Scholar! Oh some Sailor!

Oh some Wise Men from the skies!

Please to tell a little Pilgrim

Where the place called "Morning" lies!

Emily Dickinson

With thee, in the Desert

Within my Garden, rides a Bird


Within my Garden, rides a Bird

Upon a single Wheel&mdash;

Whose spokes a dizzy Music make

As 'twere a travelling Mill&mdash; He never stops, but slackens

Above the Ripest Rose&mdash;

Partakes without alighting

And praises as he goes,

Till every spice is tasted&mdash;

And then his Fairy Gig

Reels in remoter atmospheres&mdash; And I rejoin my Dog,

And He and I, perplex us

If positive, 'twere we&mdash;

Or bore the Garden in the Brain

This Curiosity&mdash;

But He, the best Logician,

Refers my clumsy eye&mdash;

To just vibrating Blossoms!

An Exquisite Reply!

Emily Dickinson





Within my reach!


Within my reach!

I could have touched!

I might have chanced that way!

Soft sauntered thro' the village&mdash; Sauntered as soft away!

So unsuspected Violets

Within the meadows go&mdash;

Too late for striving fingers

That passed, an hour ago!

Without this—there is nought


Without this—there is nought—

All other Riches be

As is the Twitter of a Bird—

Heard opposite the Sea—

I could not care—to gain

A lesser than the Whole—

For did not this include themself—

As Seams—include the Ball?

I wished a way might be

My Heart to subdivide—

'Twould magnify—the Gratitude—

And not reduce—the Gold—

Emily Dickinson

Woodpecker, The

His head, a cap and frill.

He laboreth at every tree,--

A worm his utmost goal.

Would you like summer? Taste of ours


Would you like summer? Taste of ours.

Spices? Buy here!

Ill! We have berries, for the parching!

Weary! Furloughs of down!

Perplexed! Estates of violet trouble ne'er looked on!

Captive! We bring reprieve of roses!

Fainting! Flasks of air!

Even for Death, a fairy medicine.

But, which is it, sir?

Emily Dickinson

You know that Portrait in the Moon

You left me, sweet, two legacies,--

You left me, sweet, two legacies,--

A legacy of love

A Heavenly Father would content,

Had He the offer of;

You left me boundaries of pain

Capacious as the sea,

Between eternity and time,

Your consciousness and me.

You said that I

You said that I "was Great"—one Day—

Then "Great" it be—if that please Thee—

Or Small—or any size at all—

Nay—I'm the size suit Thee—

Tall—like the Stag—would that?

Or lower—like the Wren—

Or other heights of Other Ones

I've seen?

Tell which—it's dull to guess—

And I must be Rhinoceros

Or Mouse—

At once—for Thee—

So say—if Queen it be—

Or Page—please Thee—

I'm that—or nought—

Or other thing—if other thing there be—

With just this Stipulus—

I suit Thee—

Emily Dickinson

You see I cannot see—your lifetime—

How many times for my far sake

The brave eyes film—

My own—so patient—covers—

Teasing the want—

It—only—can suffice!

You taught me Waiting with Myself


You taught me Waiting with Myself&mdash; Appointment strictly kept&mdash;

You taught me fortitude of Fate&mdash; This&mdash;also&mdash;I have learnt&mdash; An Altitude of Death, that could

No bitterer debar

Than Life&mdash;had done&mdash;before it&mdash; Yet&mdash;there is a Science more&mdash; The Heaven you know&mdash;to understand That you be not ashamed

Of Me&mdash;in Christ's bright Audience Upon the further Hand&mdash;

You'll find&mdash;it when you try to die&mdash; The Easier to let go&mdash;

For recollecting such as went&mdash; You could not spare&mdash;you know.

You'll find—it when you try to die


You'll find—it when you try to die—

The Easier to let go—

For recollecting such as went—

You could not spare—you know.

And though their places somewhat filled—

As did their Marble names

With Moss—they never grew so full—

You chose the newer names—

And when this World—sets further back—

As Dying—say it does—

The former love—distincter grows—

And supersedes the fresh—

And Thought of them—so fair invites—

It looks too tawdry Grace

To stay behind—with just the Toys

We bought—to ease their place—

Emily Dickinson

You'll know Her—by Her Foot


You'll know Her—by Her Foot—

The smallest Gamboge Hand

With Fingers—where the Toes should be—

Would more affront the Sand—

Than this Quaint Creature's Boot—

Adjusted by a Stern—

Without a Button—I could vouch—

Unto a Velvet Limb—

You'll know Her—by Her Vest—

Tight fitting—Orange—Brown—

Inside a Jacket duller—

She wore when she was born—

Her Cap is small—and snug—

Constructed for the Winds—

She'd pass for Barehead—short way off—

But as She Closer stands—

So finer 'tis than Wool—

You cannot feel the Seam—

Nor is it Clasped unto of Band—

Nor held upon—of Brim—

You'll know Her—by Her Voice—

At first—a doubtful Tone—

A sweet endeavor—but as March

To April—hurries on—

She squanders on your Ear

Such Arguments of Pearl—

You beg the Robin in your Brain

To keep the other—still—

Emily Dickinson

Your Riches&mdash;taught me&mdash;Poverty.

Myself&mdash;a Millionaire

In little Wealths, as Girls could boast Till broad as Buenos Ayre&mdash;

You drifted your Dominions&mdash;

A Different Peru&mdash;

And I esteemed All Poverty

For Life's Estate with you&mdash;

Of Mines, I little know&mdash;myself&mdash; But just the names, of Gems&mdash; The Colors of the Commonest&mdash; And scarce of Diadems&mdash;

So much, that did I meet the Queen&mdash; Her Glory I should know&mdash;

But this, must be a different Wealth&mdash; To miss it&mdash;beggars so&mdash; I'm sure 'tis India&mdash;all Day&mdash; To those who look on You&mdash;

Without a stint&mdash;without a blame, Might I&mdash;but be the Jew&mdash; I'm sure it is Golconda&mdash;

Beyond my power to deem&mdash;

To have a smile for Mine&mdash;each Day, How better, than a Gem!

At least, it solaces to know

That there exists&mdash;a Gold&mdash; Altho' I prove it, just in time

Its distance&mdash;to behold&mdash; Its far&mdash;far Treasure to surmise&mdash; And estimate the Pearl&mdash;

That slipped my simple fingers through&mdash; While just a Girl at School.

Emily Dickinson





Your Riches—taught me—Poverty


Your Riches—taught me—Poverty.

Myself—a Millionaire

In little Wealths, as Girls could boast Till broad as Buenos Ayre—

You drifted your Dominions—

A Different Peru—

And I esteemed All Poverty

For Life's Estate with you—

Of Mines, I little know—myself—

But just the names, of Gems—

The Colors of the Commonest—

And scarce of Diadems—

So much, that did I meet the Queen—

Her Glory I should know—

But this, must be a different Wealth—

To miss it—beggars so—

I'm sure 'tis India—all Day—

To those who look on You—

Without a stint—without a blame,

Might I—but be the Jew—

I'm sure it is Golconda—

Beyond my power to deem—

To have a smile for Mine—each Day,

How better, than a Gem!

At least, it solaces to know

That there exists—a Gold—

Altho' I prove it, just in time

Its distance—to behold—

Its far—far Treasure to surmise—

And estimate the Pearl—

That slipped my simple fingers through—

While just a Girl at School.

Emily Dickinson

I guess—

You've seen Balloons set—Haven't You?


You've seen Balloons set—Haven't You?

So stately they ascend—

It is as Swans—discarded You,

For Duties Diamond—

Their Liquid Feet go softly out

Upon a Sea of Blonde—

They spurn the Air, as t'were too mean For Creatures so renowned—

Their Ribbons just beyond the eye—

They struggle—some—for Breath—

And yet the Crowd applaud, below—

They would not encore—Death—

The Gilded Creature strains—and spins—

Trips frantic in a Tree—

Tears open her imperial Veins—

And tumbles in the Sea—

The Crowd—retire with an Oath—

The Dust in Streets—go down—

And Clerks in Counting Rooms

Observe—"'Twas only a Balloon"—

Emily Dickinson
